Title:  his fall. The scalp was the only admissible trophy of victory. Thus, it was
Title:  deemed more important to obtain the scalp than to kill the man. Some tribes
Title:  lay great stress on the honor of striking a dead body. These practices have
Title:  nearly disappeared among the Indians of the Atlantic states.
Title:  
Title:  2 The hunting-shirt is a picturesque smock-frock, being shorter, and
Title:  ornamented with fringes and tassels. The colors are intended to imitate the
Title:  hues of the wood, with a view to concealment. Many corps of American
Title:  riflemen have been thus attired, and the dress is one of the most striking
Title:  of modern times. The hunting-shirt is frequently white.
Title:  
Title:  3 The rifle of the army is short; that of the hunter is always long.
Title:  
Title:  4 The Mississippi. The scout alludes to a tradition which is very popular
Title:  among the tribes of the Atlantic states. Evidence of their Asiatic origin is
Title:  deduced from the circumstances, though great uncertainty hangs over the
Title:  whole history of the Indians.
Title:  
Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 4
Title:  
Title:       Well go thy way: thou shalt not from this grove
Title:       Till I torment thee for this injury.
Title:  
Title:                                                MIDSUMMER NIGHT'S DREAM.
Title:  
Title:  The words were still in the mouth of the scout, when the leader of the
Title:  party, whose approaching footsteps had caught the vigilant ear of the
Title:  Indian, came openly into view. A beaten path, such as those made by the
Title:  periodical passage of the deer, wound through a little glen at no great
Title:  distance, and struck the river at the point where the white man and his red
Title:  companions had posted themselves. Along this track the travelers, who had
Title:  produced a surprise so unusual in the depths of the forest, advanced slowly
Title:  toward the hunter, who was in front of his associates, in readiness to
Title:  receive them.
Title:  
Title:  Who comes? demanded the scout, throwing his rifle carelessly across his left
Title:  arm, and keeping the forefinger of his right hand on the trigger, though he
Title:  avoided all appearance of menace in the act. Who comes hither, among the
Title:  beasts and dangers of the wilderness?
Title:  
Title:  Believers in religion, and friends to the law and to the king, returned he
Title:  who rode foremost. Men who have journeyed since the rising sun, in the
Title:  shades of this forest, without nourishment, and are sadly tired of their
Title:  wayfaring.
Title:  
Title:  You are, then, lost, interrupted the hunter, and have found how helpless
Title:  'tis not to know whether to take the right hand or the left?
Title:  
Title:  Even so; sucking babes are not more dependent on those who guide them than
Title:  we who are of larger growth, and who may now be said to possess the stature
Title:  without the knowledge of men. Know you the distance to a post of the crown
Title:  called William Henry?
Title:  
Title:  Hoot! shouted the scout, who did not spare his open laughter, though
Title:  instantly checking the dangerous sounds he indulged his merriment at less
Title:  risk of being overheard by any lurking enemies. You are as much off the
Title:  scent as a hound would be, with Horican atwixt him and the deer! William
Title:  Henry, man! if you are friends to the king and have business with the army,
Title:  your way would be to follow the river down to Edward, and lay the matter
Title:  before Webb, who tarries there, instead of pushing into the defiles, and
Title:  driving this saucy Frenchman back across Champlain, into his den again.
Title:  
Title:  Before the stranger could make any reply to this unexpected proposition,
Title:  another horseman dashed the bushes aside, and leaped his charger into the
Title:  pathway, in front of his companion.
Title:  
Title:  What, then, may be our distance from Fort Edward? demanded a new speaker;
Title:  the place you advise us to seek we left this morning, and our destination is
Title:  the head of the lake.
Title:  
Title:  Then you must have lost your eyesight afore losing your way, for the road
Title:  across the portage is cut to a good two rods, and is as grand a path, I
Title:  calculate, as any that runs into London, or even before the palace of the
Title:  king himself.
Title:  
Title:  We will not dispute concerning the excellence of the passage, returned
Title:  Heyward, smiling; for, as the reader has anticipated, it was he. It is
Title:  enough, for the present, that we trusted to an Indian guide to take us by a
Title:  nearer, though blinder path, and that we are deceived in his knowledge. In
Title:  plain words, we know not where we are.
Title:  
Title:  An Indian lost in the woods! said the scout, shaking his head doubtingly;
Title:  When the sun is scorching the tree tops, and the water courses are full;
Title:  when the moss on every beech he sees will tell him in what quarter the north
Title:  star will shine at night. The woods are full of deer-paths which run to the
Title:  streams and licks, places well known to everybody; nor have the geese done
Title:  their flight to the Canada waters altogether! 'Tis strange that an Indian
Title:  should be lost atwixt Horican and the bend in the river! Is he a Mohawk?
Title:  
Title:  Not by birth, though adopted in that tribe; I think his birthplace was
Title:  farther north, and he is one of those you call a Huron.
Title:  
Title:  Hugh! exclaimed the two companions of the scout, who had continued until
Title:  this part of the dialogue, seated immovable, and apparently indifferent to
Title:  what passed, but who now sprang to their feet with an activity and interest
Title:  that had evidently got the better of their reserve by surprise.
Title:  
Title:  A Huron! repeated the sturdy scout, once more shaking his head in open
Title:  distrust; they are a thievish race, nor do I care by whom they are adopted;
Title:  you can never make anything of them but skulls and vagabonds. Since you
Title:  trusted yourself to the care of one of that nation, I only wonder that you
Title:  have not fallen in with more.
Title:  
Title:  Of that there is little danger, since William Henry is so many miles in our
Title:  front. You forget that I have told you our guide is now a Mohawk, and that
Title:  he serves with our forces as a friend.
Title:  
Title:  And I tell you that he who is born a Mingo will die a Mingo, returned the
Title:  other positively. A Mohawk! No, give me a Delaware or a Mohican for honesty;
Title:  and when they will fight, which they won't all do, having suffered their
Title:  cunning enemies, the Maquas, to make them women - but when they will fight
Title:  at all, look to a Delaware, or a Mohican, for a warrior!
Title:  
Title:  Enough of this, said Heyward, impatiently; I wish not to inquire into the
Title:  character of a man that I know, and to whom you must be a stranger. You have
Title:  not yet answered my question; what is our distance from the main army at
Title:  Edward?
Title:  
Title:  It seems that may depend on who is your guide. One would think such a horse
Title:  as that might get over a good deal of ground atwixt sun-up and sun-down.
Title:  
Title:  I wish no contention of idle words with you, friend, said Heyward, curbing
Title:  his dissatisfied manner, and speaking in a more gentle voice; if you will
Title:  tell me the distance to Fort Edward, and conduct me thither, your labor
Title:  shall not go without its reward.
Title:  
Title:  And in so doing, how know I that I don't guide an enemy and a spy of
Title:  Montcalm, to the works of the army? It is not every man who can speak the
Title:  English tongue that is an honest subject.
Title:  
Title:  If you serve with the troops, of whom I judge you to be a scout, you should
Title:  know of such a regiment of the king as the Sixtieth.
Title:  
Title:  The Sixtieth! you can tell me little of the Royal Americans that I don't
Title:  know, though I do wear a hunting-shirt instead of a scarlet jacket.
Title:  
Title:  Well, then, among other things, you may know the name of its major?
Title:  
Title:  Its major! interrupted the hunter, elevating his body like one who was proud
Title:  of his trust. If there is a man in the country who knows Major Effingham, he
Title:  stands before you.
Title:  
Title:  It is a corps which has many majors; the gentleman your name is the senior,
Title:  but I speak of the junior of them all; he who commands the companies in
Title:  garrison at William Henry.
Title:  
Title:  Yes, yes, I have heard that a young gentleman of vast riches, from one of
Title:  the provinces far south, has got the place. He is over young, too, to hold
Title:  such rank, and to be put above men whose heads are beginning to bleach; and
Title:  yet they say he is a soldier in his knowledge, and a gallant gentleman!
Title:  
Title:  Whatever he may be, or however he may be qualified for his rank, he now
Title:  speaks to you and, of course, can be no enemy to dread.
Title:  
Title:  The scout regarded Heyward in surprise, and then lifting his cap, he
Title:  answered, in a tone less confident than before - though still expressing
Title:  doubt.
Title:  
Title:  I have heard a party was to leave the encampment this morning for the lake
Title:  shore?
Title:  
Title:  You have heard the truth; but I preferred a nearer route, trusting to the
Title:  knowledge of the Indian I mentioned.
Title:  
Title:  And he deceived you, and then deserted?
Title:  
Title:  Neither, as I believe; certainly not the latter, for he is to be found in
Title:  the rear.
Title:  
Title:  I should like to look at the creatur'; if it is a true Iroquois I can tell
Title:  him by his knavish look, and by his paint, said the scout; stepping past the
Title:  charger of Heyward, and entering the path behind the mare of the singing
Title:  master, whose foal had taken advantage of the halt to exact the maternal
Title:  contribution. After shoving aside the bushes, and proceeding a few paces, he
Title:  encountered the females, who awaited the result of the conference with
Title:  anxiety, and not entirely without apprehension. Behind these, the runner
Title:  leaned against a tree, where he stood the close examination of the scout
Title:  with an air unmoved, though with a look so dark and savage, that it might in
Title:  itself excite fear. Satisfied with his scrutiny, the hunter soon left him.
Title:  As he repassed the females, he paused a moment to gaze upon their beauty,
Title:  answering to the smile and nod of Alice with a look of open pleasure. Thence
Title:  he went to the side of the motherly animal, and spending a minute in a
Title:  fruitless inquiry into the character of her rider, he shook his head and
Title:  returned to Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  A Mingo is a Mingo, and God having made him so, neither the Mohawks nor any
Title:  other tribe can alter him, he said, when he had regained his former
Title:  position. If we were alone, and you would leave that noble horse at the
Title:  mercy of the wolves to-night, I could show you the way to Edward myself,
Title:  within an hour, for it lies only about an hour's journey hence; but with
Title:  such ladies in your company 'tis impossible!
Title:  
Title:  And why? They are fatigued, but they are quite equal to a ride of a few more
Title:  miles.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis a natural impossibility! repeated the scout; I wouldn't walk a mile in
Title:  these woods after night gets into them, in company with that runner, for the
Title:  best rifle in the colonies. They are full of outlying Iroquois, and your
Title:  mongrel Mohawk knows where to find them too well to be my companion.
Title:  
Title:  Think you so? said Heyward, leaning forward in the saddle, and dropping his
Title:  voice nearly to a whisper; I confess I have not been without my own
Title:  suspicions, though I have endeavored to conceal them, and affected a
Title:  confidence I have not always felt, on account of my companions. It was
Title:  because I suspected him that I would follow no longer; making him, as you
Title:  see, follow me.
Title:  
Title:  I knew he was one of the cheats as soon as I laid eyes on him! returned the
Title:  scout, placing a finger on his nose, in sign of caution.
Title:  
Title:  The thief is leaning against the foot of the sugar sapling, that you can see
Title:  over them bushes; his right leg is in a line with the bark of the tree, and,
Title:  tapping his rifle, I can take him from where I stand, between the angle and
Title:  the knee, with a single shot, putting an end to his tramping through the
Title:  woods, for at least a month to come. If I should go back to him, the cunning
Title:  varmint would suspect something, and be dodging through the trees like a
Title:  frightened deer.
Title:  
Title:  It will not do. He may be innocent, and I dislike the act. Though, if I felt
Title:  confident of his treachery - -
Title:  
Title:  'Tis a safe thing to calculate on the knavery of an Iroquois, said the
Title:  scout, throwing his rifle forward, by a sort of instinctive movement.
Title:  
Title:  Hold! interrupted Heyward, it will not do - we must think of some other
Title:  scheme - and yet, I have much reason to believe the rascal has deceived me.
Title:  
Title:  The hunter, who had already abandoned his intention of maiming the runner,
Title:  mused a moment, and then made a gesture, which instantly brought his two red
Title:  companions to his side. They spoke together earnestly in the Delaware
Title:  language, though in an undertone; and by the gestures of the white man,
Title:  which were frequently directed towards the top of the sapling, it was
Title:  evident he pointed out the situation of their hidden enemy. His companions
Title:  were not long in comprehending his wishes, and laying aside their firearms,
Title:  they parted, taking opposite sides of the path, and burying themselves in
Title:  the thicket, with such cautious movements, that their steps were inaudible.
Title:  
Title:  Now, go you back, said the hunter, speaking again to Heyward, and hold the
Title:  imp in talk; these Mohicans here will take him without breaking his paint.
Title:  
Title:  Nay, said Heyward, proudly, I will seize him myself.
Title:  
Title:  Hist! what could you do, mounted, against an Indian in the bushes!
Title:  
Title:  I will dismount.
Title:  
Title:  And, think you, when he saw one of your feet out of the stirrup, he would
Title:  wait for the other to be free? Whoever comes into the woods to deal with the
Title:  natives, must use Indian fashions, if he would wish to prosper in his
Title:  undertakings. Go, then; talk openly to the miscreant, and seem to believe
Title:  him the truest friend you have on 'arth.
Title:  
Title:  xx Heyward prepared to comply, though with strong disgust at the nature of
Title:  the office he was compelled to execute. Each moment, however, pressed upon
Title:  him a conviction of the critical situation in which he had suffered his
Title:  invaluable trust to be involved through his own confidence. The sun had
Title:  already disappeared, and the woods, suddenly deprived of his light,1 were
Title:  assuming a dusky hue, which keenly reminded him that the hour the savage
Title:  usually chose for his most barbarous and remorseless acts of vengeance or
Title:  hostility, was speedily drawing near. Stimulated by apprehension, he left
Title:  the scout, who immediately entered into a loud conversation with the
Title:  stranger that had so unceremoniously enlisted himself in the party of
Title:  travelers that morning. In passing his gentler companions Heyward uttered a
Title:  few words of encouragement, and was pleased to find that, though fatigued
Title:  with the exercise of the day, they appeared to entertain no suspicion that
Title:  their present embarrassment was other than the result of accident. Giving
Title:  them reason to believe he was merely employed in a consultation concerning
Title:  the future route, he spurred his charger, and drew the reins again when the
Title:  animal had carried him within a few yards of the place where the sullen
Title:  runner still stood, leaning against the tree. You may see, Magua, he said,
Title:  endeavoring to assume an air of freedom and confidence, that the night is
Title:  closing around us, and yet we are no nearer to William Henry than when we
Title:  left the encampment of Webb with the rising sun. You have missed the way,
Title:  nor have I been more fortunate. But, happily, we have fallen in with a
Title:  hunter, he whom you hear talking to the singer, that is acquainted with the
Title:  deerpaths and by-ways of the woods, and who promises to lead us to a place
Title:  where we may rest securely till the morning.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian riveted his glowing eyes on Heyward as he asked, in his imperfect
Title:  English, Is he alone?
Title:  
Title:  Alone! hesitatingly answered Heyward, to whom deception was too new to be
Title:  assumed without embarrassment. Oh! not alone, surely, Magua, for you know
Title:  that we are with him.
Title:  
Title:  Then Le Renard Subtil will go, returned the runner, coolly raising his
Title:  little wallet from the place where it had lain at his feet; and the pale
Title:  faces will see none but their own color.
Title:  
Title:  Go! Whom call you Le Renard?
Title:  
Title:  'Tis the name his Canada fathers have given to Magua, returned the runner,
Title:  with an air that manifested his pride at the distinction. Night is the same
Title:  as day to Le Subtil, when Munro waits for him.
Title:  
Title:  And what account will Le Renard give the chief of William Henry concerning
Title:  his daughters? Will he dare to tell the hot-blooded Scotsman that his
Title:  children are left without a guide, though Magua promised to be one?
Title:  
Title:  Though the gray head has a loud voice, and a long arm, Le Renard will not
Title:  hear him, nor feel him, in the woods.
Title:  
Title:  But what will the Mohawks say? They will make him petticoats, and bid him
Title:  stay in the wigwam with the women, for he is no longer to be trusted with
Title:  the business of a man.
Title:  
Title:  Le Subtil knows the path to the great lakes, and he can find the bones of
Title:  his fathers, was the answer of the unmoved runner.
Title:  
Title:  Enough, Magua, said Heyward; are we not friends? Why should there be bitter
Title:  words between us? Munro has promised you a gift for your services when
Title:  performed, and I shall be your debtor for another. Rest your weary limbs,
Title:  then, and open your wallet to eat. We have a few moments to spare; let us
Title:  not waste them in talk like wrangling women. When the ladies are refreshed
Title:  we will proceed.
Title:  
Title:  The pale faces make themselves dogs to their women, muttered the Indian, in
Title:  his native language, and when they want to eat, their warriors must lay
Title:  aside the tomahawk to feed their laziness.
Title:  
Title:  What say you, Renard?
Title:  
Title:  Le Subtil says it is good.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian then fastened his eyes keenly on the open countenance of Heyward,
Title:  but meeting his glance, he turned them quickly away, and seating himself
Title:  deliberately on the ground, he drew forth the remnant of some former repast,
Title:  and began to eat, though not without first bending his looks slowly and
Title:  cautiously around him.
Title:  
Title:  This is well, continued Heyward; and Le Renard will have strength and sight
Title:  to find the path in the morning; he paused, for sounds like the snapping of
Title:  a dried stick, and the rustling of leaves, rose from the adjacent bushes,
Title:  but recollecting himself instantly, he continued, we must be moving before
Title:  the sun is seen, or Montcalm may lie in our path, and shut us out from the
Title:  fortress.
Title:  
Title:  The hand of Magua dropped from his mouth to his side, and though his eyes
Title:  were fastened on the ground, his head was turned aside, his nostrils
Title:  expanded, and his ears seemed even to stand more erect than usual, giving to
Title:  him the appearance of a statue that was made to represent intense attention.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, who watched his movements with a vigilant eye, carelessly
Title:  extricated one of his feet from the stirrup, while he passed a hand toward
Title:  the bear-skin covering of his holsters. Every effort to detect the point
Title:  most regarded by the runner was completely frustrated by the tremulous
Title:  glances of his organs, which seemed not to rest a single instant on any
Title:  particular object, and which, at the same time, could be hardly said to
Title:  move. While he hesitated how to proceed, Le Subtil cautiously raised himself
Title:  to his feet, though with a motion so slow and guarded, that not the
Title:  slightest noise was produced by the change. Heyward felt it had now become
Title:  incumbent on him to act. Throwing his leg over the saddle, he dismounted,
Title:  with a determination to advance and seize his treacherous companion,
Title:  trusting the result to his own manhood. In order, however, to prevent
Title:  unnecessary alarm, he still preserved an air of calmness and friendship.
Title:  
Title:  Le Renard Subtil does not eat, he said, using the appellation he had found
Title:  most flattering to the vanity of the Indian. His corn is not well parched,
Title:  and it seems dry. Let me examine; perhaps something may be found among my
Title:  own provisions that will help his appetite.
Title:  
Title:  Magua held out the wallet to the proffer of the other. He even suffered
Title:  their hands to meet, without betraying the least emotion, or varying his
Title:  riveted attitude of attention. But when he felt the fingers of Heyward
Title:  moving gently along his own naked arm, he struck up the limb of the young
Title:  man, and, uttering a piercing cry, he darted beneath it, and plunged, at a
Title:  single bound, into the opposite thicket. At the next instant the form of
Title:  Chingachgook appeared from the bushes, looking like a specter in its paint,
Title:  and glided across the path in swift pursuit. Next followed the shout of
Title:  Uncas, when the woods were lighted by a sudden flash, that was accompanied
Title:  by the sharp report of the hunter's rifle.

Title:  Chapter 5
Title:  
Title:       ...In such a night
Title:       Did Thisbe fearfully o'ertrip the dew;
Title:       And saw the lion's shadow ere himself.
Title:  
Title:                                                      MERCHANT OF VENICE
Title:  
Title:  The suddenness of the flight of his guide, and the wild cries of the
Title:  pursuers, caused Heyward to remain fixed, for a few moments, in inactive
Title:  surprise. Then recollecting the importance of securing the fugitive, he
Title:  dashed aside the surrounding bushes, and pressed eagerly forward to lend his
Title:  aid in the chase. Before he had, however, proceeded a hundred yards, he met
Title:  the three foresters already returning from their unsuccessful pursuit.
Title:  
Title:  Why so soon disheartened! he exclaimed; the scoundrel must be concealed
Title:  behind some of these trees, and may yet be secured. We are not safe while he
Title:  goes at large.
Title:  
Title:  Would you set a cloud to chase the wind? returned the disappointed scout; I
Title:  heard the imp brushing over the dry leaves, like a black snake, and blinking
Title:  a glimpse of him, just over ag'in yon big pine, I pulled as it might be on
Title:  the scent; but 'twouldn't do! and yet for a reasoning aim, if anybody but
Title:  myself had touched the trigger, I should call it a quick sight; and I may be
Title:  accounted to have experience in these matters, and one who ought to know.
Title:  Look at this sumach; its leaves are red, though everybody knows the fruit is
Title:  in the yellow blossom in the month of July!
Title:  
Title:  'Tis the blood of Le Subtil! he is hurt, and may yet fall!
Title:  
Title:  No, no, returned the scout, in decided disapprobation of this opinion, I
Title:  rubbed the bark off a limb, perhaps, but the creature leaped the longer for
Title:  it. A rifle bullet acts on a running animal, when it barks him, much the
Title:  same as one of your spurs on a horse; that is, it quickens motion, and puts
Title:  life into the flesh, instead of taking it away. But when it cuts the ragged
Title:  hole, after a bound or two, there is, commonly, a stagnation of further
Title:  leaping, be it Indian or be it deer!
Title:  
Title:  We are four able bodies, to one wounded man!
Title:  
Title:  Is life grievous to you? interrupted the scout. Yonder red devil would draw
Title:  you within swing of the tomahawks of his comrades, before you were heated in
Title:  the chase. It was an unthoughtful act in a man who has so often slept with
Title:  the war-whoop ringing in the air, to let off his piece within sound of an
Title:  ambushment! But then it was a natural temptation! 'twas very natural! Come,
Title:  friends, let us move our station, and in such fashion, too, as will throw
Title:  the cunning of a Mingo on a wrong scent, or our scalps will be drying in the
Title:  wind in front of Montcalm's marquee, ag'in this hour to-morrow.
Title:  
Title:  This appalling declaration, which the scout uttered with the cool assurance
Title:  of a man who fully comprehended, while he did not fear to face the danger,
Title:  served to remind Heyward of the importance of the charge with which he
Title:  himself had been intrusted. Glancing his eyes around, with a vain effort to
Title:  pierce the gloom that was thickening beneath the leafy arches of the forest,
Title:  he felt as if, cut off from human aid, his unresisting companions would soon
Title:  lie at the entire mercy of those barbarous enemies, who, like beasts of
Title:  prey, only waited till the gathering darkness might render their blows more
Title:  fatally certain. His awakened imagination, deluded by the deceptive light,
Title:  converted each waving bush, or the fragment of some fallen tree, into human
Title:  forms, and twenty times he fancied he could distinguish the horrid visages
Title:  of his lurking foes, peering from their hiding places, in never ceasing
Title:  watchfulness of the movements of his party. Looking upward, he found that
Title:  the thin fleecy clouds, which evening had painted on the blue sky, were
Title:  already losing their faintest tints of rose-color, while the imbedded
Title:  stream, which glided past the spot where he stood, was to be traced only by
Title:  the dark boundary of its wooded banks.
Title:  
Title:  What is to be done! he said, feeling the utter helplessness of doubt in such
Title:  a pressing strait; desert me not, for God's sake! remain to defend those I
Title:  escort, and freely name your own reward!
Title:  
Title:  His companions, who conversed apart in the language of their tribe, heeded
Title:  not this sudden and earnest appeal. Though their dialogue was maintained in
Title:  low and cautious sounds, but little above a whisper, Heyward, who now
Title:  approached, could easily distinguish the earnest tones of the younger
Title:  warrior from the more deliberate speeches of his seniors. It was evident
Title:  that they debated on the propriety of some measure, that nearly concerned
Title:  the welfare of the travelers. Yielding to his powerful interest in the
Title:  subject, and impatient of a delay that seemed fraught with so much
Title:  additional danger, Heyward drew still nigher to the dusky group, with an
Title:  intention of making his offers of compensation more definite, when the white
Title:  man, motioning with his hand, as if he conceded the disputed point, turned
Title:  away, saying in a sort of solilquy, and in the English tongue:
Title:  
Title:  Uncas is right! it would not be the act of men to leave such harmless things
Title:  to their fate, even though it breaks up the harboring place forever. If you
Title:  would save these tender blossoms from the fangs of the worst of sarpents,
Title:  gentleman, you have neither time to lose nor resolution to throw away!
Title:  
Title:  How can such a wish be doubted! Have I not already offered - -
Title:  
Title:  Offer your prayers to Him who can give us wisdom to circumvent the cunning
Title:  of the devils who fill these woods, calmly interrupted the scout, but spare
Title:  your offers of money, which neither you may live to realize, nor I to profit
Title:  by. These Mohicans and I will do what man's thoughts can invent, to keep
Title:  such flowers, which, though so sweet, were never made for the wilderness,
Title:  from harm, and that without hope of any other recompense but such as God
Title:  always gives to upright dealings. First, you must promise two things, both
Title:  in your own name and for your friends, or without serving you we shall only
Title:  injure ourselves!
Title:  
Title:  Name them.
Title:  
Title:  The one is, to be still as these sleeping woods, let what will happen and
Title:  the other is, to keep the place where we shall take you, forever a secret
Title:  from all mortal men.
Title:  
Title:  I will do my utmost to see both these conditions fulfilled.
Title:  
Title:  Then follow, for we are losing moments that are as precious as the heart's
Title:  blood to a stricken deer!
Title:  
Title:  Heyward could distinguish the impatient gesture of the scout, through the
Title:  increasing shadows of the evening, and he moved in his footsteps, swiftly,
Title:  toward the place where he had left the remainder of the party. When they
Title:  rejoined the expecting and anxious females, he briefly acquainted them with
Title:  the conditions of their new guide, and with the necessity that existed for
Title:  their hushing every apprehension in instant and serious exertions. Although
Title:  his alarming communication was not received without much secret terror by
Title:  the listeners, his earnest and impressive manner, aided perhaps by the
Title:  nature of the danger, succeeded in bracing their nerves to undergo some
Title:  unlooked-for and unusual trial. Silently, and without a moment's delay, they
Title:  permitted him to assist them from their saddles, and when they descended
Title:  quickly to the water's edge, where the scout had collected the rest of the
Title:  party, more by the agency of expressive gestures than by any use of words.
Title:  
Title:  What to do with these dumb creatures! muttered the white man, on whom the
Title:  sole control of their future movements appeared to devolve; it would be time
Title:  lost to cut their throats, and cast them into the river; and to leave them
Title:  here would be to tell the Mingoes that they have not far to seek to find
Title:  their owners!
Title:  
Title:  Then give them their bridles, and let them range the woods, Heyward ventured
Title:  to suggest.
Title:  
Title:  No; it would be better to mislead the imps, and make them believe they must
Title:  equal a horse's speed to run down their chase. Ay, ay, that will blind their
Title:  fireballs of eyes! Chingach - Hist! what stirs the bush?
Title:  
Title:  The colt.
Title:  
Title:  That colt, at least, must die, muttered the scout, grasping at the mane of
Title:  the nimble beast, which easily eluded his hand; Uncas, your arrows!
Title:  
Title:  Hold! exclaimed the proprietor of the condemned animal, aloud, without
Title:  regard to the whispering tones used by the others; spare the foal of Miriam!
Title:  it is the comely offspring of a faithful dam, and would willingly injure
Title:  naught.
Title:  
Title:  When men struggle for the single life God has given them, said the scout,
Title:  sternly, even their own kind seem no more than the beasts of the wood. If
Title:  you speak again, I shall leave you to the mercy of the Maquas! Draw to your
Title:  arrow's head, Uncas; we have no time for second blows.
Title:  
Title:  The low, muttering sounds of his threatening voice were still audible, when
Title:  the wounded foal, first rearing on its hinder legs, plunged forward to its
Title:  knees. It was met by Chingachgook, whose knife passed across its throat
Title:  quicker than thought, and then precipitating the motions of the struggling
Title:  victim, he dashed into the river, down whose stream it glided away, gasping
Title:  audibly for breath with its ebbing life. This deed of apparent cruelty, but
Title:  of real necessity, fell upon the spirits of the travelers like a terrific
Title:  warning of the peril in which they stood, heightened as it was by the calm
Title:  though steady resolution of the actors in the scene. The sisters shuddered
Title:  and clung closer to each other, while Heyward instinctively laid his hand on
Title:  one of the pistols he had just drawn from their holsters, as he placed
Title:  himself between his charge and those dense shadows that seemed to draw an
Title:  impenetrable veil before the bosom of the forest.
Title:  
Title:  The Indians, however, hesitated not a moment, but taking the bridles, they
Title:  led the frightened and reluctant horses into the bed of the river.
Title:  
Title:  At a short distance from the shore they turned, and were soon concealed by
Title:  the projection of the bank, under the brow of which they moved, in a
Title:  direction opposite to the course of the waters. In the meantime, the scout
Title:  drew a canoe of bark from its place of concealment beneath some low bushes,
Title:  whose branches were waving with the eddies of the current, into which he
Title:  silently motioned for the females to enter. They complied without
Title:  hesitation, though many a fearful and anxious glance was thrown behind them,
Title:  toward the thickening gloom, which now lay like a dark barrier along the
Title:  margin of the stream.
Title:  
Title:  So soon as Cora and Alice were seated, the scout, without regarding the
Title:  element, directed Heyward to support one side of the frail vessel, and
Title:  posting himself at the other, they bore it up against the stream, followed
Title:  by the dejected owner of the dead foal. In this manner they proceeded, for
Title:  many rods, in a silence that was only interrupted by the rippling of the
Title:  water, as its eddies played around them, or the low dash made by their own
Title:  cautious footsteps. Heyward yielded the guidance of the canoe implicitly to
Title:  the scout, who approached or receded from the shore, to avoid the fragments
Title:  of rocks, or deeper parts of the river, with a readiness that showed his
Title:  knowledge of the route they held. Occasionally he would stop; and in the
Title:  midst of a breathing stillness, that the dull but increasing roar of the
Title:  waterfall only served to render more impressive, he would listen with
Title:  painful intenseness, to catch any sounds that might arise from the
Title:  slumbering forest. When assured that all was still, and unable to detect,
Title:  even by the aid of his practiced senses, any sign of his approaching foes,
Title:  he would deliberately resume his slow and guarded progress. At length they
Title:  reached a point in the river where the roving eye of Heyward became riveted
Title:  on a cluster of black objects, collected at a spot where the high bank threw
Title:  a deeper shadow than usual on the dark waters. Hesitating to advance, he
Title:  pointed out the place to the attention of his companion.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, returned the composed scout, the Indians have hid the beasts with the
Title:  judgment of natives! Water leaves no trail, and an owl's eyes would be
Title:  blinded by the darkness of such a hole.
Title:  
Title:  The whole party was soon reunited, and another consultation was held between
Title:  the scout and his new comrades, during which, they, whose fates depended on
Title:  the faith and ingenuity of these unknown foresters, had a little leisure to
Title:  observe their situation more minutely.
Title:  
Title:  The river was confined between high and cragged rocks, one of which impended
Title:  above the spot where the canoe rested. As these, again, were surmounted by
Title:  tall trees, which appeared to totter on the brows of the precipice, it gave
Title:  the stream the appearance of running through a deep and narrow dell. All
Title:  beneath the fantastic limbs and ragged tree tops, which were, here and
Title:  there, dimly painted against the starry zenith, lay alike in shadowed
Title:  obscurity. Behind them, the curvature of the banks soon bounded the view by
Title:  the same dark and wooded outline; but in front, and apparently at no great
Title:  distance, the water seemed piled against the heavens, whence it tumbled into
Title:  caverns, out of which issued those sullen sounds that had loaded the evening
Title:  atmosphere. It seemed, in truth, to be a spot devoted to seclusion, and the
Title:  sisters imbibed a soothing impression of security, as they gazed upon its
Title:  romantic though not unappalling beauties. A general movement among their
Title:  conductors, however, soon recalled them from a comtemplation of the wild
Title:  charms that night had assisted to lend the place to a painful sense of their
Title:  real peril.
Title:  
Title:  The horses had been secured to some scattering shrubs that grew in the
Title:  fissures of the rocks, where, standing in the water, they were left to pass
Title:  the night. The scout directed Heyward and his disconsolate fellow travelers
Title:  to seat themselves in the forward end of the canoe, and took possession of
Title:  the other himself, as erect and steady as if he floated in a vessel of much
Title:  firmer materials. The Indians warily retraced their steps toward the place
Title:  they had left, when the scout, placing his pole against a rock, by a
Title:  powerful shove, sent his frail bark directly into the turbulent stream. For
Title:  many minutes the struggle between the light bubble in which they floated and
Title:  the swift current was severe and doubtful. Forbidden to stir even a hand,
Title:  and almost afraid to breath, lest they should expose the frail fabric to the
Title:  fury of the stream, the passengers watched the glancing waters in feverish
Title:  suspense. Twenty times they thought the whirling eddies were sweeping them
Title:  to destruction, when the masterhand of their pilot would bring the bows of
Title:  the canoe to stem the rapid. A long, a vigorous, and, as it appeared to the
Title:  females, a desperate effort, closed the struggle. Just as Alice veiled her
Title:  eyes in horror, under the impression that they were about to be swept within
Title:  the vortex at the foot of the cataract, the canoe floated, stationary, at
Title:  the side of a flat rock, that lay on a level with the water.
Title:  
Title:  Where are we, and what is next to be done! demanded Heyward, perceiving that
Title:  the exertions of the scout had ceased.
Title:  
Title:  You are at the foot of Glenn's, returned the other, speaking aloud, without
Title:  fear of consequences within the roar of the cataract; and the next thing is
Title:  to make a steady landing, lest the canoe upset, and you should go down again
Title:  the hard road we have traveled faster than you came up; 'tis a hard rift to
Title:  stem, when the river is a little swelled; and five is an unnatural number to
Title:  keep dry, in a hurry-skurry, with a little birchen bark and gum. There, go
Title:  you all on the rock, and I will bring up the Mohicans with the venison. A
Title:  man had better sleep without his scalp, than famish in the midst of plenty.
Title:  
Title:  His passengers gladly complied with these directions. As the last foot
Title:  touched the rock, the canoe whirled from its station, when the tall form of
Title:  the scout was seen, for an instant, gliding above the waters, before it
Title:  disappeared in the impenetrable darkness that rested on the bed of the
Title:  river. Left by their guide, the travelers remained a few minutes in helpless
Title:  ignorance, afraid even to move along the broken rocks, lest a false step
Title:  should precipitate them down some one of the many deep and roaring caverns,
Title:  into which the water seemed to tumble, on every side of them. Their
Title:  suspense, however, was soon relieved; for, aided by the skill of the
Title:  natives, the canoe shot back into the eddy, and floated again at the side of
Title:  the low rock, before they thought the scout had even time to rejoin his
Title:  companions.
Title:  
Title:  We are now fortified, garrisoned, and provisioned, cried Heyward cheerfully,
Title:  and may set Montcalm and his allies at defiance. How, now, my vigilant
Title:  sentinel, can see anything of those you call the Iroquois, on the main land!
Title:  
Title:  I call them Iroquois, because to me every native, who speaks a foreign
Title:  tongue, is accounted an enemy, though he may pretend to serve the king! If
Title:  Webb wants faith and honesty in an Indian, let him bring out the tribes of
Title:  the Delawares, and send these greedy and lying Mohawks and Oneidas, with
Title:  their six nations of varlets, where in nature they belong, among the French!
Title:  
Title:  We should then exchange a warlike for a useless friend! I have heard that
Title:  the Delawares have laid aside the hatchet, and are content to be called
Title:  women!
Title:  
Title:  Aye, shame on the Hollanders1 and Iroquois, who circumvented them by their
Title:  deviltries, into such a treaty! But I have known them for twenty years, and
Title:  I call him liar that says cowardly blood runs in the veins of a Delaware.
Title:  You have driven their tribes from the seashore, and would now believe what
Title:  their enemies say, that you may sleep at night upon an easy pillow. No, no;
Title:  to me, every Indian who speaks a foreign tongue is an Iroquois, whether the
Title:  castle2 of his tribe be in Canada, or be in York. Heyward, perceiving that
Title:  the stubborn adherence of the scout to the cause of his friends the
Title:  Delawares, or Mohicans, for they were branches of the same numerous people,
Title:  was likely to prolong a useless discussion, changed the subject.
Title:  
Title:  Treaty or no treaty, I know full well that your two companions are brave and
Title:  cautious warriors! have they heard or seen anything of our enemies!
Title:  
Title:  An Indian is a mortal to be felt afore he is seen, returned the scout,
Title:  ascending the rock, and throwing the deer carelessly down. I trust to other
Title:  signs than such as come in at the eye, when I am outlying on the trail of
Title:  the Mingoes.
Title:  
Title:  Do your ears tell you that they have traced our retreat?
Title:  
Title:  I should be sorry to think they had, though this is a spot that stout
Title:  courage might hold for a smart scrimmage. I will not deny, however, but the
Title:  horses cowered when I passed them, as though they scented the wolves; and a
Title:  wolf is a beast that is apt to hover about an Indian ambushment, craving the
Title:  offals of the deer the savages kill.
Title:  
Title:  You forget the buck at your feet! or, may we not owe their visit to the dead
Title:  colt? Ha! what noise is that?
Title:  
Title:  Poor Miriam! murmured the stranger; thy foal was foreordained to become a
Title:  prey to ravenous beasts! Then, suddenly lifting up his voice, amid the
Title:  eternal din of the waters, he sang aloud:
Title:  
Title:       First born of Egypt, smite did he,
Title:       Of mankind, and of beast also:
Title:       O, Egypt! wonders sent 'midst thee,
Title:       On Pharaoh and his servants too!
Title:  
Title:  The death of the colt sits heavy on the heart of its owner, said the scout;
Title:  but it's a good sign to see a man account upon his dumb friends. He has the
Title:  religion of the matter, in believing what is to happen will happen; and with
Title:  such a consolation, it won't be long afore he submits to the rationality of
Title:  killing a four-footed beast to save the lives of human men. It may be as you
Title:  say, he continued, reverting to the purport of Heyward's last remark; and
Title:  the greater the reason why we should cut our steaks, and let the carcass
Title:  drive down the stream, or we shall have the pack howling along the cliffs,
Title:  begrudging every mouthful we swallow. Besides, though the Delaware tongue is
Title:  the same as a book to the Iroquois, the cunning varlets are quick enough at
Title:  understanding the reason of a wolf's howl.
Title:  
Title:  The scout, while making his remarks, was busied in collecting certain
Title:  necessary implements; as he concluded, he moved silently by the group of
Title:  travelers, accompanied by the Mohicans, who seemed to comprehend his
Title:  intentions with instinctive readiness, when the whole three disappeared in
Title:  succession, seeming to vanish against the dark face of a perpendicular rock
Title:  that rose to the height of a few yards, within as many feet of the water's
Title:  edge.

Title:  
Title:  1 New York was originally a colony of the Dutch.
Title:  
Title:  2 The principal villages of the Indians are still called castles by the
Title:  whites of New York. Oneida castle is no more than a scattered hamlet; but
Title:  the name is in general use.

Title:  Chapter 6
Title:  
Title:       Those strains that once did sweet in Zion glide;
Title:       He wales a portion with judicious care;
Title:       And Let us worship God, he says, with solemn air.
Title:  
Title:                                                                   BURNS
Title:  
Title:  Heyward and his female companions witnessed this mysterious movement with
Title:  secret uneasiness; for, though the conduct of the white man had hitherto
Title:  been above reproach, his rude equipments, blunt address, and strong
Title:  antipathies, together with the character of his silent associates, were all
Title:  causes for exciting distrust in minds that had been so recently alarmed by
Title:  Indian treachery.
Title:  
Title:  The stranger alone disregarded the passing incidents. He seated himself on a
Title:  projection of the rocks, whence he gave no other signs of consciousness than
Title:  by the struggles of his spirit, as manifested in frequent and heavy sighs.
Title:  Smothered voices were next heard, as though men called to each other in the
Title:  bowels of the earth, when a sudden light flashed upon those without, and
Title:  laid bare the much-prized secret of the place.
Title:  
Title:  At the further extremity of a narrow, deep cavern in the rock, whose length
Title:  appeared much extended by the perspective and the nature of the light by
Title:  which it was seen, was seated the scout, holding a blazing knot of pine. The
Title:  strong glare of the fire fell full upon his sturdy, weather-beaten
Title:  countenance and forest attire, lending an air of romantic wildness to the
Title:  aspect of an individual, who, seen by the sober light of day, would have
Title:  exhibited the peculiarities of a man remarkable for the strangeness of his
Title:  dress, the iron-like inflexibility of his frame, and the singular compound
Title:  of quick, vigilant sagacity, and of exquisite simplicity, that by turns
Title:  usurped the possession of his muscular features. At a little distance in
Title:  advance stood Uncas, his whole person thrown powerfully into view. The
Title:  travelers anxiously regarded the upright, flexible figure of the young
Title:  Mohican, graceful and unrestrained in the attitudes and movements of nature.
Title:  Though his person was more than usually screened by a green and fringed
Title:  hunting-shirt, like that of the white man, there was no concealment to his
Title:  dark, glancing, fearless eye, alike terrible and calm; the bold outline of
Title:  his high, haughty features, pure in their native red; or to the dignified
Title:  elevation of his receding forehead, together with all the finest proportions
Title:  of a noble head, bared to the generous scalping tuft. It was the first
Title:  opportunity possessed by Duncan and his companions to view the marked
Title:  lineaments of either of their Indian attendants, and each individual of the
Title:  party felt relieved from a burden of doubt, as the proud and determined,
Title:  though wild expression of the features of the young warrior forced itself on
Title:  their notice. They felt it might be a being partially benighted in the vale
Title:  of ignorance, but it could not be one who would willingly devote his rich
Title:  natural gifts to the purposes of wanton treachery. The ingenuous Alice gazed
Title:  at his free air and proud carriage, as she would have looked upon some
Title:  precious relic of the Grecian chisel, to which life had been imparted by the
Title:  intervention of a miracle; while Heyward, though accustomed to see the
Title:  perfection of form which abounds among the uncorrupted natives, openly
Title:  expressed his admiration at such an unblemished specimen of the noblest
Title:  proportions of man.
Title:  
Title:  I could sleep in peace, whispered Alice, in reply, with such a fearless and
Title:  generous-looking youth for my sentinel. Surely, Duncan, those cruel murders,
Title:  those terrific scenes of torture, of which we read and hear so much, are
Title:  never acted in the presence of such as he!
Title:  
Title:  This certainly is a rare and brilliant instance of those natural qualities
Title:  in which these peculiar people are said to excel, he answered. I agree with
Title:  you, Alice, in thinking that such a front and eye were formed rather to
Title:  intimidate than to deceive; but let us not practice a deception upon
Title:  ourselves, by expecting any other exhibition of what we esteem virtue than
Title:  according to the fashion of the savage. As bright examples of great
Title:  qualities are but too uncommon among Christians, so are they singular and
Title:  solitary with the Indians; though, for the honor of our common nature,
Title:  neither are incapable of producing them. Let us then hope that this Mohican
Title:  may not disappoint our wishes, but prove what his looks assert him to be, a
Title:  brave and constant friend.
Title:  
Title:  Now Major Heyward speaks as Major Heyward should, said Cora; who that looks
Title:  at this creature of nature, remembers the shade of his skin?
Title:  
Title:  A short and apparently an embarrassed silence succeeded this remark, which
Title:  was interrupted by the scout calling to them, aloud, to enter.
Title:  
Title:  This fire begins to show too bright a flame, he continued, as they complied,
Title:  and might light the Mingoes to our undoing. Uncas, drop the blanket, and
Title:  show the knaves its dark side. This is not such a supper as a major of the
Title:  Royal Americans has a right to expect, but I've known stout detachments of
Title:  the corps glad to eat their venison raw, and without a relish, too.1 Here,
Title:  you see, we have plenty of salt, and can make a quick broil. There's fresh
Title:  sassafras boughs for the ladies to sit on, which may not be as proud as
Title:  their my-hog-guinea chairs, but which sends up a sweeter flavor, than the
Title:  skin of any hog can do, be it of Guinea, or be it of any other land. Come,
Title:  friend, don't be mournful for the colt; 'twas an innocent thing, and had not
Title:  seen much hardship. Its death will save the creature many a sore back and
Title:  weary foot!
Title:  
Title:  Uncas did as the other had directed, and when the voice of Hawkeye ceased,
Title:  the roar of the cataract sounded like the rumbling of distant thunder.
Title:  
Title:  Are we quite safe in this cavern? demanded Heyward. Is there no danger of
Title:  surprise? A single armed man, at its entrance, would hold us at his mercy.
Title:  
Title:  A spectral-looking figure stalked from out of the darkness behind the scout,
Title:  and seizing a blazing brand, held it toward the further extremity of their
Title:  place of retreat. Alice uttered a faint shriek, and even Cora rose to her
Title:  feet, as this appalling object moved into the light; but a single word from
Title:  Heyward calmed them, with the assurance it was only their attendant,
Title:  Chingachgook, who, lifting another blanket, discovered that the cavern had
Title:  two outlets. Then, holding the brand, he crossed a deep, narrow chasm in the
Title:  rocks which ran at right angles with the passage they were in, but which,
Title:  unlike that, was open to the heavens, and entered another cave, answering to
Title:  the description of the first, in every essential particular.
Title:  
Title:  Such old foxes as Chingachgook and myself are not often caught in a barrow
Title:  with one hole, said Hawkeye, laughing; you can easily see the cunning of the
Title:  place - the rock is black limestone, which everybody knows is soft; it makes
Title:  no uncomfortable pillow, where brush and pine wood is scarce; well, the fall
Title:  was once a few yards below us, and I dare to say was, in its time, as
Title:  regular and as handsome a sheet of water as any along the Hudson. But old
Title:  age is a great injury to good looks, as these sweet young ladies have yet to
Title:  l'arn! The place is sadly changed! These rocks are full of cracks, and in
Title:  some places they are softer than at othersome, and the water has worked out
Title:  deep hollows for itself, until it has fallen back, ay, some hundred feet,
Title:  breaking here and wearing there, until the falls have neither shape nor
Title:  consistency.
Title:  
Title:  In what part of them are we? asked Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  Why, we are nigh the spot that Providence first placed them at, but where,
Title:  it seems, they were too rebellious to stay. The rock proved softer on each
Title:  side of us, and so they left the center of the river bare and dry, first
Title:  working out these two little holes for us to hide in.
Title:  
Title:  We are then on an island!
Title:  
Title:  Ay! there are the falls on two sides of us, and the river above and below.
Title:  If you had daylight, it would be worth the trouble to step up on the height
Title:  of this rock, and look at the perversity of the water. It falls by no rule
Title:  at all; sometimes it leaps, sometimes it tumbles; there it skips; here it
Title:  shoots; in one place 'tis white as snow, and in another 'tis green as grass;
Title:  hereabouts, it pitches into deep hollows, that rumble and crush the 'arth;
Title:  and thereaways, it ripples and sings like a brook, fashioning whirlpools and
Title:  gullies in the old stone, as if 'twas no harder than trodden clay. The whole
Title:  design of the river seems disconcerted. First it runs smoothly, as if
Title:  meaning to go down the descent as things were ordered; then it angles about
Title:  and faces the shores; nor are there places wanting where it looks backward,
Title:  as if unwilling to leave the wilderness, to mingle with the salt. Ay, lady,
Title:  the fine cobweb-looking cloth you wear at your throat is coarse, and like a
Title:  fishnet, to little spots I can show you, where the river fabricates all
Title:  sorts of images, as if having broke loose from order, it would try its hand
Title:  at everything. And yet what does it amount to! After the water has been
Title:  suffered so to have its will, for a time, like a headstrong man, it is
Title:  gathered together by the hand that made it, and a few rods below you may see
Title:  it all, flowing on steadily toward the sea, as was foreordained from the
Title:  first foundation of the 'arth!
Title:  
Title:  While his auditors received a cheering assurance of the security of their
Title:  place of concealment from this untutored description of Glenn's,2 they were
Title:  much inclined to judge differently from Hawkeye, of its wild beauties. But
Title:  they were not in a situation to suffer their thoughts to dwell on the charms
Title:  of natural objects; and, as the scout had not found it necessary to cease
Title:  his culinary labors while he spoke, unless to point out, with a broken fork,
Title:  the direction of some particularly obnoxious point in the rebellious stream,
Title:  they now suffered their attention to be drawn to the necessary though more
Title:  vulgar consideration of their supper.
Title:  
Title:  The repast, which was greatly aided by the addition of a few delicacies that
Title:  Heyward had the precaution to bring with him when they left their horses,
Title:  was exceedingly refreshing to the weary party. Uncas acted as attendant to
Title:  the females, performing all the little offices within his power, with a
Title:  mixture of dignity and anxious grace, that served to amuse Heyward, who well
Title:  knew that it was an utter innovation on the Indian customs, which forbid
Title:  their warriors to descend to any menial employment, especially in favor of
Title:  their women. As the rights of hospitality were, however, considered sacred
Title:  among them, this little departure from the dignity of manhood excited no
Title:  audible comment. Had there been one there sufficiently disengaged to become
Title:  a close observer, he might have fancied that the services of the young chief
Title:  were not entirely impartial. That while he tendered to Alice the gourd of
Title:  sweet water, and the venison in a trencher, neatly carved from the knot of
Title:  the pepperidge, with sufficient courtesy, in performing the same offices to
Title:  her sister, his dark eye lingered on her rich, speaking countenance. Once or
Title:  twice he was compelled to speak, to command her attention of those he
Title:  served. In such cases he made use of English, broken and imperfect, but
Title:  sufficiently intelligible, and which he rendered so mild and musical, by his
Title:  deep, guttural voice, that it never failed to cause both ladies to look up
Title:  in admiration and astonishment. In the course of these civilities, a few
Title:  sentences were exchanged, that served to establish the appearance of an
Title:  amicable intercourse between the parties.
Title:  
Title:  In the meanwhile, the gravity of Chingcachgook remained immovable. He had
Title:  seated himself more within the circle of light, where the frequent, uneasy
Title:  glances of his guests were better enabled to separate the natural expression
Title:  of his face from the artificial terrors of the war paint. They found a
Title:  strong resemblance between father and son, with the difference that might be
Title:  expected from age and hardships. The fierceness of his countenance now
Title:  seemed to slumber, and in its place was to be seen the quiet, vacant
Title:  composure which distinguishes an Indian warrior, when his faculties are not
Title:  required for any of the greater purposes of his existence. It was, however,
Title:  easy to be seen, by the occasional gleams that shot across his swarthy
Title:  visage, that it was only necessary to arouse his passions, in order to give
Title:  full effect to the terrific device which he had adopted to intimidate his
Title:  enemies. On the other hand, the quick, roving eye of the scout seldom
Title:  rested. He ate and drank with an appetite that no sense of danger could
Title:  disturb, but his vigilance seemed never to desert him. Twenty times the
Title:  gourd or the venison was suspended before his lips, while his head was
Title:  turned aside, as though he listened to some distant and distrusted sounds -
Title:  a movement that never failed to recall his guests from regarding the
Title:  novelties of their situation, to a recollection of the alarming reasons that
Title:  had driven them to seek it. As these frequent pauses were never followed by
Title:  any remark, the momentary uneasiness they created quickly passed away, and
Title:  for a time was forgotten.
Title:  
Title:  Come, friend, said Hawkeye, drawing out a keg from beneath a cover of
Title:  leaves, toward the close of the repast, and addressing the stranger who sat
Title:  at his elbow, doing great justice to his culinary skill, try a little
Title:  spruce; 'twill wash away all thoughts of the colt, and quicken the life in
Title:  your bosom. I drink to our better friendship, hoping that a little
Title:  horse-flesh may leave no heart-burnings atween us. How do you name yourself?
Title:  
Title:  Gamut - David Gamut, returned the singing master, preparing to wash down his
Title:  sorrows in a powerful draught of the woodsman's high-flavored and well-laced
Title:  compound.
Title:  
Title:  A very good name, and, I dare say, handed down from honest forefathers. I'm
Title:  an admirator of names, though the Christian fashions fall far below savage
Title:  customs in this particular. The biggest coward I ever knew as called Lyon;
Title:  and his wife, Patience, would scold you out of hearing in less time than a
Title:  hunted deer would run a rod. With an Indian 'tis a matter of conscience;
Title:  what he calls himself, he generally is - not that Chingachgook, which
Title:  signifies Big Sarpent, is really a snake, big or little; but that he
Title:  understands the windings and turnings of human natur, and is silent, and
Title:  strikes his enemies when they least expect him. What may be your calling?
Title:  
Title:  I am an unworthy instructor in the art of psalmody.
Title:  
Title:  Anan!
Title:  
Title:  I teach singing to the youths of the Connecticut levy.
Title:  
Title:  You might be better employed. The young hounds go laughing and singing too
Title:  much already through the woods, when they ought not to breathe louder than a
Title:  fox in his cover. Can you use the smoothbore, or handle the rifle?
Title:  
Title:  Praised be God, I have never had occasion to meddle with murderous
Title:  implements!
Title:  
Title:  Perhaps you understand the compass, and lay down the watercourses and
Title:  mountains of the wilderness on paper, in order that they who follow may find
Title:  places by their given names?
Title:  
Title:  I practice no such employment.
Title:  
Title:  You have a pair of legs that might make a long path seem short! you journey
Title:  sometimes, I fancy, with tidings for the general.
Title:  
Title:  Never; I follow no other than my own high vocation, which is instruction in
Title:  sacred music!
Title:  
Title:  'Tis a strange calling! muttered Hawkeye, with an inward laugh, to go
Title:  through life, like a catbird, mocking all the ups and downs that may happen
Title:  to come out of other men's throats. Well, friend, I suppose it is your gift,
Title:  and mustn't be denied any more than if 'twas shooting, or some other better
Title:  inclination. Let us hear what you can do in that way; 'twill be a friendly
Title:  manner of saying good-night, for 'tis time that these ladies should be
Title:  getting strength for a hard and a long push, in the pride of the morning,
Title:  afore the Maquas are stirring.
Title:  
Title:  With joyful pleasure do I consent, said David, adjusting his iron-rimmed
Title:  spectacles, and producing his beloved little volume, which he immediately
Title:  tendered to Alice. What can be more fitting and consolatory, than to offer
Title:  up evening praise, after a day of such exceeding jeopardy!
Title:  
Title:  Alice smiled; but, regarding Heyward, she blushed and hesitated.
Title:  
Title:  Indulge yourself, he whispered; ought not the suggestion of the worthy
Title:  namesake of the Psalmist to have its weight at such a moment?
Title:  
Title:  Encouraged by his opinion, Alice did what her pious inclinations, and her
Title:  keen relish for gentle sounds, had before so strongly urged. The book was
Title:  open at a hymn not ill adapted to their situation, and in which the poet, no
Title:  longer goaded by his desire to excel the inspired King of Israel, had
Title:  discovered some chastened and respectable powers. Cora betrayed a
Title:  disposition to support her sister, and the sacred song proceeded, after the
Title:  indispensable preliminaries of the pitchpipe, and the tune had been duly
Title:  attended to by the methodical David.
Title:  
Title:  The air was solemn and slow. At times it rose to the fullest compass of the
Title:  rich voices of the females, who hung over their little book in holy
Title:  excitement, and again it sank so low, that the rushing of the waters ran
Title:  through their melody, like a hollow accompaniment. The natural taste and
Title:  true ear of David governed and modified the sounds to suit the confined
Title:  cavern, every crevice and cranny of which was filled with the thrilling
Title:  notes of their flexible voices. The Indians riveted their eyes on the rocks,
Title:  and listened with an attention that seemed to turn them into stone. But the
Title:  scout, who had placed his chin in his hand, with an expression of cold
Title:  indifference, gradually suffered his rigid features to relax, until, as
Title:  verse succeeded verse, he felt his iron nature subdued, while his
Title:  recollection was carried back to boyhood, when his ears had been accustomed
Title:  to listen to similar sounds of praise, in the settlements of the colony. His
Title:  roving eyes began to moisten, and before the hymn was ended scalding tears
Title:  rolled out of fountains that had long seemed dry, and followed each other
Title:  down those cheeks, that had oftener felt the storms of heaven than any
Title:  testimonials of weakness. The singers were dwelling on one of those low,
Title:  dying chords, which the ear devours with such greedy rapture, as if
Title:  conscious that it is about to lose them, when a cry, that seemed neither
Title:  human nor earthly, rose in the outward air, penetrating not only the
Title:  recesses of the cavern, but to the inmost hearts of all who heard it. It was
Title:  followed by a stillness apparently as deep as if the waters had been checked
Title:  in their furious progress, at such a horrid and unusual interruption.
Title:  
Title:  What is it? murmured Alice, after a few moments of terrible suspense.
Title:  
Title:  What is it? repeated Hewyard aloud.
Title:  
Title:  Neither Hawkeye nor the Indians made any reply. They listened, as if
Title:  expecting the sound would be repeated, with a manner that expressed their
Title:  own astonishment. At length they spoke together, earnestly, in the Delaware
Title:  language, when Uncas, passing by the inner and most concealed aperture,
Title:  cautiously left the cavern. When he had gone, the scout first spoke in
Title:  English.
Title:  
Title:  What it is, or what it is not, none here can tell, though two of us have
Title:  ranged the woods for more than thirty years. I did believe there was no cry
Title:  that Indian or beast could make, that my ears had not heard; but this has
Title:  proved that I was only a vain and conceited mortal.
Title:  
Title:  Was it not, then, the shout the warriors make when they wish to intimidate
Title:  their enemies? asked Cora who stood drawing her veil about her person, with
Title:  a calmness to which her agitated sister was a stranger.
Title:  
Title:  No, no; this was bad, and shocking, and had a sort of unhuman sound; but
Title:  when you once hear the war-whoop, you will never mistake it for anything
Title:  else. Well, Uncas! speaking in Delaware to the young chief as he re-entered,
Title:  what see you? do our lights shine through the blankets?
Title:  
Title:  The answer was short, and apparently decided, being given in the same
Title:  tongue.
Title:  
Title:  There is nothing to be seen without, continued Hawkeye, shaking his head in
Title:  discontent; and our hiding-place is still in darkness. Pass into the other
Title:  cave, you that need it, and seek for sleep; we must be afoot long before the
Title:  sun, and make the most of our time to get to Edward, while the Mingoes are
Title:  taking their morning nap.
Title:  
Title:  Cora set the example of compliance, with a steadiness that taught the more
Title:  timid Alice the necessity of obedience. Before leaving the place, however,
Title:  she whispered a request to Duncan, that he would follow. Uncas raised the
Title:  blanket for their passage, and as the sisters turned to thank him for this
Title:  act of attention, they saw the scout seated again before the dying embers,
Title:  with his face resting on his hands, in a manner which showed how deeply he
Title:  brooded on the unaccountable interruption which had broken up their evening
Title:  devotions.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward took with him a blazing knot, which threw a dim light through the
Title:  narrow vista of their new apartment. Placing it in a favorable position, he
Title:  joined the females, who now found themselves alone with him for the first
Title:  time since they had left the friendly ramparts of Fort Edward.
Title:  
Title:  Leave us not, Duncan, said Alice: we cannot sleep in such a place as this,
Title:  with that horrid cry still ringing in our ears.
Title:  
Title:  First let us examine into the security of your fortress, he answered, and
Title:  then we will speak of rest.
Title:  
Title:  He approached the further end of the cavern, to an outlet, which, like the
Title:  others, was concealed by blankets; and removing the thick screen, breathed
Title:  the fresh and reviving air from the cataract. One arm of the river flowed
Title:  through a deep, narrow ravine, which its current had worn in the soft rock,
Title:  directly beneath his feet, forming an effectual defense, as he believed,
Title:  against any danger from that quarter; the water, a few rods above them,
Title:  plunging, glancing, and sweeping along in its most violent and broken
Title:  manner.
Title:  
Title:  Nature has made an impenetrable barrier on this side, he continued, pointing
Title:  down the perpendicular declivity into the dark current before he dropped the
Title:  blanket; and as you know that good men and true are on guard in front I see
Title:  no reason why the advice of our honest host should be disregarded. I am
Title:  certain Cora will join me in saying that sleep is necessary to you both.
Title:  
Title:  Cora may submit to the justice of your opinion though she cannot put it in
Title:  practice, returned the elder sister, who had placed herself by the side of
Title:  Alice, on a couch of sassafras; there would be other causes to chase away
Title:  sleep, though we had been spared the shock of this mysterious noise. Ask
Title:  yourself, Heyward, can daughters forget the anxiety a father must endure,
Title:  whose children lodge he knows not where or how, in such a wilderness, and in
Title:  the midst of so many perils?
Title:  
Title:  He is a soldier, and knows how to estimate the chances of the woods.
Title:  
Title:  He is a father, and cannot deny his nature.
Title:  
Title:  How kind has he ever been to all my follies, how tender and indulgent to all
Title:  my wishes! sobbed Alice. We have been selfish, sister, in urging our visit
Title:  at such hazard.
Title:  
Title:  I may have been rash in pressing his consent in a moment of much
Title:  embarrassment, but I would have proved to him, that however others might
Title:  neglect him in his strait his children at least were faithful.
Title:  
Title:  When he heard of your arrival at Edward, said Heyward, kindly, there was a
Title:  powerful struggle in his bosom between fear and love; though the latter,
Title:  heightened, if possible, by so long a separation, quickly prevailed. It is
Title:  the spirit of my noble- minded Cora that leads them, Duncan, he said, and I
Title:  will not balk it. Would to God, that he who holds the honor of our royal
Title:  master in his guardianship, would show but half her firmness!
Title:  
Title:  And did he not speak of me, Heyward? demanded Alice, with jealous affection;
Title:  surely, he forgot not altogether his little Elsie?
Title:  
Title:  That were impossible, returned the young man; he called you by a thousand
Title:  endearing epithets, that I may not presume to use, but to the justice of
Title:  which, I can warmly testify. Once, indeed, he said - -
Title:  
Title:  Duncan ceased speaking; for while his eyes were riveted on those of Alice,
Title:  who had turned toward him with the eagerness of filial affection, to catch
Title:  his words, the same strong, horrid cry, as before, filled the air, and
Title:  rendered him mute. A long, breathless silence succeeded, during which each
Title:  looked at the others in fearful expectation of hearing the sound repeated.
Title:  At length, the blanket was slowly raised, and the scout stood in the
Title:  aperture with a countenance whose firmness evidently began to give way
Title:  before a mystery that seemed to threaten some danger, against which all his
Title:  cunning and experience might prove of no avail.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 In vulgar parlance the condiments of a repast are called by the American a
Title:  relish, substituting the thing for its effect. These provincial terms are
Title:  frequently put in the mouths of the speakers, according to their several
Title:  conditions in life. Most of them are of local use, and others quite peculiar
Title:  to the particular class of men to which the character belongs. In the
Title:  present instance, the scout uses the word with immediate reference to the
Title:  salt, with which his own party was so fortunate as to be provided. 2 Glenn's
Title:  Falls are on the Hudson, some forty or fifty miles above the head of tide,
Title:  or that place where the river becomes navigable for sloops. The description
Title:  of this picturesque and remakable little cataract, as given by the scout, is
Title:  sufficiently correct, though the application of the water to uses of
Title:  civilized life has materially injured its beauties. The rocky island and the
Title:  two caverns are known to every traveler, since the former sustains the pier
Title:  of a bridge, which is now thrown across the river, immediately above the
Title:  fall. In explanation of the taste of Hawkeye, it should be remembered that
Title:  men always prize that most which is least enjoyed. Thus, in a new country,
Title:  the woods and other objects, which in an old country would be maintained at
Title:  great cost, are got rid of, simply with a view of improving as it is called.

Title:  
Title:  Chapter 7
Title:  
Title:       They do not sleep,
Title:       On yonder cliffs, a grizzly band,
Title:       I see them sit.
Title:  
Title:                                                                    GRAY
Title:  
Title:  'Twould be neglecting a warning that is given for our good to lie hid any
Title:  longer, said Hawkeye when such sounds are raised in the forest. These gentle
Title:  ones may keep close, but the Mohicans and I will watch upon the rock, where
Title:  I suppose a major of the Sixtieth would wish to keep us company.
Title:  
Title:  Is, then, our danger so pressing? asked Cora.
Title:  
Title:  He who makes strange sounds, and gives them out for man's information, alone
Title:  knows our danger. I should think myself wicked, unto rebellion against His
Title:  will, was I to burrow with such warnings in the air! Even the weak soul who
Title:  passes his days in singing is stirred by the cry, and, as he says, is ready
Title:  to go forth to the battle. If 'twere only a battle, it would be a thing
Title:  understood by us all, and easily managed; but I have heard that when such
Title:  shrieks are atween heaven and 'arth, it betokens another sort of warfare!
Title:  
Title:  If all our reasons for fear, my friend, are confined to such as proceed from
Title:  supernatural causes, we have but little occasion to be alarmed, continued
Title:  the undisturbed Cora, are you certain that our enemies have not invented
Title:  some new and ingenious method to strike us with terror, that their conquest
Title:  may become more easy?
Title:  
Title:  Lady, returned the scout, solemnly, I have listened to all the sounds of the
Title:  woods for thirty years, as a man will listen whose life and death depend on
Title:  the quickness of his ears. There is no whine of the panther, no whistle of
Title:  the catbird, nor any invention of the devilish Mingoes, that can cheat me! I
Title:  have heard the forest moan like mortal men in their affliction; often, and
Title:  again, have I listened to the wind playing its music in the branches of the
Title:  girdled trees; and I have heard the lightning cracking in the air like the
Title:  snapping of blazing brush as it spitted forth sparks and forked flames; but
Title:  never have I thought that I heard more than the pleasure of him who sported
Title:  with the things of his hand. But neither the Mohicans, nor I, who am a white
Title:  man without a cross, can explain the cry just heard. We, therefore, believe
Title:  it a sign given for our good.
Title:  
Title:  It is extraordinary! said Heyward, taking his pistols from the place where
Title:  he had laid them on entering; be it a sign of peach or a signal of war, it
Title:  must be looked to. Lead the way, my friend; I follow.
Title:  
Title:  On issuing from their place of confinement, the whole party instantly
Title:  experienced a grateful renovation of spirits, by exchanging the pent air of
Title:  the hiding-place for the cool and invigorating atmosphere which played
Title:  around the whirlpools and pitches of the cataract. A heavy evening breeze
Title:  swept along the surface of the river, and seemed to drive the roar of the
Title:  falls into the recesses of their own cavern, whence it issued heavily and
Title:  constant, like thunder rumbling beyond the distant hills. The moon had
Title:  risen, and its light was already glancing here and there on the waters above
Title:  them; but the extremity of the rock where they stood still lay in shadow.
Title:  With the exception of the sounds produced by the rushing waters, and an
Title:  occasional breathing of the air, as it murmured past them in fitful
Title:  currents, the scene was as still as night and solitude could make it. In
Title:  vain were the eyes of each individual bent along the opposite shores, in
Title:  quest of some signs of life, that might explain the nature of the
Title:  interruption they had heard. Their anxious and eager looks were baffled by
Title:  the deceptive light, or rested only on naked rocks, and straight and
Title:  immovable trees.
Title:  
Title:  Here is nothing to be seen but the gloom and quiet of a lovely evening,
Title:  whispered Duncan; how much should we prize such a scene, and all this
Title:  breathing solitude, at any other moment, Cora! Fancy yourselves in security,
Title:  and what now, perhaps, increases your terror, may be made conducive to
Title:  enjoyment - -
Title:  
Title:  Listen! interrupted Alice.
Title:  
Title:  The caution was unnecessary. One more the same sound arose, as if from the
Title:  bed of the river, and having broken out of the narrow bounds of the cliffs,
Title:  was heard undulating through the forest, in distant and dying cadences.
Title:  
Title:  Can any here give a name to such a cry? demanded Hawkeye, when the last echo
Title:  was lost in the woods; if so, let him speak; for myself, I judge it not to
Title:  belong to 'arth!
Title:  
Title:  Here, then, is one who can undeceive you, said Duncan; I know the sound full
