Title:  frightful yell, which declared the extent of their disappointment. Some ran
Title:  furiously to the water's edge, beating the air with frantic gestures, while
Title:  others spat upon the element, to resent the supposed treason it had
Title:  committed against their acknowledged rights as conquerors. A few, and they
Title:  not the least powerful and terrific of the band, threw lowering looks, in
Title:  which the fiercest passion was only tempered by habitual self-command, at
Title:  those captives who still remained in their power, while one or two even gave
Title:  vent to their malignant feelings by the most menacing gestures, against
Title:  which neither the sex nor the beauty of the sisters was any protection. The
Title:  young soldier made a desperate but fruitless effort to spring to the side of
Title:  Alice, when he saw the dark hand of a savage twisted in the rich tresses
Title:  which were flowing in volumes over her shoulders, while a knife was passed
Title:  around the head from which they fell, as if to denote the horrid manner in
Title:  which it was about to be robbed of its beautiful ornament. But his hands
Title:  were bound; and at the first movement he made, he felt the grasp of the
Title:  powerful Indian who directed the band, pressing his shoulder like a vise.
Title:  Immediately conscious how unavailing any struggle against such an
Title:  overwhelming force must prove, he submitted to his fate, encouraging his
Title:  gentle companions by a few low and tender assurances, that the natives
Title:  seldom failed to threaten more than they performed.
Title:  
Title:  But while Duncan resorted to these words of consolation to quiet the
Title:  apprehensions of the sisters, he was not so weak as to deceive himself. He
Title:  well knew that the authority of an Indian chief was so little conventional,
Title:  that it was oftener maintained by physical superiority than by any moral
Title:  supremacy he might possess. The danger was, therefore, magnified exactly in
Title:  proportion to the number of the savage spirits by which they were
Title:  surrounded. The most positive mandate from him who seemed the acknowledged
Title:  leader, was liable to be violated at each moment by any rash hand that might
Title:  choose to sacrifice a victim to the manes of some dead friend or relative.
Title:  While, therefore, he sustained an outward appearance of calmness and
Title:  fortitude, his heart leaped into his throat, whenever any of their fierce
Title:  captors drew nearer than common to the helpless sisters, or fastened one of
Title:  their sullen, wandering looks on those fragile forms which were so little
Title:  able to resist the slightest assault.
Title:  
Title:  His apprehensions were, however, greatly relieved, when he saw that the
Title:  leader had summoned his warriors to himself in counsel. Their deliberations
Title:  were short, and it would seem, by the silence of most of the party, the
Title:  decision unanimous. By the frequency with which the few speakers pointed in
Title:  the direction of the encampment of Webb, it was apparent they dreaded the
Title:  approach of danger from that quarter. This consideration probably hastened
Title:  their determination, and quickened the subsequent movements.
Title:  
Title:  During his short conference, Heyward, finding a respite from his gravest
Title:  fears, had leisure to admire the cautious manner in which the Hurons had
Title:  made their approaches, even after hostilities had ceased.
Title:  
Title:  It has already been stated that the upper half of the island was a naked
Title:  rock, and destitute of any other defenses than a few scattered logs of
Title:  driftwood. They had selected this point to make their descent, having borne
Title:  the canoe through the wood around the cataract for that purpose. Placing
Title:  their arms in the little vessel a dozen men clinging to its sides had
Title:  trusted themselves to the direction of the canoe, which was controlled by
Title:  two of the most skillful warriors, in attitudes that enabled them to command
Title:  a view of the dangerous passage. Favored by this arrangement, they touched
Title:  the head of the island at that point which had proved so fatal to their
Title:  first adventurers, but with the advantages of superior numbers, and the
Title:  possession of firearms. That such had been the manner of their descent was
Title:  rendered quite apparent to Duncan; for they now bore the light bark from the
Title:  upper end of the rock, and placed it in the water, near the mouth of the
Title:  outer cavern. As soon as this change was made, the leader made signs to the
Title:  prisoners to descend and enter.
Title:  
Title:  As resistance was impossible, and remonstrance useless, Heyward set the
Title:  example of submission, by leading the way into the canoe, where he was soon
Title:  seated with the sisters and the still wondering David. Notwithstanding the
Title:  Hurons were necessarily ignorant of the little channels among the eddies and
Title:  rapids of the stream, they knew the common signs of such a navigation too
Title:  well to commit any material blunder. When the pilot chosen for the task of
Title:  guiding the canoe had taken his station, the whole band plunged again into
Title:  the river, the vessel glided down the current, and in a few moments the
Title:  captives found themselves on the south bank of the stream, nearly opposite
Title:  to the point where they had struck it the preceding evening.
Title:  
Title:  Here was held another short but earnest consultation, during which the
Title:  horses, to whose panic their owners ascribed their heaviest misfortune, were
Title:  led from the cover of the woods, and brought to the sheltered spot. The band
Title:  now divided. The great chief, so often mentioned, mounting the charger of
Title:  Heyward, led the way directly across the river, followed by most of his
Title:  people, and disappeared in the woods, leaving the prisoners in charge of six
Title:  savages, at whose head was Le Renard Subtil. Duncan witnessed all their
Title:  movements with renewed uneasiness.
Title:  
Title:  He had been fond of believing, from the uncommon forbearance of the savages,
Title:  that he was reserved as a prisoner to be delivered to Montcalm. As the
Title:  thoughts of those who are in misery seldom slumber, and the invention is
Title:  never more lively than when it is stimulated by hope, however feeble and
Title:  remote, he had even imagined that the parental feelings of Munro were to be
Title:  made instrumental in seducing him from his duty to the king. For though the
Title:  French commander bore a high character for courage and enterprise, he was
Title:  also thought to be expert in those political practises which do not always
Title:  respect the nicer obligations of morality, and which so generally disgraced
Title:  the European diplomacy of that period.
Title:  
Title:  All those busy and ingenious speculations were now annihilated by the
Title:  conduct of his captors. That portion of the band who had followed the huge
Title:  warrior took the route toward the foot of the Horican, and no other
Title:  expectation was left for himself and companions, than that they were to be
Title:  retained as hopeless captives by their savage conquerors. Anxious to know
Title:  the worst, and willing, in such an emergency, to try the potency of gold he
Title:  overcame his reluctance to speak to Magua. Addressing himself to his former
Title:  guide, who had now assumed the authority and manner of one who was to direct
Title:  the future movements of the party, he said, in tones as friendly and
Title:  confiding as he could assume:
Title:  
Title:  I would speak to Magua, what is fit only for so great a chief to hear.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian turned his eyes on the young soldier scornfully, as he answered:
Title:  
Title:  Speak; trees have no ears.
Title:  
Title:  But the red Hurons are not deaf; and counsel that is fit for the great men
Title:  of a nation would make the young warriors drunk. If Magua will not listen,
Title:  the officer of the king knows how to be silent.
Title:  
Title:  The savage spoke carelessly to his comrades, who were busied, after their
Title:  awkward manner, in preparing the horses for the reception of the sisters,
Title:  and moved a little to one side, whither by a cautious gesture he induced
Title:  Heyward to follow.
Title:  
Title:  Now, speak, he said; if the words are such as Magua should hear.
Title:  
Title:  Le Renard Subtil has proved himself worthy of the honorable name given to
Title:  him by his Canada fathers, commenced Heyward; I see his wisdom, and all that
Title:  he has done for us, and shall remember it when the hour to reward him
Title:  arrives. Yes! Renard has proved that he is not only a great chief in
Title:  council, but one who knows how to deceive his enemies!
Title:  
Title:  What has Renard done? coldly demanded the Indian.
Title:  
Title:  What! has he not seen that the woods were filled with outlying parties of
Title:  the enemies, and that the serpent could not steal through them without being
Title:  seen? Then, did he not lose his path to blind the eyes of the Hurons? Did he
Title:  not pretend to go back to his tribe, who had treated him ill, and driven him
Title:  from their wigwams like a dog? And when he saw what he wished to do, did we
Title:  not aid him, by making a false face, that the Hurons might think the white
Title:  man believed that his friend was his enemy? Is not all this true? And when
Title:  Le Subtil had shut the eyes and stopped the ears of his nation by his
Title:  wisdom, did they not forget that they had once done him wrong, and forced
Title:  him to flee to the Mohawks? And did they not leave him on the south side of
Title:  the river, with their prisoners, while they have gone foolishly on the
Title:  north? Does not Renard mean to turn like a fox on his footsteps, and to
Title:  carry to the rich and gray-headed Scotchman his daughters? Yes, Magua, I see
Title:  it all, and I have already been thinking how so much wisdom and honesty
Title:  should be repaid. First, the chief of William Henry will give as a great
Title:  chief should for such a service. The medal1 of Magua will no longer be on
Title:  tin, but of beaten gold; his horn will run over with powder; dollars will be
Title:  as plenty in his pouch as pebbles on the shore of Horican; and the deer will
Title:  lick his hand, for they will know it to be vain to fly from the rifle he
Title:  will carry! As for myself, I know not how to exceed the gratitude of the
Title:  Scotchman, but I - yes, I will - -
Title:  
Title:  What will the young chief, who comes from toward the sun, give? demanded the
Title:  Huron, observing that Heyward hesitated in his desire to end the enumeration
Title:  of benefits with that which might form the climax of an Indian's wishes.
Title:  
Title:  He will make the fire-water from the islands in the salt lake flow before
Title:  the wigwam of Magua, until the heart of the Indian shall be lighter than the
Title:  feathers of the humming-bird, and his breath sweeter than the wild
Title:  honeysuckle.
Title:  
Title:  Le Renard had listened gravely as Heyward slowly proceeded in this subtle
Title:  speech. When the young man mentioned the artifice he supposed the Indian to
Title:  have practised on his own nation, the countenance of the listener was veiled
Title:  in an expression of cautious gravity. At the allusion to the injury which
Title:  Duncan affected to believe had driven the Huron from his native tribe, a
Title:  gleam of such ungovernable ferocity flashed from the other's eyes, as
Title:  induced the adventurous speaker to believe he had struck the proper chord.
Title:  And by the time he reached the part where he so artfully blended the thirst
Title:  of vengeance with the desire of gain, he had, at least, obtained a command
Title:  of the deepest attention of the savage. The question put by Le Renard had
Title:  been calm, and with all the dignity of an Indian; but it was quite apparent,
Title:  by the thoughtful expression of the listener's countenance, that the answer
Title:  was most cunningly devised. The Huron mused a few moments, and then laying
Title:  his hand on the rude bandages of his wounded shoulder, he said, with some
Title:  energy:
Title:  
Title:  Do friends make such marks?
Title:  
Title:  Would La Longue Carbine cut one so slight on an enemy?
Title:  
Title:  Do the Delawares crawl upon those they love like snakes, twisting themselves
Title:  to strike?
Title:  
Title:  Would Le Gros Serpent have been heard by the ears of one he wished to be
Title:  deaf?
Title:  
Title:  Does the white chief burn his powder in the faces of his brothers?
Title:  
Title:  Does he ever miss his aim, when seriously bent to kill? returned Duncan,
Title:  smiling with well acted sincerity.
Title:  
Title:  Another long and deliberate pause succeeded these sententious questions and
Title:  ready replies. Duncan saw that the Indian hesitated. In order to complete
Title:  his victory, he was in the act of recommencing the enumeration of the
Title:  rewards, when Magua made an expressive gesture and said:
Title:  
Title:  Enough; Le Renard is a wise chief, and what he does will be seen. Go, and
Title:  keep the mouth shut. When Magua speaks, it will be the time to answer.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, perceiving that the eyes of his companion were warily fastened on
Title:  the rest of the band, fell back immediately, in order to avoid the
Title:  appearance of any suspicious confederacy with their leader. Magua approached
Title:  the horses, and affected to be well pleased with the diligence and ingenuity
Title:  of his comrades. He then signed to Heyward to assist the sisters into the
Title:  saddles, for he seldom deigned to use the English tongue, unless urged by
Title:  some motive of more than usual moment.
Title:  
Title:  There was no longer any plausible pretext for delay; and Duncan was obliged,
Title:  however reluctantly, to comply. As he performed this office, he whispered
Title:  his reviving hopes in the ears of the trembling females, who, through dread
Title:  of encountering the savage countenances of their captors, seldom raised
Title:  their eyes from the ground. The mare of David had been taken with the
Title:  followers of the large chief; in consequence, its owner, as well as Duncan,
Title:  was compelled to journey on foot. The latter did not, however, so much
Title:  regret this circumstance, as it might enable him to retard the speed of the
Title:  party; for he still turned his longing looks in the direction of Fort
Title:  Edward, in the vain expectation of catching some sound from that quarter of
Title:  the forest, which might denote the approach of succor. When all were
Title:  prepared, Magua made the signal to proceed, advancing in front to lead the
Title:  party in person. Next followed David, who was gradually coming to a true
Title:  sense of his condition, as the effects of the wound became less and less
Title:  apparent. The sisters rode in his rear, with Heyward at their side, while
Title:  the Indians flanked the party, and brought up the close of the march, with a
Title:  caution that seemed never to tire.
Title:  
Title:  In this manner they proceeded in uninterrupted silence, except when Heyward
Title:  addressed some solitary word of comfort to the females, or David gave vent
Title:  to the moanings of his spirit, in piteous exclamations, which he intended
Title:  should express the humility of resignation. Their direction lay toward the
Title:  south, and in a course nearly opposite to the road to William Henry.
Title:  Notwithstanding this apparent adherence in Magua to the original
Title:  determination of his conquerors, Hyeward could not believe his tempting bait
Title:  was so soon forgotten; and he knew the windings of an Indian's path too well
Title:  to suppose that its apparent course led directly to its object, when
Title:  artifice was at all necessary. Mile after mile was, however, passed through
Title:  the boundless woods, in this painful manner, without any prospect of a
Title:  termination to their journey. Heyward watched the sun, as he darted his
Title:  meridian rays through the branches of the trees, and pined for the moment
Title:  when the policy of Magua should change their route to one more favorable to
Title:  his hopes. Sometimes he fancied the wary savage, despairing of passing the
Title:  army of Montcalm in safety, was holding his way toward a well-known border
Title:  settlement, where a distinguished officer of the crown, and a favored friend
Title:  of the Six Nations, held his large possessions, as well as his usual
Title:  residence. To be delivered into the hands of Sir William Johnson was far
Title:  preferable to being led into the wilds of Canada; but in order to effect
Title:  even the former, it would be necessary to traverse the forest for many weary
Title:  leagues, each step of which was carrying him further from the scene of the
Title:  war, and, consequently, from the post, not only of honor, but of duty.
Title:  
Title:  Cora alone remembered the parting injunctions of the scout, and whenever an
Title:  opportunity offered, she stretched forth her arm to bend aside the twigs
Title:  that met her hands. But the vigilance of the Indians rendered this act of
Title:  precaution both difficult and dangerous. She was often defeated in her
Title:  purpose, by encountering their watchful eyes, when it became necessary to
Title:  feign an alarm she did not feel, and occupy the limb by some gesture of
Title:  feminine apprehension. Once, and once only, was she completely successful;
Title:  when she broke down the bough of a large sumach, and by a sudden thought,
Title:  let her glove fall at the same instant. This sign, intended for those that
Title:  might follow, was observed by one of her conductors, who restored the glove,
Title:  broke the remaining branches of the bush in such a manner that it appeared
Title:  to proceed from the struggling of some beast in its branches, and then laid
Title:  his hand on his tomahawk, with a look so significant, that it put an
Title:  effectual end to these stolen memorials of their passage.
Title:  
Title:  As there were horses, to leave the prints of their footsteps, in both bands
Title:  of the Indians, this interruption cut off any probable hopes of assistance
Title:  being conveyed through the means of their trail.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward would have ventured a remonstrance had there been anything
Title:  encouraging in the gloomy reserve of Magua. But the savage, during all this
Title:  time, seldom turned to look at his followers, and never spoke. With the sun
Title:  for his only guide, or aided by such blind marks as are only known to the
Title:  sagacity of a native, he held his way along the barrens of pine, through
Title:  occasional little fertile vales, across brooks and rivulets, and over
Title:  undulating hills, with the accuracy of instinct, and nearly with the
Title:  directness of a bird. He never seemed to hesitate. Whether the path was
Title:  hardly distinguishable, whether it disappeared, or whether it lay beaten and
Title:  plain before him, made no sensible difference in his speed or certainty. It
Title:  seemed as if fatigue could not affect him. Whenever the eyes of the wearied
Title:  travelers rose from the decayed leaves over which they trod, his dark form
Title:  was to be seen glancing among the stems of the trees in front, his head
Title:  immovably fastened in a forward position, with the light plume on his crest
Title:  fluttering in a current of air, made solely by the swiftness of his own
Title:  motion.
Title:  
Title:  But all this diligence and speed were not without an object. After crossing
Title:  a low vale, through which a gushing brook meandered, he suddenly ascended a
Title:  hill, so steep and difficult of ascent, that the sisters were compelled to
Title:  alight in order to follow. When the summit was gained, they found themselves
Title:  on a level spot, but thinly covered with trees, under one of which Magua had
Title:  thrown his dark form, as if willing and ready to seek that rest which was so
Title:  much needed by the whole party.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 It has long been a practice with the whites to conciliate the important
Title:  men of the Indians by presenting medals, which are worn in the place of
Title:  their own rude ornaments. Those given by the English generally bear the
Title:  impression of the reigning king, and those given by the Americans that of
Title:  the president.
Title:  
Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 11
Title:  
Title:       Shylock: Cursed be my tribe If I forgive him.
Title:  
Title:                                                      MERCHANT OF VENICE
Title:  
Title:  The Indian had selected for this desirable purpose one of those steep,
Title:  pyramidal hills, which bear a strong resemblance to artificial mounds, and
Title:  which so frequently occur in the valleys of America. The one in question was
Title:  high and precipitous; its top flattened, as usual; but with one of its sides
Title:  more than oridinarily irregular. It possessed no other apparent advantage
Title:  for a resting place, than in its elevation and form, which might render
Title:  defense easy, and surprise nearly impossible. As Heyward, however, no longer
Title:  expected that rescue which time and distance now rendered so improbable, he
Title:  regarded these little peculiarities with an eye devoid of interest, devoting
Title:  himself entirely to the comfort and condolence of his feebler companions.
Title:  The Narragansetts were suffered to browse on the branches of the trees and
Title:  shrubs that were thinly scattered over the summit of the hill, while the
Title:  remains of their provisions were spread under the shade of a beech, that
Title:  stretched its horizontal limbs like a canopy above them.
Title:  
Title:  Notwithstanding the swiftness of their flight, one of the Indians had found
Title:  an opportunity to strike a straggling fawn with an arrow, and had borne the
Title:  more preferable fragments of the victim, patiently on his shoulders, to the
Title:  stopping place. Without any aid from the science of cookery, he was
Title:  immediately employed, in common with his fellows, in gorging himself with
Title:  this digestible sustenance. Magua alone sat apart, without participating in
Title:  the revolting meal, and apparently buried in the deepest thought.
Title:  
Title:  This abstinence, so remarkable in an Indian, when he possessed the means of
Title:  satisfying hunger, at length attracted the notice of Heyward. The young man
Title:  willingly believed that the Huron deliberated on the most eligible manner of
Title:  eluding the vigilance of his associates. With a view to assist his plans by
Title:  any suggestion of his own, and to strengthen the temptation, he left the
Title:  beech, and straggled, as if without an object, to the spot where Le Renard
Title:  was seated.
Title:  
Title:  Has not Magua kept the sun in his face long enough to escape all danger from
Title:  the Canadians? he asked, as though no longer doubtful of the good
Title:  intelligence established between them; and will not the chief of William
Title:  Henry be better pleased to see his daughters before another night may have
Title:  hardened his heart to their loss, to make him less liberal in his reward?
Title:  
Title:  Do the pale faces love their children less in the morning than at night?
Title:  asked the Indian, coldly.
Title:  
Title:  By no means, returned Heyward, anxious to recall his error, if he had made
Title:  one; the white man may, and does often, forget the burial place of his
Title:  fathers; he sometimes ceases to remember those he should love, and has
Title:  promised to cherish; but the affection of a parent for his child is never
Title:  permitted to die.
Title:  
Title:  And is the heart of the white-headed chief soft, and will he think of the
Title:  babes that his squaws have given him? He is hard on his warriors and his
Title:  eyes are made of stone?
Title:  
Title:  He is severe to the idle and wicked, but to the sober and deserving he is a
Title:  leader, both just and humane. I have known many fond and tender parents, but
Title:  never have I seen a man whose heart was softer toward his child. You have
Title:  seen the gray-head in front of his warriors, Magua; but I have seen his eyes
Title:  swimming in water, when he spoke of those children who are now in your
Title:  power!
Title:  
Title:  Heyward paused, for he knew not how to construe the remarkable expression
Title:  that gleamed across the swarthy features of the attentive Indian. At first
Title:  it seemed as if the remembrance of the promised reward grew vivid in his
Title:  mind, while he listened to the sources of parental feeling which were to
Title:  assure its possession; but, as Duncan proceeded, the expression of joy
Title:  became so fiercely malignant that it was impossible not to apprehend it
Title:  proceeded from some passion more sinister than avarice.
Title:  
Title:  Go, said the Huron, suppressing the alarming exhibition in an instant, in a
Title:  death-like calmness of countenance; go to the dark-haired daughter, and say,
Title:  Magua waits to speak. The father will remember what the child promises.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, who interpreted this speech to express a wish for some additional
Title:  pledge that the promised gifts should not be withheld, slowly and
Title:  reluctantly repaired to the place where the sisters were now resting from
Title:  their fatigue, to communicate its purport to Cora.
Title:  
Title:  You understand the nature of an Indian's wishes, he concluded, as he led her
Title:  toward the place where she was expected, and must be prodigal of your offers
Title:  of powder and blankets. Ardent spirits are, however, the most prized by such
Title:  as he; nor would it be amiss to add some boon from your own hand, with that
Title:  grace you so well know how to practise. Remember, Cora, that on your
Title:  presence of mind and ingenuity, even your life, as well as that of Alice,
Title:  may in some measure depend.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, and yours!
Title:  
Title:  Mine is of little moment; it is already sold to my king, and is a prize to
Title:  be seized by any enemy who may possess the power. I have no father to expect
Title:  me, and but few friends to lament a fate which I have courted with the
Title:  insatiable longings of youth after distinction. But hush! we approach the
Title:  Indian. Magua, the lady with whom you wish to speak, is here.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian rose slowly from his seat, and stood for near a minute silent and
Title:  motionless. He then signed with his hand for Heyward to retire, saying,
Title:  coldly:
Title:  
Title:  When the Huron talks to the women, his tribe shut their ears.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, still lingering, as if refusing to comply, Coras said, with a calm
Title:  smile:
Title:  
Title:  You hear, Heyward, and delicacy at least should urge you to retire. Go to
Title:  Alice, and comfort her with our reviving prospects.
Title:  
Title:  She waited until he had departed, and then turning to the native, with the
Title:  dignity of her sex in her voice and manner, she added: What would Le Renard
Title:  say to the daughter of Munro?
Title:  
Title:  Listen, said the Indian, laying his hand firmly upon her arm, as if willing
Title:  to draw her utmost attention to his words; a movement that Cora as firmly
Title:  but quietly repulsed, by extricating the limb from his grasp: Magua was born
Title:  a chief and a warrior among the red Hurons of the lakes; he saw the suns of
Title:  twenty summers make the snows of twenty winters run off in the streams
Title:  before he saw a pale face; and he was happy! Then his Canada fathers came
Title:  into the woods, and taught him to drink the fire-water, and he became a
Title:  rascal. The Hurons drove him from the graves of his fathers, as they would
Title:  chase the hunted buffalo. He ran down the shores of the lakes, and followed
Title:  their outlet to the city of cannon. There he hunted and fished, till the
Title:  people chased him again through the woods into the arms of his enemies. The
Title:  chief, who was born a Huron, was at last a warrior among the Mohawks!
Title:  
Title:  Something like this I had heard before, said Cora, observing that he paused
Title:  to suppress those passions which began to burn with too bright a flame, as
Title:  he recalled the recollection of his supposed injuries.
Title:  
Title:  Was it the fault of Le Renard that his head was not made of rock? Who gave
Title:  him the fire-water? who made him a villain? 'Twas the pale faces, the people
Title:  of your own color.
Title:  
Title:  And am I answerable that thoughtless and unprincipled men exist, whose
Title:  shades of countenance may resemble mine? Cora calmly demanded of the excited
Title:  savage.
Title:  
Title:  No; Magua is a man, and not a fool; such as you never open their lips to the
Title:  burning stream: the Great Spirit has given you wisdom!
Title:  
Title:  What, then, have I do to, or say, in the matter of your misfortunes, not to
Title:  say of your errors?
Title:  
Title:  Listen, repeated the Indian, resuming his earnest attitude; when his English
Title:  and French fathers dug up the hatchet, Le Renard struck the war-post of the
Title:  Mohawks, and went out against his own nation. The pale faces have driven the
Title:  red-skins from their hunting grounds, and now when they fight, a white man
Title:  leads the way. The old chief at Horican, your father, was the great captain
Title:  of our war-party. He said to the Mohawks do this, and do that, and he was
Title:  minded. He made a law, that if an Indian swallowed the fire-water, and came
Title:  into the cloth wigwams of his warriors, it should not be forgotten. Magua
Title:  foolishly opened his mouth, and the hot liquor led him into the cabin of
Title:  Munro. What did the gray-head? let his daughter say.
Title:  
Title:  He forgot not his words, and did justice, by punishing the offender, said
Title:  the undaunted daughter.
Title:  
Title:  Justice! repeated the Indian, casting an oblique glance of the most
Title:  ferocious expression at her unyielding countenance; is it justice to make
Title:  evil and then punish for it? Magua was not himself; it was the fire-water
Title:  that spoke and acted for him! but Munro did believe it. The Huron chief was
Title:  tied up before all the pale-faced warriors, and whipped like a dog.
Title:  
Title:  Cora remained silent, for she knew not how to palliate this imprudent
Title:  severity on the part of her father in a manner to suit the comprehension of
Title:  an Indian.
Title:  
Title:  See! continued Magua, tearing aside the slight calico that very imperfectly
Title:  concealed his painted breast; here are scars given by knives and bullets -
Title:  of these a warrior may boast before his nation; but the gray-head has left
Title:  marks on the back of the Huron chief that he must hide like a squaw, under
Title:  this painted cloth of the whites.
Title:  
Title:  I had thought, resumed Cora, that an Indian warrior was patient, and that
Title:  his spirit felt not and knew not the pain his body suffered.
Title:  
Title:  When the Chippewas tied Magua to the stake, and cut this gash, said the
Title:  other, laying his finger on a deep scar, the Huron laughed in their faces,
Title:  and told them, Women struck so light! His spirit was then in the clouds! But
Title:  when he felt the blows of Munro, his spirit lay under the birch. The spirit
Title:  of a Huron is never drunk; it remembers forever!
Title:  
Title:  But it may be appeased. If my father has done you this injustice, show him
Title:  how an Indian can forgive an injury, and take back his daughters. You have
Title:  heard from Major Heyward - -
Title:  
Title:  Magua shook his head, forbidding the repetition of offers he so much
Title:  despised.
Title:  
Title:  What would you have? continued Cora, after a most painful pause, while the
Title:  conviction forced itself on her mind that the too sanguine and generous
Title:  Duncan had been cruelly deceived by the cunning of the savage.
Title:  
Title:  What a Huron loves - good for good; bad for bad!
Title:  
Title:  You would, then, revenge the injury inflicted by Munro on his helpless
Title:  daughters. Would it not be more like a man to go before his face, and take
Title:  the satisfaction of a warrior?
Title:  
Title:  The arms of the pale faces are long, and their knives sharp! returned the
Title:  savage, with a malignant laugh: why should Le Renard go among the muskets of
Title:  his warriors, when he holds the spirit of the gray-head in his hand?
Title:  
Title:  Name your intention, Magua, said Cora, struggling with herself to speak with
Title:  steady calmness. Is it to lead us prisoners to the woods, or do you
Title:  contemplate even some greater evil? Is there no reward, no means of
Title:  palliating the injury, and of softening your heart? At least, release my
Title:  gentle sister, and pour out all your malice on me. Purchase wealth by her
Title:  safety and satisfy your revenge with a single victim. The loss of both his
Title:  daughters might bring the aged man to his grave, and where would then be the
Title:  satisfaction of Le Renard?
Title:  
Title:  Listen, said the Indian again. The light eyes can go back to the Horican,
Title:  and tell the old chief what has been done, if the dark-haired woman will
Title:  swear by the Great Spirit of her fathers to tell no lie.
Title:  
Title:  What must I promise? demanded Cora, still maintaining a secret ascendency
Title:  over the fierce native by the collected and feminine dignity of her
Title:  presence.
Title:  
Title:  When Magua left his people his wife was given to another chief; he has now
Title:  made friends with the Hurons, and will go back to the graves of his tribe,
Title:  on the shores of the great lake. Let the daughter of the English chief
Title:  follow, and live in his wigwam forever.
Title:  
Title:  However revolting a proposal of such a character might prove to Cora, she
Title:  retained, notwithstanding her powerful disgust, sufficient self-command to
Title:  reply, without betraying the weakness.
Title:  
Title:  And what pleasure would Magua find in sharing his cabin with a wife he did
Title:  not love; one who would be of a nation and color different from his own? It
Title:  would be better to take the gold of Munro, and buy the heart of some Huron
Title:  maid with his gifts.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian made no reply for near a minute, but bent his fierce looks on the
Title:  countenance of Cora, in such wavering glances, that her eyes sank with
Title:  shame, under an impression that for the first time they had encountered an
Title:  expression that no chaste female might endure. While she was shrinking
Title:  within herself, in dread of having her ears wounded by some proposal still
Title:  more shocking than the last, the voice of Magua answered, in its tones of
Title:  deepest malignancy:
Title:  
Title:  When the blows scorched the back of the Huron, he would know where to find a
Title:  woman to feel the smart. The daughter of Munro would draw his water, hoe his
Title:  corn, and cook his venison. The body of the gray-head would sleep among his
Title:  cannon, but his heart would lie within reach of the knife of Le Subtil.
Title:  
Title:  Monster! well dost thou deserve thy treacherous name, cried Cora, in an
Title:  ungovernable burst of filial indignation. None but a fiend could meditate
Title:  such a vengeance. But thou overratest thy power! You shall find it is, in
Title:  truth, the heart of Munro you hold, and that it will defy your utmost
Title:  malice!
Title:  
Title:  The Indian answered this bold defiance by a ghastly smile, that showed an
Title:  unaltered purpose, while he motioned her away, as if to close the conference
Title:  forever. Cora, already regretting her precipitation, was obliged to comply,
Title:  for Magua instantly left the spot, and approached his gluttonous comrades.
Title:  Heyward flew to the side of the agitated female, and demanded the result of
Title:  a dialogue that he had watched at a distance with so much interest. But,
Title:  unwilling to alarm the fears of Alice, she evaded a direct reply, betraying
Title:  only by her anxious looks fastened on the slightest movements of her
Title:  captors. To the reiterated and earnest questions of her sister concerning
Title:  their probable destination, she made no other answer than by pointing toward
Title:  the dark group, with an agitation she could not control, and murmuring as
Title:  she folded Alice to her bosom.
Title:  
Title:  There, there; read our fortunes in their faces; we shall see; we shall see!
Title:  
Title:  The action, and the choked utterance of Cora, spoke more impressively than
Title:  any words, and quickly drew the attention of her companions on that spot
Title:  where her own was riveted with an intenseness that nothing but the
Title:  importance of the stake could create.
Title:  
Title:  When Magua reached the cluster of lolling savages, who, gorged with their
Title:  disgusting meal, lay stretched on the earth in brutal indulgence, he
Title:  commenced speaking with the dignity of an Indian chief. The first syllables
Title:  he uttered had the effect to cause his listeners to raise themselves in
Title:  attitudes of respectful attention. As the Huron used his native language,
Title:  the prisoners, notwithstanding the caution of the natives had kept them
Title:  within the swing of their tomahawks, could only conjecture the substance of
Title:  his harangue from the nature of those significant gestures with which an
Title:  Indian always illustrates his eloquence.
Title:  
Title:  At first, the language, as well as the action of Magua, appeared calm and
Title:  deliberative. When he had succeeded in sufficiently awakening the attention
Title:  of his comrades, Heyward fancied, by his pointing so frequently toward the
Title:  direction of the great lakes, that he spoke of the land of their fathers,
Title:  and of their distant tribe. Frequent indications of applause escaped the
Title:  listeners, who, as they uttered the expressive Hugh! looked at each other in
Title:  commendation of the speaker. Le Renard was too skillful to neglect his
Title:  advantage. He now spoke of the long and painful route by which they had left
Title:  those spacious grounds and happy villages, to come and battle against the
Title:  enemies of their Canadian fathers. He enumerated the warriors of the party;
Title:  their several merits; their frequent services to the nation; their wounds,
Title:  and the number of the scalps they had taken. Whenever he alluded to any
Title:  present (and the subtle Indian neglected none), the dark countenance of the
Title:  flattered individual gleamed with exultation, nor did he even hesitate to
Title:  assert the truth of the words, by gestures of applause and confirmation.
Title:  Then the voice of the speaker fell, and lost the loud, animated tones of
Title:  triumph with which he had enumerated their deeds of success and victory. He
Title:  described the cataract of Glenn's; the impregnable position of its rocky
Title:  island, with its caverns and its numerous rapids and whirlpools; he named
Title:  the name of La Longue Carabine, and paused until the forest beneath them had
Title:  sent up the last echo of a loud and long yell, with which the hated
Title:  appellation was received. He pointed toward the youthful military captive,
Title:  and described the death of a favorite warrior, who had been precipitated
Title:  into the deep ravine by his hand. He not only mentioned the fate of him who,
Title:  hanging between heaven and earth, had presented such a spectacle of horror
Title:  to the whole band, but he acted anew the terrors of his situation, his
Title:  resolution and his death, on the branches of a sapling; and, finally, he
Title:  rapidly recounted the manner in which each of their friends had fallen,
Title:  never failing to touch upon their courage, and their most acknowledged
Title:  virtues. When this recital of events was ended, his voice once more changed,
Title:  and became plaintive and even musical, in its low guttural sounds. He now
Title:  spoke of the wives and children of the slain; their destitution; their
Title:  misery, both physical and moral; their distance; and, at last, of their
Title:  unavenged wrongs. Then suddenly lifting his voice to a pitch of terrific
Title:  energy, he concluded by demanding:
Title:  
Title:  Are the Hurons dogs to bear this? Who shall say to the wife of Menowgua that
Title:  the fishes have his scalp, and that his nation have not taken revenge! Who
Title:  will dare meet the mother of Wassawattimie, that scornful woman, with his
Title:  hands clean! What shall be said to the old men when they ask us for scalps,
Title:  and we have not a hair from a white head to give them! The women will point
Title:  their fingers at us. There is a dark spot on the names of the Hurons, and it
Title:  must be hid in blood! His voice was no longer audible in the burst of rage
Title:  which now broke into the air, as if the wood, instead of containing so small
Title:  a band, was filled with the nation. During the foregoing address the
Title:  progress of the speaker was too plainly read by those most interested in his
Title:  success through the medium of the countenances of the men he addressed. They
Title:  had answered his melancholy and mourning by sympathy and sorrow; his
Title:  assertions, by gestures of confirmation; and his boasting, with the
Title:  exultation of savages. When he spoke of courage, their looks were firm and
Title:  responsive; when he alluded to their injuries, their eyes kindled with fury;
Title:  when he mentioned the taunts of the women, they dropped their heads in
Title:  shame; but when he pointed out their means of vengeance, he struck a chord
Title:  which never failed to thrill in the breast of an Indian. With the first
Title:  intimation that it was within their reach, the whole band sprang upon their
Title:  feet as one man; giving utterance to their rage in the most frantic cries,
Title:  they rushed upon their prisoners in a body with drawn knives and uplifted
Title:  tomahawks. Heyward threw himself between the sisters and the foremost, whom
Title:  he grappled with a desperate strength that for a moment checked his
Title:  violence. This unexpected resistance gave Magua time to interpose, and with
Title:  rapid enunciation and animated gesture, he drew the attention of the band
Title:  again to himself. In that language he knew so well how to assume, he
Title:  diverted his comrades from their instant purpose, and invited them to
Title:  prolong the misery of their victims. His proposal was received with
Title:  acclamations, and executed with the swiftness of thought.
Title:  
Title:  Two powerful warriors cast themselves on Heyward, while another was occupied
Title:  in securing the less active singing-master. Neither of the captives,
Title:  however, submitted without a desperate, though fruitless, struggle. Even
Title:  David hurled his assailant to the earth; nor was Heyward secured until the
Title:  victory over his companion enabled the Indians to direct their united force
Title:  to that object. He was then bound and fastened to the body of the sapling,
Title:  on whose branches Magua had acted the pantomime of the falling Huron. When
Title:  the young soldier regained his recollection, he had the painful certainty
Title:  before his eyes that a common fate was intended for the whole party. On his
Title:  right was Cora in a durance similar to his own, pale and agitated, but with
Title:  an eye whose steady look still read the proceedings of their enemies. On his
Title:  left, the withes which bound her to a pine, performed that office for Alice
Title:  which her trembling limbs refused, and alone kept her fragile form from
Title:  sinking. Her hands were clasped before her in prayer, but instead of looking
Title:  upward toward that power which alone could rescue them, her unconscious
Title:  looks wandered to the countenance of Duncan with infantile dependency. David
Title:  had contended, and the novelty of the circumstance held him silent, in
Title:  deliberation on the propriety of the unusual occurrence.
Title:  
Title:  The vengeance of the Hurons had now taken a new direction, and they prepared
Title:  to execute it with that barbarous ingenuity with which they were
Title:  familiarized by the practise of centuries. Some sought knots, to raise the
Title:  blazing pile; one was riving the splinters of pine, in order to pierce the
Title:  flesh of their captives with the burning fragments; and others bent the tops
Title:  of two saplings to the earth, in order to suspend Heyward by the arms
Title:  between the recoiling branches. But the vengeance of Magua sought a deeper
Title:  and more malignant enjoyment.
Title:  
Title:  While the less refined monsters of the band prepared, before the eyes of
Title:  those who were to suffer, these well-known and vulgar means of torture, he
Title:  approached Cora, and pointed out, with the most malign expression of
Title:  countenance, the speedy fate that awaited her:
Title:  
Title:  Ha! he added, what says the daughter of Munro? Her head is too good to find
Title:  a pillow in the wigwam of Le Renard; will she like it better when it rolls
Title:  about this hill a plaything for the wolves? Her bosom cannot nurse the
Title:  children of a Huron; she will see it spit upon by Indians!
Title:  
Title:  What means the monster! demanded the astonished Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  Nothing! was the firm reply. He is a savage, a barbarous and ignorant
Title:  savage, and knows not what he does. Let us find leisure, with our dying
Title:  breath, to ask for him penitence and pardon.
Title:  
Title:  Pardon! echoed the fierce Huron, mistaking in his anger, the meaning of her
Title:  words; the memory of an Indian is no longer than the arm of the pale faces;
Title:  his mercy shorter than their justice! Say; shall I send the yellow hair to
Title:  her father, and will you follow Magua to the great lakes, to carry his
Title:  water, and feed him with corn?
Title:  
Title:  Cora beckoned him away, with an emotion of disgust she could not control.
Title:  
Title:  Leave me, she said, with a solemnity that for a moment checked the barbarity
Title:  of the Indian; you mingle bitterness in my prayers; you stand between me and
Title:  my God!
Title:  
Title:  The slight impression produced on the savage was, however, soon forgotten,
Title:  and he continued pointing, with taunting irony, toward Alice.
Title:  
Title:  Look! the child weeps! She is too young to die! Send her to Munro, to comb
Title:  his gray hairs, and keep life in the heart of the old man.
Title:  
Title:  Cora could not resist the desire to look upon her youthful sister, in whose
Title:  eyes she met an imploring glance, that betrayed the longings of nature.
Title:  
Title:  What says he, dearest Cora? asked the trembling voice of Alice. Did he speak
Title:  of sending me to our father?
Title:  
Title:  For many moments the elder sister looked upon the younger, with a
Title:  countenance that wavered with powerful and contending emotions. At length
Title:  she spoke, though her tones had lost their rich and calm fullness, in an
Title:  expression of tenderness that seemed maternal.
Title:  
Title:  Alice, she said, the Huron offers us both life, nay, more than both; he
Title:  offers to restore Duncan, our invaluable Duncan, as well as you, to our
Title:  friends - to our father - to our heart-stricken, childless father, if I will
Title:  bow down this rebellious, stubborn pride of mine, and consent - -
Title:  
Title:  Her voice became choked, and clasping her hands, she looked upward, as if
Title:  seeking, in her agony, intelligence from a wisdom that was infinite.
Title:  
Title:  Say on, cried Alice; to what, dearest Cora? Oh! that the proffer were made
Title:  to me! to save you, to cheer our aged father, to restore Duncan, how
Title:  cheerfully could I die!
Title:  
Title:  Die! repeated Cora, with a calmer and firmer voice that were easy! Perhaps
Title:  the alternative may not be less so. He would have me, she continued, her
Title:  accents sinking under a deep consciousness of the degradation of the
Title:  proposal, follow him to the wilderness; go to the habitations of the Hurons;
Title:  to remain there; in short, to become his wife! Speak, then, Alice; child of
Title:  my affections! sister of my love! And you, too, Major Heyward, aid my weak
Title:  reason with your counsel. Is life to be purchased by such a sacrifice? Will
Title:  you, Alice, receive it at my hands at such a price? And you, Duncan, guide
Title:  me; control me between you; for I am wholly yours!
Title:  
Title:  Would I! echoed the indignant and astonished youth. Cora! Cora! you jest
Title:  with our misery! Name not the horrid alternative again; the thought itself
Title:  is worse than a thousand deaths.
Title:  
Title:  That such would be your answer, I well knew! exclaimed Cora, her cheeks
Title:  flushing, and her dark eyes once more sparkling with the lingering emotions
Title:  of a woman. What says my Alice? for her will I submit without another
Title:  murmur.
Title:  
Title:  Although both Heyward and Cora listened with painful suspense and the
Title:  deepest attention, no sounds were heard in reply. It appeared as if the
Title:  delicate and sensitive form of Alice would shrink into itself, as she
Title:  listened to this proposal. Her arms had fallen lengthwise before her, the
Title:  fingers moving in slight convulsions; her head dropped upon her bosom, and
Title:  her whole person seemed suspended against the tree, looking like some
Title:  beautiful emblem of the wounded delicacy of her sex, devoid of animation and
Title:  yet keenly conscious. In a few moments, however, her head began to move
Title:  slowly, in a sign of deep, unconquerable disapprobation.
Title:  
Title:  No, no, no; better that we die as we have lived, together!
Title:  
Title:  Then die! shouted Magua, hurling his tomahawk with violence at the
Title:  unresisting speaker, and gnashing his teeth with a rage that could no longer
Title:  be bridled at this sudden exhibition of firmness in the one he believed the
Title:  weakest of the party. The axe cleaved the air in front of Heyward, and
Title:  cutting some of the flowing ringlets of Alice, quivered in the tree above
Title:  her head. The sight maddened Duncan to desperation. Collecting all his
Title:  energies in one effort he snapped the twigs which bound him and rushed upon
Title:  another savage, who was preparing, with loud yells and a more deliberate
Title:  aim, to repeat the blow. They encountered, grappled, and fell to the earth
Title:  together. The naked body of his antagonist afforded Heyward no means of
Title:  holding his adversary, who glided from his grasp, and rose again with one
Title:  knee on his chest, pressing him down with the weight of a giant. Duncan
Title:  already saw the knife gleaming in the air, when a whistling sound swept past
Title:  him, and was rather accompanied than followed by the sharp crack of a rifle.
Title:  He felt his breast relieved from the load it had endured; he saw the savage
Title:  expression of his adversary's countenance change to a look of vacant
Title:  wildness, when the Indian fell dead on the faded leaves by his side.
Title:  
Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 12
Title:  
Title:       Clown: I am gone, sire,
Title:       And anon, sire,
Title:       I'll be with you again.
Title:  
Title:                                                           TWELFTH NIGHT
Title:  
Title:  The Hurons stood aghast at this sudden visitation of death on one of their
Title:  band. But as they regarded the fatal accuracy of an aim which had dared to
Title:  immolate an enemy at so much hazard to a friend, the name of La Longue
Title:  Carabine burst simultaneously from every lip, and was succeeded by a wild
Title:  and a sort of plaintive howl. The cry was answered by a loud shout from a
Title:  little thicket, where the incautious party had piled their arms; and at the
Title:  next moment, Hawkeye, too eager to load the rifle he had regained, was seen
Title:  advancing upon them, brandishing the clubbed weapon, and cutting the air
Title:  with wide and powerful sweeps. Bold and rapid as was the progress of the
Title:  scout, it was exceeded by that of a light and vigorous form which, bounding
Title:  past him, leaped, with incredible activity and daring, into the very center
Title:  of the Hurons, where it stood, whirling a tomahawk, and flourishing a
Title:  glittering knife, with fearful menaces, in front of Cora. Quicker than the
Title:  thoughts could follow those unexpected and audacious movements, an image,
Title:  armed in the emblematic panoply of death, glided before their eyes, and
Title:  assumed a threatening attitude at the other's side. The savage tormentors
Title:  recoiled before these warlike intruders, and uttered, as they appeared in
Title:  such quick succession, the often repeated and peculiar exclamations of
Title:  surprise, followed by the well-known and dreaded appellations of:
Title:  
Title:  Le Cerf Agile! Le Gros Serpent!
Title:  
Title:  But the wary and vigilant leader of the Hurons was not so easily
Title:  disconcerted. Casting his keen eyes around the little plain, he comprehended
Title:  the nature of the assault at a glance, and encouraging his followers by his
Title:  voice as well as by his example, he unsheathed his long and dangerous knife,
Title:  and rushed with a loud whoop upon the expected Chingachgook. It was the
Title:  signal for a general combat. Neither party had firearms, and the contest was
Title:  to be decided in the deadliest manner, hand to hand, with weapons of
Title:  offense, and none of defense.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas answered the whoop, and leaping on an enemy, with a single,
Title:  well-directed blow of his tomahawk, cleft him to the brain. Heyward tore the
Title:  weapon of Magua from the sapling, and rushed eagerly toward the fray. As the
Title:  combatants were now equal in number, each singled an opponent from the
Title:  adverse band. The rush and blows passed with the fury of a whirlwind, and
Title:  the swiftness of lightning. Hawkeye soon got another enemy within reach of
Title:  his arm, and with one sweep of his formidable weapon he beat down the slight
Title:  and inartificial defenses of his antagonist, crushing him to the earth with
Title:  the blow. Heyward ventured to hurl the tomahawk he had seized, too ardent to
Title:  await the moment of closing. It struck the Indian he had selected on the
Title:  forehead, and checked for an instant his onward rush. Encouraged by this
Title:  slight advantage, the impetuous young man continued his onset, and sprang
Title:  upon his enemy with naked hands. A single instant was enough to assure him
Title:  of the rashness of the measure, for he immediately found himself fully
Title:  engaged, with all his activity and courage, in endeavoring to ward the
Title:  desperate thrusts made with the knife of the Huron. Unable longer to foil an
Title:  enemy so alert and vigilant, he threw his arms about him, and succeeded in
Title:  pinning the limbs of the other to his side, with an iron grasp, but one that
Title:  was far too exhausting to himself to continue long. In this extremity he
Title:  heard a voice near him, shouting:
Title:  
Title:  Extarminate the varlets! no quarter to an accursed Mingo!
Title:  
Title:  At the next moment, the breech of Hawkeye's rifle fell on the naked head of
Title:  his adversary, whose muscles appeared to wither under the shock, as he sank
Title:  from the arms of Duncan, flexible and motionless.
Title:  
Title:  When Uncas had brained his first antagonist, he turned, like a hungry lion,
Title:  to seek another. The fifth and only Huron disengaged at the first onset had
Title:  paused a moment, and then seeing that all around him were employed in the
Title:  deadly strife, he had sought, with hellish vengeance, to complete the
Title:  baffled work of revenge. Raising a shout of triumph, he sprang toward the
Title:  defenseless Cora, sending his keen axe as the dreadful precursor of his
Title:  approach. The tomahawk grazed her shoulder, and cutting the withes which
Title:  bound her to the tree, left the maiden at liberty to fly. She eluded the
Title:  grasp of the savage, and reckless of her own safety, threw herself on the
Title:  bosom of Alice, striving with convulsed and ill-directed fingers, to tear
Title:  asunder the twigs which confined the person of her sister. Any other than a
Title:  monster would have relented at such an act of generous devotion to the best
Title:  and purest affection; but the breast of the Huron was a stranger to
Title:  sympathy. Seizing Cora by the rich tresses which fell in confusion about her
Title:  form, he tore her from her frantic hold, and bowed her down with brutal
Title:  violence to her knees. The savage drew the flowing curls through his hand,
Title:  and raising them on high with an outstretched arm, he passed the knife
Title:  around the exquisitely molded head of his victim, with a taunting and
Title:  exulting laugh. But he purchased this moment of fierce gratification with
Title:  the loss of the fatal opportunity. It was just then the sight caught the eye
Title:  of Uncas. Bounding from his footsteps he appeared for an instant darting
Title:  through the air and descending in a ball he fell on the chest of his enemy,
Title:  driving him many yards from the spot, headlong and prostrate. The violence
Title:  of the exertion cast the young Mohican at his side. They arose together,
Title:  fought, and bled, each in his turn. But the conflict was soon decided; the
Title:  tomahawk of Heyward and the rifle of Hawkeye descended on the skull of the
Title:  Huron, at the same moment that the knife of Uncas reached his heart.
Title:  
Title:  The battle was now entirely terminated with the exception of the protracted
Title:  struggle between Le Renard Subtil and Le Gros Serpent. Well did these
Title:  barbarous warriors prove that they deserved those significant names which
Title:  had been bestowed for deeds in former wars. When they engaged, some little
Title:  time was lost in eluding the quick and vigorous thrusts which had been aimed
Title:  at their lives. Suddenly darting on each other, they closed, and came to the
Title:  earth, twisted together like twining serpents, in pliant and subtle folds.
Title:  At the moment when the victors found themselves unoccupied, the spot where
Title:  these experienced and desperate combatants lay could only be distinguished
Title:  by a cloud of dust and leaves, which moved from the center of the little
Title:  plain toward its boundary, as if raised by the passage of a whirlwind. Urged
Title:  by the different motives of filial affection, friendship and gratitude,
Title:  Heyward and his companions rushed with one accord to the place, encircling
Title:  the little canopy of dust which hung above the warriors. In vain did Uncas
Title:  dart around the cloud, with a wish to strike his knife into the heart of his
Title:  father's foe; the threatening rifle of Hawkeye was raised and suspended in
Title:  vain, while Duncan endeavored to seize the limbs of the Huron with hands
Title:  that appeared to have lost their power. Covered as they were with dust and
Title:  blood, the swift evolutions of the combatants seemed to incorporate their
Title:  bodies into one. The death-like looking figure of the Mohican, and the dark
Title:  form of the Huron, gleamed before their eyes in such quick and confused
Title:  succession, that the friends of the former knew not where to plant the
Title:  succoring blow. It is true there were short and fleeting moments, when the
Title:  fiery eyes of Magua were seen glittering, like the fabled organs of the
Title:  basilisk through the dusty wreath by which he was enveloped, and he read by
Title:  those short and deadly glances the fate of the combat in the presence of his
Title:  enemies; ere, however, any hostile hand could descend on his devoted head,
Title:  its place was filled by the scowling visage of Chingachgook. In this manner
Title:  the scene of the combat was removed from the center of the little plain to
Title:  its verge. The Mohican now found an opportunity to make a powerful thrust
Title:  with his knife; Magua suddenly relinquished his grasp, and fell backward
Title:  without motion, and seemingly without life. His adversary leaped on his
Title:  feet, making the arches of the forest ring with the sounds of triumph.
Title:  
Title:  Well done for the Delawares! victory to the Mohicans! cried Hawkeye, once
Title:  more elevating the butt of the long and fatal rifle; a finishing blow from a
Title:  man without a cross will never tell against his honor, nor rob him of his
Title:  right to the scalp.
Title:  
Title:  But at the very moment when the dangerous weapon was in the act of
Title:  descending, the subtle Huron rolled swiftly from beneath the danger, over
Title:  the edge of the precipice, and falling on his feet, was seen leaping, with a
Title:  single bound, into the center of a thicket of low bushes, which clung along
Title:  its sides. The Delawares, who had believed their enemy dead, uttered their
Title:  exclamation of surprise, and were following with speed and clamor, like
Title:  hounds in open view of the deer, when a shrill and peculiar cry from the
Title:  scout instantly changed their purpose, and recalled them to the summit of
Title:  the hill.
Title:  
Title:  'Twas like himself! cried the inveterate forester, whose prejudices
Title:  contributed so largely to veil his natural sense of justice in all matters
Title:  which concerned the Mingoes; a lying and deceitful varlet as he is. An
Title:  honest Delaware now, being fairly vanquished, would have lain still, and
Title:  been knocked on the head, but these knavish Maquas cling to life like so
Title:  many cats-o'-the-mountain. Let him go - let him go; 'tis but one man, and he
Title:  without rifle or bow, many a long mile from his French commerades; and like
Title:  a rattler that lost his fangs, he can do no further mischief, until such
Title:  time as he, and we too, may leave the prints of our moccasins over a long
Title:  reach of sandy plain. See, Uncas, he added, in Delaware, your father if
Title:  flaying the scalps already. It may be well to go round and feel the
Title:  vagabonds that are left, or we may have another of them loping through the
Title:  woods, and screeching like a jay that has been winged.
Title:  
Title:  So saying the honest but implacable scout made the circuit of the dead, into
Title:  whose senseless bosoms he thrust his long knife, with as much coolness as
Title:  though they had been so many brute carcasses. He had, however, been
Title:  anticipated by the elder Mohican, who had already torn the emblems of
Title:  victory from the unresisting heads of the slain.
Title:  
Title:  But Uncas, denying his habits, we had almost said his nature, flew with
Title:  instinctive delicacy, accompanied by Heyward, to the assistance of the
Title:  females, and quickly releasing Alice, placed her in the arms of Cora. We
Title:  shall not attempt to describe the gratitude to the Almighty Disposer of
Title:  Events which glowed in the bosoms of the sisters, who were thus unexpectedly
Title:  restored to life and to each other. Their thanksgivings were deep and
Title:  silent; the offerings of their gentle spirits burning brightest and purest
Title:  on the secret altars of their hearts; and their renovated and more earthly
Title:  feelings exhibiting themselves in long and fervent though speechless
Title:  caresses. As Alice rose from her knees, where she had sunk by the side of
Title:  Cora, she threw herself on the bosom of the latter, and sobbed aloud the
Title:  name of their aged father, while her soft, dove-like eyes, sparkled with the
Title:  rays of hope.
Title:  
Title:  We are saved! we are saved! she murmured; to return to the arms of our dear,
Title:  dear father, and his heart will not be broken with grief. And you, too,
Title:  Cora, my sister, my more than sister, my mother; you, too, are spared. And
Title:  Duncan, she added, looking round upon the youth with a smile of ineffable
Title:  innocence, even our own brave and noble Duncan has escaped without a hurt.
Title:  
Title:  To these ardent and nearly innocent words Cora made no other answer than by
Title:  straining the youthful speaker to her heart, as she bent over her in melting
Title:  tenderness. The manhood of Heyward felt no shame in dropping tears over this
Title:  spectacle of affectionate rapture; and Uncas stood, fresh and blood-stained
Title:  from the combat, a calm, and, apparently, an unmoved looker-on, it is true,
Title:  but with eyes that had already lost their fierceness, and were beaming with
Title:  a sympathy that elevated him far above the intelligence, and advanced him
Title:  probably centuries before, the practises of his nation.
Title:  
Title:  During this display of emotions so natural in their situation, Hawkeye,
Title:  whose vigilant distrust had satisfied itself that the Hurons, who disfigured
Title:  the heavenly scene, no longer possessed the power to interrupt its harmony,
Title:  approached David, and liberated him from the bonds he had, until that
Title:  moment, endured with the most exemplary patience.
Title:  
Title:  There, exclaimed the scout, casting the last withe behind him, you are once
Title:  more master of your own limbs, though you seem not to use them with much
Title:  greater judgment than that in which they were first fashioned. If advice
Title:  from one who is not older than yourself, but who, having lived most of his
Title:  time in the wilderness, may be said to have experience beyond his years,
Title:  will give no offense, you are welcome to my thoughts; and these are, to part
Title:  with the little tooting instrument in your jacket to the first fool you meet
Title:  with, and buy some we'pon with the money, if it be only the barrel of a
Title:  horseman's pistol. By industry and care, you might thus come to some
Title:  prefarment; for by this time, I should think, your eyes would plainly tell
Title:  you that a carrion crow is a better bird than a mocking-thresher. The one
Title:  will, at least, remove foul sights from before the face of man, while the
Title:  other is only good to brew disturbances in the woods, by cheating the ears
Title:  of all that hear them.
Title:  
Title:  Arms and the clarion for the battle, but the song of thanksgiving to the
Title:  victory! answered the liberated David. Friend, he added, thrusting forth his
Title:  lean, delicate hand toward Hawkeye, in kindness, while his eyes twinkled and
Title:  grew moist, I thank thee that the hairs of my head still grow where they
Title:  were first rooted by Providence; for, though those of other men may be more
Title:  glossy and curling, I have ever found mine own well suited to the brain they
Title:  shelter. That I did not join myself to the battle, was less owing to
Title:  disinclination, than to the bonds of the heathen. Valiant and skillful hast
Title:  thou proved thyself in the conflict, and I hereby thank thee, before
Title:  proceeding to discharge other and more important duties, because thou hast
Title:  proved thyself well worthy of a Christian's praise.
Title:  
Title:  The thing is but a trifle, and what you may often see if you tarry long
Title:  among us, returned the scout, a good deal softened toward the man of song,
Title:  by this unequivocal expression of gratitude. I have got back my old
Title:  companion, killdeer, he added, striking his hand on the breech of his rifle;
Title:  and that in itself is a victory. These Iroquois are cunning, but they
Title:  outwitted themselves when they placed their firearms out of reach; and had
Title:  Uncas or his father been gifted with only their common Indian patience, we
Title:  should have come in upon the knaves with three bullets instead of one, and
Title:  that would have made a finish of the whole pack; yon loping varlet, as well
Title:  as his commerades. But 'twas all fore-ordered, and for the best.
Title:  
Title:  Thou sayest well, returned David, and hast caught the true spirit of
Title:  Christianity. He that is to be saved will be saved, and he that is
Title:  predestined to be damned will be damned. This is the doctrine of truth, and
Title:  most consoling and refreshing it is to the true believer.
Title:  
Title:  The scout, who by this time was seated, examining into the state of his
Title:  rifle with a species of parental assiduity, now looked up at the other in a
Title:  displeasure that he did not affect to conceal, roughly interrupting further
Title:  speech.
Title:  
Title:  Doctrine or no doctrine, said the sturdy woodsman, 'tis the belief of
Title:  knaves, and the curse of an honest man. I can credit that yonder Huron was
Title:  to fall by my hand, for with my own eyes I have seen it; but nothing short
Title:  of being a witness will cause me to think he has met with any reward, or
Title:  that Chingachgook there will be condemned at the final day.
Title:  
Title:  You have no warranty for such an audacious doctrine, nor any covenant to
Title:  support it, cried David who was deeply tinctured with the subtle
Title:  distinctions which, in his time , and more especially in his province, had
Title:  been drawn around the beautiful simplicity of revelation, by endeavoring to
Title:  penetrate the awful mystery of the divine nature, supplying faith by
Title:  self-sufficiency, and by consequence, involving those who reasoned from such
Title:  human dogmas in absurdities and doubt; your temple is reared on the sands,
Title:  and the first tempest will wash away its foundation. I demand your
Title:  authorities for such an uncharitable assertion (like other advocates of a
Title:  system, David was not always accurate in his use of terms). Name chapter and
Title:  verse; in which of the holy books do you find language to support you?
Title:  
Title:  Book! repeated Hawkeye, with singular and ill-concealed disdain; do you take
Title:  me for a whimpering boy at the apronstring of one of your old gals; and this
Title:  good rifle on my knee for the feather of a goose's wing, my ox's horn for a
Title:  bottle of ink, and my leathern pouch for a cross-barred handkercher to carry
Title:  my dinner? Book! what have such as I, who am a warrior of the wilderness,
Title:  though a man without a cross, to do with books? I never read but in one, and
Title:  the words that are written there are too simple and too plain to need much
Title:  schooling; though I may boast that of forty long and hard-working years.
Title:  
Title:  What call you the volume? said David, misconceiving the other's meaning.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis open before your eyes, returned the scout; and he who owns it is not a
Title:  niggard of its use. I have heard it said that there are men who read in
Title:  books to convince themselves there is a God. I know not but man may so
Title:  deform his works in the settlement, as to leave that which is so clear in
Title:  the wilderness a matter of doubt among traders and priests. If any such
Title:  there be, and he will follow me from sun to sun, through the windings of the
Title:  forest, he shall see enough to teach him that he is a fool, and that the
Title:  greatest of his folly lies in striving to rise to the level of One he can
Title:  never equal, be it in goodness, or be it in power.
Title:  
Title:  The instant David discovered that he battled with a disputant who imbibed
Title:  his faith from the lights of nature, eschewing all subtleties of doctrine,
Title:  he willingly abondoned a controversy from which he believed neither profit
Title:  nor credit was to be derived. While the scout was speaking, he had also
Title:  seated himself, and producing the ready little volume and the iron-rimmed
Title:  spectacles, he prepared to discharge a duty, which nothing but the
Title:  unexpected assault he had received in his orthodoxy could have so long
Title:  suspended. He was, in truth, a minstrel of the western continent - of a much
Title:  later day, certainly, than those gifted bards, who formerly sang the profane
Title:  renown of baron and prince, but after the spirit of his own age and country;
Title:  and he was now prepared to exercise the cunning of his craft, in celebration
Title:  of, or rather in thanksgiving for, the recent victory. He waited patiently
Title:  for Hawkeye to cease, then lifting his eyes, together with his voice, he
Title:  said, aloud:
Title:  
Title:  I invite you, friends, to join in praise for this signal deliverance from
Title:  the hands of barbarians and infidels, to the comfortable and solemn tones of
Title:  the tune called Northampton.
Title:  
Title:  He next named the page and verse where the rhymes selected were to be found,
Title:  and applied the pitch-pipe to his lips, with the decent gravity that he had
Title:  been wont to use in the temple. This time he was, however, without any
Title:  accompaniment, for the sisters were just then pouring out those tender
Title:  effusions of affection which have been already alluded to. Nothing deterred
Title:  by the smallness of his audience, which, in truth, consisted only of the
Title:  discontented scout, he raised his voice, commencing and ending the sacred
Title:  song without accident or interruption of any kind.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye listened while he coolly adjusted his flint and reloaded his rifle;
Title:  but the sounds, wanting the extraneous assistance of scene and sympathy,
Title:  failed to awaken his slumbering emotions. Never minstrel, or by whatever
Title:  more suitable name David should be known, drew upon his talents in the
Title:  presence of more insensible auditors; though considering the singleness and
Title:  sincerity of his motive, it is probably that no bard of profane song ever
Title:  uttered notes that ascended so near to that throne where all homage and
Title:  praise is due. The scout shook his head, and muttering some unintelligible
Title:  words, among which throat and Iroquois were alone audible, he walked away,
Title:  to collect and to examine into the state of the captured arsenal of the
Title:  Hurons. In this office he was now joined by Chingachgook, who found his own,
Title:  as well as the rifle of his son, among the arms. Even Heyward and David were
Title:  furnished with weapons; nor was ammunition wanting to render them all
Title:  effectual.
Title:  
Title:  When the foresters had made their selection, and distributed their prizes,
Title:  the scout announced that the hour had arrived when it was necessary to move.
Title:  By this time the song of Gamut had ceased, and the sisters had learned to
Title:  still the exhibition of their emotions. Aided by Duncan and the younger
Title:  Mohican, the two latter descended the precipitous sides of that hill which
Title:  they had so lately ascended under so very different auspices, and whose
Title:  summit had so nearly proved the scene of their massacre. At the foot they
Title:  found the Narragansetts browsing the herbage of the bushes, and having
Title:  mounted, they followed the movements of a guide, who, in the most deadly
Title:  straits, had so often proved himself their friend. The journey was, however,
Title:  short. Hawkeye, leaving the blind path that the Hurons had followed, turned
Title:  short to his right, and entering the thicket, he crossed a babbling brook,
Title:  and halted in a narrow dell, under the shade of a few water elms. Their
Title:  distance from the base of the fatal hill was but a few rods, and the steeds
Title:  had been serviceable only in crossing the shallow stream.
Title:  
Title:  The scout and the Indians appeared to be familiar with the sequestered place
Title:  where they now were; for, leaning their rifle against the trees, they
Title:  commenced throwing aside the dried leaves, and opening the blue clay, out of
Title:  which a clear and sparkling spring of bright, glancing water, quickly
Title:  bubbled. The white man then looked about him, as though seeking for some
Title:  object, which was not to be found as readily as he expected.
Title:  
Title:  Them careless imps, the Mohawks, with their Tuscarora and Onondaga brethren,
Title:  have been here slaking their thirst, he muttered, and the vagabonds have
Title:  thrown away the gourd! This is the way with benefits, when they are bestowed
Title:  on such disremembering hounds! Here has the Lord laid his hand, in the midst
Title:  of the howling wilderness, for their good, and raised a fountain of water
Title:  from the bowels of the 'arth, that might laugh at the richest shop of
Title:  apothecary's ware in all the colonies; and see! the knaves have trodden in
Title:  the clay, and deformed the cleanliness of the place, as though they were
Title:  brute beasts, instead of human men.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas silently extended toward him the desired gourd, which the spleen of
Title:  Hawkeye had hitherto prevented him from observing on a branch of an elm.
Title:  Filling it with water, he retired a short distance, to a place where the
Title:  ground was more firm and dry; here he coolly seated himself, and after
Title:  taking a long, and, apparently, a grateful draught, he commenced a very
Title:  strict examination of the fragments of food left by the Hurons, which had
Title:  hung in a wallet on his arm.
Title:  
Title:  Thank you, lad! he continued, returning the empty gourd to Uncas; now we
Title:  will see how these rampaging Hurons lived, when outlying in ambushments.
Title:  Look at this! The varlets know the better pieces of the deer; and one would
Title:  think they might carve and roast a saddle, equal to the best cook in the
Title:  land! But everything is raw, for the Iroquois are thorough savages. Uncas,
Title:  take my steel and kindle a fire; a mouthful of a tender broil will give
Title:  natur' a helping hand, after so long a trail.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, perceiving that their guides now set about their repast in sober
Title:  earnest, assisted the ladies to alight, and placed himself at their side,
Title:  not unwilling to enjoy a few moments of grateful rest, after the bloody
Title:  scene he had just gone through. While the culinary process was in hand,
Title:  curiosity induced him to inquire into the circumstances which had led to
Title:  their timely and unexpected rescue:
Title:  
Title:  How is it that we see you so soon, my generous friend, he asked, and without
Title:  aid from the garrison of Edward?
Title:  
Title:  Had we gone to the bend in the river, we might have been in time to rake the
