Title:  leaves over your bodies, but too late to have saved your scalps, coolly
Title:  answered the scout. No, no; instead of throwing away strength and
Title:  opportunity by crossing to the fort, we lay by, under the bank of the
Title:  Hudson, waiting to watch the movements of the Hurons.
Title:  
Title:  You were, then, witnesses of all that passed?
Title:  
Title:  Not of all; for Indian sight is too keen to be easily cheated, and we kept
Title:  close. A difficult matter it was, too, to keep this Mohican boy snug in the
Title:  ambushment. Ah! Uncas, Uncas, your behavior was more like that of a curious
Title:  woman than of a warrior on his scent.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas permitted his eyes to turn for an instant on the sturdy countenance of
Title:  the speaker, but he neither spoke nor gave any indication of repentance. On
Title:  the contrary, Heyward thought the manner of the young Mohican was
Title:  disdainful, if not a little fierce, and that he suppressed passions that
Title:  were ready to explode, as much in compliment to the listeners, as from the
Title:  deference he usually paid to his white associate.
Title:  
Title:  You saw our capture? Heyward next demanded.
Title:  
Title:  We heard it, was the significant answer. An Indian yell is plain language to
Title:  men who have passed their days in the woods. But when you landed, we were
Title:  driven to crawl like sarpents, beneath the leaves; and then we lost sight of
Title:  you entirely, until we placed eyes on you again trussed to the trees, and
Title:  ready bound for an Indian massacre.
Title:  
Title:  Our rescue was the deed of Providence. It was nearly a miracle that you did
Title:  not mistake the path, for the Hurons divided, and each band had its horses.
Title:  
Title:  Ay! there we were thrown off the scent, and might, indeed, have lost the
Title:  trail, had it not been for Uncas; we took the path, however, that led into
Title:  the wilderness; for we judged, and judged rightly, that the savages would
Title:  hold that course with their prisoners. But when we had followed it for many
Title:  miles, without finding a single twig broken, as I had advised, my mind
Title:  misgave me; especially as all the footsteps had the prints of moccasins.
Title:  
Title:  Our captors had the precaution to see us shod like themselves, said Duncan,
Title:  raising a foot, and exhibiting the buckskin he wore.
Title:  
Title:  Aye, 'twas judgmatical and like themselves; though we were too expart to be
Title:  thrown from a trail by so common an invention.
Title:  
Title:  To what, then, are we indebted for our safety?
Title:  
Title:  To what, as a white man who has no taint of Indian blood, I should be
Title:  ashamed to own; to the judgment of the young Mohican, in matters which I
Title:  should know better than he, but which I can now hardly believe to be true,
Title:  though my own eyes tell me it is so.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis extraordinary! will you not name the reason?
Title:  
Title:  Uncas was bold enough to say, that the beasts ridden by the gentle ones,
Title:  continued Hawkeye, glancing his eyes, not without curious interest, on the
Title:  fillies of the ladies, planted the legs of one side on the ground at the
Title:  same time, which is contrary to the movements of all trotting four-footed
Title:  animals of my knowledge, except the bear. And yet here are horses that
Title:  always journey in this manner, as my own eyes have seen, and as their trail
Title:  has shown for twenty long miles.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis the merit of the animal! They come from the shores of Narrangansett
Title:  Bay, in the small province of Providence Plantations, and are celebrated for
Title:  their hardihood, and the ease of this peculiar movement; though other horses
Title:  are not unfrequently trained to the same.
Title:  
Title:  It may be - it may be, said Hawkeye, who had listened with singular
Title:  attention to this explanation; though I am a man who has the full blood of
Title:  the whites, my judgment in deer and beaver is greater than in beasts of
Title:  burden. Major Effingham has many noble chargers, but I have never seen one
Title:  travel after such a sidling gait.
Title:  
Title:  True; for he would value the animals for very different properties. Still is
Title:  this a breed highly esteemed and, as you witness, much honored with the
Title:  burdens it is often destined to bear.
Title:  
Title:  The Mohicans had suspended their operations about the glimmering fire to
Title:  listen; and, when Duncan had done, they looked at each other significantly,
Title:  the father uttering the never-failing exclamation of surprise. The scout
Title:  ruminated, like a man digesting his newly-acquired knowledge, and once more
Title:  stole a glance at the horses.
Title:  
Title:  I dare to say there are even stranger sights to be seen in the settlements!
Title:  he said, at length natur' is sadly abused by man, when he once gets the
Title:  mastery. But, go sidling or go straight, Uncas had seen the movement, and
Title:  their trail led us on to the broken bush. The outer branch, near the prints
Title:  of one of the horses, was bent upward, as a lady breaks a flower from its
Title:  stem, but all the rest were ragged and broken down, as if the strong hand of
Title:  a man had been tearing them! So I concluded that the cunning varments had
Title:  seen the twig bent, and had torn the rest, to make us believe a buck had
Title:  been feeling the boughs with his antlers.
Title:  
Title:  I do believe your sagacity did not deceive you; for some such thing
Title:  occurred!
Title:  
Title:  That was easy to see, added the scout, in no degree conscious of having
Title:  exhibited any extraordinary sagacity; and a very different matter it was
Title:  from a waddling horse! It then struck me the Mingoes would push for this
Title:  spring, for the knaves well know the vartue of its waters!
Title:  
Title:  Is it, then, so famous? demanded Heyward, examining, with a more curious
Title:  eye, the secluded dell, with its bubbling fountain, surrounded, as it was,
Title:  by earth of a deep, dingy brown.
Title:  
Title:  Few red-skins, who travel south and east of the great lakes but have heard
Title:  of its qualities. Will you taste for yourself?
Title:  
Title:  Heyward took the gourd, and after swallowing a little of the water, threw it
Title:  aside with grimaces of discontent. The scout laughed in his silent but
Title:  heartfelt manner, and shook his head with vast satisfaction.
Title:  
Title:  Ah! you want the flavor that one gets by habit; the time was when I liked it
Title:  as little as yourself; but I have come to my taste, and I now crave it, as a
Title:  deer does the licks.1 Your high-spiced wines are not better liked than a
Title:  red-skin relishes this water; especially when his natur' is ailing. But
Title:  Uncas has made his fire, and it is time we think of eating, for our journey
Title:  is long, and all before us.
Title:  
Title:  Interrrupting the dialogue by this abrupt transition, the scout had instant
Title:  recourse to the fragments of food which had escaped the voracity of the
Title:  Hurons. A very summary process completed the simple cookery, when he and the
Title:  Mohicans commenced their humble meal, with the silence and characteristic
Title:  diligence of men who ate in order to enable themselves to endure great and
Title:  unremitting toil.
Title:  
Title:  When this necessary, and, happily, grateful duty had been performed, each of
Title:  the foresters stooped and took a long and parting draught at that solitary
Title:  and silent spring,2 around which and its sister fountains, within fifty
Title:  years, the wealth, beauty and talents of a hemisphere were to assemble in
Title:  throngs, in pursuit of health and pleasure. Then Hawkeye announced his
Title:  determination to proceed. The sisters resumed their saddles; Duncan and
Title:  David grapsed their rifles, and followed on footsteps; the scout leading the
Title:  advance, and the Mohicans bringing up the rear. The whole party moved
Title:  swiftly through the narrow path, toward the north, leaving the healing
Title:  waters to mingle unheeded with the adjacent brooks and the bodies of the
Title:  dead to fester on the neighboring mount, without the rites of sepulture; a
Title:  fate but too common to the warriors of the woods to excite either
Title:  commiseration or comment.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 Many of the animals of the American forests resort to those spots where
Title:  salt springs are found. These are called licks or salt licks, in the
Title:  language of the country, from the circumstance that the quadruped is often
Title:  obliged to lick the earth, in order to obtain the saline particles. These
Title:  licks are great places of resort with the hunters, who waylay their game
Title:  near the paths that lead to them.
Title:  
Title:  2 The scene of the foregoing incidents is on the spot where the village of
Title:  Ballston now stands; one of the two principal watering places of America.
Title:  
Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 13
Title:  
Title:       I'll seek a readier path.
Title:  
Title:                                                                 PARNELL
Title:  
Title:  The route taken by Hawkeye lay across those sandy plains, relived by
Title:  occasional valleys and swells of land, which had been traversed by their
Title:  party on the morning of the same day, with the baffled Magua for their
Title:  guide. The sun had now fallen low toward the distant mountains; and as their
Title:  journey lay through the interminable forest, the heat was no longer
Title:  oppressive. Their progress, in consequence, was proportionate; and long
Title:  before the twilight gathered about them, they had made good many toilsome
Title:  miles on their return.
Title:  
Title:  The hunter, like the savage whose place he filled, seemed to select among
Title:  the blind signs of their wild route, with a species of instinct, seldom
Title:  abating his speed, and never pausing to deliberate. A rapid and oblique
Title:  glance at the moss on the trees, with an occasional upward gaze toward the
Title:  setting sun, or a steady but passing look at the direction of the numerous
Title:  water courses, through which he waded, were sufficient to determine his
Title:  path, and remove his greatest difficulties. In the meantime, the forest
Title:  began to change its hues, losing that lively green which had embellished its
Title:  arches, in the graver light which is the usual precursor of the close of
Title:  day.
Title:  
Title:  While the eyes of the sisters were endeavoring to catch glimpses through the
Title:  trees, of the flood of golden glory which formed a glittering halo around
Title:  the sun, tinging here and there with ruby streaks, or bordering with narrow
Title:  edgings of shining yellow, a mass of clouds that lay piled at no great
Title:  distance above the western hills, Hawkeye turned suddenly and pointing
Title:  upward toward the gorgeous heavens, he spoke:
Title:  
Title:  Yonder is the signal given to man to seek his food and natural rest, he
Title:  said; better and wiser would it be, if he could understand the signs of
Title:  nature, and take a lesson from the fowls of the air and the beasts of the
Title:  field! Our night, however, will soon be over, for with the moon we must be
Title:  up and moving again. I remember to have fou't the Maquas, hereaways, in the
Title:  first war in which I ever drew blood from man; and we threw up a work of
Title:  blocks, to keep the ravenous varmints from handling our scalps. If my marks
Title:  do not fail me, we shall find the place a few rods further to our left.
Title:  
Title:  Without waiting for an assent, or, indeed, for any reply, the sturdy hunter
Title:  moved boldly into a dense thicket of young chestnuts, shoving aside the
Title:  branches of the exuberant shoots which nearly covered the ground, like a man
Title:  who expected, at each step, to discover some object he had formerly known.
Title:  The recollection of the scout did not deceive him. After penetrating through
Title:  the brush, matted as it was with briars, for a few hundred feet, he entered
Title:  an open space, that surrounded a low, green hillock, which was crowned by
Title:  the decayed blockhouse in question. This rude and neglected building was one
Title:  of those deserted works, which, having been thrown up on an emergency, had
Title:  been abandoned with the disappearance of danger, and was now quietly
Title:  crumbling in the solitude of the forest, neglected and nearly forgotten,
Title:  like the circumstances which had caused it to be reared. Such memorials of
Title:  the passage and struggles of man are yet frequent throughout the broad
Title:  barrier of wilderness which once separated the hostile provinces, and form a
Title:  species of ruins that are intimately associated with the recollections of
Title:  colonial history, and which are in appropriate keeping with the gloomy
Title:  character of the surrounding scenery.1 The roof of bark had long since
Title:  fallen, and mingled with the soil, but the huge logs of pine, which had been
Title:  hastily thrown together, still preserved their relative positions, though
Title:  one angle of the work had given way under the pressure, and threatened a
Title:  speedy downfall to the remainder of the rustic edifice. While Heyward and
Title:  his companions hesitated to approach a building so decayed, Hawkeye and the
Title:  Indians entered within the low walls, not only without fear, but with
Title:  obvious interest. While the former surveyed the ruins, both internally and
Title:  externally, with the curiosity of one whose recollections were reviving at
Title:  each moment, Chingachgook related to his son, in the language of the
Title:  Delawares, and with the pride of a conqueror, the brief history of the
Title:  skirmish which had been fought, in his youth, in that secluded spot. A
Title:  strain of melancholy, however, blended with his triumph, rendering his
Title:  voice, as usual, soft and musical.
Title:  
Title:  In the meantime, the sisters gladly dismounted, and prepared to enjoy their
Title:  halt in the coolness of the evening, and in a security which they believed
Title:  nothing but the beasts of the forest could invade.
Title:  
Title:  Would not our resting-place have been more retired, my worthy friend,
Title:  demanded the more vigilant Duncan, perceiving that the scout had already
Title:  finished his short survey, had we chosen a spot less known, and one more
Title:  rarely visited than this?
Title:  
Title:  Few live who know the blockhouse was ever raised, was the slow and musing
Title:  answer; 'tis not often that books are made, and narratives written of such a
Title:  scrimmage as was here fou't atween the Mohicans and the Mohawks, in a war of
Title:  their own waging. I was then a younker, and went out with the Delawares,
Title:  because I know'd they were a scandalized and wronged race. Forty days and
Title:  forty nights did the imps crave our blood around this pile of logs, which I
Title:  designed and partly reared, being, as you'll remember, no Indian myself, but
Title:  a man without a cross. The Delawares lent themselves to the work, and we
Title:  made it good, ten to twenty, until our numbers were nearly equal, and then
Title:  we sallied out upon the hounds, and not a man of them ever got back to tell
Title:  the fate of his party. Yes, yes; I was then young, and new to the sight of
Title:  blood; and not relishing the thought that creatures who had spirits like
Title:  myself should lay on the naked ground, to be torn asunder by beasts, or to
Title:  bleach in the rains, I buried the dead with my own hands, under that very
Title:  little hillock where you have placed yourselves; and no bad seat does it
Title:  make neither, though it be raised by the bones of mortal men.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward and the sisters arose, on the instant, from the grassy sepulcher;
Title:  nor could the two latter, notwithstanding the terrific scenes they had so
Title:  recently passed through, entirely suppress an emotion of natural horror,
Title:  when they found themselves in such familiar contact with the grave of the
Title:  dead Mohawks. The gray light, the gloomy little area of dark grass,
Title:  surrounded by its border of brush, beyond which the pines rose, in breathing
Title:  silence, apparently into the very clouds, and the deathlike stillness of the
Title:  vast forest, were all in unison to deepen such a sensation. They are gone,
Title:  and they are harmless, continued Hawkeye, waving his hand, with a melancholy
Title:  smile at their manifest alarm; they'll never shout the war-whoop nor strike
Title:  a blow with the tomahawk again! And of all those who aided in placing them
Title:  where they lie, Chingachgook and I only are living! The brothers and family
Title:  of the Mohican formed our war party; and you see before you all that are now
Title:  left of his race.
Title:  
Title:  The eyes of the listeners involuntarily sought the forms of the Indians,
Title:  with a compassionate interest in their desolate fortune. Their dark persons
Title:  were still to be seen within the shadows of the blockhouse, the son
Title:  listening to the relation of his father with that sort of intenseness which
Title:  would be created by a narrative that redounded so much to the honor of those
Title:  whose names he had long revered for their courage and savage virtues.
Title:  
Title:  I had thought the Delawares a pacific people, said Duncan, and that they
Title:  never waged war in person; trusting the defense of their hands to those very
Title:  Mohawks that you slew!
Title:  
Title:  'Tis true in part, returned the scout, and yet, at the bottom, 'tis a wicked
Title:  lie. Such a treaty was made in ages gone by, through the deviltries of the
Title:  Dutchers, who wished to disarm the natives that had the best right to the
Title:  country, where they had settled themselves. The Mohicans, though a part of
Title:  the same nation, having to deal with the English, never entered into the
Title:  silly bargain, but kept to their manhood; as in truth did the Delawares,
Title:  when their eyes were open to their folly. You see before you a chief of the
Title:  great Mohican Sagamores! Once his family could chase their deer over tracts
Title:  of country wider than that which belongs to the Albany Patteroon, without
Title:  crossing brook or hill that was not their on; but what is left of their
Title:  descendant? He may find his six feet of earth when God chooses, and keep it
Title:  in peace, perhaps, if he has a friend who will take the pains to sink his
Title:  head so low that the plowshares cannot reach it!
Title:  
Title:  Enough! said Heyward, apprehensive that the subject might lead to a
Title:  discussion that would interrupt the harmony so necessary to the preservation
Title:  of his fair companions; we have journeyed far, and few among us are blessed
Title:  with forms like that of yours, which seems to know neither fatigue nor
Title:  weakness.
Title:  
Title:  The sinews and bones of a man carry me through it all, said the hunter,
Title:  surveying his muscular limbs with a simplicity that betrayed the honest
Title:  pleasure the compliment afforded him; there are larger and heavier men to be
Title:  found in the settlements, but you might travel many days in a city before
Title:  you could meet one able to walk fifty miles without stopping to take breath,
Title:  or who has kept the hounds within hearing during a chase of hours. However,
Title:  as flesh and blood are not always the same, it is quite reasonable to
Title:  suppose that the gentle ones are willing to rest, after all they have seen
Title:  and done this day. Uncas, clear out the spring, while your father and I make
Title:  a cover for their tender heads of these chestnut shoots, and a bed of grass
Title:  and leaves.
Title:  
Title:  The dialogue ceased, while the hunter and his companions busied themselves
Title:  in preparations for the comfort and protection of those they guided. A
Title:  spring, which many long years before had induced the natives to select the
Title:  place for their temporary fortification, was soon cleared of leaves, and a
Title:  fountain of crystal gushed from the bed, diffusing its waters over the
Title:  verdant hillock. A corner of the building was then roofed in such a manner
Title:  as to exclude the heavy dew of the climate, and piles of sweet shrubs and
Title:  dried leaves were laid beneath it for the sisters to repose on.
Title:  
Title:  While the diligent woodsmen were employed in this manner, Cora and Alice
Title:  partook of that refreshment which duty required much more than inclination
Title:  prompted them to accept. They then retired within the walls, and first
Title:  offering up their thanksgivings for past mercies, and petitioning for a
Title:  continuance of the Divine favor throughout the coming night, they laid their
Title:  tender forms on the fragrant couch, and in spite of recollections and
Title:  forebodings, soon sank into those slumbers which nature so imperiously
Title:  demanded, and which were sweetened by hopes for the morrow. Duncan had
Title:  prepared himself to pass the night in watchfulness near them, just without
Title:  the ruin, but the scout, perceiving his intention, pointed toward
Title:  Chingachgook, as he coolly disposed his own person on the grass, and said:
Title:  
Title:  The eyes of a white man are too heavy and too blind for such a watch as
Title:  this! The Mohican will be our sentinel, therefore let us sleep.
Title:  
Title:  I proved myself a sluggard on my post during the past night, said Heyward,
Title:  and have less need of repose than you, who did more credit to the character
Title:  of a soldier. Let all the party seek their rest, then, while I hold the
Title:  guard.
Title:  
Title:  If we lay among the white tents of the Sixtieth, and in front of an enemy
Title:  like the French, I could not ask for a better watchman, returned the scout;
Title:  but in the darkness and among the signs of the wilderness your judgment
Title:  would be like the folly of a child, and your vigilance thrown away. Do then,
Title:  like Uncas and myself, sleep, and sleep in safety.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward perceived, in truth, that the younger Indian had thrown his form on
Title:  the side of the hillock while they were talking, like one who sought to make
Title:  the most of the time allotted to rest, and that his example had been
Title:  followed by David, whose voice literally clove to his jaws, with the fever
Title:  of his wound, heightened, as it was, by their toilsome march. Unwilling to
Title:  prolong a useless discussion, the young man affected to comply, by posting
Title:  his back against the logs of the blockhouse, in a half recumbent posture,
Title:  though resolutely determined, in his own mind, not to close an eye until he
Title:  had delivered his precious charge into the arms of Munro himself. Hawkeye,
Title:  believing he had prevailed, soon fell asleep, and a silence as deep as the
Title:  solitude in which they had found it, pervaded the retired spot.
Title:  
Title:  For many minutes Duncan succeeded in keeping his senses on the alert, and
Title:  alive to every moaning sound that arose from the forest. His vision became
Title:  more acute as the shades of evening settled on the place; and even after the
Title:  stars were glimmering above his head, he was able to distinguish the
Title:  recumbent forms of his companions, as they lay stretched on the grass, and
Title:  to note the person of Chingachgook, who sat upright and motionless as one of
Title:  the trees which formed the dark barrier on every side. He still heard the
Title:  gentle breathings of the sisters, who lay within a few feet of him, and not
Title:  a leaf was ruffled by the passing air of which his ear did not detect the
Title:  whispering sound. At length, however, the mournful notes of a whip-poor-will
Title:  became blended with the moanings of an owl; his heavy eyes occasionally
Title:  sought the bright rays of the stars, and he then fancied he saw them through
Title:  the fallen lids. At instants of momentary wakefulness he mistook a bush for
Title:  his associate sentinel; his head next sank upon his shoulder, which, in its
Title:  turn, sought the support of the ground; and, finally, his whole person
Title:  became relaxed and pliant, and the young man sank into a deep sleep,
Title:  dreaming that he was a knight of ancient chivalry, holding his midnight
Title:  vigils before the tent of a recaptured princess, whose favor he did not
Title:  despair of gaining, by such a proof of devotion and watchfulness.
Title:  
Title:  How long the tired Duncan lay in this insensible state he never knew
Title:  himself, but his slumbering visions had been long lost in total
Title:  forgetfulness, when he was awakened by a light tap on the shoulder. Aroused
Title:  by this signal, slight as it was, he sprang upon his feet with a confused
Title:  recollection of the self-imposed duty he had assumed with the commencement
Title:  of the night.
Title:  
Title:  Who comes? he demanded, feeling for his sword, at the place where it was
Title:  usually suspended. Speak! friend or enemy?
Title:  
Title:  Friend, replied the low voice of Chingachgook; who, pointing upward at the
Title:  luminary which was shedding its mild light through the opening in the trees,
Title:  directly in their bivouac, immediately added, in his rude English: Moon
Title:  comes and white man's fort far - far off; time to move, when sleep shuts
Title:  both eyes of the Frenchman!
Title:  
Title:  You say true! Call up your friends, and bridle the horses while I prepare my
Title:  own companions for the march!
Title:  
Title:  We are awake, Duncan, said the soft, silvery tones of Alice within the
Title:  building, and ready to travel very fast after so refreshing a sleep; but you
Title:  have watched through the tedious night in our behalf, after having endured
Title:  so much fatigue the livelong day!
Title:  
Title:  Say, rather, I would have watched, but my treacherous eyes betrayed me;
Title:  twice have I proved myself unfit for the trust I bear.
Title:  
Title:  Nay, Duncan, deny it not, interrupted the smiling Alice, issuing from the
Title:  shadows of the building into the light of the moon, in all the loveliness of
Title:  her freshened beauty; I know you to be a heedless one, when self is the
Title:  object of your care, and but too vigilant in favor of others. Can we not
Title:  tarry here a little longer while you find the rest you need? Cheerfully,
Title:  most cheerfully, will Cora and I keep the vigils, while you and all these
Title:  brave men endeavor to snatch a little sleep!
Title:  
Title:  If shame could cure me of my drowsiness, I should never close an eye again,
Title:  said the uneasy youth, gazing at the ingenuous countenance of Alice, where,
Title:  however, in its sweet solicitude, he read nothing to confirm his
Title:  half-awakened suspicion. It is but too true, that after leading you into
Title:  danger by my heedlessness, I have not even the merit of guarding your
Title:  pillows as should become a soldier.
Title:  
Title:  No one but Duncan himself should accuse Duncan of such a weakness. Go, then,
Title:  and sleep; believe me, neither of us, weak girls as we are, will betray our
Title:  watch.
Title:  
Title:  The young man was relieved from the awkwardness of making any further
Title:  protestations of his own demerits, by an exclamation from Chingachgook, and
Title:  the attitude of riveted attention assumed by his son.
Title:  
Title:  The Mohicans hear an enemy! whispered Hawkeye, who, by this time, in common
Title:  with the whole party, was awake and stirring. They scent danger in the wind!
Title:  
Title:  God forbid! exclaimed Heyward. Surely we have had enough of bloodshed!
Title:  
Title:  While he spoke, however, the young soldier seized his rifle, and advancing
Title:  toward the front, prepared to atone for his venial remissness, by freely
Title:  exposing his life in defense of those he attended.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis some creature of the forest prowling around us in quest of food, he
Title:  said, in a whisper, as soon as the low, and apparently distant sounds, which
Title:  had startled the Mohicans, reached his own ears.
Title:  
Title:  Hist! returned the attentive scout; 'tis man; even I can now tell his tread,
Title:  poor as my senses are when compared to an Indian's! That Scampering Huron
Title:  has fallen in with one of Montcalm's outlying parties, and they have struck
Title:  upon our trail. I shouldn't like, myself, to spill more human blood in this
Title:  spot, he added, looking around with anxiety in his features, at the dim
Title:  objects by which he was surrounded; but what must be, must! Lead the horses
Title:  into the blockhouse, Uncas; and, friends, do you follow to the same shelter.
Title:  Poor and old as it is, it offers a cover, and has rung with the crack of a
Title:  rifle afore to-night!
Title:  
Title:  He was instantly obeyed, the Mohicans leading the Narrangansetts within the
Title:  ruin, whither the whole party repaired with the most guarded silence.
Title:  
Title:  The sound of approaching footsteps were now too distinctly audible to leave
Title:  any doubts as to the nature of the interruption. They were soon mingled with
Title:  voices calling to each other in an Indian dialect, which the hunter, in a
Title:  whisper, affirmed to Heyward was the language of the Hurons. When the party
Title:  reached the point where the horses had entered the thicket which surrounded
Title:  the blockhouse, they were evidently at fault, having lost those marks which,
Title:  until that moment, had directed their pursuit.
Title:  
Title:  It would seem by the voices that twenty men were soon collected at that one
Title:  spot, mingling their different opinions and advice in noisy clamor.
Title:  
Title:  The knaves know our weakness, whispered Hawkeye, who stood by the side of
Title:  Heyward, in deep shade, looking through an opening in the logs, or they
Title:  wouldn't indulge their idleness in such a squaw's march. Listen to the
Title:  reptiles! each man among them seems to have two tongues, and but a single
Title:  leg.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, brave as he was in the combat, could not, in such a moment of
Title:  painful suspense, make any reply to the cool and characteristic remark of
Title:  the scout. He only grasped his rifle more firmly, and fastened his eyes upon
Title:  the narrow opening, through which he gazed upon the moonlight view with
Title:  increasing anxiety. The deeper tones of one who spoke as having authority
Title:  were next heard, amid a silence that denoted the respect with which his
Title:  orders, or rather advice, was received. After which, by the rustling of
Title:  leaves, and crackling of dried twigs, it was apparent the savages were
Title:  separating in pursuit of the lost trail. Fortunately for the pursued, the
Title:  light of the moon, while it shed a flood of mild luster upon the little area
Title:  around the ruin, was not sufficiently strong to penetrate the deep arches of
Title:  the forest, where the objects still lay in deceptive shadow. The search
Title:  proved fruitless; for so short and sudden had been the passage from the
Title:  faint path the travelers had journeyed into the thicket, that every trace of
Title:  their footsteps was lost in the obscurity of the woods.
Title:  
Title:  It was not long, however, before the restless savages were heard beating the
Title:  brush, and gradually approaching the inner edge of that dense border of
Title:  young chestnuts which encircled the little area.
Title:  
Title:  They are coming, muttered Heyward, endeavoring to thrust his rifle through
Title:  the chink in the logs; let us fire on their approach.
Title:  
Title:  Keep everything in the shade, returned the scout; the snapping of a flint,
Title:  or even the smell of a single karnel of the brimstone, would bring the
Title:  hungry varlets upon us in a body. Should it please God that we must give
Title:  battle for the scalps, trust to the experience of men who know the ways of
Title:  the savages, and who are not often backward when the war-whoop is howled.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan cast his eyes behind him, and saw that the trembling sisters were
Title:  cowering in the far corner of the building, while the Mohicans stood in the
Title:  shadow, like two upright posts, ready, and apparently willing, to strike
Title:  when the blow should be needed. Curbing his impatience, he again looked out
Title:  upon the area, and awaited the result in silence. At that instant the
Title:  thicket opened, and a tall and armed Huron advanced a few paces into the
Title:  open space. As he gazed upon the silent blockhouse, the moon fell upon his
Title:  swarthy countenance, and betrayed its surprise and curiosity. He made the
Title:  exclamation which usually accompanies the former emotion in an Indian, and,
Title:  calling in a low voice, soon drew a companion to his side.
Title:  
Title:  These children of the woods stood together for several moments pointing at
Title:  the crumbling edifice, and conversing in the unintelligible language of
Title:  their tribe. They then approached, though with slow and cautious steps,
Title:  pausing every instant to look at the building, like startled deer whose
Title:  curiosity struggled powerfully with their awakened apprehensions for the
Title:  mastery. The foot of one of them suddenly rested on the mound, and he
Title:  stopped to examine its nature. At this moment, Heyward observed that the
Title:  scout loosened his knife in its sheath, and lowered the muzzle of his rifle.
Title:  Imitating these movements, the young man prepared himself for the struggle
Title:  which now seemed inevitable.
Title:  
Title:  The savages were so near, that the least motion in one of the horses, or
Title:  even a breath louder than common, would have betrayed the fugitives. But in
Title:  discovering the character of the mound, the attention of the Hurons appeared
Title:  directed to a different object. They spoke together, and the sounds of their
Title:  voices were low and solemn, as if influenced by a reverence that was deeply
Title:  blended with awe. Then they drew warily back, keeping their eyes riveted on
Title:  the ruin, as if they expected to see the apparitions of the dead issue from
Title:  its silent walls, until, having reached the boundary of the area, they moved
Title:  slowly into the thicket and disappeared.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye dropped the breech of his rifle to the earth, and drawing a long,
Title:  free breath, exclaimed, in an audible whisper:
Title:  
Title:  Ay! they respect the dead, and it has this time saved their own lives, and,
Title:  it may be, the lives of better men too.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward lent his attention for a single moment to his companion, but without
Title:  replying, he again turned toward those who just then interested him more. He
Title:  heard the two Hurons leave the bushes, and it was soon plain that all the
Title:  pursuers were gathered about them, in deep attention to their report. After
Title:  a few minutes of earnest and solemn dialogue, altogether different from the
Title:  noisy clamor with which they had first collected about the spot, the sounds
Title:  grew fainter and more distant, and finally were lost in the depths of the
Title:  forest.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye waited until a signal from the listening Chingachgook assured him
Title:  that every sound from the retiring party was completely swallowed by the
Title:  distance, when he motioned to Heyward to lead forth the horses, and to
Title:  assist the sisters into their saddles. The instant this was done they issued
Title:  through the broken gateway, and stealing out by a direction opposite to the
Title:  one by which they entered, they quitted the spot, the sisters casting
Title:  furtive glances at the silent, grave and crumbling ruin, as they left the
Title:  soft light of the moon, to bury themselves in the gloom of the woods.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 Some years since, the writer was shooting in the vicinity of the ruins of
Title:  Fort Oswego, which stands on the shoes of Lake Ontario. His game was deer,
Title:  and his chase a forest that stretched, with little interruption, fifty miles
Title:  inland. Unexpectedly he came upon six or eight ladders lying in the woods
Title:  within a short distance of each other. They were rudely made and much
Title:  decayed. Wondering what could have assembled so many of these instruments in
Title:  such a place, he sought an old man who resided near for the explanation.
Title:  
Title:  During the war of 1776 Fort Oswego was held by the British. An expedition
Title:  had been sent two hundred miles through the wilderness to surprise the fort.
Title:  It appears that the Americans, on reaching the spot named, which was within
Title:  a mile or two of the fort, first learned that they were expected, and in
Title:  great danger of being cut off. They threw away their scaling ladders, and
Title:  made a rapid retreat. These ladders had lain unmolested thirty years, in the
Title:  spot where they had thus been cast.
Title:  
Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 14
Title:  
Title:       Guard: Qui est l?
Title:       Puc: Paisans, pauvres gens de France.
Title:  
Title:                                                           KING HENRY VI
Title:  
Title:  During the rapid movement from the blockhouse, and until the party was
Title:  deeply buried in the forest, each individual was too much interested in the
Title:  escape to hazard a word even in whispers. The scout resumed his post in
Title:  advance, though his steps, after he had thrown a safe distance between
Title:  himself and his enemies, were more deliberate than in their previous march,
Title:  in consequence of his utter ignorance of the localities of the surrounding
Title:  woods. More than once he halted to consult with his confederates, the
Title:  Mohicans, pointing upward at the moon, and examining the barks of the trees
Title:  with care. In these brief pauses, Heyward and the sisters listened, with
Title:  senses rendered doubly acute by the danger, to detect any symptoms which
Title:  might announce the proximity of their foes. At such moments, it seemed as if
Title:  a vast range of country lay buried in eternal sleep; not the least sound
Title:  arising from the forest, unless it was the distant and scarcely audible
Title:  rippling of a water-course. Birds, beasts, and man, appeared to slumber
Title:  alike, if, indeed, any of the latter were to be found in that wide tract of
Title:  wilderness. But the sounds of the rivulet, feeble and murmuring as they
Title:  were, relieved the guides at once from no trifling embarrassment, and toward
Title:  it they immediately held their way.
Title:  
Title:  When the banks of the little stream were gained, Hawkeye made another halt;
Title:  and taking the moccasins from his feet, he invited Heyward and Gamut to
Title:  follow his example. He then entered the water, and for near an hour they
Title:  traveled in the bed of the brook, leaving no trail. The moon had already
Title:  sunk into an immense pile of black clouds, which lay impending above the
Title:  western horizon, when they issued from the low and devious water-course to
Title:  rise again to the light and level of the sandy but wooded plain. Here the
Title:  scout seemed to be once more at home, for he held on this way with the
Title:  certainty and diligence of a man who moved in the security of his own
Title:  knowledge. The path soon became more uneven, and the travelers could plainly
Title:  perceive that the mountains drew nigher to them on each hand, and that they
Title:  were, in truth, about entering one of their gorges. Suddenly, Hawkeye made a
Title:  pause, and, waiting until he was joined by the whole party, he spoke, though
Title:  in tones so low and cautious, that they added to the solemnity of his words,
Title:  in the quiet and darkness of the place.
Title:  
Title:  It is easy to know the pathways, and to find the licks and water-courses of
Title:  the wilderness, he said; but who that saw this spot could venture to say,
Title:  that a mighty army was at rest among yonder silent trees and barren
Title:  mountains?
Title:  
Title:  We are, then, at no great distance from William Henry? said Heyward,
Title:  advancing nigher to the scout.
Title:  
Title:  It is yet a long and weary path, and when and where to strike it is now our
Title:  greatest difficulty. See, he said, pointing through the trees toward a spot
Title:  where a little basin of water reflected the stars from its placid bosom,
Title:  here is the bloody pond'; and I am on ground that I have not only often
Title:  traveled, but over which I have fou't the enemy, from the rising to the
Title:  setting sun.
Title:  
Title:  Ha! that sheet of dull and dreary water, then, is the sepulcher of the brave
Title:  men who fell in the contest. I have heard it named, but never have I stood
Title:  on its banks before.
Title:  
Title:  Three battles did we make with the Dutch-Frenchman1 in a day, continued
Title:  Hawkeye, pursuing the train of his own thoughts, rather than replying to the
Title:  remark of Duncan. He met us hard by, in our outward march to ambush his
Title:  advance, and scattered us, like driven deer, through the defile, to the
Title:  shores of Horican. Then we rallied behind our fallen trees, and made head
Title:  against him, under Sir William - who was made Sir William for that very
Title:  deed; and well did we pay him for the disgrace of the morning! Hundreds of
Title:  Frenchmen saw the sun that day for the last time; and even their leader,
Title:  Dieskau himself, fell into our hands, so cut and torn with the lead, that he
Title:  has gone back to his own country, unfit for further acts in war.
Title:  
Title:  'Twas a noble repulse! exclaimed Heyward, in the heat of his youthful ardor;
Title:  the fame of it reached us early, in our southern army.
Title:  
Title:  Ay! but it did not end there. I was sent by Major Effingham, at Sir
Title:  William's own bidding, to outflank the French, and carry the tidings of
Title:  their disaster across the portage, to the fort on the Hudson. Just hereaway,
Title:  where you see the trees rise into a mountain swell, I met a party coming
Title:  down to our aid, and I led them where the enemy were taking their meal,
Title:  little dreaming that they had not finished the bloody work of the day.
Title:  
Title:  And you surprised them?
Title:  
Title:  If death can be a surprise to men who are thinking only of the cravings of
Title:  their appetites. We gave them but little breathing time, for they had borne
Title:  hard upon us in the fight of the morning, and there were few in our party
Title:  who had not lost friend or relative by their hands.
Title:  
Title:  When all was over, the dead, and some say the dying, were cast into that
Title:  little pond. These eyes have seen its waters colored with blood, as natural
Title:  water never yet flowed from the bowels of the 'arth.
Title:  
Title:  It was a convenient, and, I trust, will prove a peaceful grave for a
Title:  soldier. You have then seen much service on this frontier?
Title:  
Title:  Ay! said the scout, erecting his tall person with an air of military pride;
Title:  there are not many echoes among these hills that haven't rung with the crack
Title:  of my rifle, nor is there the space of a square mile atwixt Horican and the
Title:  river, that killdeer hasn't dropped a living body on, be it an enemy or be
Title:  it a brute beast. As for the grave there being as quiet as you mention, it
Title:  is another matter. There are them in the camp who say and think, man, to lie
Title:  still, should not be buried while the breath is in the body; and certain it
Title:  is that in the hurry of that evening, the doctors had but little time to say
Title:  who was living and who was dead. Hist! see you nothing walking on the shore
Title:  of the pond?
Title:  
Title:  'Tis not probable that any are as houseless as ourselves in this dreary
Title:  forest.
Title:  
Title:  Such as he may care but little for house or shelter, and night dew can never
Title:  wet a body that passes its days in the water, returned the scout, grasping
Title:  the shoulder of Heyward with such convulsive strength as to make the young
Title:  soldier painfully sensible how much superstitious terror had got the mastery
Title:  of a man usually so dauntless.
Title:  
Title:  By heaven, there is a human form, and it approaches! Stand to your arms, my
Title:  friends; for we know not whom we encounter.
Title:  
Title:  Qui vive? demanded a stern, quick voice, which sounded like a challenge from
Title:  another world, issuing out of that solitary and solemn place.
Title:  
Title:  What says it? whispered the scout; it speaks neither Indian nor English.
Title:  
Title:  Qui vive? repeated the same voice, which was quickly followed by the
Title:  rattling of arms, and a menacing attitude.
Title:  
Title:  France! cried Heyward, advancing from the shadow of the trees to the shore
Title:  of the pond, within a few yards of the sentinel.
Title:  
Title:  D'o venez-vous - o allez-vous, d'aussi bonne heure? demanded the
Title:  grenadier, in the language and with the accent of a man from old France.
Title:  
Title:  Je viens de la dcouverte, et je vais me coucher.
Title:  
Title:  Etes-vous officier du roi?
Title:  
Title:  Sans doute, mon camarade; me prends-tu pour un provincial! Je suis capitaine
Title:  de chasseurs (Heyward well knew that the other was of a regiment in the
Title:  line); j'ai ici, avec moi, les filles du commandant de la fortification.
Title:  Aha! tu en as entendu parler! je les ai fait prisonnires prs de l'autre
Title:  fort, et je les conduis au gnral.
Title:  
Title:  Ma foi! mesdames; j'en suis fch pour vous, exlaimed the young soldier,
Title:  touching his cap with grace; mais - fortune de guerre! vous trouverez notre
Title:  gnral un brave homme, et bien poli avec les dames.
Title:  
Title:  C'est le caractre des gens de guerre, said Cora, with admirable
Title:  self-possession. Adieu, mon ami; je vous souhaiterais un devoir plus
Title:  agrable  remplir.
Title:  
Title:  The soldier made a low and humble acknowledgment for her civility; and
Title:  Heyward adding a Bonne nuit, mon camarade, they moved deliberately forward,
Title:  leaving the sentinel pacing the banks of the silent pond, little suspecting
Title:  an enemy of so much effrontery, and humming to himself those words which
Title:  were recalled to his mind by the sight of women, and, perhaps, by
Title:  recollections of his own distant and beautiful France:
Title:  
Title:       Vive le vin, vive l'amour, &c., &c.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis well you understood the knave! whispered the scout, when they had
Title:  gained a little distance from the place, and letting his rifle fall into the
Title:  hollow of his arm again; I soon saw that he was one of them uneasy
Title:  Frenchers; and well for him it was that his speech was friendly and his
Title:  wishes kind, or a place might have been found for his bones among those of
Title:  his countrymen.
Title:  
Title:  He was interrupted by a long and heavy groan which arose from the little
Title:  basin, as though, in truth, the spirits of the departed lingered about their
Title:  watery sepulcher.
Title:  
Title:  Surely it was of flesh, continued the scout; no spirit could handle its arms
Title:  so steadily.
Title:  
Title:  It was of flesh; but whether the poor fellow still belongs to this world may
Title:  well be doubted, said Heyward, glancing his eyes around him, and missing
Title:  Chingachgook from their little band. Another groan more faint than the
Title:  former was succeeded by a heavy and sullen plunge into the water, and all
Title:  was still again as if the borders of the dreary pool had never been awakened
Title:  from the silence of creation. While they yet hesitated in uncertainty, the
Title:  form of the Indian was seen gliding out of the thicket. As the chief
Title:  rejoined them, with one hand he attached the reeking scalp of the
Title:  unfortunate young Frenchman to his girdle, and with the other he replaced
Title:  the knife and tomahawk that had drunk his blood. He then took his wonted
Title:  station, with the air of a man who believed he had done a deed of merit.
Title:  
Title:  The scout dropped one end of his rifle to the earth, and leaning his hands
Title:  on the other, he stood musing in profound silence. Then, shaking his head in
Title:  a mournful manner, he muttered:
Title:  
Title:  'Twould have been a cruel and an unhuman act for a white-skin; but 'tis the
Title:  gift and natur' of an Indian, and I suppose it should not be denied. I could
Title:  wish, though it had befallen an accursed Mingo, rather than that gay young
Title:  boy from the old countries.
Title:  
Title:  Enough! said Heyward, apprehensive the unconscious sisters might comprehend
Title:  the nature of the detention, and conquering his disgust by a train of
Title:  reflections very much like that of the hunter; 'tis done; and though better
Title:  it were left undone, cannot be amended. You see, we are, too obviously
Title:  within the sentinels of the enemy; what course do you propose to follow?
Title:  
Title:  Yes, said Hawkeye, rousing himself again; 'tis as you say, too late to
Title:  harbor further thoughts about it. Ay, the French have gathered around the
Title:  fort in good earnest and we have a delicate needle to thread in passing
Title:  them.
Title:  
Title:  And but little time to do it in, added Heyward, glancing his eyes upwards,
Title:  toward the bank of vapor that concealed the setting moon.
Title:  
Title:  And little time to do it in! repeated the scout. The thing may be done in
Title:  two fashions, by the help of Providence, without which it may not be done at
Title:  all.
Title:  
Title:  Name them quickly for time presses.
Title:  
Title:  One would be to dismount the gentle ones, and let their beasts range the
Title:  plain, by sending the Mohicans in front, we might then cut a lane through
Title:  their sentries, and enter the fort over the dead bodies.
Title:  
Title:  It will not do - it will not do! interrupted the generous Heyward; a soldier
Title:  might force his way in this manner, but never with such a convoy.
Title:  
Title:  'Twould be, indeed, a bloody path for such tender feet to wade in, returned
Title:  the equally reluctant scout; but I thought it befitting my manhood to name
Title:  it. We must, then, turn in our trail and get without the line of their
Title:  lookouts, when we will bend short to the west, and enter the mountains;
Title:  where I can hide you, so that all the devil's hounds in Montcalm's pay would
Title:  be thrown off the scent for months to come.
Title:  
Title:  Let it be done, and that instantly.
Title:  
Title:  Further words were unnecessary; for Hawkeye, merely uttering the mandate to
Title:  follow, moved along the route by which they had just entered their present
Title:  critical and even dangerous situation. Their progress, like their late
Title:  dialogue, was guarded, and without noise; for none knew at what moment a
Title:  passing patrol, or a crouching picket of the enemy, might rise upon their
Title:  path. As they held their silent way along the margin of the pond, again
Title:  Heyward and the scout stole furtive glances at its appalling dreariness.
Title:  They looked in vain for the form they had so recently seen stalking along in
Title:  silent shores, while a low and regular wash of the little waves, by
Title:  announcing that the waters were not yet subsided, furnished a frightful
Title:  memorial of the deed of blood they had just witnessed. Like all that passing
Title:  and gloomy scene, the low basin, however, quickly melted in the darkness,
Title:  and became blended with the mass of black objects in the rear of the
Title:  travelers.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye soon deviated from the line of their retreat, and striking off
Title:  towards the mountains which form the western boundary of the narrow plain,
Title:  he led his followers, with swift steps, deep within the shadows that were
Title:  cast from their high and broken summits. The route was now painful; lying
Title:  over ground ragged with rocks, and intersected with ravines, and their
Title:  progress proportionately slow. Bleak and black hills lay on every side of
Title:  them, compensating in some degree for the additional toil of the march by
Title:  the sense of security they imparted. At length the party began slowly to
Title:  rise a steep and rugged ascent, by a path that cruiously wound among rocks
Title:  and trees, avoiding the one and supported by the other, in a manner that
Title:  showed it had been devised by men long practised in the arts of the
Title:  wilderness. As they gradually rose from the level of the valleys, the thick
Title:  darkness which usually precedes the approach of day began to disperse, and
Title:  objects were seen in the plain and palpable colors with which they had been
Title:  gifted by nature. When they issued from the stunted woods which clung to the
Title:  barren sides of the mountain, upon a flat and mossy rock that formed its
Title:  summit, they met the morning, as it came blushing above the green pines of a
Title:  hill that lay on the opposite side of the valley of the Horican.
Title:  
Title:  The scout now told the sisters to dismount; and taking the bridles from the
Title:  mouths, and the saddles off the backs of the jaded beasts, he turned them
Title:  loose, to glean a scanty subsistence among the shrubs and meager herbage of
Title:  that elevated region.
Title:  
Title:  Go, he said, and seek your food where natur' gives it to you; and beware
Title:  that you become not food to ravenous wolves yourselves, among these hills.
Title:  
Title:  Have we no further need of them? demanded Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  See, and judge with your own eyes, said the scout, advancing toward the
Title:  eastern brow of the mountain, whither he beckoned for the whole party to
Title:  follow; if it was as easy to look into the heart of man as it is to spy out
Title:  the nakedness of Montcalm's camp from this spot, hypocrites would grow
Title:  scarce, and the cunning of a Mingo might prove a losing game, compared to
Title:  the honesty of a Delaware.
Title:  
Title:  When the travelers reached the verge of the precipices they saw, at a
Title:  glance, the truth of the scout's declaration, and the admirable foresight
Title:  with which he had led them to their commanding station.
Title:  
Title:  The mountain on which they stood, elevated perhaps a thousand feet in the
Title:  air, was a high cone that rose a little in advance of that range which
Title:  stretches for miles along the western shores of the lake, until meeting its
Title:  sisters miles beyond the water, it ran off toward the Canadas, in confused
Title:  and broken masses of rock, thinly sprinkled with evergreens. Immediately at
Title:  the feet of the party, the southern shore of the Horican swept in a broad
Title:  semicircle from mountain to mountain, marking a wide strand, that soon rose
Title:  into an uneven and somewhat elevated plain. To the north stretched the
Title:  limpid, and, as it appeared from that dizzy height, the narrow sheet of the
Title:  holy lake, indented with numberless bays, embellished by fantastic
Title:  headlands, and dotted with countless islands. At the distance of a few
Title:  leagues, the bed of the water became lost among mountains, or was wrapped in
Title:  the masses of vapor that came slowly rolling along their bosom, before a
Title:  light morning air. But a narrow opening between the crests of the hills
Title:  pointed out the passage by which they found their way still further north,
Title:  to spread their pure and ample sheets again, before pouring out their
Title:  tribute into the distant Champlain. To the shout stretched the defile, or
Title:  rather broken plain, so often mentioned. For several miles in this
Title:  direction, the mountains appeared reluctant to yield their dominion, but
Title:  within reach of the eye they diverged, and finally melted into the level and
Title:  sandy lands, across which we have accompanied our adventurers in their
Title:  double journey. Along both ranges of hills, which bounded the opposite sides
Title:  of the lake and valley, clouds of light vapor were rising in spiral wreaths
Title:  from the uninhabited woods, looking like the smoke of hidden cottages; or
Title:  rolled lazily down the declivities, to mingle with the fogs of the lower
Title:  land. A single, solitary, snow-white cloud floated above the valley, and
Title:  marked the spot beneath which lay the silent pool of the bloody pond.
Title:  
Title:  Directly on the shore of the lake, and nearer to its western than to its
Title:  eastern margin, lay the extensive earthen ramparts and low buildings of
Title:  William Henry. Two of the sweeping bastions appeared to rest on the water
Title:  which washed their bases, while a deep ditch and extensive morasses guarded
Title:  its other sides and angles. The land had been cleared of wood for a
Title:  reasonable distance around the work, but every other part of the scene lay
Title:  in the green livery of nature, except where the limpid water mellowed the
Title:  view, or the bold rocks thrust their black and naked heads above the
Title:  undulating outline of the mountain ranges. In its front might be seen the
Title:  scattered sentinels, who held a weary watch against their numerous foes; and
Title:  within the walls themselves, the travelers looked down upon men still drowsy
Title:  with a night of vigilance. Toward the southeast, but in immediate contact
Title:  with the fort, was an entrenched camp, posted on a rocky eminence, that
Title:  would have been far more eligible for the work itself, in which Hawkeye
Title:  pointed out the presence of those auxiliary regiments that had so recently
Title:  left the Hudson in their company. From the woods, a little further to the
Title:  south, rose numerous dark and lurid smokes, that were easily to be
Title:  distinguished from the purer exhalations of the springs, and which the scout
Title:  also showed to Heyward, as evidences that the enemy lay in force in that
Title:  direction.
Title:  
Title:  But the spectacle which most concerned the young soldier was on the western
Title:  bank of the lake, though quite near to its southern termination. On a strip
Title:  of land, which appeared from his stand too narrow to contain such an army,
Title:  but which, in truth, extended many hundreds of yards from the shores of the
Title:  Horican to the base of the mountain, were to be seen the white tents and
Title:  military engines of an encampment of ten thousand men. Batteries were
Title:  already thrown up in their front, and even while the spectators above them
Title:  were looking down, with such different emotions, on a scene which lay like a
Title:  map beneath their feet, the roar of artillery rose from the valley, and
Title:  passed off in thundering echoes along the eastern hills.
Title:  
Title:  Morning is just touching them below, said the deliberate and musing scout,
Title:  and the watchers have a mind to wake up the sleepers by the sound of cannon.
Title:  We are a few hours too late! Montcalm has already filled the woods with his
Title:  accursed Iroquois.
Title:  
Title:  The place is, indeed, invested, returned Duncan; but is there no expedient
Title:  by which we may enter? capture in the works would be far preferable to
Title:  falling again into the hands of roving Indians.
Title:  
Title:  See! exclaimed the scout, unconsciously directing the attention of Cora to
Title:  the quarters of her own father, how that shot has made the stones fly from
Title:  the side of the commandant's house! Ay! these Frenchers will pull it to
Title:  pieces faster than it was put together, solid and thick though it be!
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, I sicken at the sight of danger that I cannot share, said the
Title:  undaunted but anxious daughter. Let us go to Montcalm, and demand admission:
Title:  he dare not deny a child the boon.
Title:  
Title:  You would scarce find the tent of the Frenchman with the hair on your head;
Title:  said the blunt scout. If I had but one of the thousand boats which lie empty
Title:  along that shore, it might be done! Ha! here will soon be an end of the
Title:  firing, for yonder comes a fog that will turn day to night, and make an
Title:  Indian arrow more dangerous than a molded cannon. Now, if you are equal to
Title:  the work, and will follow, I will make a push; for I long to get down into
Title:  that camp, if it be only to scatter some Mingo dogs that I see lurking in
Title:  the skirts of yonder thicket of birch.
Title:  
Title:  We are equal, said Cora, firmly; on such an errand we will follow to any
Title:  danger.
Title:  
Title:  The scout turned to her with a smile of honest and cordial approbation, as
Title:  he answered:
Title:  
Title:  I would I had a thousand men, of brawny limbs and quick eyes, that feared
Title:  death as little as you! I'd send them jabbering Frenchers back into their
Title:  den again, afore the week was ended, howling like so many fettered hounds or
Title:  hungry wolves. But, sir, he added, turning from her to the rest of the
Title:  party, the fog comes rolling down so fast, we shall have but just the time
Title:  to meet it on the plain, and use it as a cover. Remember, if any accident
Title:  should befall me, to keep the air blowing on your left cheeks - or, rather,
Title:  follow the Mohicans; they'd scent their way, be it in day or be it at night.
Title:  
Title:  He then waved his hand for them to follow, and threw himself down the steep
Title:  declivity, with free, but careful footsteps. Heyward assisted the sisters to
Title:  descend, and in a few minutes they were all far down a mountain whose sides
Title:  they had climbed with so much toil and pain.
Title:  
Title:  The direction taken by Hawkeye soon brought the travelers to the level of
Title:  the plain, nearly opposite to a sally-port in the western curtain of the
Title:  fort, which lay itself at the distance of about half a mile from the point
Title:  where he halted to allow Duncan to come up with his charge. In their
Title:  eagerness, and favored by the nature of the ground, they had anticipated the
Title:  fog, which was rolling heavily down the lake, and it became necessary to
Title:  pause, until the mists had wrapped the camp of the enemy in their fleecy
Title:  mantle. The Mohicans profited by the delay, to steal out of the woods, and
Title:  to make a survey of surrounding objects. They were followed at a little
Title:  distance by the scout, with a view to profit early by their report, and to
Title:  obtain some faint knowledge for himself of the more immediate localities.
Title:  
Title:  In a very few moments he returned, his face reddened with vexation, while he
Title:  muttered his disappointment in words of no very gentle import.
Title:  
Title:  Here has the cunning Frenchman been posting a picket directly in our path,
Title:  he said; red-skins and whites; and we shall be as likely to fall into their
Title:  midst as to pass them in the fog!
Title:  
Title:  Cannot we make a circuit to avoid the danger, asked Heyward, and come into
Title:  our path again when it is passed?
Title:  
Title:  Who that once bends from the line of his march in a fog can tell when or how
Title:  to find it again! The mists of Horican are not like the curls from a
Title:  peace-pipe, or the smoke which settles above a mosquito fire.
Title:  
Title:  He was yet speaking, when a crashing sound was heard, and a cannon-ball
Title:  entered the thicket, striking the body of a sapling, and rebounding to the
Title:  earth, its force being much expended by previous resistance. The Indians
Title:  followed instantly like busy attendants on the terrible messenger, and Uncas
Title:  commenced speaking earnestly and with much action, in the Delaware tongue.
Title:  
Title:  It may be so, lad, muttered the scout, when he had ended; for desperate
Title:  fevers are not to be treated like a toothache. Come, then, the fog is
Title:  shutting in.
Title:  
Title:  Stop! cried Heyward; first explain your expectations.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis soon done, and a small hope it is; but it is better than nothing. This
Title:  shot that you see, added the scout, kicking the harmless iron with his foot,
Title:  has plowed the 'arth in its road from the fort, and we shall hunt for the
Title:  furrow it has made, when all other signs may fail. No more words, but
Title:  follow, or the fog may leave us in the middle of our path, a mark for both
Title:  armies to shoot at.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward perceiving that, in fact, a crisis had arrived, when acts were more
Title:  required than words, placed himself between the sisters, and drew them
Title:  swiftly forward, keeping the dim figure of their leader in his eye. It was
Title:  soon apparent that Hawkeye had not magnified the power of the fog, for
Title:  before they had proceeded twenty yards, it was difficult for the different
Title:  individuals of the party to distinguish each other in the vapor.
Title:  
Title:  They had made their little circuit to the left, and were already inclining
Title:  again toward the right, having, as Heyward thought, got over nearly half the
Title:  distance to the friendly works, when his ears were saluted with the fierce
Title:  summons, apparently within twenty feet of them, of:
Title:  
Title:  Qui va la?
Title:  
Title:  Push on! whispered the scout, once more bending to the left.
Title:  
Title:  Push on! repeated Heyward; when the summons was renewed by a dozen voices,
Title:  each of which seemed charged with menace.
Title:  
Title:  C'est moi, cried Duncan, dragging rather than leading those he supported
Title:  swiftly onward.
Title:  
Title:  Bete! - qui? - moi!
Title:  
Title:  Ami de la France.
Title:  
Title:  Tu m'as plus l'air d'un ennemi de la France; arrete ou pardieu je te ferai
Title:  ami du diable. Non! feu, camarades, feu!
Title:  
Title:  The order was instantly obeyed, and the fog was stirred by the explosion of
Title:  fifty muskets. Happily, the aim was bad, and the bullets cut the air in a
Title:  direction a little different from that taken by the fugitives; though still
Title:  so nigh them, that to the unpractised ears of David and the two females, it
Title:  appeared as if they whistled within a few inches of the organs. The outcry
Title:  was renewed, and the order, not only to fire again, but to pursue, was too
Title:  plainly audible. When Heyward briefly explained the meaning of the words
Title:  they heard, Hawkeye halted and spoke with quick decision and great firmness.
Title:  
Title:  Let us deliver our fire, he said; they will believe it a sortie, and give
Title:  way, or they will wait for reinforcements.
Title:  
Title:  The scheme was well conceived, but failed in its effects. The instant the
Title:  French heard the pieces, it seemed as if the plain was alive with men,
Title:  muskets rattling along its whole extent, from the shores of the lake to the
Title:  furthest boundary of the woods.
Title:  
Title:  We shall draw their entire army upon us, and bring on a general assault,
Title:  said Duncan: lead on, my friend, for your own life and ours.
Title:  
Title:  The scout seemed willing to comply; but, in the hurry of the moment, and in
Title:  the change of position, he had lost the direction. In vain he turned either
Title:  cheek toward the light air; they felt equally cool. In this dilemma, Uncas
Title:  lighted on the furrow of the cannon ball, where it had cut the ground in
Title:  three adjacent ant-hills.
Title:  
Title:  Give me the range! said Hawkeye, bending to catch a glimpse of the
Title:  direction, and then instantly moving onward.
Title:  
Title:  Cries, oaths, voices calling to each other, and the reports of muskets, were
Title:  now quick and incessant, and, apparently, on every side of them. Suddenly a
Title:  strong glare of light flashed across the scene, the fog rolled upward in
Title:  thick wreaths, and several cannons belched across the plain, and the roar
Title:  was thrown heavily back from the bellowing echoes of the mountain.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis from the fort! exclaimed Hawkeye, turning short on his tracks; and we,
Title:  like stricken fools, were rushing to the woods, under the very knives of the
Title:  Maquas.
Title:  
Title:  The instant their mistake was rectified, the whole party retraced the error
Title:  with the utmost diligence. Duncan willingly relinquished the support of Cora
Title:  to the arm of Uncas and Cora as readily accepted the welcome assistance.
Title:  Men, hot and angry in pursuit, were evidently on their footsteps, and each
Title:  instant threatened their capture, if not their destruction.
Title:  
Title:  Point de quartier aux coquins! cried an eager pursuer, who seemed to direct
Title:  the operations of the enemy.
Title:  
Title:  Stand firm, and be ready, my gallant Sixtieths! suddenly exclaimed a voice
Title:  above them; wait to see the enemy, fire low and sweep the glacis.
Title:  
Title:  Father! father! exclaimed a piercing cry from out the mist: it is I! Alice!
Title:  thy own Elsie! Spare, oh! save your daughters!
Title:  
Title:  Hold! shouted the former speaker, in the awful tones of parental agony, the
Title:  sound reaching even to the woods, and rolling back in solemn echo. 'Tis she!
Title:  God has restored me to my children! Throw open the sally-port; to the field,
Title:  Sixtieths, to the field; pull not a trigger, lest ye kill my lambs! Drive
Title:  off these dogs of France with your steel.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan heard the grating of the rusty hinges, and darting to the spot,
Title:  directed by the sound, he met a long line of dark red warriors, passing
Title:  swiftly toward the glacis. He knew them for his own battalion of the Royal
Title:  Americans, and flying to their head, soon swept every trace of his pursuers
Title:  from before the works.
Title:  
Title:  For an instant, Cora and Alice had stood trembling and bewildered by this
Title:  unexpected desertion; but before either had leisure for speech, or even
Title:  thought, an officer of gigantic frame, whose locks were bleached with years
Title:  and service, but whose air of military grandeur had been rather softened
Title:  than destroyed by time, rushed out of the body of mist, and folded them to
Title:  his bosom, while large scalding tears rolled down his pale and wrinkled
Title:  cheeks, and he exclaimed, in the peculiar accent of Scotland:
Title:  
Title:  For this I thank thee, Lord! Let danger come as it will, thy servant is now
Title:  prepared!
Title:

Title:  
Title:  1 Baron Dieskau, a German, in the service of France. A few years previously
Title:  to the period of the tale, this officer was defeated by Sir William Johnson,
Title:  of Johnstown, New York, on the shores of Lake George.
