Title:  
Title:  Chapter 15
Title:  
Title:       Then go we in, to know his embassy;
Title:       Which I could, with ready guess, declare,
Title:       Before the Frenchmen speak a word of it.
Title:  
Title:                                                            KING HENRY V
Title:  
Title:  A few succeeding days were passed amid the privations, the uproar, and the
Title:  dangers of the siege, which was vigorously pressed by a power, against whose
Title:  approaches Munro possessed no competent means of resistance. It appeared as
Title:  if Webb, with his army, which lay slumbering on the banks of the Hudson, had
Title:  utterly forgotten the strait to which his countrymen were reduced. Montcalm
Title:  had filled the woods of the portage with his savages, every yell and whoop
Title:  from whom rang through the British encampment, chilling the hearts of men
Title:  who were already but too much disposed to magnify the danger.
Title:  
Title:  Not so, however, with the besieged. Animated by the words, and stimulated by
Title:  the examples of their leaders, they had found their courage, and maintained
Title:  their ancient reputation, with a zeal that did justice to the stern
Title:  character of their commander. As if satisfied with the toil of marching
Title:  through the wilderness to encounter his enemy, the French general, though of
Title:  approved skill, had neglected to seize the adjacent mountains; whence the
Title:  besieged might have been exterminated with impunity, and which, in the more
Title:  modern warfare of the country, would not have been neglected for a single
Title:  hour. This sort of contempt for eminences, or rather dread of the labor of
Title:  ascending them, might have been termed the besetting weakness of the warfare
Title:  of the period. It originated in the simplicity of the Indian contests, in
Title:  which, from the nature of the combats, and the density of the forests,
Title:  fortresses were rare, and artillery next to useless. The carelessness
Title:  engendered by these usages descended even to the war of the Revolution and
Title:  lost the States the important fortress of Ticonderoga opening a way for the
Title:  army of Burgoyne into what was then the bosom of the country. We look back
Title:  at this ignorance, or infatuation, whichever it may be called, with wonder,
Title:  knowing that the neglect of an eminence, whose difficultires, like those of
Title:  Mount Defiance, have been so greatly exaggerated, would, at the present
Title:  time, prove fatal to the reputation of the engineer who had planned the
Title:  works at their base, or to that of the general whose lot it was to defend
Title:  them.
Title:  
Title:  The tourist, the valetudinarian, or the amateur of the beauties of nature,
Title:  who, in the train of his four-in-hand, now rolls through the scenes we have
Title:  attempted to describe, in quest of information, health, or pleasure, or
Title:  floats steadily toward his object on those artificial waters which have
Title:  sprung up under the administration of a statesman1 who has dared to stake
Title:  his political character on the hazardous issue, is not to suppose that his
Title:  ancestors traversed those hills, or struggled with the same currents with
Title:  equal facility. The transportation of a single heavy gun was often
Title:  considered equal to a victory gained; if happily, the difficulties of the
Title:  passage had not so far separated it from its necessary concomitant, the
Title:  ammunition, as to render it no more than a useless tube of unwieldy iron.
Title:  
Title:  The evils of this state of things pressed heavily on the fortunes of the
Title:  resolute Scotsman who now defended William Henry. Though his adversary
Title:  neglected the hills, he had planted his batteries with judgment on the
Title:  plain, and caused them to be served with vigor and skill. Against this
Title:  assualt, the besieged could only oppose the imperfect and hasty preparations
Title:  of a fortress in the wilderness.
Title:  
Title:  It was in the afternoon of the fifth day of the siege, and the fourth of his
Title:  own service in it, that Major Heyward profited by a parley that had just
Title:  been beaten, by repairing to the ramparts of one of the water bastions, to
Title:  breathe the cool air from the lake, and to take a survey of the progress of
Title:  the siege. He was alone, if the solitary sentinel who paced the mound be
Title:  excepted; for the artillerists had hastened also to profit by the temporary
Title:  suspension of their arduous duties. The evening was delightfully calm, and
Title:  the light air from the limpid water fresh and soothing. It seemed as if,
Title:  with the termination of the roar of artillery and the plunging of shot,
Title:  nature had also seized the moment to assume her mildest and most captivating
Title:  form. The sun poured down his parting glory on the scene, without the
Title:  oppression of those fierce rays that belong to the climate and the season.
Title:  The mountains looked green, and fresh, and lovely, tempered with the milder
Title:  light, or softened in shadow, as thin vapors floated between them and the
Title:  sun. The numerous islands rested on the bosom of the Horican, some low and
Title:  sunken, as if embedded in the waters, and others appearing to hover about
Title:  the element, in little hillocks of green velvet; among which the fishermen
Title:  of the beleaguering army peacefully rowed their skiffs, or floated at rest
Title:  on the glassy mirror in quiet pursuit of their employment.
Title:  
Title:  The scene was at once animated and still. All that pertained to nature was
Title:  sweet, or simply grand; while those parts which depended on the temper and
Title:  movements of man were lively and playful.
Title:  
Title:  Two little spotless flags were abroad, the one on a salient angle of the
Title:  fort, and the other on the advanced battery of the besiegers; emblems of the
Title:  truth which existed, not only to the acts, but it would seem, also, to the
Title:  enmity of the combatants.
Title:  
Title:  Behind these again swung, heavily opening and closing in silken folds, the
Title:  rival standards of England and France.
Title:  
Title:  A hundred gay and thoughtless young Frenchmen were drawing a net to the
Title:  pebbly beach, within dangerous proximity to the sullen but silent cannon of
Title:  the fort, while the eastern mountain was sending back the loud shouts and
Title:  gay merriment that attended their sport. Some were rushing eagerly to enjoy
Title:  the aquatic games of the lake, and others were already toiling their way up
Title:  the neighboring hills, with the restless curiosity of their nation. To all
Title:  these sports and pursuits, those of the enemy who watched the besieged, and
Title:  the besieged themselves, were, however, merely the idle though sympathizing
Title:  spectators. Here and there a picket had, indeed, raised a song, or mingled
Title:  in a dance, which had drawn the dusky savages around them, from their lairs
Title:  in the forest. In short, everything wore rather the appearance of a day of
Title:  pleasure, than of an hour stolen from the dangers and toil of a bloody and
Title:  vindictive warfare.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan had stood in a musing attitude, contemplating this scene a few
Title:  minutes, when his eyes were directed to the glacis in front of the
Title:  sally-port already mentioned, by the sounds of approaching footsteps. He
Title:  walked to an angle of the bastion, and beheld the scout advancing, under the
Title:  custody of a French officer, to the body of the fort. The countenance of
Title:  Hawkeye was haggard and careworn, and his air dejected, as though he felt
Title:  the deepest degradation at having fallen into the power of his enemies. He
Title:  was without his favorite weapon, and his arms were even bound behind him
Title:  with thongs, made of the skin of a deer. The arrival of flags to cover the
Title:  messengers of summons, had occurred so often of late, that when Heyward
Title:  first threw his careless glance on this group, he expected to see another of
Title:  the officers of the enemy, charged with a similar office but the instant he
Title:  recognized the tall person and still sturdy though downcast features of his
Title:  friend, the woodsman, he started with surprise, and turned to descend from
Title:  the bastion into the bosom of the work.
Title:  
Title:  The sounds of other voices, however, caught his attention, and for a moment
Title:  caused him to forget his purpose. At the inner angle of the mound he met the
Title:  sisters, walking along the parapet, in search, like himself, of air and
Title:  relief from confinement. They had not met from that painful moment when he
Title:  deserted them on the plain, only to assure their safety. He had parted from
Title:  them worn with care, and jaded with fatigue; he now saw them refreshed and
Title:  blooming, though timid and anxious. Under such an inducement it will cause
Title:  no surprise that the young man lost sight for a time, of other objects in
Title:  order to address them. He was, however, anticipated by the voice of the
Title:  ingenuous and youthful Alice.
Title:  
Title:  Ah! thou tyrant! thou recreant knight! he who abandons his damsels in the
Title:  very lists, she cried; here have we been days, nay, ages, expecting you at
Title:  our feet, imploring mercy and forgetfulness of your craven backsliding, or I
Title:  should rather say, backrunning - for verily you fled in the manner that no
Title:  striken deer, as our worthy friend the scout would say, could equal!
Title:  
Title:  You know that Alice means our thanks and our blessings, added the graver and
Title:  more thoughtful Cora. In truth, we have a little wonder why you should so
Title:  rigidly absent yourself from a place where the gratitude of the daughters
Title:  might receive the support of a parent's thanks.
Title:  
Title:  Your father himself could tell you, that, though absent from your presence,
Title:  I have not been altogether forgetful of your safety, returned the young man;
Title:  the mastery of yonder village of huts, pointing to the neighboring
Title:  entrenched camp, has been keenly disputed; and he who holds it is sure to be
Title:  possessed of this fort, and that which it contains. My days and nights have
Title:  all been passed there since we separated, because I thought that duty called
Title:  me thither. But, he added, with an air of chagrin, which he endeavored,
Title:  though unsuccessfully, to conceal, had I been aware that what I then
Title:  believed a soldier's conduct could be so construed, shame would have been
Title:  added to the list of reasons.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward! Duncan! exclaimed Alice, bending forward to read his half-averted
Title:  countenance, until a lock of her golden hair rested on her flushed cheek,
Title:  and nearly concealed the tear that had started to her eye; did I think this
Title:  idle tongue of mine had pained you, I would silence it forever. Cora can
Title:  say, if Cora would, how justly we have prized your services, and how deep -
Title:  I had almost said, how fervent - is our gratitude. And will Cora attest the
Title:  truth of this? cried Duncan, suffering the cloud to be chased from his
Title:  countenance by a smile of open pleasure. What says our graver sister? Will
Title:  she find an excuse for the neglect of the knight in the duty of a soldier?
Title:  
Title:  Cora made no immediate answer, but turned her face toward the water, as if
Title:  looking on the sheet of the Horican. When she did bend her dark eyes on the
Title:  young man, they were yet filled with an expression of anguish that at once
Title:  drove every thought but that of kind solicitude from his mind.
Title:  
Title:  You are not well, dearest Miss Munro! he exclaimed; we have trifled while
Title:  you are in suffering!
Title:  
Title:  'Tis nothing, she answered, refusing his support with feminine reserve. That
Title:  I cannot see the sunny side of the picture of life, like this artless but
Title:  ardent enthusiast, she added, laying her hand lightly, but affectionately,
Title:  on the arm of her sister, is the penalty of experience, and, perhaps, the
Title:  misfortune of my nature. See, she continued, as if determined to shake off
Title:  infirmity, in a sense of duty; look around you, Major Heyward, and tell me
Title:  what a prospect is this for the daughter of a soldier whose greatest
Title:  happiness is his honor and his military renown.
Title:  
Title:  Neither ought nor shall be tarnished by circumstances over which he has had
Title:  no control, Duncan warmly replied. But your words recall me to my own duty.
Title:  I go now to your gallant father, to hear his determination in matters of the
Title:  last moment to the defense. God bless you in every fortune, noble - Cora - I
Title:  may and must call you. She frankly gave him her hand, though her lip
Title:  quivered, and her cheeks gradually became of ashly palness. In every
Title:  fortune, I know you will be an ornament and honor to your sex. Alice, adieu
Title:  - his voice changed from admiration to tenderness - adieu, Alice; we shall
Title:  soon meet again; as conquerors, I trust, and amid rejoicings!
Title:  
Title:  Without waiting for an answer from either, the young man threw himself down
Title:  the grassy steps of the bastion, and moving rapidly across the parade, he
Title:  was quickly in the presence of their father. Munro was pacing his narrow
Title:  apartment with a disturbed air and gigantic strides as Duncan entered.
Title:  
Title:  You have anticipated my wishes, Major Heyward, he said; I was about to
Title:  request this favor.
Title:  
Title:  I am sorry to see, sir, that the messenger I so warmly recommended has
Title:  returned in custody of the French! I hope there is no reason to distrust his
Title:  fidelity?
Title:  
Title:  The fidelity of The Long Rifle is well known to me, returned Munro, and is
Title:  above suspicion; though his usual good fortune seems, at last, to have
Title:  failed. Montcalm has got him, and with the accursed politeness of his
Title:  nation, he has sent him in with a doleful tale, of knowing how I valued the
Title:  fellow, he could not think of retaining him. A Jesuitical way that, Major
Title:  Duncan Heyward, of telling a man of his misfortunes!
Title:  
Title:  But the general and his succor?
Title:  
Title:  Did ye look to the south as ye entered, and could ye not see them? said the
Title:  old soldier, laughting bitterly.
Title:  
Title:  Hoot! hoot! you're an impatient boy, sir, and cannot give the gentlemen
Title:  leisure for their march!
Title:  
Title:  They are coming, then? The scout has said as much?
Title:  
Title:  When? and by what path? for the dunce has omitted to tell me this. There is
Title:  a letter, it would seem, too; and that is the only agreeable part of the
Title:  matter. For the customary attentions of your Marquis of Montcalm - I warrant
Title:  me, Duncan, that he of Lothian would buy a dozen such marquisates - but if
Title:  the news of the letter were bad, the gentility of this French monsieur would
Title:  certainly compel him to let us know it.
Title:  
Title:  He keeps the letter, then, while he releases the messenger?
Title:  
Title:  Ay, that does he, and all for the sake of what you call your bonhommie I
Title:  would venture, if the truth was known, the fellow's grandfather taught the
Title:  noble science of dancing.
Title:  
Title:  But what says the scout? he has eyes and ears, and a tongue. What verbal
Title:  report does he make?
Title:  
Title:  Oh! sir, he is not wanting in natural organs, and he is free to tell all
Title:  that he has seen and heard. The whole amount is this; there is a fort of his
Title:  majesty's on the banks of the Hudson, called Edward, in honor of his
Title:  gracious highness of York, you'll know; and it is well filled with armed
Title:  men, as such a work should be.
Title:  
Title:  But was there no movement, no signs of any intention to advance to our
Title:  relief?
Title:  
Title:  There were the morning and evening parades; and when one of the provincial
Title:  loons - you'll know, Dunca, you're half a Scotsman yourself - when one of
Title:  them dropped his powder over his porretch, if it touched the coals, it just
Title:  burned! Then, suddenly changing his bitter, ironical manner, to one more
Title:  grave and thoughtful, he continued: and yet there might, and must be,
Title:  something in that letter which it would be well to know!
Title:  
Title:  Our decision should be speedy, said Duncan, gladly availing himself of this
Title:  change of humor, to press the more important objects of their interview; I
Title:  cannot conceal from you, sir, that the camp will not be much longer tenable;
Title:  and I am sorry to add, that things appear no better in the fort; more than
Title:  half the guns are bursted.
Title:  
Title:  And how should it be otherwise? Some were fished from the bottom of the
Title:  lake; some have been rusting in woods since the discovery of the country;
Title:  and some were never guns at all - mere privateersmen's playthings! Do you
Title:  think, sir, you can have Woolwich Warren in the midst of a wilderness, three
Title:  thousand miles from Great Britain?
Title:  
Title:  The walls are crumbling about our ears, and provisions begin to fail us,
Title:  continued Heyward, without regarding the new burst of indignation; even the
Title:  men show signs of discontent and alarm.
Title:  
Title:  Major Heyward, said Munro, turning to his youthful associate with the
Title:  dignity of his years and superior rank; I should have served his majesty for
Title:  half a century, and earned these gray hairs in vain, were I ignorant of all
Title:  you say, and of the pressing nature of our circumstances; still, there is
Title:  everything due to the honor of the king's arms, and something to ourselves.
Title:  While there is hope of succor, this fortress will I defend, though it be to
Title:  be done with pebbles gathered on the lake shore. It is a sight of the
Title:  letter, therefore, that we want, that we may know the intentions of the man
Title:  the earl of Loudon has left among us as his substitute.
Title:  
Title:  And can I be of service in the matter?
Title:  
Title:  Sir, you can; the marquis of Montcalm has, in addition to his other
Title:  civilities, invited me to a personal interview between the works and his own
Title:  camp; in order, as he says, to impart some additional information. Now, I
Title:  think it would not be wise to show any undue solicitude to meet him, and I
Title:  would employ you, an officer of rank, as my substitute; for it would but ill
Title:  comport with the honor of Scotland to let it be said one of her gentlemen
Title:  was outdone in civility by a native of any other country on earth.
Title:  
Title:  Without assuming the supererogatory task of entering into a discussion of
Title:  the comparative merits of national courtesy, Duncan cheerfully assented to
Title:  supply the place of the veteran in the approaching interview. A long
Title:  andconfidential communication now succeeded, during which the young man
Title:  received some additional insight into his duty, from the experience and
Title:  native acuteness of his commander, and then the former took his leave.
Title:  
Title:  As Duncan could only act as the representative of the commandant of the
Title:  fort, the ceremonies which should have accompanied a meeting between the
Title:  heads of the adverse forces were, of course, dispensed with. The truce still
Title:  existed, and with a roll and beat of the drum, and covered by a little white
Title:  flag, Duncan left the sally-port, within ten minutes after his instructions
Title:  were ended. He was received by the French officer in advance with the usual
Title:  formalities, and immediately accompanied to a distant marquee of the
Title:  renowned soldier who led the forces of France.
Title:  
Title:  The general of the enemy received the youthful messenger, surrounded by his
Title:  principal officers, and by a swarthy band of the native chiefs, who had
Title:  followed him to the field, with the warriors of their several tribes.
Title:  Heyward paused short, when, in glancing his eyes rapidly over the dark group
Title:  of the latter, he beheld the malignant countenance of Magua, regarding him
Title:  with the calm but sullen attention which marked the expression of that
Title:  subtle savage. A slight exclamation of surprise even burst from the lips of
Title:  the young man, but instantly, recollecting his errand, and the presence in
Title:  which he stood, he suppressed every appearance of emotion, and turned to the
Title:  hostile leader, who had already advanced a step to receive him.
Title:  
Title:  The marquis of Montcalm was, at the period of which we write, in the flower
Title:  of his age, and, it may be added, in the zenith of his fortunes. But even in
Title:  that enviable situation, he was affable, and distinguished as much for his
Title:  attention to the forms of courtesy, as for that chivalrous courage which,
Title:  only two short years afterward, induced him to throw away his life on the
Title:  plains of Abraham. Duncan, in turning his eyes from the malign expression of
Title:  Magua, suffered them to rest with pleasure on the smiling and polished
Title:  features, and the noble military air, of the French general.
Title:  
Title:  Monsieur, said the latter, j'ai beaucoup de plaisir a - bah! - ou est cet
Title:  interprete?
Title:  
Title:  Je crois, monsieur, qu'il ne sear pas necessaire, Heyward modestly replied;
Title:  je parle un peu francais.
Title:  
Title:  Ah! j'en suis bien aise, said Montcalm, taking Duncan familiarly by the arm,
Title:  and leading him deep into the marquee, a little out of earshot; je deteste
Title:  ces fripons-la; on ne sait jamais sur quel pie on est avec eux. Eh, bien!
Title:  monsieur, he continued still speaking in French; though I should have been
Title:  proud of receiving your commandant, I am very happy that he has seen proper
Title:  to employ an officer so distinguished, and who, I am sure, is so amiable, as
Title:  yourself.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan bowed low, pleased with the compliment, in spite of a most heroic
Title:  determination to suffer no artifice to allure him into forgetfulness of the
Title:  interest of his prince; and Montcalm, after a pause of a moment, as if to
Title:  collect his thoughts, proceeded:
Title:  
Title:  Your commandant is a brave man, and well qualified to repel my assault.
Title:  Mais, monsieur, is it not time to begin to take more counsel of humanity,
Title:  and less of your courage? The one as strongly characterizes the hero as the
Title:  other.
Title:  
Title:  We consider the qualities as inseparable, returned Duncan, smiling; but
Title:  while we find in the vigor of your excellency every motive to stimulate the
Title:  one, we can, as yet, see no particular call for the exercise of the other.
Title:  
Title:  Montcalm, in his turn, slightly bowed, but it was with the air of a man too
Title:  practised to remember the language of flattery. After musing a moment, he
Title:  added:
Title:  
Title:  It is possible my glasses have deceived me, and that your works resist our
Title:  cannon better than I had supposed. You know our force?
Title:  
Title:  Our accounts vary, said Duncan, carelessly; the highest, however, has not
Title:  exceeded twenty thousand men.
Title:  
Title:  The Frenchman bit his lip, and fastened his eyes keenly on the other as if
Title:  to read his thoughts; then, with a readiness peculiar to himself, he
Title:  continued, as if assenting to the truth of an enumeration which quite
Title:  doubled his army:
Title:  
Title:  It is a poor compliment to the vigilance of us soldiers, monsieur, that, do
Title:  what we will, we never can conceal our numbers. If it were to be done at
Title:  all, one would believe it might succeed in these woods. Though you think it
Title:  too soon to listen to the calls of humanity, he added, smiling archly, I may
Title:  be permitted to believe that gallantry is not forgotten by one so young as
Title:  yourself. The daughters of the commandant, I learn, have passed into the
Title:  fort since it was invested?
Title:  
Title:  It is true, monsieur; but, so far from weakening our efforts, they set us an
Title:  example of courage in their own fortitude. Were nothing but resolution
Title:  necessary to repel so accomplished a soldier as M. de Montcalm, I would
Title:  gladly trust the defense of William Henry to the elder of those ladies.
Title:  
Title:  We have a wise ordinance in our Salique laws, which says, The crown of
Title:  France shall never degrade the lance to the distaff, said Montcalm, dryly,
Title:  and with a little hauteur; but instantly adding, with his former frank and
Title:  easy air: as all the nobler qualities are hereditary, I can easily credit
Title:  you; though, as I said before, courage has its limits, and humanity must not
Title:  be forgotten. I trust, monsieur, you come authorized to treat for the
Title:  surrender of the place?
Title:  
Title:  Has your excellency found our defense so feeble as to believe the measure
Title:  necessary?
Title:  
Title:  I should be sorry to have the defense protracted in such a manner as to
Title:  irritate my red friends there, continued Montcalm, glancing his eyes at the
Title:  group of grave and attentive Indians, without attending to the other's
Title:  questions; I find it difficult, even now, to limit them to the usages of
Title:  war.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward was silent; for a painful recollection of the dangers he had so
Title:  recently escaped came over his mind, and recalled the images of those
Title:  defenseless beings who had shared in all his sufferings.
Title:  
Title:  Ces messieurs-la, said Montcalm, following up the advantage which he
Title:  conceived he had gained, are most formidable when baffled; and it is
Title:  unnecessary to tell you with what difficulty they are restrained in their
Title:  anger. Eh bien, monsieur! shall we speak of the terms?
Title:  
Title:  I fear your excellency has been deceived as to the strength of William
Title:  Henry, and the resources of its garrison!
Title:  
Title:  I have not sat down before Quebec, but an earthen work, that is defended by
Title:  twenty-three hundred gallant men, was the laconic reply.
Title:  
Title:  Our mounds are earthen, certainly - nor are they seated on the rocks of Cape
Title:  Diamond; but they stand on that shore which proved so destructive to Dieskau
Title:  and his army. There is also a powerful force within a few hours' march of
Title:  us, which we account upon as a part of our means.
Title:  
Title:  Some six or eight thousand men, returned Montcalm, with much apparent
Title:  indifference, whom their leader wisely judges to be safer in their works
Title:  than in the field.
Title:  
Title:  It was now Heyward's turn to bite his lip with vexation as the other so
Title:  coolly alluded to a force which the young man knew to be overrated. Both
Title:  mused a little while in silence, when Montcalm renewed the conversation, in
Title:  a way that showed he believed the visit of his guest was solely to propose
Title:  terms of capitulation. On the other hand, Heyward began to throw sundry
Title:  inducements in the way of the French general, to betray the discoveries he
Title:  had made through the intercepted letter. The artifice of neither, however,
Title:  succeeded; and after a protracted and fruitless interview, Duncan took his
Title:  leave, favorably impressed with an opinion of the courtesy and talents of
Title:  the enemy's captain, but as ignorant of what he came to learn as when he
Title:  arrived. Montcalm followed him as far as the entrance of the marquee,
Title:  renewing his invitations to the commandant of the fort to give him an
Title:  immediate meeting in the open ground between the two armies.
Title:  
Title:  There they separated, and Duncan returned to the advanced post of the
Title:  French, accompanied as before; whence he instantly proceeded to the fort,
Title:  and to the quarters of his own commander.

Title:  Chapter 16
Title:  
Title:       Edgar: Before you fight the battle ope this letter.
Title:  
Title:                                                                    LEAR
Title:  
Title:  Major Heyward found Munro attended only by his daughters. Alice sat upon his
Title:  knee, parting the gray hairs on the forehead of the old man with her
Title:  delicate fingers; and whenever he affected to frown on her trifling,
Title:  appeasing his assumed anger by pressing her ruby lips fondly on his wrinkled
Title:  brow. Cora was seated nigh them, a calm and amused looker-on; regarding the
Title:  wayward movements of her more youthful sister with that species of maternal
Title:  fondness which characterized her love for Alice. Not only the dangers
Title:  through which they had passed, but those which still impended above them,
Title:  appeared to be momentarily forgotten, in the soothing indulgence of such a
Title:  family meeting. It seemed as if they had profited by the short truce, to
Title:  devote an instant to the purest and best affection; the daughters forgetting
Title:  their fears, and the veteran his cares, in the security of the moment. Of
Title:  this scene, Duncan, who, in his eagerness to report his arrival, had entered
Title:  unannounced, stood many moments an unobserved and a delighted spectator. But
Title:  the quick and dancing eyes of Alice soon caught a glimpse of his figure
Title:  reflected from a glass, and she sprang blushing from her father's knee,
Title:  exclaiming aloud:
Title:  
Title:  Major Heyward!
Title:  
Title:  What of the lad? demanded her father; I have sent him to crack a little with
Title:  the Frenchman. Ha, sir, you are young, and you're nimble! Away with you, ye
Title:  baggage; as if there were not troubles enough for a soldier, without having
Title:  his camp filled with such prattling hussies as yourself!
Title:  
Title:  Alice laughingly followed her sister, who instantly led the way from an
Title:  apartment where she perceived their presence was no longer desirable. Munro,
Title:  instead of demanding the result of the young man's mission, paced the room
Title:  for a few moments, with his hands behind his back, and his head inclined
Title:  toward the floor, like a man lost in thought. At length he raised his eyes,
Title:  glistening with a father's fondness, and exclaimed:
Title:  
Title:  They are a pair of excellent girls, Heyward, and such as any one may boast
Title:  of.
Title:  
Title:  You are not now to learn my opinion of your daughters, Colonel Munro.
Title:  
Title:  True, lad, true, interrupted the impatient old man; you were about opening
Title:  your mind more fully on that matter the day you got in, but I did not think
Title:  it becoming in an old soldier to be talking of nuptial blessings and wedding
Title:  jokes when the enemies of his king were likely to be unbidden guests at the
Title:  feast. But I was wrong, Duncan, boy, I was wrong there; and I am now ready
Title:  to hear what you have to say.
Title:  
Title:  Notwithstanding the pleasure your assurance gives me, dear sir, I have just
Title:  now, a message from Montcalm - -
Title:  
Title:  Let the Frenchman and all his host go to the devil, sir! exclaimed the hasty
Title:  veteran. He is not yet master of William Henry, nor shall he ever be,
Title:  provided Webb proves himself the man he should. No, sir, thank Heaven we are
Title:  not yet in such a strait that it can be said Munro is too much pressed to
Title:  discharge the little domestic duties of his own family. Your mother was the
Title:  only child of my bosom friend, Duncan; and I'll just give you a hearing,
Title:  though all the knights of St. Louis were in a body at the sally-port, with
Title:  the French saint at their head, crying to speak a word under favor. A pretty
Title:  degree of knighthood, sir, is that which can be bought with sugar hogsheads!
Title:  and then your twopenny marquisates. The thistle is the order for dignity and
Title:  antiquity; the veritable nemo me impune lacessit of chivalry. Ye had
Title:  ancestors in that degree, Duncan, and they were an ornamnet to the nobles of
Title:  Scotland.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, who perceived that his superior took a malicious pleasure in
Title:  exhibiting his contempt for the message of the French general, was fain to
Title:  humor a spleen that he knew would be short-lived; he therefore, replied with
Title:  as much indifference as he could assume on such a subject:
Title:  
Title:  My request, as you know, sir, went so far as to presume to the honor of
Title:  being your son.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, boy, you found words to make yourself very plainly comprehended. But,
Title:  let me ask ye, sir, have you been as intelligible to the girl?
Title:  
Title:  On my honor, no, exclaimed Duncan, warmly; there would have been an abuse of
Title:  a confided trust, had I taken advantage of my situation for such a purpose.
Title:  
Title:  Your notions are those of a gentleman, Major Heyward, and well enough in
Title:  their place. But Cora Munro is a maiden too discreet, and of a mind too
Title:  elevated and improved, to need the guardianship even of a father.
Title:  
Title:  Cora!
Title:  
Title:  Ay - Cora! we are talking of your pretensions to Miss Munro, are we not,
Title:  sir?
Title:  
Title:  I - I - I was not conscious of having mentioned her name, said Duncan,
Title:  stammering.
Title:  
Title:  And to marry whom, then, did you wish my consent, Major Heyward? demanded
Title:  the old soldier, erecting himself in the dignity of offended feeling.
Title:  
Title:  You have another, and not less lovely child.
Title:  
Title:  Alice! exclaimed the father, in an astonishment equal to that with which
Title:  Duncan had just repeated the name of her sister.
Title:  
Title:  Such was the direction of my wishes, sir.
Title:  
Title:  The young man awaited in silence the result of the extraordinary effect
Title:  produced by a communication, which, as it now appeared, was so unexpected.
Title:  For several minutes Munro paced the chamber with long and rapid strides, his
Title:  rigid features working convulsively, and every faculty seemingly absorbed in
Title:  the musings of his own mind. At length, he paused directly in front of
Title:  Heyward, and riveting his eyes upon those of the other, he said, with a lip
Title:  that quivered violently:
Title:  
Title:  Duncan Heyward, I have loved you for the sake of him whose blood is in your
Title:  veins; I have loved you for your own good qualities; and I have loved you,
Title:  because I thought you would contribute to the happiness of my child. But all
Title:  this love would turn to hatred, were I assured that what I so much apprehend
Title:  is true.
Title:  
Title:  God forbid that any act or thought of mine should lead to such a change!
Title:  exclaimed the young man, whose eye never quailed under the penetrating look
Title:  it encountered. Without adverting to the impossibility of the other's
Title:  comprehending those feelings which were hid in his own bosom, Munro suffered
Title:  himself to be appeased by the unaltered countenance he met, and with a voice
Title:  sensibly softened, he continued:
Title:  
Title:  You would be my son, Duncan, and you're ignorant of the history of the man
Title:  you wish to call your father. Sit ye down, young man, and I will open to you
Title:  the wounds of a seared heart, in as few words as may be suitable.
Title:  
Title:  By this time, the message of Montcalm was as much forgotten by him who bore
Title:  it as by the man for whose ears it was intended. Each drew a chair, and
Title:  while the veteran communed a few moments with his own thoughts, apparently
Title:  in sadness, the youth suppressed his impatience in a look and attitude of
Title:  respectful attention. At length, the former spoke:
Title:  
Title:  You'll know, already, Major Heyward, that my family was both ancient and
Title:  honorable, commenced the Scotsman; though it might not altogether be endowed
Title:  with that amount of wealth that should correspond with its degree. I was,
Title:  maybe, such an one as yourself when I plighted my faith to Alice Graham, the
Title:  only child of a neighboring laird of some estate. But the connection was
Title:  disagreeable to her father, on more accounts than my poverty. I did,
Title:  therefore, what an honest man should - restored the maiden her troth, and
Title:  departed the country in the service of my king. I had seen many regions, and
Title:  had shed much blood in different lands, before duty called me to the islands
Title:  of the West Indies. There it was my lot to form a connection with one who in
Title:  time became my wife, and the mother of Cora. She was the daughter of a
Title:  gentleman of those isles, by a lady whose misfortune it was, if you will,
Title:  said the old man, proudly, to be descended, remotely, from that unfortunate
Title:  class who are so basely enslaved to administer to the wants of a luxurious
Title:  people. Ay, sir, that is a curse, entailed on Scotland by her unnatural
Title:  union with a foreign and trading people. But could I find a man among them
Title:  who would dare to reflect on my child, he should feel the weight of a
Title:  father's anger! Ha! Major Heyward, you are yourself born at the south, where
Title:  these unfortunate beings are considered of a race inferior to your own.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis most unfortunately true, sir, said Duncan, unable any longer to prevent
Title:  his eyes from sinking to the floor in embarrassment.
Title:  
Title:  And you cast it on my child as a reproach! You scorn to mingle the blood of
Title:  the Heywards with one so degraded - lovely and virtuous though she be?
Title:  fiercely demanded the jealous parent.
Title:  
Title:  Heaven protect me from a prejudice so unworthy of my reason! returned
Title:  Duncan, at the same time conscious of such a feeling, and that as deeply
Title:  rooted as if it had been ingrafted in his nature. The sweetness, the beauty,
Title:  the witchery of your younger daughter, Colonel Munro, might explain my
Title:  motives without imputing to me this injustice.
Title:  
Title:  Ye are right, sir, returned the old man, again changing his tones to those
Title:  of gentleness, or rather softness; the girl is the image of what her mother
Title:  was at her years, and before she had become acquainted with grief. When
Title:  death deprived me of my wife I returned to Scotland, enriched by the
Title:  marriage; and, would you think it, Duncan! the suffering angel had remained
Title:  in the heartless state of celibacy twenty long years, and that for the sake
Title:  of a man who could forget her! She did more, sir; she overlooked my want of
Title:  faith, and, all difficulties being now removed, she took me for her husband.
Title:  
Title:  And became the mother of Alice? exclaimed Duncan, with an eagerness that
Title:  might have proved dangerous at a moment when the thoughts of Munro were less
Title:  occupied that at present.
Title:  
Title:  She did, indeed, said the old man, and dearly did she pay for the blessing
Title:  she bestowed. But she is a saint in heaven, sir; and it ill becomes one
Title:  whose foot rests on the grave to mourn a lot so blessed. I had her but a
Title:  single year, though; a short term of happiness for one who had seen her
Title:  youth fade in hopeless pining.
Title:  
Title:  There was something so commanding in the distress of the old man, that
Title:  Heyward did not dare to venture a syllable of consolation. Munro sat utterly
Title:  unconscious of the other's presence, his features exposed and working with
Title:  the anguish of his regrets, while heavy tears fell from his eyes, and rolled
Title:  unheeded from his cheeks to the floor. At length he moved, and as if
Title:  suddenly recovering his recollection; when he arose, and taking a single
Title:  turn across the room, he approached his companion with an air of military
Title:  grandeur, and demanded:
Title:  
Title:  Have you not, Major Heyward, some communication that I should hear from the
Title:  marquis de Montcalm?
Title:  
Title:  Duncan started in his turn, and immediately commenced in an embarrassed
Title:  voice, the half-forgotten message. It is unnecessary to dwell upon the
Title:  evasive though polite manner with which the French general had eluded every
Title:  attempt of Heyward to worm from him the purport of the communication he had
Title:  proposed making, or on the decided, though still polished message, by which
Title:  he now gave his enemy to understand, that, unless he chose to receive it in
Title:  person, he should not receive it at all. As Munro listened to the detail of
Title:  Duncan, the excited feelings of the father gradually gave way before the
Title:  obligations of his station, and when the other was done, he saw before him
Title:  nothing but the veteran, swelling with the wounded feelings of a soldier.
Title:  
Title:  You have said enough, Major Heyward, exclaimed the angry old man; enough to
Title:  make a volume of commentary on French civility. Here has this gentleman
Title:  invited me to a conference, and when I send him a capable substitute, for
Title:  ye're all that, Duncan, though your years are but few, he answers me with a
Title:  riddle.
Title:  
Title:  He may have thought less favorably of the substitue, my dear sir; and you
Title:  will remember that the invitation, which he now repeats, was to the
Title:  commandant of the works, and not to his second.
Title:  
Title:  Well, sir, is not a substitute clothed with all the power and dignity of him
Title:  who grants the commission? He wishes to confer with Munro! Faith, sir, I
Title:  have much inclination to indulge the man, if it should only be to let him
Title:  behold the firm countenance we maintain in spite of his numbers and his
Title:  summons. There might be not bad policy in such a stroke, young man.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, who believe it of the last importance that they should speedily come
Title:  to the contents of the letter borne by the scout, gladly encouraged this
Title:  idea.
Title:  
Title:  Without doubt, he could gather no confidence by witnessing our indifference,
Title:  he said.
Title:  
Title:  You never said truer word. I could wish, sir, that he would visit the works
Title:  in open day, and in the form of a storming party; that is the least failing
Title:  method of proving the countenance of an enemy, and would be far preferable
Title:  to the battering system he has chosen. The beauty and manliness of warfare
Title:  has been much deformed, Major Heyward, by the arts of your Monsieur Vauban.
Title:  Our ancestors were far above such scientific cowardice!
Title:  
Title:  It may be very true, sir; but we are now obliged to repel art by art. What
Title:  is your pleasure in the matter of the interview?
Title:  
Title:  I will meet the Frenchman, and that without fear or delay; promptly, sir, as
Title:  becomes a servant of my royal master. Go, Major Heyward, and give them a
Title:  flourish of the music; and send out a messenger to let them know who is
Title:  coming. We will follow with a small guard, for such respect is due to one
Title:  who holds the honor of his king in keeping; and hark'ee, Duncan, he added,
Title:  in a half whisper, though they were alone, it may be prudent to have some
Title:  aid at hand, in case there should be treachery at the bottom of it all.
Title:  
Title:  The young man availed himself of this order to quit the apartment; and, as
Title:  the day was fast coming to a close, he hastened without delay, to make the
Title:  necessary arrangements. A very few minutes only were necessary to parade a
Title:  few files, and to dispatch an orderly with a flag to announce the approach
Title:  of the commandant of the fort. When Duncan had done both these, he led the
Title:  guard to the sally-port, near which he found his superior ready, waiting his
Title:  appearance. As soon as the usual ceremonials of a military departure were
Title:  observed, the veteran and his more youthful companion left the fortress,
Title:  attended by the escort.
Title:  
Title:  They had proceeded only a hundred yards from the works, when the little
Title:  array which attended the French general to the conference was seen issuing
Title:  from the hollow way which formed the bed of a brook that ran between the
Title:  batteries of the besiegers and the fort. From the moment that Munro left his
Title:  own works to appear in front of his enemy's, his air had been grand, and his
Title:  step and countenance highly military. The instant he caught a glimpse of the
Title:  white plume that waved in the hat of Montcalm, his eye lighted, and age no
Title:  longer appeared to possess any influence over his vast and still muscular
Title:  person.
Title:  
Title:  Speak to the boys to be watchful, sir, he said, in an undertone, to Duncan;
Title:  and to look well to their flints and steel, for one is never safe with a
Title:  servant of these Louis's; at the same time, we shall show them the front of
Title:  men in deep security. Ye'll understand me, Major Heyward!
Title:  
Title:  He was interrupted by the clamor of a drum from the approaching Frenchmen,
Title:  which was immediately answered, when each party pushed an orderly in
Title:  advance, bearing a white flag, and the wary Scotsman halted with his guard
Title:  close at his back. As soon as this slight salutation had passed, Montcalm
Title:  moved toward them with a quick but graceful step, baring his head to the
Title:  veteran, and dropping his spotless plume nearly to the earth in courtesy. If
Title:  the air of Munro was more commanding and manly, it wanted both the ease and
Title:  insinuating polish of that of the Frenchman. Neither spoke for a few
Title:  moments, each regarding the other with curious and interested eyes. Then, as
Title:  became his superior rank and the nature of the interview, Montcalm broke the
Title:  silence. After uttering the usual words of greeting, he turned to Duncan,
Title:  and continued, with a smile of recognition, speaking always in French:
Title:  
Title:  I am rejoiced, monsieur, that you have given us the pleasure of your company
Title:  on this occasion. There will be no necessity to employ an ordinary
Title:  interpreter; for, in your hands, I feel the same security as if I spoke your
Title:  langauge myself.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan acknowledged the compliment, when Montcalm, turning to his guard,
Title:  which in imitation of that of their enemies, pressed close upon him,
Title:  continued:
Title:  
Title:  En arriere, mes enfants - il fait chaud - retirez-vous un peu.
Title:  
Title:  Before Major Heyward would imitate this proof of confidence, he glanced his
Title:  eyes around the plain, and beheld with uneasiness the numerous dusky groups
Title:  of savages, who looked out from the margin of the surrounding woods, curious
Title:  spectators of the interview.
Title:  
Title:  Monsieur de Montcalm will readily acknowledge the difference in our
Title:  situation, he said, with some embarrassment, pointing at the same time
Title:  toward those dangerous foes, who were to be seen in almost every direction.
Title:  were we to dismiss our guard, we should stand here at the mercy of our
Title:  enemies.
Title:  
Title:  Monsieur, you have the plighted faith of un gentilhomme Francais, for your
Title:  safety, returned Montcalm, laying his hand impressively on his heart; it
Title:  should suffice.
Title:  
Title:  It shall. Fall back, Duncan added to the officer who led the escort; fall
Title:  back, sir, beyond hearing, and wait for orders.
Title:  
Title:  Munro witnessed this movement with manifest uneasiness; nor did he fail to
Title:  demand an instant explanation.
Title:  
Title:  Is it not our interest, sir, to betray distrust? retorted Duncan. Monsieur
Title:  de Montcalm pledges his word for our safety, and I have ordered the men to
Title:  withdraw a little, in order to prove how much we depend on his assurance.
Title:  
Title:  It may be all right, sir, but I have no overweening reliance on the faith of
Title:  these marquesses, or marquis, as they call themselves. Their patents of
Title:  nobility are too common to be certain that they bear the seal of true honor.
Title:  
Title:  You forget, dear sir, that we confer with an officer, distinguished alike in
Title:  Europe and America for his deeds. From a soldier of his reputation we can
Title:  have nothing to apprehend.
Title:  
Title:  The old man made a gesture of resignation, though his rigid features still
Title:  betrayed his obstinate adherence to a distrust, which he derived from a sort
Title:  of hereditary contempt of his enemy, rather than from any present signs
Title:  which might warrant so uncharitable a feeling. Montcalm waited patiently
Title:  until this little dialogue in demi-voice was ended, when he drew nigher, and
Title:  opened the subject of their conference.
Title:  
Title:  I have solicited this interview from your superior, monsieur, he said,
Title:  because I believe he will allow himself to be persuaded that he has already
Title:  done everything which is necessary for the honor of his prince, and will now
Title:  listen to the admonitions of humanity. I will forever bear testimony that
Title:  his resistance has been gallant, and was continued as long as there was
Title:  hope.
Title:  
Title:  When this opening was translated to Munro, he answered with dignity, but
Title:  with sufficienct courtesy:
Title:  
Title:  However I may prize such testimony from Monsieur Montcalm, it will be more
Title:  valuable when it shall be better merited.
Title:  
Title:  The French general smiled, as Duncan gave him the purport of this reply, and
Title:  observed:
Title:  
Title:  What is now so freely accorded to approved courage, may be refused to
Title:  useless obstinacy. Monsieur would wish to see my camp, and witness for
Title:  himself our numbers, and the impossibility of his resisting them with
Title:  success?
Title:  
Title:  I know that the king of France is well served, returned the unmoved
Title:  Scotsman, as soon as Duncan ended his translation; but my own royal master
Title:  has as many and as faithful troops.
Title:  
Title:  Though not at hand, fortunately for us, said Montcalm, without waiting, in
Title:  his ardor, for the interpreter. There is a destiny in war, to which a brave
Title:  man knows how to submit with the same courage that he faces his foes.
Title:  
Title:  Had I been conscious that Monsieur Montcalm was master of the English, I
Title:  should have spared myself the trouble of so awkward a translation, said the
Title:  vexed Duncan, dryly; remembering instantly his recent by-play with Munro.
Title:  
Title:  Your pardon, monsieur, rejoined the Frenchman, suffering a slight color to
Title:  appear on his dark cheek. There is a vast difference between understanding
Title:  and speaking a foreign tongue; you will, therefore, please to assist me
Title:  still. Then, after a short pause, he added: These hills afford us every
Title:  opportunity of reconnoitering your works, messieurs, and I am possibly as
Title:  well acquainted with their weak condition as you can be yourselves.
Title:  
Title:  Ask the French general if his glasses can reach to the Hudson, said Munro,
Title:  proudly; and if he knows when and where to expect the army of Webb.
Title:  
Title:  Let General Webb be his own interpreter, returned the politic Montcalm,
Title:  suddenly extending an open letter toward Munro as he spoke; you will there
Title:  learn, monsieur, that his movements are not likely to prove embarrassing to
Title:  my army.
Title:  
Title:  The veteran seized the offered paper, without waiting for Duncan to
Title:  translate the speech, and with an eagerness that betrayed how important he
Title:  deemed its contents. As his eye passed hastily over the words, his
Title:  countenance changed from its look of military pride to one of deep chagrin;
Title:  his lip began to quiver; and suffering the paper to fall from his hand, his
Title:  head dropped upon his chest, like that of a man whose hopes were withered at
Title:  a single blow. Duncan caught the letter from the ground, and without apology
Title:  for the liberty he took, he read at a glance its cruel purport. Their common
Title:  superior, so far from encouraging them to resist, advised a speedy
Title:  surrender, urging in the plainest language, as a reason, the utter
Title:  impossibility of his sending a single man to their rescue.
Title:  
Title:  Here is no deception! exclaimed Duncan, examining the billet both inside and
Title:  out; this is the signature of Webb, and must be the captured letter.
Title:  
Title:  The man has betrayed me! Munro at length bitterly exclaimed; he has brought
Title:  dishonor to the door of one where disgrace was never before known to dwell,
Title:  and shame has he heaped heavily on my gray hairs.
Title:  
Title:  Say not so, cried Duncan; we are yet masters of the fort, and of our honor.
Title:  Let us, then, sell our lives at such a rate as shall make our enemies
Title:  believe the purchase too dear.
Title:  
Title:  Boy, I thank thee, exclaimed the old man, rousing himself from his stupor;
Title:  you have, for once, reminded Munro of his duty. We will go back, and dig our
Title:  graves behind those ramparts.
Title:  
Title:  Messieurs, said Montcalm, advancing toward them a step, in generous
Title:  interest, you little know Louis de St. Veran if you believe him capable of
Title:  profiting by this letter to humble brave men, or to build up a dishonest
Title:  reputation for himself. Listen to my terms before you leave me.
Title:  
Title:  What says the Frenchman? demanded the veteran, sternly; does he make a merit
Title:  of having captured a scout, with a note from headquarters? Sir, he had
Title:  better raise this siege, to go and sit down before Edward if he wishes to
Title:  frighten his enemy with words.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan explained the other's meaning.
Title:  
Title:  Monsieur de Montcalm, we will hear you, the veteran added, more calmly, as
Title:  Duncan ended.
Title:  
Title:  To retain the fort is now impossible, said his liberal enemy; it is
Title:  necessary to the interests of my master that it should be destroyed; but as
Title:  for yourselves and your brave comrades, there is no privilege dear to a
Title:  soldier that shall be denied.
Title:  
Title:  Our colors? demanded Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  Carry them to England, and show them to your king.
Title:  
Title:  Our arms?
Title:  
Title:  Keep them; none can use them better.
Title:  
Title:  Our march; the surrender of the place?
Title:  
Title:  Shall all be done in a way most honorable to yourselves.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan now turned to explain these proposals to his commander, who heard him
Title:  with amazement, and a sensibility that was deeply touched by so unusual and
Title:  unexpected generosity.
Title:  
Title:  Go you, Duncan, he said; go with this marquess, as, indeed, marquess he
Title:  should be; go to his marquee and arrange it all. I have lived to see two
Title:  things in my old age that never did I expect to behold. An Englishman afraid
Title:  to support a friend, and a Frenchman too honest to profit by his advantage.
Title:  
Title:  So saying, the veteran again dropped his head to his chest, and returned
Title:  slowly toward the fort, exhibiting, by the dejection of his air, to the
Title:  anxious garrison, a harbinger of evil tidings.
Title:  
Title:  From the shock of this unexpected blow the haughty feelings of Munro never
Title:  recovered; but from that moment there commenced a change in his determined
Title:  character, which accompanied him to a speedy grave. Duncan remained to
Title:  settle the terms of the capitulation. He was seen to re-enter the works
Title:  during the first watches of the night, and immediately after a private
Title:  conference with the commandant, to leave them again. It was then openly
Title:  announced that hostilities must cease - Munro having signed a treaty by
Title:  which the place was to be yielded to the enemy, with the morning; the
Title:  garrison to retain their arms, the colors and their baggage, and,
Title:  consequently, according to military opinion, their honor.
Title:
