Title:  
Title:  Chapter 17
Title:  
Title:       Weave we the woof. The thread is spun.
Title:       The web is wove. The work is done.
Title:  
Title:                                                                    GRAY
Title:  
Title:  The hostile armies, which lay in the wilds of the Horican, passed the night
Title:  of the ninth of August, 1757, much in the manner they would, had they
Title:  encountered on the fairest field of Europe. While the conquered were still,
Title:  sullen, and dejected, the victors triumphed. But there are limits alike to
Title:  grief and joy; and long before the watches of the morning came the stillness
Title:  of those boundless woods was only broken by a gay call from some exulting
Title:  young Frenchman of the advanced pickets, or a menacing challenge from the
Title:  fort, which sternly forbade the approach of any hostile footsteps before the
Title:  stipulated moment. Even these occasional threatening sounds ceased to be
Title:  heard in that dull hour which precedes the day, at which period a listener
Title:  might have sought in vain any evidence of the presence of those armed powers
Title:  that then slumbered on the shores of the holy lake.
Title:  
Title:  It was during these moments of deep silence that the canvas which concealed
Title:  the entrance to a spacious marquee in the French encampment was shoved
Title:  aside, and a man issued from beneath the drapery into the open air. He was
Title:  enveloped in a cloak that might have been intended as a protection from the
Title:  chilling damps of the woods, but which served equally well as a mantle to
Title:  conceal his person. He was permitted to pass the grenadier, who watched over
Title:  the slumbers of the French commander, without interruption, the man making
Title:  the usual salute which betokens military deference, as the other passed
Title:  swiftly through the little city of tents, in the direction of William Henry.
Title:  Whenever this unknown individual encountered one of the numberless sentinels
Title:  who crossed his path, his answer was prompt, and, as it appeared,
Title:  satisfactory; for he was uniformly allowed to proceed without further
Title:  interrogation.
Title:  
Title:  With the exception of such repeated but brief interruptions, he had moved
Title:  silently from the center of the camp to its most advanced outposts, when he
Title:  drew nigh the soldier who held his watch nearest to the works of the enemy.
Title:  As he approached he was received with the usual challenge:
Title:  
Title:  Qui vive?
Title:  
Title:  France, was the reply.
Title:  
Title:  Le mot d'ordre?
Title:  
Title:  La victorie, said the other, drawing so nigh as to be heard in a loud
Title:  whisper.
Title:  
Title:  C'est bien, returned the sentinel, throwing his musket from the charge to
Title:  his shoulder; vous promenez bien matin, monsieur!
Title:  
Title:  Il est necessaire d'etre vigilant, mon enfant, the other observed, dropping
Title:  a fold of his cloak, and looking the soldier close in the face as he passed
Title:  him, still continuing his way toward the British fortification. The man
Title:  started; his arms rattled heavily as he threw them forward in the lowest and
Title:  most respectful salute; and when he had again recovered his piece, he turned
Title:  to walk his post, muttering between his teeth:
Title:  
Title:  Il faut etre vigilant, en verite! je crois que nous avons la, un caporal qui
Title:  ne dort jamais!
Title:  
Title:  The officer proceeded, without affecting to hear the words which escaped the
Title:  sentinel in his surprise; nor did he again pause until he had reached the
Title:  low strand, and in a somewhat dangerous vicinity to the western water
Title:  bastion of the fort. The light of an obscure moon was just sufficient to
Title:  render objects, though dim, perceptible in their outlines. He, therefore,
Title:  took the precaution to place himself against the trunk of a tree, where he
Title:  leaned for many minutes, and seemed to contemplate the dark and silent
Title:  mounds of the English works in profound attention. His gaze at the ramparts
Title:  was not that of a curious or idle spectator; but his looks wandered from
Title:  point to point, denoting his knowledge of military usages, and betraying
Title:  that his search was not unaccompanied by distrust. At length he appeared
Title:  satisfied; and having cast his eyes impatiently upward toward the summit of
Title:  the eastern mountain, as if anticipating the approach of the morning, he was
Title:  in the act of turning on his footsteps, when a light sound on the nearest
Title:  angle of the bastion caught his ear, and induced him to remain.
Title:  
Title:  Just then a figure was seen to approach the edge of the rampart, where it
Title:  stood, apparently contemplating in its turn the distant tents of the French
Title:  encampment. Its head was then turned toward the east, as though equally
Title:  anxious for the appearance of light, when the form leaned against the mound,
Title:  and seemed to gaze upon the glassy expanse of the waters, which, like a
Title:  submarine firmament, glittered with its thousand mimic stars. The melancholy
Title:  air, the hour, together with the vast frame of the man who thus leaned,
Title:  musing, against the English ramparts, left no doubt as to his person in the
Title:  mind of the observant spectator. Delicacy, no less than prudence, now urged
Title:  him to retire; and he had moved cautiously round the body of the tree for
Title:  that purpose, when another sound drew his attention, and once more arrested
Title:  his footsteps. It was a low and almost inaudible movement of the water, and
Title:  was succeeded by a grating of pebbles one against the other. In a moment he
Title:  saw a dark form rise, as it were, out of the lake, and steal without further
Title:  noise to the land, within a few feet of the place where he himself stood. A
Title:  rifle next slowly rose between his eyes and the watery mirror; but before it
Title:  could be discharged his own hand was on the lock.
Title:  
Title:  Hugh! exclaimed the savage, whose treacherous aim was so singularly and so
Title:  unexpectedly interrupted.
Title:  
Title:  Without making any reply, the French officer laid his hand on the shoulder
Title:  of the Indian, and led him in profound silence to a distance from the spot,
Title:  where their subsequent dialogue might have proved dangerous, and where it
Title:  seemed that one of them, at least, sought a victim. Then throwing open his
Title:  cloak, so as to expose his uniform and the cross of St. Louis which was
Title:  suspended at his breast, Montcalm sternly demanded:
Title:  
Title:  What means this? Does not my son know that the hatchet is buried between the
Title:  English and his Canadian Father?
Title:  
Title:  What can the Hurons do? returned the savage, speaking also, though
Title:  imperfectly, in the French language.
Title:  
Title:  Not a warrior has a scalp, and the pale faces make friends!
Title:  
Title:  Ha, Le Renard Subtil! Methinks this is an excess of zeal for a friend who
Title:  was so late an enemy! How many suns have set since Le Renard struck the
Title:  war-post of the English?
Title:  
Title:  Where is that sun? demanded the sullen savage. Behind the hill; and it is
Title:  dark and cold. But when he comes again, it will be bright and warm. Le
Title:  Subtil is the sun of his tribe. There have been clouds, and many mountains
Title:  between him and his nation; but now he shines and it is a clear sky!
Title:  
Title:  That Le Renard has power with his people, I well know, said Montcalm; for
Title:  yesterday he hunted for their scalps, and to-day they hear him at the
Title:  council-fire.
Title:  
Title:  Magua is a great chief.
Title:  
Title:  Let him prove it, by teaching his nation how to conduct themselves toward
Title:  our new friends.
Title:  
Title:  Why did the chief of the Canadas bring his young men into the woods, and
Title:  fire his cannon at the earthen house? demanded the subtle Indian.
Title:  
Title:  To subdue it. My master owns the land, and your father was ordered to drive
Title:  off these English squatters. They have consented to go, and now he calls
Title:  them enemies no longer.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis well. Magua took the hatchet to color it with blood. It is now bright;
Title:  when it is red, it shall be buried.
Title:  
Title:  But Magua is pledged not to sully the lilies of France. The enemies of the
Title:  great king across the salt lake are his enemies; his friends, the friends of
Title:  the Hurons.
Title:  
Title:  Friends! repeated the Indian in scorn. Let his father give Magua a hand.
Title:  
Title:  Montcalm, who felt that his influence over the warlike tribes he had
Title:  gathered was to be maintained by concession rather than by power, complied
Title:  reluctantly with the other's request. The savage placed the fingers of the
Title:  French commander on a deep scar in his bosom, and then exultingly demanded:
Title:  
Title:  Does my father know that?
Title:  
Title:  What warrior does not? 'Tis where a leaden bullet has cut.
Title:  
Title:  And this? continued the Indian, who had turned his naked back to the other,
Title:  his body being without its usual calico mantle.
Title:  
Title:  This! - my son has been sadly injured here; who has done this?
Title:  
Title:  Magua slept hard in the English wigwams, and the sticks have left their
Title:  mark, returned the savage, with a hollow laugh, which did not conceal the
Title:  fierce temper that nearly choked him. Then, recollecting himself, with
Title:  sudden and native dignity, he added: Go; teach your young men it is peace.
Title:  Le Renard Subtil knows how to speak to a Huron warrior.
Title:  
Title:  Without deigning to bestow further words, or to wait for any answer, the
Title:  savage cast his rifle into the hollow of his arm, and moved silently through
Title:  the encampment toward the woods where his own tribe was known to lie. Every
Title:  few yards as he proceeded he was challenged by the sentinels; but he stalked
Title:  sullenly onward, utterly disregarding the summons of the soldiers, who only
Title:  spared his life because they knew the air and tread no less than the
Title:  obstinate daring of an Indian.
Title:  
Title:  Montcalm lingered long and melancholy on the strand where he had been left
Title:  by his companion, brooding deeply on the temper which his ungovernable ally
Title:  had just discovered. Already had his fair fame been tarnished by one horrid
Title:  scene, and in circumstances fearfully resembling those under which he how
Title:  found himself. As he mused he became keenly sensible of the deep
Title:  responsibility they assume who disregard the means to attain the end, and of
Title:  all the danger of setting in motion an engine which it exceeds human power
Title:  to control. Then shaking off a train of reflections that he accounted a
Title:  weakness in such a moment of triumph, he retraced his steps toward his tent,
Title:  giving the order as he passed to make the signal that should arouse the army
Title:  from its slumbers.
Title:  
Title:  The first tap of the French drums was echoed from the bosom of the fort, and
Title:  presently the valley was filled with the strains of martial music, rising
Title:  long, thrilling and lively above the rattling accompaniment. The horns of
Title:  the victors sounded merry and cheerful flourishes, until the last laggard of
Title:  the camp was at his post; but the instant the British fifes had blown their
Title:  shrill signal, they became mute. In the meantime the day had dawned, and
Title:  when the line of the French army was ready to receive its general, the rays
Title:  of a brilliant sun were glancing along the glittering array. Then that
Title:  success, which was already so well known, was officially announced; the
Title:  favored band who were selected to guard the gates of the fort were detailed,
Title:  and defiled before their chief; the signal of their approach was given, and
Title:  all the usual preparations for a change of masters were ordered and executed
Title:  directly under the guns of the contested works.
Title:  
Title:  A very different scene presented itself within the lines of the
Title:  Anglo-American army. As soon as the warning signal was given, it exhibited
Title:  all the signs of a hurried and forced departure. The sullen soldiers
Title:  shouldered their empty tubes and fell into their places, like men whose
Title:  blood had been heated by the past contest, and who only desired the
Title:  opportunity to revenge an indignity which was still wounding to their pride,
Title:  concealed as it was under the observances of military etiquette.
Title:  
Title:  Women and children ran from place to place, some bearing the scanty remnants
Title:  of their baggage, and others searching in the ranks for those countenances
Title:  they looked up to for protection.
Title:  
Title:  Munro appeared among his silent troops firm but dejected. It was evident
Title:  that the unexpected blow had struck deep into his heart, though he struggled
Title:  to sustain his misfortune with the port of a man.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan was touched at the quiet and impressive exhibition of his grief. He
Title:  had discharged his own duty, and he now pressed to the side of the old man,
Title:  to know in what particular he might serve him.
Title:  
Title:  My daughters, was the brief but expressive reply.
Title:  
Title:  Good heavens! are not arrangements already made for their convenience?
Title:  
Title:  To-day I am only a soldier, Major Heyward, said the veteran. All that you
Title:  see here, claim alike to be my children.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan had heard enough. Without losing one of those moments which had now
Title:  become so precious, he flew toward the quarters of Munro, in quest of the
Title:  sisters. He found them on the threshold of the low edifice, already prepared
Title:  to depart, and surrounded by a clamorous and weeping assemblage of their own
Title:  sex, that had gathered about the place, with a sort of instinctive
Title:  consciousness that it was the point most likely to be protected. Though the
Title:  cheeks of Cora were pale and her countenance anxious, she had lost none of
Title:  her firmness; but the eyes of Alice were inflamed, and betrayedhow long and
Title:  bitterly she had wept. They both, however, received the young man with
Title:  undisguised pleasure; the former, for a novelty, being the first to speak.
Title:  
Title:  The fort is lost, she said, with a melancholy smile; though our good name, I
Title:  trust, remains.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis brighter than ever. But, dearest Miss Munro, it is time to think less
Title:  of others, and to make some provision for yourself. Military usage - pride -
Title:  that pride on which you so much value yourself, demands that your father and
Title:  I should for a little while continue with the troops. Then where to seek a
Title:  proper protector for you against the confusion and chances of such a scene?
Title:  
Title:  None is necessary, returned Cora; who will dare to injure or insult the
Title:  daughter of such a father, at a time like this?
Title:  
Title:  I would not leave you alone, continued the youth, looking about him in a
Title:  hurried manner, for the command of the best regiment in the pay of the king.
Title:  Remember, our Alice is not gifted with all your firmness, and God only knows
Title:  the terror she might endure.
Title:  
Title:  You may be right, Cora replied, smiling again, but far more sadly than
Title:  before. Listen! chance has already sent us a friend when he is most needed.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan did listen, and on the instant comprehended her meaning. The low and
Title:  serious sounds of the sacred music, so well known to the eastern provinces,
Title:  caught his ear, and instantly drew him to an apartment in an adjacent
Title:  building, which had already been deserted by its customary tenants. There he
Title:  found David, pouring out his pious feelings through the only medium in which
Title:  he ever indulged. Duncan waited, until, by the cessation of the movement of
Title:  the hand, he believed the strain was ended, when, by touching his shoulder,
Title:  he drew the attention of the other to himself, and in a few words explained
Title:  his wishes.
Title:  
Title:  Even so, replied the single-minded disciple of the King of Israel, when the
Title:  young man had ended; I have found much that is comely and melodious in the
Title:  maidens, and it is fitting that we who have consorted in so much peril,
Title:  should abide together in peace. I will attend them, when I have completed my
Title:  morning praise, to which nothing is now wanting but the doxology. Wilt thou
Title:  bear a part, friend? The meter is common, and the tune Southwell.
Title:  
Title:  Then, extending the little volume, and giving the pitch of the air anew with
Title:  considerate attention, David recommenced and finished his strains, with a
Title:  fixedness of manner that it was not easy to interrupt. Heyward was fain to
Title:  wait until the verse ws ended; when, seeing David relieving himself from the
Title:  spectacles, and replacing the book, he continued.
Title:  
Title:  It will be your duty to see that none dare to approach the ladies with any
Title:  rude intention, or to offer insult or taunt at the misfortune of their brave
Title:  father. In this task you will be seconded by the domestics of their
Title:  household.
Title:  
Title:  Even so.
Title:  
Title:  It is possible that the Indians and stragglers of the enemy may intrude, in
Title:  which case you will remind them of the terms of the capitulation, and
Title:  threaten to report their conduct to Montcalm. A word will suffice.
Title:  
Title:  If not, I have that here which shall, returned David, exhibiting his book,
Title:  with an air in which meekness and confidence were singularly blended. Here
Title:  are words which, uttered, or rather thundered, with proper emphasis, and in
Title:  measured time, shall quiet the most unruly temper:
Title:  
Title:       Why rage the heathen furiously?
Title:  
Title:  Enough, said Heyward, interrupting the burst of his musical invocation; we
Title:  understand each other; it is time that we should now assume our respective
Title:  duties.
Title:  
Title:  Gamut cheerfully assented, and together they sought the females. Cora
Title:  received her new and somewhat extraordinary protector courteously, at least;
Title:  and even the pallid features of Alice lighted again with some of their
Title:  native archness as she thanked Heyward for his care. Duncan took occasion to
Title:  assure them he had done the best that circumstances permitted, and, as he
Title:  believed, quite enough for the security of their feelings; of danger there
Title:  was none. He then spoke gladly of his intention to rejoin them the moment he
Title:  had led the advance a few miles toward the Hudson, and immediately took his
Title:  leave.
Title:  
Title:  By this time the signal for departure had been given, and the head of the
Title:  English column was in motion. The sisters started at the sound, and glancing
Title:  their eyes around, they saw the white uniforms of the French grenadiers, who
Title:  had already taken possession of the gates of the fort. At that moment an
Title:  enormous cloud seemed to pass suddenly above their heads, and, looking
Title:  upward, they discovered that they stood beneath the wide folds of the
Title:  standard of France.
Title:  
Title:  Let us go, said Cora; this is no longer a fit place for the children of an
Title:  English officer.
Title:  
Title:  Alice clung to the arm of her sister, and together they left the parade,
Title:  accompanied by the moving throng that surrounded them.
Title:  
Title:  As they passed the gates, the French officers, who had learned their rank,
Title:  bowed often and low, forbearing, however, to intrude those attentions which
Title:  they saw, with peculiar tact, might not be agreeable. As every vehicle and
Title:  each beast of burden was occupied by the sick and wounded, Cora had decided
Title:  to endure the fatigues of a foot march, rather than interfere with their
Title:  comforts. Indeed, many a maimed and feeble soldier was compelled to drag his
Title:  exhausted limbs in the rear of the columns, for the want of the necessary
Title:  means of conveyance in that wilderness. The whole, however, was in motion;
Title:  the weak and wounded, groaning and in suffering; their comrades silent and
Title:  sullen; and the women and children in terror, they knew not of what.
Title:  
Title:  As the confused and timid throng left the protecting mounds of the fort, and
Title:  issued on the open plain, the whole scene was at once presented to their
Title:  eyes. At a little distance on the right, and somewhat in the rear, the
Title:  French army stood to their arms, Montcalm having collected his parties, so
Title:  soon as his guards had possession of the works. They were attentive but
Title:  silent observers of the proceedings of the vanquished, failing in none of
Title:  the stipulated military honors, and offering no taunt or insult, in their
Title:  success, to their less fortunate foes. Living masses of the English, to the
Title:  amount, in the whole, of near three thousand, were moving slowly across the
Title:  plain, toward the common center, and gradually approached each other, as
Title:  they converged to the point of their march, a vista cut through the lofty
Title:  trees, where the road to the Hudson entered the forest. Along the sweeping
Title:  borders of the woods hung a dark cloud of savages, eyeing the passage of
Title:  their enemies, and hovering at a distance, like vultures who were only kept
Title:  from swooping on their prey by the presence and restraint of a superior
Title:  army. A few had straggled among the conquered columns, where they stalked in
Title:  sullen discontent; attentive, though, as yet, passive observers of the
Title:  moving multitude.
Title:  
Title:  The advance, with Heyward at its head, had already reached the defile, and
Title:  was slowly disappearing, when the attention of Cora was drawn to a
Title:  collection of stragglers by the sounds of contention. A truant provincial
Title:  was paying the forfeit of his disobedience, by being plundered of those very
Title:  effects which had caused him to desert his place in the ranks. The man was
Title:  of powerful frame, and too avaricious to part with his goods without a
Title:  struggle. Individuals from either party interfered; the one side to prevent
Title:  and the other to aid in the robbery. Voices grew loud and angry, and a
Title:  hundred savages appeared, as it were, by magic, where a dozen only had been
Title:  seen a minute before. It was then that Cora saw the form of Magua gliding
Title:  among his countrymen, and speaking with his fatal and artful eloquence. The
Title:  mass of women and children stopped, and hovered together like alarmed and
Title:  fluttering birds. But the cupidity of the Indian was soon gratified, and the
Title:  different bodies again moved slowly onward.
Title:  
Title:  The savages now fell back, and seemed content to let their enemies advance
Title:  without further molestation. But, as the female crowd approached them, the
Title:  gaudy colors of a shawl attracted the eyes of a wild and untutored Huron. He
Title:  advanced to seize it without the least hesitation. The woman, more in terror
Title:  than through love of the ornament, wrapped her child in the coveted article,
Title:  and folded both more closely to her bosom. Cora was in the act of speaking,
Title:  with an intent to advise the woman to abandon the trifle, when the savage
Title:  relinquished his hold of the shawl, and tore the screaming infant from her
Title:  arms. Abandoning everything to the greedy grasp of those around her, the
Title:  mother darted, with distraction in her mien, to reclaim her child. The
Title:  Indian smiled grimly, and extended one hand, in sign of a willingness to
Title:  exchange, while, with the other, he flourished the babe over his head,
Title:  holding it by the feet as if to enhance the value of the ransom.
Title:  
Title:  Here - here - there - all - any - everything! exclaimed the breathless
Title:  woman, tearing the lighter articles of dress from her person with
Title:  ill-directed and trembling fingers; take all, but give me my babe!
Title:  
Title:  The savage spurned the worthless rags, and perceiving that the shawl had
Title:  already become a prize to another, his bantering but sullen smile changing
Title:  to a gleam of ferocity, he dashed the head of the infant against a rock, and
Title:  cast its quivering remains to her very feet. For an instant the mother
Title:  stood, like a statue of despair, looking wildly down at the unseemly object,
Title:  which had so lately nestled in her bosom and smiled in her face; and then
Title:  she raised her eyes and countenance toward heaven, as if calling on God to
Title:  curse the perpetrator of the foul deed. She was spared the sin of such a
Title:  prayer for, maddened at his disappointment, and excited at the sight of
Title:  blood, the Huron mercifully drove his tomahawk into her own brain. The
Title:  mother sank under the blow, and fell, grasping at her child, in death, with
Title:  the same engrossing love that had caused her to cherish it when living.
Title:  
Title:  At that dangerous moment, Magua placed his hands to his mouth, and raised
Title:  the fatal and appalling whoop. The scattered Indians started at the
Title:  well-known cry, as coursers bound at the signal to quit the goal; and
Title:  directly there arose such a yell along the plain, and through the arches of
Title:  the wood, as seldom burst from human lips before. They who heard it listened
Title:  with a curdling horror at the heart, little inferior to that dread which may
Title:  be expected to attend the blasts of the final summons.
Title:  
Title:  More than two thousand raving savages broke from the forest at the signal,
Title:  and threw themselves across the fatal plain with instinctive alacrity. We
Title:  shall not dwell on the revolting horrors that succeeded. Death was
Title:  everywhere, and in his most terrific and disgusting aspects. Resistance only
Title:  served to inflame the murderers, who inflicted their furious blows long
Title:  after their victims were beyond the power of their resentment. The flow of
Title:  blood might be likened to the outbreaking of a torrent; and as the natives
Title:  became heated and maddened by the sight, many among them even kneeled to the
Title:  earth, and drank freely, exultingly, hellishly, of the crimson tide.
Title:  
Title:  The trained bodies of the troops threw themselves quickly into solid masses,
Title:  endeavoring to awe their assailants by the imposing appearance of a military
Title:  front. The experiment in some measure succeeded, though far too many
Title:  suffered their unloaded muskets to be torn from their hands, in the vain
Title:  hope of appeasing the savages.
Title:  
Title:  In such a scene none had leisure to note the fleeting moments. It might have
Title:  been ten minutes (it seemed an age) that the sisters had stood riveted to
Title:  one spot, horror-stricken and nearly helpless. When the first blow was
Title:  struck, their screaming companions had pressed upon them in a body,
Title:  rendering flight impossible; and now that fear or death had scattered most,
Title:  if not all, from around them, they saw no avenue open, but such as conducted
Title:  to the tomahawks of their foes. On every side arose shrieks, groans,
Title:  exhortations and curses. At this moment, Alice caught a glimpse of the vast
Title:  form of her father, moving rapidly across the plain, in the direction of the
Title:  French army. He was, in truth, proceeding to Montcalm, fearless of every
Title:  danger, to claim the tardy escort for which he had before conditioned. Fifty
Title:  glittering axes and barbed spears were offered unheeded at his life, but the
Title:  savages respected his rank and calmness, even in their fury. The dangerous
Title:  weapons were brushed aside by the still nervous arm of the veteran, or fell
Title:  of themselves, after menacing an act that it would seem no one had courage
Title:  to perform. Fortunately, the vindictive Magua was searching for his victim
Title:  in the very band the veteran hd just quitted.
Title:  
Title:  Father - father - we are here! shrieked Alice, as he passed, at no great
Title:  distance, without appearing to heed them. Come to us, father, or we die!
Title:  
Title:  The cry was repeated, and in terms and tones that might have melted a heart
Title:  of stone, but it was unanswered. Once, indeed, the old man appeared to catch
Title:  the sound, for he paused and listened; but Alice had dropped senseless on
Title:  the earth, and Cora had sunk at her side, hovering in untiring tenderness
Title:  over her lifeless form. Munro shook his head in disappointment, and
Title:  proceeded, bent on the high duty of his station.
Title:  
Title:  Lady, said Gamut, who, helpless and useless as he was, had not yet dreamed
Title:  of deserting his trust, it is the jubilee of the devils, and this is not a
Title:  meet place for Christians to tarry in. Let us up and fly.
Title:  
Title:  Go, said Cora, still gazing at her unconscious sister; save thyself. To me
Title:  thou canst not be of further use.
Title:  
Title:  David comprehended the unyielding character of her resolution, by the simple
Title:  but expressive gesture that accompanied her words. He gazed for a moment at
Title:  the dusky forms that were acting their hellish rites on every side of him,
Title:  and his tall person grew more erect while his chest heaved, and every
Title:  feature swelled, and seemed to speak with the power of the feelings by which
Title:  he was governed.
Title:  
Title:  If the Jewish boy might tame the great spirit of Saul by the sound of his
Title:  harp, and the words of sacred song, it may not be amiss, he said, to try the
Title:  potency of music here.
Title:  
Title:  Then raising his voice to its highest tone, he poured out a strain so
Title:  powerful as to be heard even amid the din of that bloody field. More than
Title:  one savage rushed toward them, thinking to rifle the unprotected sisters of
Title:  their attire, and bear away their scalps; but when they found this strange
Title:  and unmoved figure riveted to his post, they paused to listen. Astonishment
Title:  soon changed to admiration, and they passed on to other and less courageous
Title:  victims, openly expressing their satisfaction at the firmness with which the
Title:  white warrior sang his death song. Encouraged and deluded by his success,
Title:  David exerted all his powers to extend what he believed so holy an
Title:  influence. The unwonted sounds caught the ears of a distant savage, who flew
Title:  raging from group to group, like one who, scorning to touch the vulgar herd,
Title:  hunted for some victim more worthy of his renown. It was Magua, who uttered
Title:  a yell of pleasure when he beheld his ancient prisoners again at his mercy.
Title:  
Title:  Come, he said, laying his soiled hands on the dress of Cora, the wigwam of
Title:  the Huron is still open. Is it not better than this place?
Title:  
Title:  Away! cried Cora, veiling her eyes from his revolting aspect.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian laughed tauntingly, as he held up his reeking hand, and answered:
Title:  It is red, but it comes from white veins!
Title:  
Title:  Monster! there is blood, oceans of blood, upon thy soul; thy spirit has
Title:  moved this scene.
Title:  
Title:  Magua is a great chief! returned the exulting savage, will the dark-hair go
Title:  to his tribe?
Title:  
Title:  Never! strike if thou wilt, and complete thy revenge. He hesitated a moment,
Title:  and then catching the light and senseless form of Alice in his arms, the
Title:  subtle Indian moved swiftly across the plain toward the woods.
Title:  
Title:  Hold! shrieked Cora, following wildly on his footsteps; release the child!
Title:  wretch! what is't you do?
Title:  
Title:  But Magua was deaf to her voice; or, rather, he knew his power, and was
Title:  determined to maintain it.
Title:  
Title:  Stay - lady - stay, called Gamut, after the unconscious Cora. The holy charm
Title:  is beginning to be felt, and soon shalt thou see this horrid tumult stilled.
Title:  
Title:  Perceiving that, in his turn, he was unheeded, the faithful David followed
Title:  the distracted sister, raising his voice again in sacred song, and sweeping
Title:  the air to the measure, with his long arm, in diligent accompaniment. In
Title:  this manner they traversed the plain, through the flying, the wounded and
Title:  the dead. The fierce Huron was, at any time, sufficient for himself and the
Title:  victim that he bore; though Cora would have fallen more than once under the
Title:  blows of her savage enemies, but for the extraordinary being who stalked in
Title:  her rear, and who now appeared to the astonished natives gifted with the
Title:  protecting spirit of madness.
Title:  
Title:  Magua, who knew how to avoid the more pressing dangers, and also to elude
Title:  pursuit, entered the woods through a low ravine, where he quickly found the
Title:  Narragansetts, which the travelers had abandoned so shortly before, awaiting
Title:  his appearance, in custody of a savage as fierce and malign in his
Title:  expression as himself. Laying Alice on one of the horses, he made a sign to
Title:  Cora to mount the other.
Title:  
Title:  Notwithstanding the horror excited by the presence of her captor, there was
Title:  a present relief in escaping from the bloody scene enacting on the plain, to
Title:  which Cora could not be altogether insensible. She took her seat, and held
Title:  forth her arms for her sister, with an air of entreaty and love that even
Title:  the Huron could not deny. Placing Alice, then, on the same animal with Cora,
Title:  he seized the bridle, and commenced his route by plunging deeper into the
Title:  forest. David, perceiving that he was left alone, utterly disregarded as a
Title:  subject too worthless even to destroy, threw his long limb across the saddle
Title:  of the beast they had deserted, and made such progress in the pursuit as the
Title:  difficulties of the path permitted.
Title:  
Title:  They soon began to ascend; but as the motion had a tendency to revive the
Title:  dormant faculties of her sister, the attention of Cora was too much divided
Title:  between the tenderest solicitude in her behalf, and in listening to the
Title:  cries which were still too audible on the plain, to note the direction in
Title:  which they journeyed. When, however, they gained the flattened surface of
Title:  the mountain-top, and approached the eastern precipice, she recognized the
Title:  spot to which she had once before been led under the more friendly auspices
Title:  of the scout. Here Magua suffered them to dismount; and notwithstanding
Title:  their own captivity, the curiosity which seems inseparable from horror,
Title:  induced them to gaze at the sickening sight below.
Title:  
Title:  The cruel work was still unchecked. On every side the captured were flying
Title:  before their relentless persecutors, while the armed columns of the
Title:  Christian king stood fast in an apathy which has never been explained, and
Title:  which has left an immovable blot on the otherwise fair escutcheon of their
Title:  leader. Nor was the sword of death stayed until cupidity got the mastery of
Title:  revenge. Then, indeed, the shrieks of the wounded, and the yells of their
Title:  murderers grew less frequent, until, finally, the cries of horror were lost
Title:  to their ear, or were drowned in the loud, long and piercing whoops of the
Title:  triumphant savages. 1

Title:  
Title:  1 The accounts of the number who fell in this unhappy affair vary between
Title:  five and fifteen hundred.

Title:  Chapter 18
Title:  
Title:       Why, anything;
Title:       An honorable murderer, if you will;
Title:       For naught I did in hate, but all in honor.
Title:  
Title:                                                                 OTHELLO
Title:  
Title:  The bloody and inhuman scene rather incidentally mentioned than described in
Title:  the preceding chapter, is conspicuous in the pages of colonial history by
Title:  the merited title of The Massacre of William Henry. It so far deepened the
Title:  stain which a previous and very similar event had left upon the reputation
Title:  of the French commander that it was not entirely erased by his early and
Title:  glorious death. It is now becoming obscured by time; and thousands, who know
Title:  that Montcalm died like a hero on the plains of Abraham, have yet to learn
Title:  how much he was deficient in that moral courage without which no man can be
Title:  truly great. Pages might be written to prove, from this illustrious example,
Title:  the defects of human excellence; to show how easy it is for generous
Title:  sentiments, high courtesy, and chivalrous courage to lose their influence
Title:  beneath the chilling blight of selfishness, and to exhibit to the world a
Title:  man who was great in all the minor attributes of character, but who was
Title:  found wanting when it became necessary to prove how much principle is
Title:  superior to policy. But the task would exceed our prerogatives; and, as
Title:  history, like love, is so apt to surround her heroes with an atmosphere of
Title:  imaginary brightness, it is probable that Louis de Saint Veran will be
Title:  viewed by posterity only as the gallant defender of his country, while his
Title:  cruel apathy on the shores of the Oswego and of the Horican will be
Title:  forgotten. Deeply regretting this weakness on the part of a sister muse, we
Title:  shall at once retire from her sacred precincts, within the proper limits of
Title:  our own humble vocation.
Title:  
Title:  The third day from the capture of the fort was drawing to a close, but the
Title:  business of the narrative must still detain the reader on the shores of the
Title:  holy lake. When last seen, the environs of the works were filled with
Title:  violence and uproar. They were now possessed by stillness and death. The
Title:  blood-stained conquerors had departed; and their camp, which had so lately
Title:  rung with the merry rejoicings of a victorious army, lay a silent and
Title:  deserted city of huts. The fortress was a smoldering ruin; charred rafters,
Title:  fragments of exploded artillery, and rent mason-work covering its earthen
Title:  mounds in confused disorder.
Title:  
Title:  A frightful change had also occurred in the season. The sun had hid its
Title:  warmth behind an impenetrable mass of vapor, and hundreds of human forms,
Title:  which had blackened beneath the fierce heats of August, were stiffening in
Title:  their deformity before the blasts of a premature November. The curling and
Title:  spotless mists, which had been seen sailing above the hills toward the
Title:  north, were now returning in an interminable dusky sheet, that was urged
Title:  along by the fury of a tempest. The crowded mirror of the Horican was gone;
Title:  and, in its place, the green and angry waters lashed the shores, as if
Title:  indignantly casting back its impurities to the polluted strand. Still the
Title:  clear fountain retained a portion of its charmed influence, but it reflected
Title:  only the somber gloom that fell from the impending heavens. That humid and
Title:  congenial atmosphere which commonly adorned the view, veiling its harshness,
Title:  and softening its asperities, had disappeared, the northern air poured
Title:  across the waste of water so harsh and unmingled, that nothing was left to
Title:  be conjectured by the eye, or fashioned by the fancy.
Title:  
Title:  The fiercer element had cropped the verdure of the plain, which looked as
Title:  though it were scathed by the consuming lightning. But, here and there, a
Title:  dark green tuft rose in the midst of the desolation; the earliest fruits of
Title:  a soil that had been fattened with human blood. The whole landscape, which,
Title:  seen by a favoring light, and in a genial temperature, had been found so
Title:  lovely, appeared now like some pictured allegory of life, in which objects
Title:  were arrayed in their harshest but truest colors, and without the relief of
Title:  any shadowing.
Title:  
Title:  The solitary and arid blades of grass arose from the passing gusts fearfully
Title:  perceptible; the bold and rocky mountains were too distinct in their
Title:  barrenness, and the eye even sought relief, in vain, by attempting to pierce
Title:  the illimitable void of heaven, which was shut to its gaze by the dusky
Title:  sheet of ragged and driving vapor.
Title:  
Title:  The wind blew unequally; sometimes sweeping heavily along the ground,
Title:  seeming to whisper its moanings in the cold ears of the dead, then rising in
Title:  a shrill and mournful whistling, it entered the forest with a rush that
Title:  filled the air with the leaves and branches it scattered in its path. Amid
Title:  the unnatural shower, a few hungry ravens struggled with the gale; but no
Title:  sooner was the green ocean of woods which stretched beneath them, passed,
Title:  than they gladly stopped, at random, to their hideous banquet.
Title:  
Title:  In short, it was a scene of wildness and desolation; and it appeared as if
Title:  all who had profanely entered it had been stricken, at a blow, by the
Title:  relentless arm of death. But the prohibition had ceased; and for the first
Title:  time since the perpetrators of those foul deeds which had assisted to
Title:  disfigure the scene were gone, living human beings had now presumed to
Title:  approach the place.
Title:  
Title:  About an hour before the setting of the sun, on the day already mentioned,
Title:  the forms of five men might have been seen issuing from the narrow vista of
Title:  trees, where the path to the Hudson entered the forest, and advancing in the
Title:  direction of the ruined works. At first their progress was slow and guarded,
Title:  as though they entered with reluctance amid the horrors of the post, or
Title:  dreaded the renewal of its frightful incidents. A light figure preceded the
Title:  rest of the party, with the caution and activity of a native; ascending
Title:  every hillock to reconnoiter, and indicating by gestures, to his companions,
Title:  the route he deemed it most prudent to pursue. Nor were those in the rear
Title:  wanting in every caution and foresight known to forest warfare. One among
Title:  them, he also was an Indian, moved a little on one flank, and watched the
Title:  margin of the woods, with eyes long accustomed to read the smallest sign of
Title:  danger. The remaining three were white, though clad in vestments adapted,
Title:  both in quality and color, to their present hazardous pursuit - that of
Title:  hanging on the skirts of a retiring army in the wilderness.
Title:  
Title:  The effects produced by the appalling sights that constantly arose in their
Title:  path to the lake shore, were as different as the characters of the
Title:  respective individuals who composed the party. The youth in front threw
Title:  serious but furtive glances at the mangled victims, as he stepped lightly
Title:  across the plain, afraid to exhibit his feelings, and yet too inexperienced
Title:  to quell entirely their sudden and powerful influence. His red associate,
Title:  however, was superior to such a weakness. He passed the groups of dead with
Title:  a steadiness of purpose, and an eye so calm, that nothing but long and
Title:  inveterate practise could enable him to maintain. The sensations produced in
Title:  the minds of even the white men were different, though uniformly sorrowful.
Title:  One, whose gray locks and furrowed lineaments, blending with a martial air
Title:  and tread, betrayed, in spite of the disguise of a woodsman's dress, a man
Title:  long experienced in scenes of war, was not ashamed to groan aloud, whenever
Title:  a spectacle of more than usual horror came under his view. The young man at
Title:  his elbow shuddered, but seemed to suppress his feelings in tenderness to
Title:  his companion. Of them all, the straggler who brought up the rear appeared
Title:  alone to betray his real thoughts, without fear of observation or dread of
Title:  consequences. He gazed at the most appalling sight with eyes and muscles
Title:  that knew not how to waver, but with execrations so bitter and deep as to
Title:  denote how much he denounced the crime of his enemies.
Title:  
Title:  The reader will perceive at once, in these respective characters, the
Title:  Mohicans, and their white friend, the scout; together with Munro and
Title:  Heyward. It was, in truth, the father in quest of his children, attended by
Title:  the youth who felt so deep a stake in their happiness, and those brave and
Title:  trusty foresters, who had already proved their skill and fidelity through
Title:  the trying scenes related.
Title:  
Title:  When Uncas, who moved in front, had reached the center of the plain, he
Title:  raised a cry that drew his companions in a body to the spot. The young
Title:  warrior had halted over a group of females who lay in a cluster, a confused
Title:  mass of dead. Notwithstanding the revolting horror of the exhibition, Munro
Title:  and Heyward flew toward the festering heap, endeavoring, with a love that no
Title:  unseemliness could extinguish, to discover whether any vestiges of those
Title:  they sought were to be seen among the tattered and many-colored garments.
Title:  The father and the lover found instant relief in the search; though each was
Title:  condemned again to experience the misery of an uncertainty that was hardly
Title:  less insupportable than the most revolting truth. They were standing, silent
Title:  and thoughtful, around the melancholy pile, when the scout approached.
Title:  Eyeing the sad spectacle with an angry countenance, the sturdy woodsman, for
Title:  the first time since his entering the plain, spoke intelligibly and aloud:
Title:  
Title:  I have been on many a shocking field, and have followed a trail of blood for
Title:  weary miles, he said, but never have I found the hand of the devil so plain
Title:  as it is here to be seen! Revenge is an Indian feeling, and all who know me
Title:  know that there is no cross in my veins; but this much will I say - here, in
Title:  the face of heaven, and with the power of the Lord so manifest in this
Title:  howling wilderness - that should these Frenchers ever trust themselves again
Title:  within the range of a ragged bullet, there is one rifle which shall play its
Title:  part so long as flint will fire or powder burn! I leave the tomahawk and
Title:  knife to such as have a natural gift to use them. What say you,
Title:  Chingachgook, he added, in Delaware; shall the Hurons boast of this to their
Title:  women when the deep snows come?
Title:  
Title:  A gleam of resentment flashed across the dark lineaments of the Mohican
Title:  chief; he loosened his knife in his sheath; and then turning calmly from the
Title:  sight, his countenance settled into a repose as deep as if he knew the
Title:  instigation of passion.
Title:  
Title:  Montcalm! Montcalm! continued the deeply resentful and less self-restrained
Title:  scout; they say a time must come when all the deeds done in the flesh will
Title:  be seen at a single look; and that by eyes cleared from mortal infirmities.
Title:  Woe betide the wretch who is born to behold this plain, with the judgment
Title:  hanging about his soul! Ha - as I am a man of white blood, yonder lies a
Title:  red-skin, without the hair of his head where nature rooted it! Look to him,
Title:  Delaware; it may be one of your missing people; and he should have burial
Title:  like a stout warrior. I see it in your eye, Sagamore; a Huron pays for this,
Title:  afore the fall winds have blown away the scent of the blood!
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook approached the mutilated form, and, turning it over, he found
Title:  the distinguishing marks of one of those six allied tribes, or nations, as
Title:  they were called, who, while they fought in the English ranks, were so
Title:  deadly hostile to his own people. Spurning the loathsome object with his
Title:  foot, he turned from it with the same indifference he would have quitted a
Title:  brute carcass. The scout comprehended the action, and very deliberately
Title:  pursued his own way, continuing, however, his denunciations against the
Title:  French commander in the same resentful strain.
Title:  
Title:  Nothing but vast wisdom and unlimited power should dare to sweep off men in
Title:  multitudes, he added; for it is only the one that can know the necessity of
Title:  the judgment; and what is there, short of the other, that can replace the
Title:  creatures of the Lord? I hold it a sin to kill the second buck afore the
Title:  first is eaten, unless a march in front, or an ambushment, be contemplated.
Title:  It is a different matter with a few warriors in open and rugged fight, for
Title:  'tis their gift to die with the rifle or the tomahawk in hand; according as
Title:  their natures may happen to be, white or red. Uncas, come this way, lad, and
Title:  let the ravens settle upon the Mingo. I know, from often seeing it, that
Title:  they have a craving for the flesh of an Oneida; and it is as well to let the
Title:  bird follow the gift of its natural appetite.
Title:  
Title:  Hugh! exclaimed the young Mohican, rising on the extremities of his feet,
Title:  and gazing intently in his front, frightening the ravens to some other prey
Title:  by the sound and the action.
Title:  
Title:  What is it, boy? whispered the scout, lowering his tall form into a
Title:  crouching attitude, like a panther about to take his leap; God send it be a
Title:  tardy Frencher, skulking for plunder. I do believe killdeer would take an
Title:  uncommon range today!
Title:  
Title:  Uncas, without making any reply, bounded away from the spot, and in the next
Title:  instant he was seen tearing from a bush, and waving in triumph, a fragment
Title:  of the green riding-veil of Cora. The movement, the exhibition, and the cry
Title:  which again burst from the lips of the young Mohican, instantly drew the
Title:  whole party about him.
Title:  
Title:  My child! said Munro, speaking quickly and wildly; give me my child!
Title:  
Title:  Uncas will try, was the short and touching answer.
Title:  
Title:  The simple but meaning assurance was lost on the father, who seized the
Title:  piece of gauze, and crushed it in his hand, while his eyes roamed fearfully
Title:  among the bushes, as if he equally dreaded and hoped for the secrets they
Title:  might reveal.
Title:  
Title:  Here are no dead, sadi Heyward; the storm seems not to have passed this way.
Title:  
Title:  That's manifest; and clearer than the heavens above our heads, returned the
Title:  undisturbed scout; but either she, or they that have robbed her, have passed
Title:  the bush; for I remember the rag she wore to hide a face that all did love
Title:  to look upon. Uncas, you are right; the dark-hair has been here, and she has
Title:  fled like a frightened fawn, to the wood; none who could fly would remain to
Title:  be murdered. Let us search for the marks she left; for, to Indian eyes, I
Title:  sometimes think a humming-bird leaves his trail in the air.
Title:  
Title:  The young Mohican darted away at the suggestion, and the scout had hardly
Title:  done speaking, before the former raised a cry of success from the margin of
Title:  the forest. On reaching the spot, the anxious party perceived another
Title:  portion of the veil fluttering on the lower branch of a beech.
Title:  
Title:  Softly, softly, said the scout, extending his long rifle in front of the
Title:  eager Heyward; we now know our work, but the beauty of the trail must not be
Title:  deformed. A step too soon may give us hours of trouble. We have them,
Title:  though; that much is beyond denial.
Title:  
Title:  Bless ye, bless ye, worthy man! exclaimed Munro; whither then, have they
Title:  fled, and where are my babes?
Title:  
Title:  The path they have taken depends on many chances. If they have gone alone,
Title:  they are quite as likely to move in a circle as straight, and they may be
Title:  within a dozen miles of us; but if the Hurons, or any of the French Indians,
Title:  have laid hands on them, 'tis probably they are now near the borders of the
Title:  Canadas. But what matters that? continued the deliberate scout, observing
Title:  the powerful anxiety and disappointment the listeners exhibited; here are
Title:  the Mohicans and I on one end of the trail, and, rely on it, we find the
Title:  other, though they should be a hundred leagues asunder! Gently, gently,
Title:  Uncas, you are as impatient as a man in the settlements; you forget that
Title:  light feet leave but faint marks!
Title:  
Title:  Hugh! exclaimed Chingachgook, who had been occupied in examining an opening
Title:  that had been evidently made through the low underbrush which skirted the
Title:  forest; and who now stood erect, as he pointed downward, in the attitude and
Title:  with the air of a man who beheld a disgusting serpent.
Title:  
Title:  Here is the palpable impression of the footstep of a man, cried Heyward,
Title:  bending over the indicated spot; he has trod in the margin of this pool, and
Title:  the mark cannot be mistaken. They are captives.
Title:  
Title:  Better so than left to starve in the wilderness, returned the scout; and
Title:  they will leave a wider trail. I would wager fifty beaver skins against as
Title:  many flints, that the Mohicans and I enter their wigwams within the month!
Title:  Stoop to it, Uncas, and try what you can make of the moccasin; for moccasin
Title:  it plainly is, and no shoe.
Title:  
Title:  The young Mohican bent over the track, and removing the scattered leaves
Title:  from around the place, he examined it with much of that sort of scrutiny
Title:  that a money dealer, in these days of pecuniary doubts, would bestow on a
Title:  suspected due-bill. At length he arose from his knees, satisfied with the
Title:  result of the examination.
Title:  
Title:  Well, boy, demanded the attentive scout; what does it say? Can you make
Title:  anything of the tell-tale?
Title:  
Title:  Le Renard Subtil!
Title:  
Title:  Ha! that rampaging devil again! there will never be an end of his loping
Title:  till killdeer has said a friendly word to him.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward reluctantly admitted the truth of this intelligence, and now
Title:  expressed rather his hopes than his doubts by saying:
Title:  
Title:  One moccasin is so much like another, it is probable there is some mistake.
Title:  
Title:  One moccasin like another! you may as well say that one foot is like
Title:  another; though we all know that some are long, and others short; some broad
Title:  and others narrow; some with high, and some with low insteps; some intoed,
Title:  and some out. One moccasin is no more like another than one book is like
Title:  another: though they who can read in one are seldom able to tell the marks
Title:  of the other. Which is all ordered for the best, giving to every man his
Title:  natural advantages. Let me get down to it, Uncas; neither book nor moccasin
Title:  is the worse for having two opinions, instead of one. The scout stooped to
Title:  the task, and instantly added:
Title:  
Title:  You are right, boy; here is the patch we saw so often in the other chase.
Title:  And the fellow will drink when he can get an opportunity; your drinking
Title:  Indian always learns to walk with a wider toe than the natural savage, it
Title:  being the gift of a drunkard to straddle, whether of white or red skin. 'Tis
Title:  just the length and breadth, too! look at it, Sagamore; you measured the
Title:  prints more than once, when we hunted the varmints from Glenn's to the
Title:  health springs.
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook complied; and after finishing his short examination, he arose,
Title:  and with a quiet demeanor, he merely pronounced the word:
Title:  
Title:  Magua!
Title:  
Title:  Ay, 'tis a settled thing; here, then, have passed the dark-hair and Magua.
Title:  
Title:  And not Alice? demanded Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  Of her we have not yet seen the signs, returned the scout, looking closely
Title:  around at the trees, the bushes and the ground. What have we there? Uncas,
Title:  bring hither the thing you see dangling from yonder thorn-bush.
Title:  
Title:  When the Indian had complied, the scout received the prize, and holding it
Title:  on high, he laughed in his silent but heartfelt manner.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis the tooting we'pon of the singer! now we shall have a trail a priest
Title:  might travel, he said. Uncas, look for the marks of a shoe that is long
Title:  enough to uphold six feet two of tottering human flesh. I begin to have some
Title:  hopes of the fellow, since he has given up squalling to follow some better
Title:  trade.
Title:  
Title:  At least he has been faithful to his trust, said Heyward. And Cora and Alice
Title:  are not without a friend.
Title:  
Title:  Yes, said Hawkeye, dropping his rifle, and leaning on it with an air of
Title:  visible contempt, he will do their singing. Can he slay a buck for their
Title:  dinner; journey by the moss on the beeches, or cut the throat of a Huron? If
Title:  not, the first catbird1 he meets is the cleverer of the two. Well, boy, any
Title:  signs of such a foundation?
Title:  
Title:  Here is something like the footstep of one who has worn a shoe; can it be
Title:  that of our friend?
Title:  
Title:  Touch the leaves lightly or you'll disconsart the formation. That! that is
Title:  the print of a foot, but 'tis the dark-hair's; and small it is, too, for one
Title:  of such a noble height and grand appearance. The singer would cover it with
Title:  his heel.
Title:  
Title:  Where! let me look on the footsteps of my child, said Munro, shoving the
Title:  bushes aside, and bending fondly over the nearly obliterated impression.
Title:  Though the tread which had left the mark had been light and rapid, it ws
Title:  still plainly visible. The aged soldier examined it with eyes that grew dim
Title:  as he gazed; nor did he rise from this stooping posture until Heyward saw
Title:  that he had watered the trace of his daughter's passage with a scalding
Title:  tear. Willing to divert a distress which threatened each moment to break
Title:  through the restraint of appearances, by giving the veteran something to do,
Title:  the young man said to the scout:
Title:  
Title:  As we now possess these infallible signs, let us commence our march. A
Title:  moment, at such a time, will appear an age to the captives.
Title:  
Title:  It is not the swiftest leaping deer that gives the longest chase, returned
Title:  Hawkeye, without moving his eyes from the different marks that had come
Title:  under his view; we know that the rampaging Huron has passed, and the
Title:  dark-hair, and the singer, but where is she of the yellow locks and blue
Title:  eyes? Though little, and far from being as bold as her sister, she is fair
Title:  to the view, and pleasant in discourse. Has she no friend, that none care
Title:  for her?
Title:  
Title:  God forbid she should ever want hundreds! Are we not now in her pursuit? For
Title:  one, I will never cease the search till she be found.
Title:  
Title:  In that case we may have to journey by different paths; for here she has not
Title:  passed, light and little as her footsteps would be.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward drew back, all his ardor to proceed seeming to vanish on the
Title:  instant. Without attending to this sudden change in the other's humor, the
Title:  scout after musing a moment continued:
Title:  
Title:  There is no woman in this wilderness could leave such a print as that, but
Title:  the dark-hair or her sister. We know that the first has been here, but where
Title:  are the signs of the other? Let us push deeper on the trail, and if nothing
Title:  offers, we must go back to the plain and strike another scent. Move on,
Title:  Uncas, and keep your eyes on the dried leaves. I will watch the bushes,
Title:  while your father shall run with a low nose to the ground. Move on, friends;
Title:  the sun is getting behind the hills.
Title:  
Title:  Is there nothing that I can do? demanded the anxious Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  You? repeated the scout, who, with his red friends, was already advancing in
Title:  the order he had prescribed; yes, you can keep in our rear and be careful
Title:  not to cross the trail.
Title:  
Title:  Before they had proceeded many rods, the Indians stopped, and appeared to
Title:  gaze at some signs on the earth with more than their usual keenness. Both
Title:  father and son spoke quick and loud, now looking at the object of their
Title:  mutual admiration, and now regarding each other with the most unequivocal
Title:  pleasure.
Title:  
Title:  They have found the little foot! exclaimed the scout, moving forward,
Title:  without attending further to his own portion of the duty. What have we here?
Title:  An ambushment has been planted in the spot! No, by the truest rifle on the
Title:  frontiers, here have been them one-sided horses again! Now the whole secret
Title:  is out, and all is plain as the north star at midnight. Yes, here they have
Title:  mounted. There the beasts have been bound to a sapling, in waiting; and
Title:  yonder runs the broad path away to the north, in full sweep for the Canadas.
Title:  
Title:  But still there are no signs of Alice, of the younger Miss Munro, said
Title:  Duncan.
Title:  
Title:  Unless the shining bauble Uncas has just lifted from the ground should prove
Title:  one. Pass it this way, lad, that we may look at it.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward instantly knew it for a trinket that Alice was fond of wearing, and
Title:  which he recollected, with the tenacious memory of a lover, to have seen, on
Title:  the fatal morning of the massacre, dangling from the fair neck of his
Title:  mistress. He seized the highly prized jewel; and as he proclaimed the fact,
Title:  it vanished from the eyes of the wondering scout, who in vain looked for it
Title:  on the ground, long after it was warmly pressed against the beating heart of
Title:  Duncan.
Title:  
Title:  Pshaw! said the disappointed Hawkeye, ceasing to rake the leaves with the
Title:  breech of his rifle; 'tis a certain sign of age, when the sight begins to
Title:  weaken. Such a glittering gewgaw, and not to be seen! Well, well, I can
Title:  squint along a clouded barrel yet, and that is enough to settle all disputes
Title:  between me and the Mingoes. I should like to find the thing, too, if it were
Title:  only to carry it to the right owner, and that would be bringing the two ends
Title:  of what I call a long trail together, for by this time the broad St.
Title:  Lawrence, or perhaps, the Great Lakes themselves, are between us.
Title:  
Title:  So much the more reason why we should not delay our march, returned Heyward;
Title:  let us proceed.
Title:  
Title:  Young blood and hot blood, they say, are much the same thing. We are not
Title:  about to start on a squirrel hunt, or to drive a deer into the Horican, but
Title:  to outlie for days and nights, and to stretch across a wilderness where the
Title:  feet of men seldom go, and where no bookish knowledge would carry you
Title:  through harmless. An Indian never starts on such an expedition without
Title:  smoking over his council-fire; and, though a man of white blood, I honor
Title:  their customs in this particular, seeing that they are deliberate and wise.
Title:  We will, therefore, go back, and light our fire to-night in the ruins of the
Title:  old fort, and in the morning we shall be fresh, and ready to undertake our
Title:  work like men, and not like babbling women or eager boys.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward saw, by the manner of the scout, that altercation would be useless.
Title:  Munro had again sunk into that sort of apathy which had beset him since his
Title:  late overwhelming misfortunes, and from which he was apparently to be roused
Title:  only by some new and powerful excitement. Making a merit of necessity, the
Title:  young man took the veteran by the arm, and followed in the footsteps of the
Title:  Indians and the scout, who had already begun to retrace the path which
Title:  conducted them to the plain.

Title:  
Title:  1 The powers of the American mocking-bird are generally known. But the true
Title:  mocking-bird is not found so far north as the state of New York, where it
Title:  has, however, two substitutes of inferior excellence, the catbird, so often
Title:  named by the scout, and the bird vulgarly called ground-thresher. Either of
Title:  these last two birds is superior to the nightingale or the lark, though, in
Title:  general, the American birds are less musical than those of Europe.
