Title:  Chapter 19
Title:  
Title:       Salarino. - Why, I am sure, if he forfeit, thou wilt not take his
Title:       flesh; what's that good for?
Title:  
Title:       Shylock. - To bait fish withal; if it will feed nothing else, it
Title:       will feed my revenge.
Title:  
Title:                                                      MERCHANT OF VENICE
Title:  
Title:  The shades of evening had come to increase the dreariness of the place, when
Title:  the party entered the ruins of William Henry. The scout and his companions
Title:  immediately made their preparations to pass the night there; but with an
Title:  earnestness and sobriety of demeanor that betrayed how much the unusual
Title:  horrors they had just witnessed worked on even their practised feelings. A
Title:  few fragments of rafters were reared against a blackened wall; and when
Title:  Uncas had covered them slightly with brush, the temporary accommodations
Title:  were deemed sufficient. The young Indian point3ed toward his rude hut when
Title:  his labor was ended; and Heyward, who understood the meaning of the silent
Title:  gestures, gently urged Munro to enter. Leaving the bereaved old man alone
Title:  with his sorrows, Duncan immediately returned into the open air, too much
Title:  excited himself to seek the repose he had recommended to his veteran friend.
Title:  
Title:  While Hawkeye and the Indians lighted their fire and took their evening's
Title:  repast, a frugal meal of dried bear's meat, the young man paid a visit to
Title:  that curtain of the dilapidated fort which looked out on the sheet of the
Title:  Horican. The wind had fallen, and th e waves were already rolling on the
Title:  sandy beach beneath him, in a more regular and tempered succession. The
Title:  clouds, as if tired of their furious chase, were breaking asunder; the
Title:  heavier volumes, gathering in black masses about the horizon, while the
Title:  lighter scud still hurried above the water, or eddied among the tops of the
Title:  mountains, like broken flights of birds, hovering around their roosts. Here
Title:  and there, a red and fiery star struggled through the drifting vapor,
Title:  furnishing a lurid gleam of brightness to the dull aspect of the heavens.
Title:  Within the bosom of the encircling hills, an impenetrable darkness had
Title:  already settled; and the plain lay like a vast and deserted charnel-house,
Title:  without omen or whisper to disturb the slumbers of its numerous and hapless
Title:  tenants.
Title:  
Title:  Of this scene, so chillingly in accordance with the past, Duncan stood for
Title:  many minutes a rapt observer. His eyes wandered from the bosom of the mound,
Title:  where the foresters were seated around their glimmering fire, to the fainter
Title:  light which still lingered in the skies, and then rested long and anxiously
Title:  on the embodied gloom, which lay like a dreary void on that side of him
Title:  where the dead reposed. He soon fancied that inexplicable sounds arose from
Title:  the place, though so indistinct and stolen, as to render not only their
Title:  nature but even their existence uncertain. Ashamed of his apprehensions, the
Title:  young man turned toward the water, and strove to divert his attention to the
Title:  mimic stars that dimly glimmered on its moving surface. Still, his
Title:  too-conscious ears performed their ungrateful duty, as if to warn him of
Title:  some lurking danger. At length, a swift trampling seemed, quite audibly, to
Title:  rush athwart the darkness. Unable any longer to quiet his uneasiness, Duncan
Title:  spoke in a low voice to the scout, requesting him to ascend the mound to the
Title:  place where he stood. Hawkeye threw his rifle across an arm and complied,
Title:  but with an air so unmoved and calm, as to prove how much he counted on the
Title:  security of their position.
Title:  
Title:  Listen! said Duncan, when the other placed himself deliberately at his
Title:  elbow; there are suppressed noises on the plain which may show Montcalm has
Title:  not yet entirely deserted his conquest.
Title:  
Title:  Then ears are better than eyes, said the undisturbed scout, who, having just
Title:  deposited a portion of a bear between his grinders, spoke thick and slow,
Title:  like one whose mouth was doubly occupied. I myself saw him caged in Ty, with
Title:  all his host; for your Frenchers, when they have done a clever thing, like
Title:  to get back, and have a dance, or a merry-making, with the women over their
Title:  success.
Title:  
Title:  I know not. An Indian seldom sleeps in war, and plunder may keep a Huron
Title:  here after his tribe has departed. It would be well to extinguish the fire,
Title:  and have a watch - listen! you hear the noise I mean!
Title:  
Title:  An Indian more rarely lurks about the graves. Though ready to slay, and not
Title:  over regardful of the means, he is commonly content with the scalp, unless
Title:  when blood is hot, and temper up; but after spirit is once fairly gone, he
Title:  forgets his enmity, and is willling to let the dead find their natural rest.
Title:  Speaking of spirits, major, are you of opinion that the heaven of a red-skin
Title:  and of us whites will be of one and the same?
Title:  
Title:  No doubt - no doubt. I thought I heard it again! or was it the rustling of
Title:  the leaves in the top of the beech?
Title:  
Title:  For my own part, continued Hawkeye, turning his face for a moment in the
Title:  direction indicated by Heyward, but with a vacant and careless manner, I
Title:  believe that paradise is ordained for happiness; and that men will be
Title:  indulged in it according to their dispositions and gifts. I, therefore,
Title:  judge that a red-skin is not far from the truth when he believes he is to
Title:  find them glorious hunting grounds of which his traditions tell; nor, for
Title:  that matter, do I think it would be any disparagement to a man without a
Title:  cross to pass his time - -
Title:  
Title:  You hear it again? interrupted Duncan.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, ay; when food is scarce, and when food is plenty, a wolf grows bold,
Title:  said the unmoved scout. There would be picking, too, among the skins of the
Title:  devils, if there was light and time for the sport. But, concerning the life
Title:  that is to come, major; I have heard preachers say, in the settlements, that
Title:  heaven was a place of rest. Now, men's minds differ as to their ideas of
Title:  enjoyment. For myself, and I say it with reverence to the ordering of
Title:  Providence, it would be no great indulgence to be kept shut up in those
Title:  mansions of which they preach, having a natural longing for motion and the
Title:  chase.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, who was now made to understand the nature of the noise he had heard,
Title:  answered, with more attention to the subject which the humor of the scout
Title:  had chosen for discussion, by saying:
Title:  
Title:  It is difficult to account for the feelings that may attend the last great
Title:  change.
Title:  
Title:  It would be a change, indeed, for a man who has passed his days in the open
Title:  air, returned the single-minded scout; and who has so often broken his fast
Title:  on the head waters of the Hudson, to sleep within sound of the roaring
Title:  Mohawk. But it is a comfort to know we serve a merciful Master, though we do
Title:  it each after his fashion, and with great tracts of wilderness atween us -
Title:  what goes there?
Title:  
Title:  Is it not the rushing of the wolves you have mentioned?
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye slowly shook his head, and beckoned for Duncan to follow him to a
Title:  spot to which the glare from the fire did not extend. When he had taken this
Title:  precaution, the scout placed himself in an attitude of intense attention and
Title:  listened long and keenly for a repetition of the low sound that had so
Title:  unexpectedly startled him. His vigilance, however, seemed exercised in vain;
Title:  for after a fruitless pause, he whispered to Duncan:
Title:  
Title:  We must give a call to Uncas. The boy has Indian senses, and he may hear
Title:  what is hid from us; for, being a white-skin, I will not deny my nature.
Title:  
Title:  The young Mohican, who was conversing in a low voice with his father,
Title:  started as he heard the moaning of an owl, and, springing on his feet, he
Title:  looked toward the black mounds, as if seeking the place whence the sounds
Title:  proceeded. The scout repeated the call, and in a few moments, Duncan saw the
Title:  figure of Uncas stealing cautiously along the rampart, to the spot where
Title:  they stood.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye explained his wishes in a very few words, which were spoken in the
Title:  Delaware tongue. So soon as Uncas was in possession of the reason why he was
Title:  summoned, he threw himself flat on the turf; where, to the eyes of Duncan,
Title:  he appeared to lie quiet and motionless. Surprised at the immovable attitude
Title:  of the young warrior, and curious to observe the manner in which he employed
Title:  his faculties to obtain the desired information, Heyward advanced a few
Title:  steps, and bent over the dark object on which he had kept his eye riveted.
Title:  Then it was he discovered that the form of Uncas vanished, and that he
Title:  beheld only the dark outline of an inequality in the embankment.
Title:  
Title:  What has become of the Mohican? he demanded of the scout, stepping back in
Title:  amazement; it was here that I saw him fall, and could have sworn that here
Title:  he yet remained.
Title:  
Title:  Hist! speak lower; for we know not what ears are open, and the Mingoes are a
Title:  quick-witted breed. As for Uncas, he is out on the plain, and the Maquas, if
Title:  any such are about us, will find their equal.
Title:  
Title:  You think that Montcalm has not called off all his Indians? Let us give the
Title:  alarm to our companions, that we may stand to our arms. Here are five of us,
Title:  who are not unused to meet an enemy.
Title:  
Title:  Not a word to either, as you value your life. Look at the Sagamore, how like
Title:  a grand Indian chief he sits by the fire. If there are any skulkers out in
Title:  the darkness, they will never discover, by his countenance, that we suspect
Title:  danger at hand.
Title:  
Title:  But they may discover him, and it will prove his death. His person can be
Title:  too plainly seen by the light of that fire, and he will become the first and
Title:  most certain victim.
Title:  
Title:  It is undeniable that now you speak the truth, returned the scout, betraying
Title:  more anxiety than was usual; yet what can be done? A single suspicious look
Title:  might bring on an attack before we are ready to receive it. He knows, by the
Title:  call I gave to Uncas, that we have struck a scent; I will tell him that we
Title:  are on the trail of the Mingoes; his Indian nature will teach him how to
Title:  act.
Title:  
Title:  The scout applied his fingers to his mouth, and raised a low hissing sound,
Title:  that caused Duncan at first to start aside, believing that he heard a
Title:  serpent. The head of Chingachgook was resting on a hand, as he sat musing by
Title:  himself but the moment he had heard the warning of the animal whose name he
Title:  bore, he arose to an upright position, and his dark eyes glanced swiftly and
Title:  keenly on every side of him. With his sudden and, perhaps, involuntary
Title:  movement, every appearance of surprise or alarm ended. His rifle lay
Title:  untouched, and apparently unnoticed, within reach of his hand. The tomahawk
Title:  that he had loosened in his belt for the sake of ease, was even suffered to
Title:  fall from its usual situation to the ground, and his form seemed to sink,
Title:  like that of a man whose nerves and sinews were suffered to relax for the
Title:  purpose of rest. Cunningly resuming his former position, though with a
Title:  change of hands, as if the movement had been made merely to relieve the
Title:  limb, the native awaited the result with a calmness and fortitude that none
Title:  but an Indian warrior would have known how to exercise.
Title:  
Title:  But Heywad saw that while to a less instructed eye the Mohican chief
Title:  appeared to slumber, his nostrils were expanded, his head was turned a
Title:  little to one side, as if to assist the organs of hearing, and that his
Title:  quick and rapid glances ran incessantly over every object within the power
Title:  of his vision.
Title:  
Title:  See the noble fellow! whispered Hawkeye, pressing the arm of Heyward; he
Title:  knows that a look or a motion might disconsart our schemes, and put us at
Title:  the mercy of them imps - -
Title:  
Title:  He was interrupted by the flash and report of a rifle. The air was filled
Title:  with sparks of fire, around that spot where the eyes of Heyward wre still
Title:  fastened, with admiration and wonder. A second look told him that
Title:  Chingachgook had disappeared in the confusion. In the meantime, the scout
Title:  had thrown forward his rifle, like one prepared for service, and awaited
Title:  impatiently the moment when an enemy might rise to view. But with the
Title:  solitary and fruitless attempt made on the life of Chingachgook, the attack
Title:  appeared to have terminated. Once or twice the listeners thought they could
Title:  distinguish the distant rustling of bushes, as bodies of some unknown
Title:  description rushed through them; nor was it long before Hawkeye pointed out
Title:  the scampering of the wolves, as they fled precipitately before the passage
Title:  of some intruder on their proper domains. After an impatient and breathless
Title:  pause, a plunge was heard in the water, and it was immediately followed by
Title:  the report of another rifle.
Title:  
Title:  There goes Uncas! said the scout; the boy bears a smart piece! I know its
Title:  crack, as well as a father knows the language of his child, for I carried
Title:  the gun myself until a better offered.
Title:  
Title:  What can this mean? demanded Duncan, we are watched, and, as it would seem,
Title:  marked for destruction.
Title:  
Title:  Yonder scattered brand can witness that no good was intended, and this
Title:  Indian will testify that no harm has been done, returned the scout, dropping
Title:  his rifle across his arm again, and following Chingachgook, who just then
Title:  reappeared within the circle of light, into the bosom of the work. How is
Title:  it, Sagamore? Are the Mingoes upon us in earnest, or is it only one of those
Title:  reptiles who hang upon the skirts of a war-party, to scalp the dead, go in,
Title:  and make their boast among the squaws of the valient deeds done on the pale
Title:  faces?
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook very quietly resumed his seat; nor did he make any reply, until
Title:  after he had examined the firebrand which had been struck by the bullet that
Title:  had nearly proved fatal to himself. After which he was content to reply,
Title:  holding a single finger up to view, with the English monosyllable:
Title:  
Title:  One.
Title:  
Title:  I thought as much, returned Hawkeye, seating himself; and as he had got the
Title:  cover of the lake afore Uncas pulled upon him, it is more than probable the
Title:  knave will sing his lies about some great ambushment, in which he was
Title:  outlying on the trail of two Mohicans and a white hunter - for the officers
Title:  can be considered as little better than idlers in such a scrimmage. Well,
Title:  let him - let him. There are always some honest men in every nation, though
Title:  heaven knows, too, that they are scarce among the Maquas, to look down an
Title:  upstart when he brags ag'in the face of reason. The varlet sent his lead
Title:  within whistle of your ears, Sagamore.
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook turned a calm and incurious eye toward the place where the ball
Title:  had struck, and then resumed his former attitude, with a composure that
Title:  could not be disturbed by so trifling an incident. Just then Uncas glided
Title:  into the circle, and seated himself at the fire, with the same appearance of
Title:  indifference as was maintained by his father.
Title:  
Title:  Of these several moments Heyward was a deeply interested and wondering
Title:  observer. It appeared to him as though the foresters had some secret means
Title:  of intelligence, which had escaped the vigilance of his own faculties. In
Title:  place of that eager and garrulous narration with which a white youth would
Title:  have endeavored to communicate, and perhaps exaggerate, that which had
Title:  passed out in the darkness of the plain, the young warrior was seemingly
Title:  content to let his deeds speak for themselves. It was, in fact, neither the
Title:  moment nor the occasion for an Indian to boast of his exploits; and it is
Title:  probably that, had Heyward neglected to inquire, not another syllable would,
Title:  just then, have been uttered on the subject.
Title:  
Title:  What has become of our enemy, Uncas? demanded Duncan; we heard your rifle,
Title:  and hoped you had not fired in vain.
Title:  
Title:  The young chief removed a fold of his hunting skirt, and quietly exposed the
Title:  fatal tuft of hair, which he bore as the symbol of victory. Chingachgook
Title:  laid his hand on the scalp, and considered it for a moment with deep
Title:  attention. Then dropping it, with disgust depicted in his strong features,
Title:  he ejaculated:
Title:  
Title:  Oneida!
Title:  
Title:  Oneida! repeated the scout, who was fast losing his interest in the scene,
Title:  in an apathy nearly assimilated to that of his red associates, but who now
Title:  advanced in uncommon earnestness to regard the bloody badge. By the Lord, if
Title:  the Oneidas are outlying upon the trail, we shall by flanked by devils on
Title:  every side of us! Now, to white eyes there is no difference between this bit
Title:  of skin and that of any other Indian, and yet the Sagamore declares it came
Title:  from the poll of a Mingo; nay, he even names the tribe of the poor devil,
Title:  with as much ease as if the scalp was the leaf of a book, and each hair a
Title:  letter. What right have Christian whites to boast of their learning, when a
Title:  savage can read a language that would prove too much for the wisest of them
Title:  all! What say you, lad, of what people was the knave?
Title:  
Title:  Uncas raised his eyes to the face of the scout, and answered, in his soft
Title:  voice:
Title:  
Title:  Oneida.
Title:  
Title:  Oneida, again! when one Indian makes a declaration it is commonly true; but
Title:  when he is supported by his people, set it down as gospel!
Title:  
Title:  The poor fellow has mistaken us for French, said Heyward; or he would not
Title:  have attempted the life of a friend.
Title:  
Title:  He mistake a Mohican in his paint for a Huron! You would be as likely to
Title:  mistake the white-coated grenadiers of Montcalm for the scarlet jackets of
Title:  the Royal Americans, returned the scout. No, no, the sarpent knew his
Title:  errand; nor was there any great mistake in the matter, for there is but
Title:  little love atween a Delaware and a Mingo, let their tribes go out to fight
Title:  for whom they may, in a white quarrel. For that matter, though the Oneidas
Title:  do serve his sacred majesty, who is my sovereign lord and master, I should
Title:  not have deliberated long about letting off killdeer at the imp myself, had
Title:  luck thrown him in my way.
Title:  
Title:  That would have been an abuse of our treaties, and unworthy of your
Title:  character.
Title:  
Title:  When a man consort much with a people, continued Hawkeye, if they were
Title:  honest and he no knave, love will grow up atwixt them. It is true that white
Title:  cunning has managed to throw the tribes into great confusion, as respects
Title:  friends and enemies; so that the Hurons and the Oneidas, who speak the same
Title:  tongue, or what may be called the same, take each other's scalps, and the
Title:  Delawares are divided among themselves; a few hanging about their great
Title:  council-fire on their own river, and fighting on the same side with the
Title:  Mingoes while the greater part are in the Canadas, out of natural enmity to
Title:  the Maquas - thus throwing everything into disorder, and destroying all the
Title:  harmony of warfare. Yet a red natur' is not likely to alter with every shift
Title:  of policy; so that the love atwixt a Mohican and a Mingo is much like the
Title:  regard between a white man and a sarpent.
Title:  
Title:  I regret to hear it; for I had believed those natives who dwelt within our
Title:  boundaries had found us too just and liberal, not to identify themselves
Title:  fully with our quarrels.
Title:  
Title:  Why, I believe it is natur' to give a preference to one's own quarrels
Title:  before those of strangers. Now, for myself, I do love justice; and,
Title:  therefore, I will not say I hate a Mingo, for that may be unsuitable to my
Title:  color and my religion, though I will just repeat, it may have been owing to
Title:  the night that killdeer had no hand in the death of this skulking Oneida.
Title:  
Title:  Then, as if satisfied with the force of his own reasons, whatever might be
Title:  their effect on the opinions of the other disputant, the honest but
Title:  implacable woodsman turned from the fire, content to let the controversy
Title:  slumber. Heyward withdrew to the rampart, too uneasy and too little
Title:  accusomed to the warfare of the woods to remain at ease under the
Title:  possibility of such insidious attacks. Not so, however, with the scout and
Title:  the Mohicans. Those acute and long-practised senses, whose powers so often
Title:  exceed the limits of all ordinary credulity, after having detected the
Title:  danger, had enabled them to ascertain its magnitude and duration. Not one of
Title:  the three appeared in the least to doubt their perfect security, as was
Title:  indicated by the preparations that were soon made to sit in council over
Title:  their future proceedings.
Title:  
Title:  The confusion of nations, and even of tribes, to which Hawkeye allluded,
Title:  existed at that period in the fullest force. The great tie of language, and,
Title:  of course, of a common origin, was severed in many places; and it was one of
Title:  its consequences, that the Delaware and the Mingo (as the people of the Six
Title:  Nations were called) were found fighting in the same ranks, while the latter
Title:  sought the scalp of the Huron, though believed to be the root of his own
Title:  stock. The Delawares were even divided among themselves. Though love for the
Title:  soil which had belonged to his ancestors kept the Sagamore of the Mohicans
Title:  with a small band of followers who were serving at Edward, under the banners
Title:  of the English king, by far the largest portion of his nation were known to
Title:  be in the field as allies of Montcalm. The reader probably knows, if enough
Title:  has not already been gleaned form this narrative, that the Delaware, or
Title:  Lenape, claimed to be the progenitors of that numerous people, who once were
Title:  masters of most of the eastern and northern states of America, of whom the
Title:  community of the Mohicans was an ancient and highly honored member.
Title:  
Title:  It was, of course, with a perfect understanding of the minute and intricate
Title:  interests which had armed friend against friend, and brought natural enemies
Title:  to combat by each other's side, that the scout and his companions now
Title:  disposed themselves to deliberate on the measures that were to govern their
Title:  future movements, amid so many jarring and savage races of men. Duncan knew
Title:  enough of Indian customs to understand the reason that the fire was
Title:  replenished, and why the warriors, not excepting Hawkeye, took their seats
Title:  within the curl of its smoke with so much gravity and decorum. Placing
Title:  himself at an angle of the works, where he might be a spectator of the scene
Title:  without, he awaited the result with as much patience as he could summon.
Title:  
Title:  After a short and impressive pause, Chingachgook lighted a pipe whose bowl
Title:  was curiously carved in one of the soft stones of the country, and whose
Title:  stem was a tube of wood, and commenced smoking. When he had inhaled enough
Title:  of the fragrance of the soothing weed, he passed the instrument into the
Title:  hands of the scout. In this manner the pipe had made its rounds three
Title:  several times, amid the most profound silence, before either of the party
Title:  opened his lips. Then the Sagamore, as the oldest and highest in rank, in a
Title:  few calm and dignified words, proposed the subject for deliberation. He was
Title:  answered by the scout; and Chingachgook rejoined, when the other objected to
Title:  his opinions. But the youthful Uncas continued a silent and respectful
Title:  listener, until Hawkeye, in complaisance, demanded his opinion. Heyward
Title:  gathered from the manners of the different speakers, that the father and son
Title:  espoused one side of a disputed question, while the white man maintained the
Title:  other. The contest gradually grew warmer, until it was quite evident the
Title:  feelings of the speakers began to be somewhat enlisted in the debate.
Title:  
Title:  Notwithstanding the increasing warmth of the amicable contest, the most
Title:  decorous Christian assembly, not even excepting those in which its reverend
Title:  ministers are collected, might have learned a wholesome lesson of moderation
Title:  from the forbearance and courtesy of the disputants. The words of Uncas were
Title:  received with the same deep attention as those which fell from the maturer
Title:  wisdom of his father; and so far from manifesting any impatience, neither
Title:  spoke in reply, until a few moments of silent meditation were, seemingly,
Title:  bestowed in deliberating on what had already been said.
Title:  
Title:  The language of the Mohicans was accompanied by gestures so direct and
Title:  natural that Heyward had but little difficulty in following the thread of
Title:  their argument. On the other hand, the scout was obscure; because from the
Title:  lingering pride of color, he rather affected the cold and artificial manner
Title:  which characterizes all classes of Anglo-Americans when unexcited. By the
Title:  frequency with which the Indians described the marks of a forest trial, it
Title:  was evident they urged a pursuit by land, while the repeated sweep of
Title:  Hawkeye's arm toward the Horican denoted that he was for a passage across
Title:  its waters.
Title:  
Title:  The latter was to every appearance fast losing ground, and the point was
Title:  about to be decided agaisnt him, when he arose to his feet, and shaking off
Title:  his apathy, he suddenly assumed the manner of an Indian, and adopted all the
Title:  arts of native eloquence. Elevating an arm, he pointed out the track of the
Title:  sun, repeating the gesture for every day that was necessary to accomplish
Title:  their objects. Then he delineated a long and painful path, amid rocks and
Title:  water-courses. The age and weakness of the slumbering and unconscious Munro
Title:  were indicated by signs too palpable to be mistaken. Duncan perceived that
Title:  even his own powers were spoken lightly of, as the scout extended his palm,
Title:  and mentioned him by the appellation of the Open Hand - a name his
Title:  liberality had purchased of all the friendly tribes. Then came a
Title:  representation of the light and graceful movements of a canoe, set in
Title:  forcible contrast to the tottering steps of one enfeebled and tired. He
Title:  concluded by pointing to the scalp of the Oneida, and apparently urging the
Title:  necessity of their departing speedily, and in a manner that should leave no
Title:  trail.
Title:  
Title:  The Mohicans listened gravely, and with countenances that reflected the
Title:  sentiments of the speaker. Conviction gradually wrought its influence, and
Title:  toward the close of Hawkeye's speech, his sentences were accompanied by the
Title:  customary exclamation of commendation. In short, Uncas and his father became
Title:  converts to his way of thinking, abandoning their own previously expressed
Title:  opinions with a liberality and candor that, had they been the
Title:  representatives of some great and civilized people, would have infallibly
Title:  worked their political ruin, by destroying forever their reputation for
Title:  consistency.
Title:  
Title:  The instant the matter in discussion was decided, the debate, and everything
Title:  connected with it, except the result appeared to be forgotten. Hawkeye,
Title:  without looking round to read his triumph in applauding eyes, very
Title:  composedly stretched his tall frame before the dying embers, and closed his
Title:  own organs in sleep.
Title:  
Title:  Left now in a measure to themselves, the Mohicans, whose time had been so
Title:  much devoted to the interests of others, seized the moment to devote some
Title:  attention to themselves. Casting off at once the grave and austere demeanor
Title:  of an Indian chief, Chingachgook commenced speaking to his son in the soft
Title:  and playful tones of affection. Uncas gladly met the familiar air of his
Title:  father; and before the hard breathing of the scout announced that he slept,
Title:  a complete change was effected in the manner of his two associates.
Title:  
Title:  It is impossible to describe the music of their language, while thus engaged
Title:  in laughter and endearments, in such a way as to render it intelligible to
Title:  those whose ears have never listened to its melody. The compass of their
Title:  voices, particularly that of the youth, was wonderful - extending from the
Title:  deepest bass to tones that were even feminine in softness. The eyes of the
Title:  father followed the plastic and ingenious movements of the son with open
Title:  delight, and he never failed to smile in reply to the other's contagious but
Title:  low laughter. While under the influence of these gentle and natural
Title:  feelings, no trace of ferocity was to be seen in the softened features of
Title:  the Sagamore. His figured panoply of death looked more like a disguise
Title:  assumed in mockery than a fierce annunciation of a desire to carry
Title:  destruction in his footsteps.
Title:  
Title:  After an hour had passed in the indulgence of their better feelings,
Title:  Chingachgook abruptly announced his desire to sleep, by wrapping his head in
Title:  his blanket and stretching his form on the naked earth. The merriment of
Title:  Uncas instantly ceased; and carefully raking the coals in such a manner that
Title:  they should impart their warmth to his father's feet, the youth sought his
Title:  own pillow among the ruins of the place.
Title:  
Title:  Imbibing renewed confidence from the security of these experienced
Title:  foresters, Heyward soon imitated their example; and long before the night
Title:  had turned, they who lay in the bosom of the ruined work, seemed to slumber
Title:  as heavily as the unconscious multitude whose bones were already beginning
Title:  to bleach on the surrounding plain.
Title:

Title:  
Title:  Chapter 20
Title:  
Title:       Land of Albania! let me bend mine eyes
Title:       On thee; thou rugged nurse of savage men!
Title:  
Title:                                                          CHILDRE HAROLD
Title:  
Title:  The heavens were still studded with stars, when Hawkeye came to arouse the
Title:  sleepers. Casting aside their cloaks Munro and Heyward were on their feet
Title:  while the woodsman was still making his low calls, at the entrance of the
Title:  rude shelter where they had passed the night. When they issued from beneath
Title:  its concealment, they found the scout awaiting their appearance nigh by, and
Title:  the only salutation between them was the significant gesture for silence,
Title:  made by their sagacious leader.
Title:  
Title:  Think over your prayers, he whispered, as they approached him; for He to
Title:  whom you make them, knows all tongues; that of the heart, as well as those
Title:  of the mouth. But speak not a syllable; it is rare for a white voice to
Title:  pitch itself properly in the woods, as we have seen by the example of that
Title:  miserable devil, the singer. Come, he continued, turning toward a curtain of
Title:  the works; let us get into the ditch on this side, and be regardful to step
Title:  on the stones and fragments of wood as you go.
Title:  
Title:  His companions complied, though to two of them the reasons of this
Title:  extraordinary precaution were yet a mystery. When they were in the low
Title:  cavity that surrounded the earthen fort on three sides, they found that
Title:  passage nearly choked by the ruins. With care and patience, however, they
Title:  succeeded in clambering after the scout, until they reached the sandy shore
Title:  of the Horican.
Title:  
Title:  That's a trail that nothing but a nose can follow, said the satisfied scout,
Title:  looking back along their difficult way; grass is a treacherous carpet for a
Title:  flying party to tread on, but wood and stone take no print from a moccasin.
Title:  Had you worn your armed boots, there might, indeed, have been something to
Title:  fear; but with the deer-skin suitably prepared, a man may trust himself,
Title:  generally, on rocks with safety. Shove in the canoe nigher to the land,
Title:  Uncas; this sand will take a stamp as easily as the butter of the Jarmans on
Title:  the Mohawk. Softly, lad, softly; it must not touch the beach, or the knaves
Title:  will know by what road we have left the place.
Title:  
Title:  The young man observed the precaution; and the scout, laying a board from
Title:  the ruins to the canoe, made a sign for the two officers to enter. When this
Title:  was done, everything was studiously restored to its former disorder; and
Title:  then Hawkeye succeeded in reaching his little birchen vessel, without
Title:  leaving behind him any of those marks which he appeared so much to dread.
Title:  Heyward was silent until the Indians had cautiously paddled the canoe some
Title:  distance from the fort, and within the broad and dark shadows that fell from
Title:  the eastern mountain on the glassy surface of the lake; then he demanded:
Title:  
Title:  What need have we for this stolen and hurried departure?
Title:  
Title:  If the blood of an Oneida could stain such a sheet of pure water as this we
Title:  float on, returned the scout, your two eyes would answer your own question.
Title:  Have you forgotten the skulking reptile Uncas slew?
Title:  
Title:  By no means. But he was said to be alone, and dead men give no cause for
Title:  fear.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, he was alone in his deviltry! but an Indian whose tribe counts so many
Title:  warriors, need seldom fear his blood will run without the death shriek
Title:  coming speedily from some of his enemies.
Title:  
Title:  But our presence - the authority of Colonel Munro - would prove sufficient
Title:  protection against the anger of our allies, especially in a case where the
Title:  wretch so well merited his fate. I trust in Heaven you have not deviated a
Title:  single foot from the direct line of our course with so slight a reason!
Title:  
Title:  Do you think the bullet of that varlet's rifle would have turned aside,
Title:  though his sacred majesty the king had stood in its path? returned the
Title:  stubborn scout. Why did not the grand Frencher, he who is captain-general of
Title:  the Canadas, bury the tomahawks of the Hurons, if a word from a white can
Title:  work so strongly on the natur' of an Indian?
Title:  
Title:  The reply of Heyward was interrupted by a groan from Munro; but after he had
Title:  paused a moment, in deference to the sorrow of his aged friend he resumed
Title:  the subject.
Title:  
Title:  The marquis of Montcalm can only settle that error with his God, said the
Title:  young man solemnly.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, ay, now there is reason in your words, for they are bottomed on religion
Title:  and honesty. There is a vast difference between throwing a regiment of white
Title:  coats atwixt the tribes and the prisoners, and coaxing an angry savage to
Title:  forget he carries a knife and rifle, with words that must begin with calling
Title:  him your son. No, no, continued the scout, looking back at the dim shore of
Title:  William Henry, which was now fast receding, and laughing in his own silent
Title:  but heartfelt manner; I have put a trail of water atween us; and unless the
Title:  imps can make friends with the fishes, and hear who has paddled across their
Title:  basin this fine morning, we shall throw the length of the Horican behind us
Title:  before they have made up their minds which path to take.
Title:  
Title:  With foes in front, and foes in our rear, our journey is like to be one of
Title:  danger.
Title:  
Title:  Danger! repeated Hawkeye, calmly; no, not absolutely of danger; for, with
Title:  vigilant ears and quick eyes, we can manage to keep a few hours ahead of the
Title:  knaves; or, if we must try the rifle, there are three of us who understand
Title:  its gifts as well as any you can name on the borders. No, not of danger; but
Title:  that we shall have what you may call a brisk push of it, is probable; and it
Title:  may happen, a brush, a scrimmage, or some such divarsion, but always where
Title:  covers are good, and ammunition abundant.
Title:  
Title:  It is possible that Heyward's estimate of danger differed in some degree
Title:  from that of the scout, for, instead of replying, he now sat in silence,
Title:  while the canoe glided over several miles of water. Just as the day dawned,
Title:  they entered the narrows of the lake,1 and stole swiftly and cautiously
Title:  among their numberless little islands. It was by this road that Montcalm had
Title:  retired with his army, and the adventurers knew not but he had left some of
Title:  his Indians in ambush, to protect the rear of his forces, and collect the
Title:  stragglers. They, therefore, approached the passage with the customary
Title:  silence of their guarded habits.
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook laid aside his paddle; while Uncas and the scout urged the
Title:  light vessel through crooked and intricate channels, where every foot that
Title:  they advanced exposed them to the danger of some sudden rising on their
Title:  progress. The eyes of the Sagamore moved warily from islet to islet, and
Title:  copse to copse, as the canoe proceeded; and, when a clearer sheet of water
Title:  permitted, his keen vision was bent along the bald rocks and impending
Title:  forests that frowned upon the narrow strait.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, who was a doubly interested spectator, as well from the beauties of
Title:  the place as from the apprehension natural to his situation, was just
Title:  believing that he had permitted the latter to be excited without sufficient
Title:  reason, when the paddle ceased moving, in obedience to a signal from
Title:  Chingachgook.
Title:  
Title:  Hugh! exlaimed Uncas, nearly at the moment that the light tap his father had
Title:  made on the side of the canoe notified them of the vicinity of danger.
Title:  
Title:  What now? asked the scout; the lake is as smooth as if the winds had never
Title:  blown, and I can see along its sheet for miles; there is not so much as the
Title:  black head of a loon dotting the water.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian gravely raised his paddle, and pointed in the direction in which
Title:  his own steady look was riveted. Duncan's eyes followed the motion. A few
Title:  rods in their front lay another of the wooded islets, but it appeared as
Title:  calm and peaceful as if its solitude had never been disturbed by the foot of
Title:  man.
Title:  
Title:  I see nothing, he said, but land and water; and a lovely scene it is.
Title:  
Title:  Hist! interrupted the scout. Ay, Sagamore, there is always a reason for what
Title:  you do. 'Tis but a shade, and yet it is not natural. You see the mist,
Title:  major, that is rising above the island; you can't call it a fog, for it is
Title:  more like a streak of thin cloud - -
Title:  
Title:  It is vapor from the water.
Title:  
Title:  That a child could tell. But what is the edging of blacker smoke that hangs
Title:  along its lower side, and which you may trace down into the thicket of
Title:  hazel? 'Tis from a fire; but one that, in my judgment, has been suffered to
Title:  burn low.
Title:  
Title:  Let us, then, push for the place, and relieve our doubts, said the impatient
Title:  Duncan; the party must be small that can lie on such a bit of land.
Title:  
Title:  If you judge of Indian cunning by the rules you find in books, or by white
Title:  sagacity, they will lead you astray, if not to your death, returned Hawkeye,
Title:  examining the signs of the place with that acuteness which distinguished
Title:  him. If I may be permitted to speak in this matter, it will be to say, that
Title:  we have but two things to choose between: the one is, to return, and give up
Title:  all thoughts of following the Hurons - -
Title:  
Title:  Never! exclaimed Heyward, in a voice far too loud for their circumstances.
Title:  
Title:  Well, well, continued Hawkeye, making a hasty sign to repress his
Title:  impatience; I am much of your mind myself; though I thought it becoming my
Title:  experience to tell the whole. We must, then, make a push, and if the Indians
Title:  or Frenchers are in the narrows, run the gauntlet through these toppling
Title:  mountains. Is there reason in my words, Sagamore?
Title:  
Title:  The Indian made no other answer than by dropping his paddle into the water,
Title:  and urging forward the canoe. As he held the office of directing its course,
Title:  his resolution was sufficiently indicated by the movement. The whole party
Title:  now plied their paddles vigorously, and in a very few moments they had
Title:  reached a point whence they might command an entire view of the northern
Title:  shore of the island, the side that had hitherto been concealed.
Title:  
Title:  There they are, by all the truth of signs, whispered the scout, two canoes
Title:  and a smoke. The knaves haven't yet got their eyes out of the mist, or we
Title:  should hear the accursed whoop. Together, friends! we are leaving them, and
Title:  are already nearly out of whistle of a bullet.
Title:  
Title:  The well-known crack of a rifle, whose ball came skipping along the placid
Title:  surface of the strait, and a shrill yell from the island, interrupted his
Title:  speech, and announced that their passage was discovered. In another instant
Title:  several savages were seen rushing into canoes, which were soon dancing over
Title:  the water in pursuit. These fearful precursors of a coming struggle produced
Title:  no change in the countenances and movements of his three guides, so far as
Title:  Duncan could discover, except that the strokes of their paddles were longer
Title:  and more in unison, and caused the little bark to spring forward like a
Title:  creature possessing life and volition.
Title:  
Title:  Hold them there, Sagamore, said Hawkeye, looking coolly backward over this
Title:  left shoulder, while he still plied his paddle; keep them just there. Them
Title:  Hurons have never a piece in their nation that will execute at this
Title:  distance; but killdeer has a barrel on which a man may calculate.
Title:  
Title:  The scout having ascertained that the Mohicans were sufficient of themselves
Title:  to maintain the requisite distance, deliberately laid aside his paddle, and
Title:  raised the fatal rifle. Three several times he brought the piece to his
Title:  shoulder, and when his companions were expecting its report, he as often
Title:  lowered it to request the Indians would permit their enemies to approach a
Title:  little nigher. At length his accurate and fastidious eye seemed satisfied,
Title:  and, throwing out his left arm on the barrel, he was slowly elevating the
Title:  muzzle, when an exclamation from Uncas, who sat in the bow, once more caused
Title:  him to suspend the shot.
Title:  
Title:  What, now, lad? demanded Hawkeye; you save a Huron from the death-shriek by
Title:  that word; have you reason for what you do?
Title:  
Title:  Uncas pointed toward a rocky shore a little in their front, whence another
Title:  war canoe was darting directly across their course. It was too obvious now
Title:  that their situation was imminently perilous to need the aid of language to
Title:  confirm it. The scout laid aside his rifle, and resumed the paddle, while
Title:  Chingachgook inclined the bows of the canoe a little toward the western
Title:  shore, in order to increase the distance between them and this new enemy. In
Title:  the meantime they were reminded of the presence of those who pressed upon
Title:  their rear, by wild and exulting shouts. The stirring scene awakened even
Title:  Munro from his apathy.
Title:  
Title:  Let us make for the rocks on the main, he said, with the mien of a tired
Title:  soldier, and give battle to the savages. God forbid that I, or those
Title:  attached to me and mine, should ever trust again to the faith of any servant
Title:  of the Louis's!
Title:  
Title:  He who wishes to prosper in Indian warfare, returned the scout, must not be
Title:  too proud to learn from the wit of a native. Lay her more along the land,
Title:  Sagamore; we are doubling on the varlets, and perhaps they may try to strike
Title:  our trail on the long calculation.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye was not mistaken; for when the Huyrons found their course was likely
Title:  to throw them behind their chase they rendered it less direct, until, by
Title:  gradually bearing more and more obliquely, the two canoes were, ere long,
Title:  gliding on parallel lines, within two hundred yards of each other. It now
Title:  became entirely a trial of speed. So rapid was the progress of the light
Title:  vessles, that the lake curled in their front, in miniature waves, and their
Title:  motion became undulating by its own velocity. It was, perhaps, owing to this
Title:  circumstance, in addition to the necessity of keeping every hand employed at
Title:  the paddles, that the Hurons had not immediate recourse to their firearms.
Title:  The exertions of the fugitives were too severe to continue long, and the
Title:  pursuers had the advantage of numbers. Duncan observed with uneasiness, that
Title:  the scout began to look anxiously about him, as if searching for some
Title:  further means of assisting their flight.
Title:  
Title:  Edge her a little more from the sun, Sagamore, said the stubborn woodsman; I
Title:  see the knaves are sparing a man to the rifle. A single broken bone might
Title:  lose us our scalps. Edge more from the sun and we will put the island
Title:  between us.
Title:  
Title:  The expedient was not without its use. A long, low island lay at a little
Title:  distance before them, and, as they closed with it, the chasing canoe was
Title:  compelled to take a side opposite to that on which the pursued passed. The
Title:  scout and his companions did not neglect this advantage, but the instant
Title:  they were hid from observation by the bushes, they redoubled efforts that
Title:  before had seemed prodigious. The two canoes came round the last low point,
Title:  like two coursers at the top of their speed, the fugitives taking the lead.
Title:  This change had brought them nigher to each other, however, while it altered
Title:  their relative positions.
Title:  
Title:  You showed knowledge in the shaping of a birchen bark, Uncas, when you chose
Title:  this from among the Huron canoes, said the scout, smiling, apparently more
Title:  in satisfaction at their superiority in the race than from that prospect of
Title:  final escape which now began to open a little upon them. The imps have put
Title:  all their strength again at the paddles, and we are to struggle for our
Title:  scalps with bits of flattened wood, instead of clouded barrels and true
Title:  eyes. A long stroke, and together, friends.
Title:  
Title:  They are preparing for a shot, said Heyward; and as we are in a line with
Title:  them, it can scarcely fail.
Title:  
Title:  Get you, then, into the bottom of the canoe, returned the scout; you and the
Title:  colonel; it will be so much taken from the size of the mark.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward smiled, as he answered:
Title:  
Title:  It would be but an ill example for the highest in rank to dodge, while the
Title:  warriors were under fire.
Title:  
Title:  Lord! Lord! That is now a white man's courage! exclaimed the scout; and like
Title:  to many of his notions, not to be maintained by reason. Do you think the
Title:  Sagamore, or Uncas, or even I, who am a man without a cross, would
Title:  deliberate about finding a cover in the scrimmage, when an open body would
Title:  do no good? For what have the Frenchers reared up their Quebec, if fighting
Title:  is always to be done in the clearings?
Title:  
Title:  All that you say is very true, my friend, replied Heyward; still, our
Title:  customs must prevent us from doing as you wish.
Title:  
Title:  A volley from the Hurons interrupted the discourse, and as the bullets
Title:  whistled about them, Duncan saw the head of Uncas turned, looking back at
Title:  himself and Munro. Notwithstanding the nearness of the enemy, and his own
Title:  great personal danger, the countenance of the young warrior expressed no
Title:  other emotion, as the former was compelled to think, than amazement at
Title:  finding men willing to encounter so useless an exposure. Chingachgook was
Title:  probably better acquainted with the notions of white men, for he did not
Title:  even cast a glance aside from the riveted look his eye maintained on the
Title:  object by which he governed their course. A ball soon struck the light and
Title:  polished paddle from the hands of the chief, and drove it through the air,
Title:  far in the advance. A shout arose from the Hurons, who seized the
Title:  opportunity to fire another volley. Uncas described an arc in the water with
Title:  his own blade, and as the canoe passed swiftly on, Chingachgook recovered
Title:  his paddle, and flourishing it on high, he gave the war-whoop of the
Title:  Mohicans, and then lent his strength and skill again to the important task.
Title:  
Title:  The clamorous sounds of Le Gros Serpent! La Longue Carabine! Le Cerf Agile!
Title:  burst at once from the canoes behind, and seemed to give new zeal to the
Title:  pursuers. The scout seized killdeer in his left hand, and elevating it about
Title:  his head, he shook it in triumph at his enemies. The savages answered the
Title:  insult with a yell, and immediately another volley succeeded. The bullets
Title:  pattered along the lake, and one even pierced the bark of their little
Title:  vessel. No perceptible emotion could be discovered in the Mohicans during
Title:  this critical moment, their rigid features expressing neither hope nor
Title:  alarm; but the scout again turned his head, and, laughing in his own silent
Title:  manner, he said to Heyward:
Title:  
Title:  The knaves love to hear the sounds of their pieces; but the eye is not to be
Title:  found among the Mingoes that can calculate a true range in a dancing canoe!
Title:  You see the dumb devils have taken off a man to charge, and by the smallest
Title:  measurement that can be allowed, we move three feet to their two!
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, who was not altogether as easy under this nice estimate of distances
Title:  as his companions, was glad to find, however, that owing to their superior
Title:  dexterity, and the diversion among their enemies, they were very sensibly
Title:  obtaining the advantage. The Hurons soon fired again, and a bullet struck
Title:  the blade of Hawkeye's paddle without injury.
Title:  
Title:  That will do, said the scout, examining the slight indentation with a
Title:  curious eye; it would not have cut the skin of an infant, much less of men,
Title:  who, like us, have been blown upon by the heavens in their anger. Now,
Title:  major, if you will try to use this piece of flattened wood, I'll let
Title:  killdeer take a part in the conversation.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward seized the paddle, and applied himself to the work with an eagerness
Title:  that supplied the place of skill, while Hawkeye was engaged in inspecting
Title:  the priming of his rifle. The latter then took a swift aim and fired. The
Title:  Huron in the bows of the leading canoe had risen with a similar object, and
Title:  he now fell backward, suffering his gun to escape from his hands into the
Title:  water. In an instant, however, he recovered his feet, though his gestures
Title:  were wild and bewildered. At the same moment his companions suspended their
Title:  efforts, and the chasing canoes clustered together, and became stationary.
Title:  Chingachgook and Uncas profited by the interval to regain their wind, though
Title:  Duncan continued to work with the most persevering industry. The father and
Title:  son now cast calm but inquiring glances at each other, to learn if either
Title:  had sustained any injury by the fire; for both well knew that no cry or
Title:  exclamation would, in such a moment of necessity have been permitted to
Title:  betray the accident. A few large drops of blood were trickling down the
Title:  shoulder of the Sagamore, who, when he perceived that the eyes of Uncas
Title:  dwelt too long on the sight, raised some water in the hollow of his hand,
Title:  and washing off the stain, was content to manifest, in this simple manner,
Title:  the slightness of the injury.
Title:  
Title:  Softly, softly, major, said the scout, who by this time had reloaded his
Title:  rifle; we are a little too far already for a rifle to put forth its
Title:  beauties, and you see yonder imps are holding a council. Let them come up
Title:  within striking distance - my eye may well be trusted in such a matter - and
Title:  I will trail the varlets the length of the Horican, guaranteeing that not a
Title:  shot of theirs shall, at the worst, more than break the skin, while killdeer
Title:  shall touch the life twice in three times.
Title:  
Title:  We forget our errand, returned the diligent Duncan. For God's sake let us
Title:  profit by this advantage, and increase our distance from the enemy.
Title:  
Title:  Give me my children, said Munro, hoarsely; trifle no longer with a father's
Title:  agony, but restore me my babes.
Title:  
Title:  Long and habitual deference to the mandates of his superiors had taught the
Title:  scout the virtue of obedience. Throwing a last and lingering glance at the
Title:  distant canoes, he laid aside his rifle, and, relieving the wearied Duncan,
Title:  resumed the paddle, which he wielded with sinews that never tired. His
Title:  efforts were seconded by those of the Mohicans and a very few minutes served
Title:  to place such a sheet of water between them and their enemies, that Heyward
Title:  once more breathed freely.
Title:  
Title:  The lake now began to expand, and their route lay along a wide reach, that
Title:  was lined, as before, by high and ragged mountains. But the islands were
Title:  few, and easily avoided. The strokes of the paddles grew more measured and
Title:  regular, while they who plied them continued their labor, after the close
Title:  and deadly chase from which they had just relieved themselves, with as much
Title:  coolness as though their speed had been tried in sport, rather than under
Title:  such pressing, nay, almost desperate, circumstances.
Title:  
Title:  Instead of following the western shore, whither their errand led them, the
Title:  wary Mohican inclined his course more toward those hills behind which
Title:  Montcalm was known to have led his army into the formidable fortress of
Title:  Ticonderoga. As the Hurons, to every appearance, had abandoned the pursuit,
Title:  there was no apparent reason for this excess of caution. It was, however,
Title:  maintained for hours, until they had reached a bay, nigh the northern
Title:  termination of the lake. Here the canoe was driven upon the beach, and the
Title:  whole party landed. Hawkeye and Heyward ascended an adjacent bluff, where
Title:  the former, after considering the expanse of water beneath him, pointed out
Title:  to the latter a small black object, hovering under a headland, at the
Title:  distance of several miles.
Title:  
Title:  Do you see it? demanded the scout. Now, what would you account that spot,
Title:  were you left alone to white experience to find your way through this
Title:  wilderness?
Title:  
Title:  But for its distance and its magnitude, I should suppose it a bird. Can it
Title:  be a living object?
Title:  
Title:  'Tis a canoe of good birchen bark, and paddled by fierce and crafty Mingoes.
Title:  Though Providence has lent to those who inhabit the woods eyes that would be
Title:  needless to men in the settlements, where there are inventions to assist the
Title:  sight, yet no human organs can see all the dangers which at this moment
Title:  circumvent us. These varlets pretend to be bent chiefly on their sun-down
Title:  meal, but the moment it is dark they will be on our trail, as true as hounds
Title:  on the scent. We must throw them off, or our pursuit of Le Renard Subtil may
Title:  be given up. These lakes are useful at times, especially when the game take
Title:  the water, continued the scout, gazing about him with a countenance of
Title:  concern; but they give no cover, except it be to the fishes. God knows what
Title:  the country would be, if the settlements should ever spread far from the two
Title:  rivers. Both hunting and war would lose their beauty.
Title:  
Title:  Let us not delay a moment, without some good and obvious cause.
Title:  
Title:  I little like that smoke, which you may see worming up along the rock above
Title:  the canoe, interrupted the abstracted scout. My life on it, other eyes than
Title:  ours see it, and know its meaning. Well, words will not mend the matter, and
Title:  it is time that we were doing.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye moved away from the lookout, and descended, musing profoundly, to
Title:  the shore. He communicated the result of his observations to his companions,
Title:  in Delaware, and a short and earnest consultation succeeded. When it
Title:  terminated, the three instantly set about executing their new resolutions.
Title:  
Title:  The canoe was lifted from the water, and borne on the shoulders of the
Title:  party, they proceeded into the wood, making as broad and obvious a trail as
Title:  possible. They soon reached the water-course, which they crossed, and,
Title:  continuing onward, until they came to an extensive and naked rock. At this
Title:  point, where their footsteps might be expected to be no longer visible, they
Title:  retraced their route to the brook, walking backward, with the utmost care.
Title:  They now followed the bed of the little stream to the lake, into which they
Title:  immediately launched their canoe again. A low point concealed them from the
Title:  headland, and the margin of the lake was fringed for some distance with
Title:  dense and overhanging bushes. Under the cover of these natural advantages,
Title:  they toiled their way, with patient industry, until the scout pronounced
Title:  that he believed it would be safe once more to land.
Title:  
Title:  The halt continued until evening rendered objects indistinct and uncertain
Title:  to the eye. Then they resumed their route, and, favored by the darkness,
Title:  pushed silently and vigorously toward the western shore. Although the rugged
Title:  outline of mountain, to which they were steering, presented no distinctive
Title:  marks to the eyes of Duncan, the Mohican entered the little haven he had
Title:  selected with the confidence and accuracy of an experienced pilot.
Title:  
Title:  The boat was again lifted and borne into the woods, where it was carefully
Title:  concealed under a pile of brush. The adventurers assumed their arms and
Title:  packs, and the scout announced to Munro and Heyward that he and the Indians
Title:  were at last in readiness to proceed.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 The beauties of Lake George are well known to every American tourist. In
Title:  the height of the mountains which surround it, and in artificial
Title:  accessories, it is inferior to the finest of the Swiss and Italian lakes,
Title:  while in outline and purity of water it is fully their equal; and in the
Title:  number and disposition of its isles and islets much superior to them all
Title:  together. There are said to be some hundreds of islands in a sheet of water
Title:  less than thirty miles long. The narrows, which connect what may be called,
Title:  in truth, two lakes, are crowded with islands to such a degree as to leave
Title:  passages between them frequently of only a few feet in width. The lake
Title:  itself varies in breadth from one to three miles. The state of New York is
Title:  remarkable for the number and beauty of its lakes. One of its frontiers lies
Title:  on the vast sheet of Ontario, while Champlain stretches nearly a hundred
Title:  miles along another. Oneida, Cayuga, Canandaiguia, Seneca, and George, are
Title:  all lakes of thirty miles in length, while those of a size smaller are
Title:  without number. On many of these lakes, there are now beautiful villages,
Title:  and on many of them steamboats.
