Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 21
Title:  
Title:       If you find a man there, he shall die a flea's death.
Title:  
Title:                                                  MERRY WIFES OF WINDSOR
Title:  
Title:  The party had landed on the border of a region that is, even to this day,
Title:  less known to the inhabitants of the States than the deserts of Arabia, or
Title:  the steppes of Tartary. It was the sterile and rugged district which
Title:  separates the tributaries of Champlain from those of the Hudson, the Mohawk,
Title:  and the St. Lawrence. Since the period of our tale the active spirit of the
Title:  country has surrounded it with a belt of rich and thriving settlements,
Title:  though none but the hunter or the savage is ever known even now to penetrate
Title:  its wild recesses.
Title:  
Title:  As Hawkeye and the Mohicans had, however, often traversed the mountains and
Title:  valleys of this vast wilderness, they did not hesitate to plunge into its
Title:  depth, with the freedom of men accustomed to its privations and
Title:  difficulties. For many hours the travelers toiled on their laborious way,
Title:  guided by a star, or following the direction of some water-course, until the
Title:  scout called a halt, and holding a short consultation with the Indians, they
Title:  lighted their fire, and made the usual preparations to pass the remainder of
Title:  the night where they then were.
Title:  
Title:  Imitating the example, and emulating the confidence of their more
Title:  experienced associates, Munro and Duncan slept without fear, if now without
Title:  uneasiness. The dews were suffered to exhale, and the sun had dispersed the
Title:  mists, and was shedding a strong and clear light in the forest, when the
Title:  travelers resumed their journey.
Title:  
Title:  After proceeding a few miles, the progress of Hawkeye, who led the advance,
Title:  became more deliberate and watchful. He often stopped to examine the trees;
Title:  nor did he cross a rivulet without attentively considering the quantity, the
Title:  velocity, and the color of its waters. Distrusting his own judgment, his
Title:  appeals to the opinion of Chingachgook were frequent and earnest. During one
Title:  of these conferences Heyward observed that Uncas stood a patient and silent,
Title:  though, as he imagined, an interested listener. He was strongly tempted to
Title:  address the young chief, and demand his opinion of their progress; but the
Title:  calm and dignified demeanor of the native induced him to believe, that, like
Title:  himself, the other was wholly dependent on the sagacity and intelligence of
Title:  the seniors of the party. At last the scout spoke in English, and at once
Title:  explained the embarrassment of their situation.
Title:  
Title:  When I found that the home path of the Hurons run north, he said, it did not
Title:  need the judgment of many long years to tell that they would follow the
Title:  valleys, and keep atween the waters of the Hudson and the Horican, until
Title:  they might strike the springs of the Canada streams, which would lead them
Title:  into the heart of the country of the Frenchers. Yet here are we, within a
Title:  short range of the Scaroons, and not a sign of a trail have we crossed!
Title:  Human natur' is weak, and it is possible we may not have taken the proper
Title:  scent.
Title:  
Title:  Heaven protect us from such an error! exclaimed Duncan. Let us retrace our
Title:  steps, and examine as we go, with keener eyes. Has Uncas no counsel to offer
Title:  in such a strait?
Title:  
Title:  The young Mohican cast a glance at his father, but, maintaining his quiet
Title:  and reserved mien, he continued silent. Chingachgook had caught the look,
Title:  and motioning with his hand, he bade him speak. The moment this permission
Title:  was accorded, the countenance of Uncas changed from its grave composure to a
Title:  gleam of intelligence and joy. Bounding forward like a deer, he sprang up
Title:  the side of a little acclivity, a few rods in advance, and stood,
Title:  exultingly, over a spot of fresh earth, that looked as though it had been
Title:  recently upturned by the passage of some heavy animal. The eyes of the whole
Title:  party followed the unexpected movement, and read their success in the air of
Title:  triumph that the youth assumed.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis the trail! exclaimed the scout, advancing to the spot; the lad is quick
Title:  of sight and keen of wit for his years.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis extraordinary that he should have withheld his knowledge so long,
Title:  muttered Duncan, at his elbow.
Title:  
Title:  It would have been more wonderful had he spoken without a bidding. No, no;
Title:  your young white, who gathers his learning from books and can measure what
Title:  he knows by the page, may conceit that his knowledge, like his legs, outruns
Title:  that of his fathers', but, where experience is the master, the scholar is
Title:  made to know the value of years, and respects them accordingly.
Title:  
Title:  See! said Uncas, pointing north and south, at the evident marks of the broad
Title:  trail on either side of him, the dark-hair has gone toward the forest.
Title:  
Title:  Hound never ran on a more beautiful scent, responded the scout, dashing
Title:  forward, at once, on the indicated route; we are favored, greatly favored,
Title:  and can follow with high noses. Ay, here are both your waddling beasts: this
Title:  Huron travels like a white general. The fellow is stricken with a judgment,
Title:  and is mad! Look sharp for wheels, Sagamore, he continued, looking back, and
Title:  laughing in his newly awakened satisfaction; we shall soon have the fool
Title:  journeying in a coach, and that with three of the best pair of eyes on the
Title:  borders in his rear.
Title:  
Title:  The spirits of the scout, and the astonishing success of the chase, in which
Title:  a circuitous distance of more than forty miles had been passed, did not fail
Title:  to impart a portion of hope to the whole party. Their advance was rapid; and
Title:  made with as much confidence as a traveler would proceed along a wide
Title:  highway. If a rock, or a rivulet, or a bit of earth harder than common,
Title:  severed the links of the clew they followed, the true eye of the scout
Title:  recovered them at a distance, and seldom rendered the delay of a single
Title:  moment necessary. Their progress was much facilitated by the certainty that
Title:  Magua had found it necessary to journey through the valleys; a circumstance
Title:  which rendered the general direction of the route sure. Nor had the Huron
Title:  entirely neglected the arts uniformly practised by the natives when retiring
Title:  in front of an enemy. False trails and sudden turnings were frequent,
Title:  wherever a brook or the formation of the ground rendered them feasible; but
Title:  his pursuers were rarely deceived, and never failed to detect their error,
Title:  before they had lost either time or distance on the deceptive track.
Title:  
Title:  By the middle of the afternoon they had passed the Scaroons, and were
Title:  following the route of the declining sun. After descending an eminence to a
Title:  low bottom, through which a swift stream glided, they suddenly came to a
Title:  place where the party of Le Renard had made a halt. Extinguished brands were
Title:  lying around a spring, the offals of a deer were scattered about the place,
Title:  and the trees bore evident marks of having been browsed by the horses. At a
Title:  little distance, Heyward discovered, and contemplated with tender emotion,
Title:  the small bower under which he was fain to believe that Cora and Alice had
Title:  reposed. But while the earth was trodden, and the footsteps of both men and
Title:  beasts were so plainly visible around the place, the trail appeared to have
Title:  suddenly ended.
Title:  
Title:  It was easy to follow the tracks of the Narragansetts, but they seemed only
Title:  to have wandered without guides, or any other object than the pursuit of
Title:  food. At length Uncas, who, with his father, had endeavored to trace the
Title:  route of the horses, came upon a sign of their presence that was quite
Title:  recent. Before following the clew, he communicated his success to his
Title:  companions; and while the latter were consulting on the circumstance, the
Title:  youth reappeared, leading the two fillies, with their saddles broken, and
Title:  the housings soiled, as though they had been permitted to run at will for
Title:  several days.
Title:  
Title:  What should this prove? said Duncan, turning pale, and glancing his eyes
Title:  around him, as if he feared the brush and leaves were about to give up some
Title:  horrid secret.
Title:  
Title:  That our march is come to a quick end, and that we are in an enemy's
Title:  country, returned the scout. Had the knave been pressed, and the gentle ones
Title:  wanted horses to keep up with the party, he might have taken their scalps;
Title:  but without an enemy at his heels, and with such rugged beasts as these, he
Title:  would not hurt a hair of their heads. I know your thoughts, and shame be it
Title:  to our color that you have reason for them; but he who thinks that even a
Title:  Mingo would ill-treat a woman, unless it be to tomahawk her, knows nothing
Title:  of Indian natur', or the laws of the woods. No, no; I have heard that the
Title:  French Indians had come into these hills to hunt the moose, and we are
Title:  getting within scent of their camp. Why should they not? The morning and
Title:  evening guns of Ty may be heard any day among these mountains; for the
Title:  Frenchers are running a new line atween the provinces of the king and the
Title:  Canadas. It is true that the horses are here, but the Hurons are gone; let
Title:  us, then, hunt for the path by which they parted.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye and the Mohicans now applied themselves to their task in good
Title:  earnest. A circle of a few hundred feet in circumference was drawn, and each
Title:  of the party took a segment for his portion. The examination, however,
Title:  resulted in no discovery. The impressions of footsteps were numerous, but
Title:  they all appeared like those of men who had wandered about the spot, without
Title:  any design to quit it. Again the scout and his companions made the circuit
Title:  of the halting place, each slowly following the other, until they assembled
Title:  in the center once more, no wiser than when they started.
Title:  
Title:  Such cunning is not without its deviltry, exclaimed Hawkeye, when he met the
Title:  disappointed looks of his assistants.
Title:  
Title:  We must get down to it, Sagamore, beginning at the spring, and going over
Title:  the ground by inches. The Huron shall never brag in his tribe that he has a
Title:  foot which leaves no print.
Title:  
Title:  Setting the example himself, the scout engaged in the scrutiny with renewed
Title:  zeal. Not a leaf was left unturned. The sticks were removed, and the stones
Title:  lifted; for Indian cunning was known frequently to adopt these objects as
Title:  covers, laboring with the utmost patience and industry, to conceal each
Title:  footstep as they proceeded. Still no discovery was made. At length Uncas,
Title:  whose activity had enabled him to achieve his portion of the task the
Title:  soonest, raked the earth across the turbid little rill which ran from the
Title:  spring, and diverted its course into another channel. So soon as its narrow
Title:  bed below the dam was dry, he stooped over it with keen and curious eyes. A
Title:  cry of exultation immediately announced the success of the young warrior.
Title:  The whole party crowded to the spot where Uncas pointed out the impression
Title:  of a moccasin in the moist alluvion.
Title:  
Title:  This lad will be an honor to his people, said Hawkeye, regarding the trail
Title:  with as much admiration as a naturalist would expend on the tusk of a
Title:  mammoth or the rib of a mastodon; ay, and a thorn in the sides of the
Title:  Hurons. Yet that is not the footstep of an Indian! the weight is too much on
Title:  the heel, and the toes are squared, as though one of the French dancers had
Title:  been in, pigeon-winging his tribe! Run back, Uncas, and bring me the size of
Title:  the singer's foot. You will find a beautiful print of it just opposite yon
Title:  rock, agin the hillside.
Title:  
Title:  While the youth was engaged in this commission, the scout and Chingachgook
Title:  were attentively considering the impressions. The measurements agreed, and
Title:  the former unhesitatingly pronounced that the footstep was that of David,
Title:  who had once more been made to exchange his shoes for moccasins.
Title:  
Title:  I can now read the whole of it, as plainly as if I had seen the arts of Le
Title:  Subtil, he added; the singer being a man whose gifts lay chiefly in his
Title:  throat and feet, was made to go first, and the others have trod in his
Title:  steps, imitating their formation.
Title:  
Title:  But, cried Duncan, I see no signs of - -
Title:  
Title:  The gentle ones, interrupted the scout; the varlet has found a way to carry
Title:  them, until he supposed he had thrown any followers off the scent. My life
Title:  on it, we see their pretty little feet again, before many rods go by.
Title:  
Title:  The whole party now proceeded, following the course of the rill, keeping
Title:  anxious eyes on the regular impressions. The water soon flowed into its bed
Title:  again, but watching the ground on either side, the foresters pursued their
Title:  way content with knowing that the trail lay beneath. More than half a mile
Title:  was passed, before the rill rippled close around the base of an extensive
Title:  and dry rock. Here they paused to make sure that the Hurons had not quitted
Title:  the water.
Title:  
Title:  It was fortunate they did so. For the quick and active Uncas soon found the
Title:  impression of a foot on a bunch of moss, where it would seem an Indian had
Title:  inadvertently trodden. Pursuing the direction given by this discovery, he
Title:  entered the neighboring thicket, and struck the trail, as fresh and obvious
Title:  as it had been before they reached the spring. Another shout announced the
Title:  good fortune of the youth to his companions, and at once terminated the
Title:  search.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, it has been planned with Indian judgment, said the scout, when the party
Title:  was assembled around the place, and would have blinded white eyes.
Title:  
Title:  Shall we proceed? demanded Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  Softly, softly, we know our path; but it is good to examine the formation of
Title:  things. This is my schooling, major; and if one neglects the book, there is
Title:  little chance of learning from the open land of Providence. All is plain but
Title:  one thing, which is the manner that the knave contrived to get the gentle
Title:  ones along the blind trail. Even a Huron would be too proud to let their
Title:  tender feet touch the water.
Title:  
Title:  Will this assist in explaining the difficulty? said Heyward, pointing toward
Title:  the fragments of a sort of handbarrow, that had been rudely constructed of
Title:  boughs, and bound together with withes, and which now seemed carelessly cast
Title:  aside as useless.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis explained! cried the delighted Hawkeye. If them varlets have passed a
Title:  minute, they have spent hours in striving to fabricate a lying end to their
Title:  trail! Well, I've known them to waste a day in the same manner to as little
Title:  purpose. Here we have three pair of moccasins, and two of little feet. It is
Title:  amazing that any mortal beings can journey on limbs so small! Pass me the
Title:  thong of buckskin, Uncas, and let me take the length of this foot. By the
Title:  Lord, it is no longer than a child's and yet the maidens are tall and
Title:  comely. That Providence is partial in its gifts, for its own wise reasons,
Title:  the best and most contented of us must allow.
Title:  
Title:  The tender limbs of my daughters are unequal to these hardships, said Munro,
Title:  looking at the light footsteps of his children, with a parent's love; we
Title:  shall find their fainting forms in this desert.
Title:  
Title:  Of that there is little cause of fear, returned the scout, slowly shaking
Title:  his head; this is a firm and straight, though a light step, and not over
Title:  long. See, the heel has hardly touched the ground; and there the dark-hair
Title:  has made a little jump, from root to root. No, no; my knowledge for it,
Title:  neither of them was nigh fainting, hereaway. Now, the singer was beginning
Title:  to be footsore and leg-weary, as is plain by his trail. There, you see, he
Title:  slipped; here he has traveled wide and tottered; and there again it looks as
Title:  though he journeyed on snowshoes. Ay, ay, a man who uses his throat
Title:  altogether, can hardly give his legs a proper training.
Title:  
Title:  From such undeniable testimony did the practised woodsman arrive at the
Title:  truth, with nearly as much certainty and precision as if he had been a
Title:  witness of all those events which his ingenuity so easily elucidated.
Title:  Cheered by these assurances, and satisfied by a reasoning that was so
Title:  obvious, while it was so simple, the party resumed its course, after making
Title:  a short halt, to take a hurried repast.
Title:  
Title:  When the meal was ended, the scout cast a glance upward at the setting sun,
Title:  and pushed forward with a rapidity which compelled Heyward and the still
Title:  vigorous Munro to exert all their muscles to equal. Their route now lay
Title:  along the bottom which has already been mentioned. As the Hurons had made no
Title:  further efforts to conceal their footsteps, the progress of the pursuers was
Title:  no longer delayed by uncertainty. Before an hour had elapsed, however, the
Title:  speed of Hawkeye sensibly abated, and his head, instead of maintaining its
Title:  former direct and forward look, began to turn suspiciously from side to
Title:  side, as if he were conscious of approaching danger. He soon stopped again,
Title:  and waited for the whole party to come up.
Title:  
Title:  I scent the Hurons, he said, speaking to the Mohicans; yonder is open sky,
Title:  through the treetops, and we are getting too nigh their encampment.
Title:  Sagamore, you will take the hillside, to the right; Uncas will bend along
Title:  the brook to the left, while I will try the trail. If anything should
Title:  happen, the call will be three croaks of a crow. I saw one of the birds
Title:  fanning himself in the air, just beyond the dead oak - another sign that we
Title:  are approaching an encampment.
Title:  
Title:  The Indians departed their several ways without reply, while Hawkeye
Title:  cautiously proceeded with the two gentlemen. Heyward soon pressed to the
Title:  side of their guide, eager to catch an early glimpse of those enemies he had
Title:  pursued with so much toil and anxiety. His companion told him to steal to
Title:  the edge of the wood, which, as usual, was fringed with a thicket, and wait
Title:  his coming, for he wished to examine certain suspicious signs a little on
Title:  one side. Duncan obeyed, and soon found himself in a situation to command a
Title:  view which he found as extraordinary as it was novel.
Title:  
Title:  The trees of many acres had been felled, and the glow of a mild summer's
Title:  evening had fallen on the clearing, in beautiful contrast to the gray light
Title:  of the forest. A short distance from the place where Duncan stood, the
Title:  stream had seemingly expanded into a little lake, covering most of the low
Title:  land, from mountain to mountain. The water fell out of this wide basin, in a
Title:  cataract so regular and gentle, that it appeared rather to be the work of
Title:  human hands than fashioned by nature. A hundred earthen dwellings stood on
Title:  the margin of the lake, and even in its waters, as though the latter had
Title:  overflowed its usual banks. Their rounded roofs, admirably molded for
Title:  defense against the weather, denoted more of industry and foresight than the
Title:  natives were wont to bestow on their regular habitations, much less on those
Title:  they occupied for the temporary purposes of hunting and war. In short, the
Title:  whole village or town, whichever it might be termed, possessed more of
Title:  method and neatness of execution, than the white men had been accustomed to
Title:  believe belonged, ordinarily, to the Indian habits. It appeared, however, to
Title:  be deserted. At least, so thought Duncan for many minutes; but, at length,
Title:  he fancied he discovered several human forms advancing toward him on all
Title:  fours, and apparently dragging in the train some heavy, and as he was quick
Title:  to apprehend, some formidable engine. Just then a few dark-looking heads
Title:  gleamed out of the dwellings, and the place seemed suddenly alive with
Title:  beings, which, however, glided from cover to cover so swiftly, as to allow
Title:  no opportunity of examining their humors or pursuits. Alarmed at these
Title:  suspicious and inexplicable movements, he was about to attempt the signal of
Title:  the crows, when the rustling of leaves at hand drew his eyes in another
Title:  direction.
Title:  
Title:  The young man started, and recoiled a few paces instinctively, when he found
Title:  himself within a hundred yards of a stranger Indian. Recovering his
Title:  recollection on the instant, instead of sounding an alarm, which might prove
Title:  fatal to himself, he remained stationary, an attentive observer of the
Title:  other's motions.
Title:  
Title:  An instant of calm observation served to assure Duncan that he was
Title:  undiscovered. The native, like himself, seemed occupied in considering the
Title:  low dwellings of the village, and the stolen movements of its inhabitants.
Title:  It was impossible to discover the expression of his features through the
Title:  grotesque mask of paint under which they were concealed, though Duncan
Title:  fancied it was rather melancholy than savage. His head was shaved, as usual,
Title:  with the exception of the crown, from whose tuft three or four faded
Title:  feathers from a hawk's wing were loosely dangling. A ragged calico mantle
Title:  half encircled his body, while his nether garment was composed of an
Title:  ordinary shirt, the sleeves of which were made to perform the office that is
Title:  usually executed by a much more commodious arrangement. His legs were,
Title:  however, covered with a pair of good deer-skin moccasins. Altogether, the
Title:  appearance of the individual was forlorn and miserable.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan was still curiously observing the person of his neighbor when the
Title:  scout stole silently and cautiously to his side.
Title:  
Title:  You see we have reached their settlement or encampment, whispered the young
Title:  man; and here is one of the savages himself, in a very embarrassing position
Title:  for our further movements.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye started, and dropped his rifle, when, directed by the finger of his
Title:  companion, the stranger came under his view. Then lowering the dangerous
Title:  muzzle he stretched forward his long neck, as if to assist a scrutiny that
Title:  was already intensely keen.
Title:  
Title:  The imp is not a Huron, he said, nor of any of the Canada tribes; and yet
Title:  you see, by his clothes, the knave has been plundering a white. Ay, Montcalm
Title:  has raked the woods for his inroad, and a whooping, murdering set of varlets
Title:  has he gathered together. Can you see where he has put his rifle or his bow?
Title:  
Title:  He appears to have no arms; nor does he seem to be viciously inclined.
Title:  Unless he communicate the alarm to his fellows, who, as you see, are dodging
Title:  about the water, we have but little to fear from him.
Title:  
Title:  The scout turned to Heyward, and regarded him a moment with unconcealed
Title:  amazement. Then opening wide his mouth, he indulged in unrestrained and
Title:  heartfelt laughter, though in that silent and peculiar manner which danger
Title:  had so long taught him to practise.
Title:  
Title:  Repeating the words, Fellows who are dodging about the water! he added, so
Title:  much for schooling and passing a boyhood in the settlements! The knave has
Title:  long legs, though, and shall not be trusted. Do you keep him under your
Title:  rifle while I creep in behind, through the bush, and take him alive. Fire on
Title:  no account.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward had already permitted his companion to bury part of his person in
Title:  the thicket, when, stretching forth his arm, he arrested him, in order to
Title:  ask:
Title:  
Title:  If I see you in danger, may I not risk a shot?
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye regarded him a moment, like one who knew not how to take the
Title:  question; then, nodding his head, he answered, still laughing, though
Title:  inaudibly:
Title:  
Title:  Fire a whole platoon, major.
Title:  
Title:  In the next moment he was concealed by the leaves. Duncan waited several
Title:  minutes in feverish impatience, before he caught another glimpse of the
Title:  scout. Then he reappeared, creeping along the earth, from which his dress
Title:  was hardly distinguishable, directly in the rear of his intended captive.
Title:  Having reached within a few yards of the latter, he arose to his feet,
Title:  silently and slowly. At that instant, several loud blows were struck on the
Title:  water, and Duncan turned his eyes just in time to perceive that a hundred
Title:  dark forms were plunging, in a body, into the troubled little sheet.
Title:  Grasping his rifle his looks were again bent on the Indian near him. Instead
Title:  of taking the alarm, the unconscious savage stretched forward his neck, as
Title:  if he also watched the movements about the gloomy lake, with a sort of silly
Title:  curiosity. In the meantime, the uplifted hand of Hawkeye was above him. But,
Title:  without any apparent reason, it was withdrawn, and its owner indulged in
Title:  another long, though still silent, fit of merriment. When the peculiar and
Title:  hearty laughter of Hawkeye was ended, instead of grasping his victim by the
Title:  throat, he tapped him lightly on the shoulder, and exclaimed aloud:
Title:  
Title:  How now, friend! have you a mind to teach the beavers to sing?
Title:  
Title:  Even so, was the ready answer. It would seem that the Being that gave them
Title:  power to improve His gifts so well, would not deny them voices to proclaim
Title:  His praise.
