Title:  
Title:  Chapter 22
Title:  
Title:       Bottom: Are we all met?
Title:       Quince: Pat-pat; and here's a marvelous
Title:       Convenient place for our rehearsal.
Title:  
Title:                                                 MIDSUMMER NIGHT'S DREAM
Title:  
Title:  The reader may better imagine, that we describe the surprise of Heyward. His
Title:  lurking Indians were suddenly converted into four-footed beasts; his lake
Title:  into a beaver pond; his cataract into a dam, constructed by those
Title:  industrious and ingenious quadrupeds; and a suspected enemy into his tried
Title:  friend, David Gamut, the master of psalmody. The presence of the latter
Title:  created so many unexpected hopes relative to the sisters that, without a
Title:  moment's hesitation, the young man broke out of his ambush, and sprang
Title:  forward to join the two principal actors in the scene.
Title:  
Title:  The merriment of Hawkeye was not easily appeased. Without ceremony, and with
Title:  a rough hand, he twirled the supple Gamut around on his heel, and more than
Title:  once affirmed that the Hurons had done themselves great credit in the
Title:  fashion of his costume. Then, seizing the hand of the other, he squeezed it
Title:  with a grip that brought tears into the eyes of the placid David, and wished
Title:  him joy of his new condition.
Title:  
Title:  You were about opening your throat-practisings among the beavers, were ye?
Title:  he said. The cunning devils know half the trade already, for they beat the
Title:  time with their tails, as you heard just now; and in good time it was, too,
Title:  or killdeer might have sounded the first note among them. I have known
Title:  greater fools, who could read and write, than an experienced old beaver; but
Title:  as for squalling, the animals are born dumb! What think you of such a song
Title:  as this?
Title:  
Title:  David shut his sensitive ears, and even Heyward apprised as he was of the
Title:  nature of the cry, looked upward in quest of the bird, as the cawing of a
Title:  crow rang in the air about them.
Title:  
Title:  See! continued the laughing scout, as he pointed toward the remainder of the
Title:  party, who, in obedience to the signal, were already approaching; this is
Title:  music which has its natural virtues; it brings two good rifles to my elbow,
Title:  to say nothing of the knives and tomahawks. But we see that you are safe;
Title:  now tell us what has become of the maidens.
Title:  
Title:  They are captives to the heathen, said David; and, though greatly troubled
Title:  in spirit, enjoying comfort and safety in the body.
Title:  
Title:  Both! demanded the breathless Heyward.
Title:  
Title:  Even so. Though our wayfaring has been sore and our sustenance scanty, we
Title:  have had little other cause for complaint, except the violence done our
Title:  feelings, by being thus led in captivity into a far land.
Title:  
Title:  Bless ye for these very words! exclaimed the trembling Munro; I shall then
Title:  receive my babes, spotless and angel-like, as I lost them!
Title:  
Title:  I know not that their delivery is at hand, returned the doubting David; the
Title:  leader of these savages is possessed of an evil spirit that no power short
Title:  of Omnipotence can tame. I have tried him sleeping and waking, but neither
Title:  sounds nor language seem to touch his soul.
Title:  
Title:  Where is the knave? bluntly interrupted the scout.
Title:  
Title:  He hunts the moose to-day, with his young men; and tomorrow, as I hear, they
Title:  pass further into the forests, and nigher to the borders of Canada. The
Title:  elder maiden is conveyed to a neighboring people, whose lodges are situate
Title:  beyond yonder black pinnacle of rock; while the younger is detained among
Title:  the women of the Hurons, whose dwellings are but two short miles hence, on a
Title:  table-land, where the fire had done the office of the axe, and prepared the
Title:  place for their reception.
Title:  
Title:  Alice, my gentle Alice! murmured Heyward; she has lost the consolation of
Title:  her sister's presence!
Title:  
Title:  Even so. But so far as praise and thanksgiving in psalmody can temper the
Title:  spirit in affliction, she has not suffered.
Title:  
Title:  Has she then a heart for music?
Title:  
Title:  Of the graver and more solemn character; though it must be acknowledged
Title:  that, in spite of all my endeavors, the maiden weeps oftener than she
Title:  smiles. At such moments I forbear to press the holy songs; but there are
Title:  many sweet and comfortable periods of satisfactory communication, when the
Title:  ears of the savages are astounded with the upliftings of our voices.
Title:  
Title:  And why are you permitted to go at large, unwatched?
Title:  
Title:  David composed his features into what he intended should express an air of
Title:  modest humility, before he meekly replied:
Title:  
Title:  Little be the praise to such a worm as I. But, though the power of psalmody
Title:  was suspended in the terrible business of that field of blood through which
Title:  we have passed, it has recovered its influence even over the souls of the
Title:  heathen, and I am suffered to go and come at will.
Title:  
Title:  The scout laughed, and, tapping his own forehead significantly, he perhaps
Title:  explained the singular indulgence more satisfactorily when he said:
Title:  
Title:  The Indians never harm a non-composser. But why, when the path lay open
Title:  before your eyes, did you not strike back on your own trail (it is not so
Title:  blind as that which a squirrel would make), and bring in the tidings to
Title:  Edward?
Title:  
Title:  The scout, remembering only his own sturdy and iron nature, had probably
Title:  exacted a task that David, under no circumstances, could have performed.
Title:  But, without entirely losing the meekness of his air, the latter was content
Title:  to answer:
Title:  
Title:  Though my soul would rejoice to visit the habitations of Christendom once
Title:  more, my feet would rather follow the tender spirits intrusted to my
Title:  keeping, even into the idolatrous province of the Jesuits, than take one
Title:  step backward, while they pined in captivity and sorrow.
Title:  
Title:  Though the figurative language of David wa not very intelligible, the
Title:  sincere and steady expression of his eye, and the glow of his honest
Title:  countenance, were not easily mistaken. Uncas pressed closer to his side, and
Title:  regarded the speaker with a look of commendation, while his father expressed
Title:  his satisfaction by the ordinary pithy exclamation of approbation. The scout
Title:  shook his head as he rejoined:
Title:  
Title:  The Lord never intended that the man should place all his endeavors in his
Title:  throat, to the neglect of other and better gifts! But he has fallen into the
Title:  hands of some silly woman, when he should have been gathering his education
Title:  under a blue sky, among the beauties of the forest. Here, friend; I did
Title:  intend to kindle a fire with this tooting-whistle of thine; but, as you
Title:  value the thing, take it, and blow your best on it.
Title:  
Title:  Gamut received his pitch-pipe with as strong an expression of pleasure as he
Title:  believed compatible with the grave functions he exercised. After essaying
Title:  its virtues repeatedly, in contrast with his own voice, and, satisfying
Title:  himself that none of its melody was lost, he made a very serious
Title:  demonstration toward achieving a few stanzas of one of the longest effusions
Title:  in the little volume so often mentioned.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, however, hastily interrupted his pious purpose by continuing
Title:  questions concerning the past and present condition of his fellow captives,
Title:  and in a manner more methodical than had been permitted by his feelings in
Title:  the opening of their interview. David, though he regarded his treasure with
Title:  longing eyes, was constrained to answer, especially as the venerable father
Title:  took a part in the interrogatories, with an interest too imposing to be
Title:  denied. Nor did the scout fail to throw in a pertinent inquiry, whenever a
Title:  fitting occasion presented. In this manner, though with frequent
Title:  interruptions which were filled with certain threatening sounds from the
Title:  recovered instrument, the pursuers were put in possession of such leading
Title:  circumstances as were likely to prove useful in accomplishing their great
Title:  and engrossing object - the recovery of the sisters. The narrative of David
Title:  was simple, and the facts but few.
Title:  
Title:  Magua had waited on the mountain until a safe moment to retire presented
Title:  itself, when he had descended, and taken the route along the western side of
Title:  the Horican in direction of the Canadas. As the subtle Huron was familiar
Title:  with the paths, and well knew there was no immediate danger of pursuit,
Title:  their progress had been moderate, and far from fatiguing. It appeared from
Title:  the unembellished statement of David, that his own presence had been rather
Title:  endured than desired; though even Magua had not been entirely exempt from
Title:  that veneration with which the Indians regard those whom the Great Spirit
Title:  had visited in their intellects. At night, the utmost care had been taken of
Title:  the captives, both to prevent injury from the damps of the woods and to
Title:  guard against an escape. At the spring, the horses were turned loose, as has
Title:  been seen; and, notwithstanding the remoteness and length of their trail,
Title:  the artifices already named were resorted to, in order to cut off every clue
Title:  to their place of retreat. On their arrival at the encampment of his people,
Title:  Magua, in obedience to a policy seldom departed from, separated his
Title:  prisoners. Cora had been sent to a tribe that temporarily occupied an
Title:  adjacent valley, though David was far too ignorant of the customs and
Title:  history of the natives, to be able to declare anything satisfactory
Title:  concerning their name or character. He only knew that they had not engaged
Title:  in the late expedition against William Henry; that, like the Hurons
Title:  themselves they were allies of Montcalm; and that they maintained an
Title:  amicable, though a watchful intercourse with the warlike and savage people
Title:  whom chance had, for a time, brought in such close and disagreeable contact
Title:  with themselves.
Title:  
Title:  The Mohicans and the scout listened to his interrupted and imperfect
Title:  narrative, with an interest that obviously increased as he proceeded; and it
Title:  was while attempting to explain the pursuits of the community in which Cora
Title:  was detained, that the latter abruptly demanded:
Title:  
Title:  Did you see the fashion of their knives? wee they of English or French
Title:  formation?
Title:  
Title:  My thoughts were bent on no such vanities, but rather mingled in consolation
Title:  with those of the maidens.
Title:  
Title:  The time may come when you will not consider the knife of a savage such a
Title:  despicable vanity, returned the scout, with a strong expression of contempt
Title:  for the other's dullness. Had they held their corn feast - or can you say
Title:  anything of the totems of the tribe?
Title:  
Title:  Of corn, we had many and plentiful feasts; for the grain, being in the milk
Title:  is both sweet to the mouth and comfortable to the stomach. Of totem, I know
Title:  not the meaning; but if it appertaineth in any wise to the art of Indian
Title:  music, it need not be inquired after at their hands. They never join their
Title:  voices in praise, and it would seem that they are among the profanest of the
Title:  idolatrous.
Title:  
Title:  Therein you belie the natur' of an Indian. Even the Mingo adores but the
Title:  true and loving God. 'Tis wicked fabrication of the whites, and I say it to
Title:  the shame of my color that would make the warrior bow down before images of
Title:  his own creation. It is true, they endeavor to make truces to the wicked one
Title:  - as who would not with an enemy he cannot conquer! but they look up for
Title:  favor and assistance to the Great and Good Spirit only.
Title:  
Title:  It may be so, said David; but I have seen strange and fantastic images drawn
Title:  in their paint, of which their admiration and care savored of spiritual
Title:  pride; especially one, and that, too, a foul and loathsome object.
Title:  
Title:  Was it a sarpent? quickly demanded the scout.
Title:  
Title:  Much the same. It was in the likeness of an abject and creeping tortoise.
Title:  
Title:  Hugh! exclaimed both the attentive Mohicans in a breath; while the scout
Title:  shook his head with the air of one who had made an important but by no means
Title:  a pleasing discovery. Then the father spoke, in the language of the
Title:  Delawares, and with a calmness and dignity that instantly arrested the
Title:  attention even of those to whom his words were unintelligible. His gestures
Title:  were impressive, and at times energetic. Once he lifted his arm on high;
Title:  and, as it descended, the action threw aside the folds of his light mantle,
Title:  a finger resting on his breast, as if he would enforce his meaning by the
Title:  attitude. Duncan's eyes followed the movement, and he perceived that the
Title:  animal just mentioned was beautifully, though faintly, worked in blue tint,
Title:  on the swarthy breast of the chief. All that he had ever heard of the
Title:  violent separation of the vast tribes of the Delawares rushed across his
Title:  mind, and he awaited the proper moment to speak, with a suspense that was
Title:  rendered nearly intolerable by his interest in the stake. His wish, however,
Title:  was anticipated by the scout who turned from his red friend, saying:
Title:  
Title:  We have found that which may be good or evil to us, as heaven disposes. The
Title:  Sagamore is of the high blood of the Delawares, and is the great chief of
Title:  their Tortoises! That some of this stock are among the people of whom the
Title:  singer tells us, is plain by his words; and, had he but spent half the
Title:  breath in prudent questions that he has blown away in making a trumpet of
Title:  his throat, we might have known how many warriors they numbered. It is,
Title:  altogether, a dangerous path we move in; for a friend whose face is turned
Title:  from you often bears a bloodier mind than the enemy who seeks your scalp.
Title:  
Title:  Explain, said Duncan.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis a long and melancholy tradition, and one I little like to think of; for
Title:  it is not to be denied that the evil has been mainly done by men with white
Title:  skins. But it has ended in turning the tomahawk of brother against brother,
Title:  and brought the Mingo and the Delaware to travel in the same path.
Title:  
Title:  You, then, suspect it is a portion of that people among whom Cora resides?
Title:  
Title:  The scout nodded his head in assent, though he seemed anxious to waive the
Title:  further discussion of a subject that appeared painful. The impatient Duncan
Title:  now made several hasty and desperate propositions to attempt the release of
Title:  the sisters. Munro seemed to shake off his apathy, and listened to the wild
Title:  schemes of the young man with a deference that his gray hairs and reverend
Title:  years should have denied. But the scout, after suffering the ardor of the
Title:  lover to expend itself a little, found means to convince him of the folly of
Title:  precipitation, in a manner that would require their coolest judgment and
Title:  utmost fortitude.
Title:  
Title:  It would be well, he added, to let this man go in again, as usual, and for
Title:  him to tarry in the lodges, giving notice to the gentle ones of our
Title:  approach, until we call him out, by signal, to consult. You know the cry of
Title:  a crow, friend, from the whistle of the whip-poor-will?
Title:  
Title:  'Tis a pleasing bird, returned David, and has a soft and melancholy note!
Title:  though the time is rather quick and ill-measured.
Title:  
Title:  He speaks of the wish-ton-wish, said the scout; well, since you like his
Title:  whistle, it shall be your signal. Remember, then, when you hear the
Title:  whip-poor-will's call three times repeated, you are to come into the bushes
Title:  where the bird might be supposed - -
Title:  
Title:  Stop, interrupted Heyward; I will accompany him.
Title:  
Title:  You! exclaimed the astonished Hawkeye; are you tired of seeing the sun rise
Title:  and set?
Title:  
Title:  David is a living proof that the Hurons can be merciful.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, but David can use his throat, as no man in his senses would pervart the
Title:  gift.
Title:  
Title:  I too can play the madman, the fool, the hero; in short, any or everything
Title:  to rescue her I love. Name your objections no longer: I am resolved.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye regarded the young man a moment in speechless amazement. But Duncan,
Title:  who, in deference to the other's skill and services, had hitherto submitted
Title:  somewhat implicitly to his dictation, now assumed the superior, with a
Title:  manner that was not easily resisted. He waved his hand, in sign of his
Title:  dislike to all remonstrance, and then, in more tempered language, he
Title:  continued:
Title:  
Title:  You have the means of disguise; change me; paint me, too, if you will; in
Title:  short, alter me to anything - a fool.
Title:  
Title:  It is not for one like me to say that he who is already formed by so
Title:  powerful a hand as Providence, stands in need of a change, muttered the
Title:  discontented scout. When you send your parties abroad in war, you find it
Title:  prudent, at least, to arrange the marks and places of encampment, in order
Title:  that they who fight on your side may know when and where to expect a friend.
Title:  
Title:  Listen, interrupted Duncan; you have heard from this faithful follower of
Title:  the captives, that the Indians are of two tribes, if not of different
Title:  nations. With one, whom you think to be a branch of the Delawares, is she
Title:  you call the dark-hair'; the other, and younger, of the ladies, is
Title:  undeniably with our declared enemies, the Hurons. It becomes my youth and
Title:  rank to attempt the latter adventure. While you, therefore, are negotiating
Title:  with your friends for the release of one of the sisters, I will effect that
Title:  of the other, or die.
Title:  
Title:  The awakened spirit of the young soldier gleamed in his eyes, and his form
Title:  became imposing under its influence. Hawkeye, though too much accustomed to
Title:  Indian artifices not to foresee the danger of the experiment, knew not well
Title:  how to combat this sudden resolution.
Title:  
Title:  Perhaps there was something in the proposal that suited his own hardy
Title:  nature, and that secret love of desperate adventure, which had increased
Title:  with his experience, until hazard and danger had become, in some measure,
Title:  necessary to the enjoyment of his existence. Instead of continuing to oppose
Title:  the scheme of Duncan, his humor suddenly altered, and he lent himself to its
Title:  execution.
Title:  
Title:  Come, he said, with a good-humored smile; the buck that will take to the
Title:  water must be headed, and not followed. Chingachgook has as many different
Title:  paints as the engineer officer's wife, who takes down natur' on scraps of
Title:  paper, making the mountains look like cocks of rusty hay, and placing the
Title:  blue sky in reach of your hand. The Sagamore can use them, too. Seat
Title:  yourself on the log; and my life on it, he can soon make a natural fool of
Title:  you, and that well to your liking.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan complied; and the Mohican, who had been an attentive listener to the
Title:  discourse, readily undertook the office. Long practised in all the subtle
Title:  arts of his race, he drew, with great dexterity and quickness, the fantastic
Title:  shadow that the natives were accustomed to consider as the evidence of a
Title:  friendly and jocular disposition. Every line that could possibly be
Title:  interpreted into a secret inclination for war, was carefully avoided; while,
Title:  on the other hand, he studied those conceits that might be construed into
Title:  amity.
Title:  
Title:  In short, he entirely sacrificed every appearance of the warrior to the
Title:  masquerade of a buffoon. Such exhibitions were not uncommon among the
Title:  Indians, and as Duncan was already sufficiently disguised in his dress,
Title:  there certainly did exist some reason for believing that, with his knowledge
Title:  of French, he might pass for a juggler from Ticonderoga, straggling among
Title:  the allied and friendly tribes.
Title:  
Title:  When he was thought to be sufficiently painted, the scout gave him much
Title:  friendly advice; concerted signals, and appointed the place where they
Title:  should meet, in the event of mutual success. The parting between Munro and
Title:  his young friend was more melancholy; still, the former submitted to the
Title:  separation with an indifference that his warm and honest nature would never
Title:  have permitted in a more healthful state of mind. The scout led Heyward
Title:  aside, and acquainted him with his intention to leave the veteran in some
Title:  safe encampment, in charge of Chingachgook, while he and Uncas pursued their
Title:  inquires among the people they had reason to believe were Delawares. Then,
Title:  renewing his cautions and advice, he concluded by saying, with a solemnity
Title:  and warmth of feeling, with which Duncan was deeply touched:
Title:  
Title:  And, now, God bless you! You have shown a spirit that I like; for it is the
Title:  gift of youth, more especially one of warm blood and a stout heart. But
Title:  believe the warning of a man who has reason to know all he says to be true.
Title:  You will have occasion for your best manhood, and for a sharper wit than
Title:  what is to be gathered in books, afore you outdo the cunning or get the
Title:  better of the courage of a Mingo. God bless you! if the Hurons master your
Title:  scalp, rely on the promise of one who has two stout warriors to back him.
Title:  They shall pay for their victory, with a life for every hair it holds. I
Title:  say, young gentleman, may Providence bless your undertaking, which is
Title:  altogether for good; and, remember, that to outwit the knaves it is lawful
Title:  to practise things that may not be naturally the gift of a white-skin.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan shook his worthy and reluctant associate warmly by the hand, once
Title:  more recommended his aged friend to his care, and returning his good wishes,
Title:  he motioned to David to proceed. Hawkeye gazed after the high-spirited and
Title:  adventurous young man for several moments, in open admiration; then, shaking
Title:  his head doubtingly, he turned, and led his own division of the party into
Title:  the concealment of the forest.
Title:  
Title:  The route taken by Duncan and David lay directly across the clearing of the
Title:  beavers, and along the margin of their pond.
Title:  
Title:  When the former found himself alone with one so simple, and so little
Title:  qualified to render any assistance in desperate emergencies, he first began
Title:  to be sensible of the difficulties of the task he had undertaken. The fading
Title:  light increased the gloominess of the bleak and savage wilderness that
Title:  stretched so far on every side of him, and there was even a fearful
Title:  character in the stillness of those little huts, that he knew were so
Title:  abundantly peopled. It struck him, as he gazed at the admirable structures
Title:  and the wonderful precautions of their sagacious inmates, that even the
Title:  brutes of these vast wilds were possessed of an instinct nearly commensurate
Title:  with his own reason; and he could not reflect, without anxiety, on the
Title:  unequal contest that he had so rashly courted. Then came the glowing image
Title:  of Alice; her distress; her actual danger; and all the peril of his
Title:  situation was forgotten. Cheering David, he moved on with the light and
Title:  vigorous step of youth and enterprise.
Title:  
Title:  After making nearly a semicircle around the pond, they diverged from the
Title:  water-course, and began to ascend to the level of a slight elevation in that
Title:  bottom land, over which they journeyed. Within half an hour they gained the
Title:  margin of another opening that bore all the signs of having been also made
Title:  by the beavers, and which those sagacious animals had probably been induced,
Title:  by some accident, to abandon, for the more eligible position they now
Title:  occupied. A very natural sensation caused Duncan to hesitate a moment,
Title:  unwilling to leave the cover of their bushy path, as a man pauses to collect
Title:  his energies before he essays any hazardous experiment, in which he is
Title:  secretly conscious they will all be needed. He profited by the halt, to
Title:  gather such information as might be obtained from his short and hasty
Title:  glances.
Title:  
Title:  On the opposite side of the clearing, and near the point where the brook
Title:  tumbled over some rocks, from a still higher level, some fifty or sixty
Title:  lodges, rudely fabricated of logs brush, and earth intermingled, were to be
Title:  discovered. They were arranged without any order, and seemed to be
Title:  constructed with very little attention to neatness or beauty. Indeed, so
Title:  very inferior were they in the two latter particulars to the village Duncan
Title:  had just seen, that he began to expect a second surprise, no less
Title:  astonishing that the former. This expectation was is no degree diminished,
Title:  when, by the doubtful twilight, he beheld twenty or thirty forms rising
Title:  alternately from the cover of the tall, coarse grass, in front of the
Title:  lodges, and then sinking again from the sight, as it were to burrow in the
Title:  earth. By the sudden and hasty glimpses that he caught of these figures,
Title:  they seemed more like dark, glancing specters, or some other unearthly
Title:  beings, than creatures fashioned with the ordinary and vulgar materials of
Title:  flesh and blood. A gaunt, naked form was seen, for a single instant, tossing
Title:  its arms wildly in the air, and then the spot it had filled was vacant; the
Title:  figure appearing suddenly in some other and distant place, or being
Title:  succeeded by another, possessing the same mysterious character. David,
Title:  observing that his companion lingered, pursued the direction of his gaze,
Title:  and in some measure recalled the recollection of Heyward, by speaking.
Title:  
Title:  There is much fruitful soil uncultivated here, he said; and, I may add,
Title:  without the sinful leaven of self-commendation, that, since my short sojourn
Title:  in these heathenish abodes, much good seed has been scattered by the
Title:  wayside.
Title:  
Title:  The tribes are fonder of the chase than of the arts of men of labor,
Title:  returned the unconscious Duncan, still gazing at the objects of his wonder.
Title:  
Title:  It is rather joy than labor to the spirit, to lift up the voice in praise;
Title:  but sadly do these boys abuse their gifts. Rarely have I found any of their
Title:  age, on whom nature has so freely bestowed the elements of psalmody; and
Title:  surely, surely, there are none who neglect them more. Three nights have I
Title:  now tarried here, and three several times have I assembled the urchins to
Title:  join in sacred song; and as often have they responded to my efforts with
Title:  whoopings and howlings that have chilled my soul!
Title:  
Title:  Of whom speak you?
Title:  
Title:  Of those children of the devil, who waste the precious moments in yonder
Title:  idle antics. Ah! the wholesome restraint of discipline is but little known
Title:  among this self-abandoned people. In a country of birches, a rod is never
Title:  seen, and it ought not to appear a marvel in my eyes, that the choicest
Title:  blessings of Providence are wasted in such cries as these.
Title:  
Title:  David closed his ears against the juvenile pack, whose yell just then rang
Title:  shrilly through the forest; and Duncan, suffering his lip to curl, as in
Title:  mockery of his own superstition, said firmly:
Title:  
Title:  We will proceed.
Title:  
Title:  Without removing the safeguards form his ears, the master of song complied,
Title:  and together they pursued their way toward what David was sometimes wont to
Title:  call the tents of the Philistines.
Title:  
Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 23
Title:  
Title:       But though the beast of game
Title:       The privilege of chase may claim;
Title:       Though space and law the stag we lend
Title:       Ere hound we slip, or bow we bend;
Title:       Who ever recked, where, how, or when
Title:       The prowling fox was trapped or slain?
Title:  
Title:                                                        LADY OF THE LAKE
Title:  
Title:  It is unusual to find an encampment of the natives, like those of the more
Title:  instructed whites, guarded by the presence of armed men. Well informed of
Title:  the approach of every danger, while it is yet at a distance, the Indian
Title:  generally rests secure under his knowledge of the signs of the forest, and
Title:  the long and difficult paths that separate him from those he has most reason
Title:  to dread. But the enemy who, by any lucky concurrence of accidents, has
Title:  found means to elude the vigilance of the scouts, will seldom meet with
Title:  sentinels nearer home to sound the alarm. In addition to this general usage,
Title:  the tribes friendly to the Fench knew too well the weight of the blow that
Title:  had just been struck, to apprehend any immediate danger from the hostile
Title:  nations that were tributary to the crown of Britain.
Title:  
Title:  When Duncan and David, therefore, found themselves in the center of the
Title:  children, who played the antics already mentioned, it was without the least
Title:  previous intimation of their approach. But so soon as they were observed the
Title:  whole of the juvenile pack raised, by common consent, a shrill and warning
Title:  whoop; and then sank, as it were, by magic, from before the sight of their
Title:  visitors. The naked, tawny bodies of the crouching urchins blended so nicely
Title:  at that hour, with the withered herbage, that at first it seemed as if the
Title:  earth had, in truth, swallowed up their forms; though when surprise
Title:  permitted Duncan to bend his look more curiously about the spot, he found it
Title:  everywhere met by dark, quick, and rolling eyeballs.
Title:  
Title:  Gathering no encouragement from this startling presage of the nature of the
Title:  scrutiny he was likely to undergo from the more mature judgments of the men,
Title:  there was an instant when the young soldier would have retreated. It was,
Title:  however, too late to appear to hesitate. The cry of the children had drawn a
Title:  dozen warriors to the door of the nearest lodge, where they stood clustered
Title:  in a dark and savage group, gravely awaiting the nearer approach of those
Title:  who had unexpectedly come among them.
Title:  
Title:  David, in some measure familiarized to the scene, led the way with a
Title:  steadiness that no slight obstacle was likely to disconcert, into this very
Title:  building. It was the principal edifice of the village, though roughly
Title:  constructed of the bark and branches of trees; being the lodge in which the
Title:  tribe held its councils and public meetings during their temporary residence
Title:  on the borders of the English province. Duncan found it difficult to assume
Title:  the necessary appearance of unconcern, as he brushed the dark and powerful
Title:  frames of the savages who thronged its threshold; but, conscious that his
Title:  existence depended on his presence of mind, he trusted to the discretion of
Title:  his companion, whose footsteps he closely followed, endeavoring, as he
Title:  proceeded, to rally his thoughts for the occasion. His blood curdled when he
Title:  found himself in absolute contact with such fierce and implacable enemies;
Title:  but he so far mastered his feelings as to pursue his way into the center of
Title:  the lodge, with an exterior that did not betray the weakness. Imitating the
Title:  example of the deliberate Gamut, he drew a bundle of fragrant brush from
Title:  beneath a pile that filled the corner of the hut, and seated himself in
Title:  silence.
Title:  
Title:  So soon as their visitor had passed, the observant warriors fell back from
Title:  the entrance, and arranging themselves about him, they seemed patiently to
Title:  await the moment when it might comport with the dignity of the stranger to
Title:  speak. By far the greater number stood leaning, in lazy, lounging attitudes,
Title:  against the upright posts that supported the crazy building, while three or
Title:  four of the oldest and most distinguished of the chiefs placed themselves on
Title:  the earth a little more in advance.
Title:  
Title:  A flaring torch was burning in the place, and set its red glare from face to
Title:  face and figure to figure, as it waved in the currents of air. Duncan
Title:  profited by its light to read the probable character of his reception, in
Title:  the countenances of his hosts. But his ingenuity availed him little, against
Title:  the cold artifices of the people he had encountered. The chiefs in front
Title:  scarce cast a glance at his person, keeping their eyes on the ground, with
Title:  an air that might have been intended for respect, but which it was quite
Title:  easy to construe into distrust. The men in the shadow were less reserved.
Title:  Duncan soon detected their searching, but stolen, looks which, in truth,
Title:  scanned his person and attire inch by inch; leaving no emotion of the
Title:  countenance, no gesture, no line of the paint, nor even the fashion of a
Title:  garment, unheeded, and without comment.
Title:  
Title:  At length one whose hair was beginning to be sprinkled with gray, but whose
Title:  sinewy limbs and firm tread announced that he was still equal to the duties
Title:  of manhood, advanced out of the gloom of a corner, whither he had probably
Title:  posted himself to make his observations unseen, and spoke. He used the
Title:  language of the Wyandots, or Hurons; his words were, consequently,
Title:  unintelligible to Heyward, though they seemed, by the gestures that
Title:  accompanied them, to be uttered more in courtesy than anger. The latter
Title:  shook his head, and made a gesture indicative of his inability to reply.
Title:  
Title:  Do none of my brothers speak the French or the English? he said, in the
Title:  former language, looking about him from countenance to countenance, in hopes
Title:  of finding a nod of assent.
Title:  
Title:  Though more than one had turned, as if to catch the meaning of his words,
Title:  they remained unanswered.
Title:  
Title:  I should be grieved to think, continued Duncan, speaking slowly, and using
Title:  the simplest French of which he was the master, to believe that none of this
Title:  wise and brave nation understand the language that the Grand Monarque uses
Title:  when he talks to his children. His heart would be heavy did he believe his
Title:  red warriors paid him so little respect!
Title:  
Title:  A long and grave pause succeeded, during which no movement of a limb, nor
Title:  any expression of an eye, betrayed the expression produced by his remark.
Title:  Duncan, who knew that silence was a virtue among his hosts, gladly had
Title:  recourse to the custom, in order to arrange his ideas. At length the same
Title:  warrior who had before addressed him replied, by dryly demanding, in the
Title:  language of the Canadas:
Title:  
Title:  When our Great Father speaks to his people, is it with the tongue of a
Title:  Huron?
Title:  
Title:  He knows no difference in his children, whether the color of the skin be
Title:  red, or black, or white, returned Duncan, evasively; though chiefly is he
Title:  satisfied with the brave Hurons.
Title:  
Title:  In what manner will he speak, demanded the wary chief, when the runners
Title:  count to him the scalps which five nights ago grew on the heads of the
Title:  Yengeese?
Title:  
Title:  They were his enemies, said Duncan, shuddering involuntarily; and doubtless,
Title:  he will say, it is good; my Hurons are very gallant.
Title:  
Title:  Our Canada father does not think it. Instead of looking foward to reward his
Title:  Indians, his eyes are turned backward. He sees the dead Yengeese, but no
Title:  Huron. What can this mean?
Title:  
Title:  A great chief, like him, has more thoughts than tongues. He looks to see
Title:  that no enemies are on his trail.
Title:  
Title:  The canoe of a dead warrior will not float on the Horican, returned the
Title:  savage, gloomily. His ears are open to the Delawares, who are not our
Title:  friends, and they fill them with lies.
Title:  
Title:  It cannot be. See; he has bid me, who am a man that knows the art of
Title:  healing, to go to his children, the red Hurons of the great lakes, and ask
Title:  if any are sick!
Title:  
Title:  Another silence succeeded this annunciation of the character Duncan had
Title:  assumed. Every eye was simultaneously bent on his person, as if to inquire
Title:  into the truth or falsehood of the declaration, with an intelligence and
Title:  keenness that caused the subject of their scrutiny to tremble for the
Title:  result. He was, however, relieved again by the former speaker.
Title:  
Title:  Do the cunning men of the Canadas paint their skins? the Huron coldly
Title:  continued; we have heard them boast that their faces were pale.
Title:  
Title:  When an Indian chief comes among his white fathers, returned Duncan, with
Title:  great steadiness, he lays aside his buffalo robe, to carry the shirt that is
Title:  offered him. My brothers have given me paint and I wear it.
Title:  
Title:  A low murmur of applause announced that the compliment of the tribe was
Title:  favorably received. The elderly chief made a gesture of commendation, which
Title:  was answered by most of his companions, who each threw forth a hand and
Title:  uttered a brief exclamation of pleasure. Duncan began to breathe more
Title:  freely, believing that the weight of his examination was past; and, as he
Title:  had already prepared a simple and probable tale to support his pretended
Title:  occupation, his hopes of ultimate success grew brighter.
Title:  
Title:  After a silence of a few moments, as if adjusting his thoughts, in order to
Title:  make a suitable answer to the declaration their guests had just given,
Title:  another warrior arose, and placed himself in an attitude to speak. While his
Title:  lips were yet in the act of parting, a low but fearful sound arose from the
Title:  forest, and was immediately succeeded by a high, shrill yell, that was drawn
Title:  out, until it equaled the longest and most plaintive howl of the wolf. The
Title:  sudden and terrible interruption caused Duncan to start from his seat,
Title:  unconscious of everything but the effect produced by so frightful a cry. At
Title:  the same moment, the warriors glided in a body from the lodge, and the outer
Title:  air was filled with loud shouts, that nearly drowned those awful sounds,
Title:  which were still ringing beneath the arches of the woods. Unable to command
Title:  himself any longer, the youth broke from the place, and presently stood in
Title:  the center of a disorderly throng, that included nearly everything having
Title:  life, within the limits of the encampment. Men, women, and children; the
Title:  aged, the inform, the active, and the strong, were alike abroad, some
Title:  exclaiming aloud, others clapping their hands with a joy that seemed
Title:  frantic, and all expressing their savage pleasure in some unexpected event.
Title:  Though astounded, at first, by the uproar, Heyward was soon enabled to find
Title:  its solution by the scene that followed.
Title:  
Title:  There yet lingered sufficient light in the heavens to exhibit those bright
Title:  openings among the tree-tops, where different paths left the clearing to
Title:  enter the depths of the wilderness. Beneath one of them, a line of warriors
Title:  issued from the woods, and advanced slowly toward the dwellings. One in
Title:  front bore a short pole, on which, as it afterwards appeared, were suspended
Title:  several human scalps. The startling sounds that Duncan had heard were what
Title:  the whites have not inappropriately called the death-hallo; and each
Title:  repetition of the cry was intended to announce to the tribe the fate of an
Title:  enemy. Thus far the knowledge of Heyward assisted him in the explanation;
Title:  and as he now knew that the interruption was caused by the unlooked-for
Title:  return of a succcessful war-party, every disagreeable sensation was quieted
Title:  in inward congratulation, for the opportune relief and insignificance it
Title:  conferred on himself.
Title:  
Title:  When at the distance of a few hundred feet from the lodges the newly arrived
Title:  warriors halted. Their plaintive and terrific cry, which was intended to
Title:  represent equally the wailings of the dead and the triumph to the victors,
Title:  had entirely ceased. One of their number now called aloud, in words that
Title:  were far from appalling, though not more intelligible to those for whose
Title:  ears they were intended, than their expressive yells. It would be difficult
Title:  to convey a suitable idea of the savage ecstasy with which the news thus
Title:  imparted was received. The whole encampment, in a moment, became a scene of
Title:  the most violent bustle and commotion. The warriors drew their knives, and
Title:  flourishing them, they arranged themselves in two lines, forming a lane that
Title:  extended from the war-party to the lodges. The squaws seized clubs, axes, or
Title:  whatever weapon of offense first offered itself to their hands, and rushed
Title:  eagerly to act their part in the cruel game that was at hand. Even the
Title:  children would not be excluded; but boys, little able to wield the
Title:  instruments, tore the tomahawks from the belts of their fathers, and stole
Title:  into the ranks, apt imitators of the savage traits exhibited by their
Title:  parents.
Title:  
Title:  Large piles of brush lay scattered about the clearing, and a wary and aged
Title:  squaw was occupied in firing as many as might serve to light the coming
Title:  exhibition. As the flame arose, its power exceeded that of the parting day,
Title:  and assisted to render objects at the same time more distinct and more
Title:  hideous. The whole scene formed a striking picture, whose frame was composed
Title:  of the dark and tall border of pines. The warriors just arrived were the
Title:  most distant figures. A little in advance stood two men, who were apparently
Title:  selected from the rest, as the principal actors in what was to follow. The
Title:  light was not strong enough to render their features distinct, though it was
Title:  quite evident that they were governed by very different emotions. While one
Title:  stood erect and firm, prepared to meet his fate like a hero, the other bowed
Title:  his head, as if palsied by terror or stricken with shame. The high-spirited
Title:  Duncan felt a powerful impulse of admiration and pity toward the former,
Title:  though no opportunity could offer to exhibit his generous emotions. He
Title:  watched his slightest movement, however, with eager eyes; and, as he traced
Title:  the fine outline of his admirably proportioned and active frame, he
Title:  endeavored to persuade himself, that, if the powers of man, seconded by such
Title:  noble resolution, could bear one harmless through so severe a trial, the
Title:  youthful captive before him might hope for success in the hazardous race he
Title:  was about to run. Insensibly the young man drew nigher to the swarthy lines
Title:  of the Hurons, and scarcely breathed, so intense became his interest in the
Title:  spectacle. Just then the signal yell was given, and the momentary quiet
Title:  which had preceded it was broken by a burst of cries, that far exceeded any
Title:  before heard. The more abject of the two victims continued motionless; but
Title:  the other bounded from the place at the cry, with the activity and swiftness
Title:  of a deer. Instead of rushing through the hostile lines, as had been
Title:  expected, he just entered the dangerous defile, and before time was given
Title:  for a single blow, turned short, and leaping the heads of a row of children,
Title:  he gained at once the exterior and safer side of the formidable array. The
Title:  artifice was answered by a hundred voices raised in imprecations; and the
Title:  whole of the excited multitude broke from their order, and spread themselves
Title:  about the place in wild confusion.
Title:  
Title:  A dozen blazing piles now shed their lurid brightness on the place, which
Title:  resembled some unhallowed and supernatural arena, in which malicious demons
Title:  had assembled to act their bloody and lawless rites. The forms in the
Title:  background looked like unearthly beings, gliding before the eye, and
Title:  cleaving the air with frantic and unmeaning gestures; while the savage
Title:  passions of such as passed the flames were rendered fearfully distinct by
Title:  the gleams that shot athwart their inflamed visages.
Title:  
Title:  It will easily be understood that, amid such a concourse of vindictive
Title:  enemies, no breathing time was allowed the fugitive. There was a single
Title:  moment when it seemed as if he would have reached the forest, but the whole
Title:  body of his captors threw themselves before him, and drove him back into the
Title:  center of his relentless persecutors. Turning like a headed deer, he shot,
Title:  with the swiftness of an arrow, through a pillar of forked flame, and
Title:  passing the whole multitude harmless, he appeared on the opposite side of
Title:  the clearing. Here, too, he was met and turned by a few of the older and
Title:  more subtle of the Hurons. Once more he tried the throng, as if seeking
Title:  safety in its blindness, and then several moments succeeded, during which
Title:  Duncan believed the active and courageous young stranger was lost.
Title:  
Title:  Nothing could be distinguished but a dark mass of human forms tossed and
Title:  involved in inexplicable confusion. Arms, gleaming knives, and formidable
Title:  clubs, appeared above them, but the blows were evidently given at random.
Title:  The awful effect was heightened by the piercing shrieks of the women and the
Title:  fierce yells of the warriors. Now and then Duncan caught a glimpse of a
Title:  light form cleaving the air in some desperate bound, and he rather hoped
Title:  than believed that the captive yet retained the command of his astonishing
Title:  powers of activity. Suddenly the multitude rolled backward, and approached
Title:  the spot where he himself stood. The heavy body in the rear pressed upon the
Title:  women and children in front, and bore them to the earth. The stranger
Title:  reappeared in the confusion. Human power could not, however, much longer
Title:  endure so severe a trial. Of this the captive seemed conscious. Profiting by
Title:  the momentary opening, he darted from among the warriors, and made a
Title:  desperate, and what seemed to Duncan a final effort to gain the wood. As if
Title:  aware that no danger was to be apprehended from the young soldier, the
Title:  fugitive nearly brushed his person in his flight. A tall and powerful Huron,
Title:  who had husbanded his forces, pressed close upon his heels, and with an
Title:  uplifted arm menaced a fatal blow. Duncan thrust forth a foot, and the shock
Title:  precipitated the eager savage headlong, many feet in advance of his intended
Title:  victim. Thought itself is not quicker than was the motion with which the
Title:  latter profited by the advantage; he turned, gleamed like a meteor again
Title:  before the eyes of Duncan, and, at the next moment, when the latter
Title:  recovered his recollection, and gazed around in quest of the captive, he saw
Title:  him quietly leaning against a small painted post, which stood before the
Title:  door of the principal lodge.
Title:  
Title:  Apprehensive that the part he had taken in the escape might prove fatal to
Title:  himself, Duncan left the place without delay. He followed the crowd, which
Title:  drew nigh the lodges, gloomy and sullen, like any other multitude that had
Title:  been disappointed in an execution. Curiosity, or perhaps a better feeling,
Title:  induced him to approach the stranger. He found him, standing with one arm
Title:  cast about the protecting post, and breathing thick and hard, after his
Title:  exertions, but disdaining to permit a single sign of suffering to escape.
Title:  His person was now protected by immemorial and sacred usage, until the tribe
Title:  in council had deliberated and determined on his fate. It was not difficult,
Title:  however, to foretell the result, if any presage could be drawn from the
Title:  feelings of those who crowded the place.
Title:  
Title:  There was no term of abuse known to the Huron vocabulary that the
Title:  disappointed women did not lavishly expend on the successful stranger. They
Title:  flouted at his efforts, and told him, with bitter scoffs, that his feet were
Title:  better than his hands; and that he merited wings, while he knew not the use
Title:  of an arrow or a knife. To all this the captive made no reply; but was
Title:  content to preserve an attitude in which dignity was singularly blended with
Title:  disdain. Exasperated as much by his composure as by his good-fortune, their
Title:  words became unintelligible, and were succeeded by shrill, piercing yells.
Title:  Just then the crafty squaw, who had taken the necessary precaution to fire
Title:  the piles, made her way through the throng, and cleared a place for herself
Title:  in front of the captive. The squalid and withered person of this hag might
Title:  well have obtained for her the character of possessing more than human
Title:  cunning. Throwing back her light vestment, she stretched forth her long,
Title:  skinny arm, in derision, and using the language of the Lenape, as more
Title:  intelligible to the subject of her gibes, she commenced aloud:
Title:  
Title:  Look you, Delaware, she said, snapping her fingers in his face; your nation
Title:  is a race of women, and the hoe is better fitted to your hands than the gun.
Title:  Your squaws are the mothers of deer; but if a bear, or a wildcat, or a
Title:  serpent were born among you, ye would flee. The Huron girls shall make you
Title:  petticoats, and we will find you a husband.
Title:  
Title:  A burst of savage laughter succeeded this attack, during which the soft and
Title:  musical merriment of the younger females strangely chimed with the cracked
Title:  voice of their older and more malignant companion. But the stranger was
Title:  superior to all their efforts. His head was immovable; nor did he betray the
Title:  slightest consciousness that any were present, except when his haughty eye
Title:  rolled toward the dusky forms of the warriors, who stalked in the background
Title:  silent and sullen observers of the scene.
Title:  
Title:  Infuriated at the self-command of the captive, the woman placed her arms
Title:  akimbo; and, throwing herself into a posture of defiance, she broke out
Title:  anew, in a torrent of words that no art of ours could commit successfully to
Title:  paper. Her breath was, however, expended in vain; for, although
Title:  distinguished in her nation as a proficient in the art of abuse, she was
Title:  permitted to work herself into such a fury as actually to foam at the mouth,
Title:  without causing a muscle to vibrate in the motionless figure of the
Title:  stranger. The effect of his indifference began to extend itself to the other
Title:  spectators; and a youngster, who was just quitting the condition of a boy to
Title:  enter the state of manhood, attempted to assist the termagant, by
Title:  flourishing his tomahawk before their victim, and adding his empty boasts to
Title:  the taunts of the women. Then, indeed, the captive turned his face toward
Title:  the light, and looked down on the stripling with an expression that was
Title:  superior to contempt. At the next moment he resumed his quiet and reclining
Title:  attitude against the post. But the change of posture had permitted Duncan to
Title:  exchange glances with the firm and piercing eyes of Uncas.
Title:  
Title:  Breathless with amazement, and heavily oppressed with the critical situation
Title:  of his friend, Heyward recoiled before the look, trembling lest its meaning
Title:  might, in some unknown manner, hasten the prisoner's fate. There was not,
Title:  however, any instant cause for such an apprehension. Just then a warrior
Title:  forced his way into the exasperated crowd. Motioning the women and children
Title:  aside with a stern gesture, he took Uncas by the arm, and led him toward the
Title:  door of the council-lodge. Thither all the chiefs, and most of the
Title:  distinguished warriors, followed; among whom the anxious Heyward found means
Title:  to enter without attracting any dangerous attention to himself.
Title:  
Title:  A few minutes were consumed in disposing of those present in a manner
Title:  suitable to their rank and influence in the tribe. An order very similar to
Title:  that adopted in the preceding interview was observed; the aged and superior
Title:  chiefs occupying the area of the spacious apartment, within the powerful
Title:  light of a glaring torch, while their juniors and inferiors were arranged in
Title:  the background, presenting a dark outline of swarthy and marked visages. In
Title:  the very center of the lodge, immediately under an opening that admitted the
Title:  twinkling light of one or two stars, stood Uncas, calm, elevated, and
Title:  collected. His high and haughty carriage was not lost on his captors, who
Title:  often bent their looks on his person, with eyes which, while they lost none
Title:  of their inflexibility of purpose, plainly betrayed their admiration of the
Title:  stranger's daring.
Title:  
Title:  The case was different with the individual whom Duncan had observed to stand
Title:  forth with his friend, previously to the desperate trial of speed; and who,
Title:  instead of joining in the chase, had remained, throughout its turbulent
Title:  uproar, like a cringing statue, expressive of shame and disgrace. Though not
Title:  a hand had been extended to greet him, nor yet an eye had condescended to
Title:  watch his movements, he had also entered the lodge, as though impelled by a
Title:  fate to whose decrees he submitted, seemingly, without a struggle. Heyward
Title:  profited by the first opportunity to gaze in his face, secretly apprehensive
Title:  he might find the features of another acquaintance; but they proved to be
Title:  those of a stranger, and, what was still more inexplicable, of one who bore
Title:  all the distinctive marks of a Huron warrior. Instead of mingling with his
Title:  tribe, however, he sat apart, a solitary being in a multitude, his form
Title:  shrinking into a crouching and abject attitude, as if anxious to fill as
Title:  little space as possible. When each individual had taken his proper station,
Title:  and silence reigned in the place, the gray-haired chief already introduced
Title:  to the reader, spoke aloud, in the language of the Lenni Lenape.
Title:  
Title:  Delaware, he said, though one of a nation of women, you have proved yourself
Title:  a man. I would give you food; but he who eats with a Huron should become his
Title:  friend. Rest in peace till the morning sun, when our last words shall be
Title:  spoken.
Title:  
Title:  Seven nights, and as many summer days, have I fasted on the trail of the
Title:  Hurons, Uncas coldly replied; the children of the Lenape know how to travel
Title:  the path of the just without lingering to eat.
Title:  
Title:  Two of my young men are in pursuit of your companion, resumed the other,
Title:  without appearing to regard the boast of his captive; when they get back,
Title:  then will our wise man say to you live or die.
Title:  
Title:  Has a Huron no ears? scornfully exclaimed Uncas; twice, since he has been
Title:  your prisoner, has the Delaware heard a gun that he knows. Your young men
Title:  will never come back!
Title:  
Title:  A short and sullen pause succeeded this bold assertion. Duncan, who
Title:  understood the Mohican to allude to the fatal rifle of the scout, bent
Title:  forward in earnest observation of the effect it might produce on the
Title:  conquerors; but the chief was content with simply retorting:
Title:  
Title:  If the Lenape are so skillful, why is one of their bravest warriors here?
Title:  
Title:  He followed in the steps of a flying coward, and fell into a snare. The
Title:  cunning beaver may be caught.
Title:  
Title:  As Uncas thus replied, he pointed with his finger toward the solitary Huron,
Title:  but without deigning to bestow any other notice on so unworthy an object.
Title:  The words of the answer and the air of the speaker produced a strong
Title:  sensation among his auditors. Every eye rolled sullenly toward the
Title:  individual indicated by the simple gesture, and a low, threatening murmur
Title:  passed through the crowd. The ominous sounds reached the outer door, and the
Title:  women and children pressing into the throng, no gap had been left, between
Title:  shoulder and shoulder, that was not now filled with the dark lineaments of
Title:  some eager and curious human countenance.
Title:  
Title:  In the meantime, the more aged chiefs, in the center, communed with each
Title:  other in short and broken sentences. Not a word was uttered that did not
Title:  convey the meaning of the speaker, in the simplest and most energetic form.
Title:  Again, a long and deeply solemn pause took place. It was known, by all
Title:  present, to be the brave precursor of a weighty and important judgment. They
Title:  who composed the outer circle of faces were on tiptoe to gaze; and even the
Title:  culprit for an instant forgot his shame in a deeper emotion, and exposed his
Title:  abject features, in order to cast an anxious and troubled glance at the dark
Title:  assemblage of chiefs. The silence was finally broken by the aged warrior so
Title:  often named. He arose from the earth, and moving past the immovable form of
Title:  Uncas, placed himself in a dignified attitude before the offender. At that
Title:  moment, the withered squaw already mentioned moved into the circle, in a
Title:  slow, sidling sort of a dance, holding the torch, and muttering the
Title:  indistinct words of what might have been a species of incantation. Though
Title:  her presence was altogether an intrusion, it was unheeded.
Title:  
Title:  Approaching Uncas, she held the blazing brand in such a manner as to cast
Title:  its red glare on his person, and to expose the slightest emotion of his
Title:  countenance. The Mohican maintained his firm and haughty attitude; and his
Title:  eyes, so far from deigning to meet her inquisitive look, dwelt steadily on
Title:  the distance, as though it penetrated the obstacles which impeded the view
Title:  and looked into futurity. Satisfied with her examination, she left him, with
Title:  a slight expression of pleasure, and proceeded to practise the same trying
Title:  experiment on her delinquent countryman.
Title:  
Title:  The young Huron was in his war paint, and very little of a finely molded
Title:  form was concealed by his attire. The light rendered every limb and joint
Title:  discernible, and Duncan turned away in horror when he saw they were writhing
Title:  in irrepressible agony. The woman was commencing a low and plaintive howl at
Title:  the sad and shameful spectacle, when the chief put forth his hand and gently
Title:  pushed her aside.
Title:  
Title:  Reed-that-bends, he said, addressing the young culprit by name, and in his
Title:  proper language, though the Great Spirit has made you pleasant to the eyes,
Title:  it would have been better that you had not been born. Your tongue is loud in
Title:  the village, but in battle it is still. None of my young men strike the
Title:  tomahawk deeper into the war- post - none of them so lightly on the
Title:  Yengeese. The enemy know the shape of your back, but they have never seen
Title:  the color of your eyes. Three times have they called on you to come, and as
Title:  often did you forget to answer. Your name will never be mentioned again in
Title:  your tribe - it is already forgotten.
Title:  
Title:  As the chief slowly uttered these words, pausing impressively between each
Title:  sentence, the culprit raised his face, in deference to the other's rank and
Title:  years. Shame, horror, and pride struggled in its lineaments. His eye, which
Title:  was contracted with inward anguish, gleamed on the persons of those whose
Title:  breath was his fame; and the latter emotion for an instant predominated. He
Title:  arose to his feet, and baring his bosom, looked steadily on the keen,
Title:  glittering knife, that was already upheld by his inexorable judge. As the
Title:  weapon passed slowly into his heart he even smiled, as if in joy at having
Title:  found death less dreadful than he had anticipated, and fell heavily on his
Title:  face, at the feet of the rigid and unyielding form of Uncas.
Title:  
Title:  The squaw gave a loud and plaintive yell, dashed the torch to the earth, and
Title:  buried everything in darkness. The whole shuddering group of spectators
Title:  glided from the lodge like troubled sprites; and Duncan thought that he and
Title:  the yet throbbing body of the victim of an Indian judgment had now become
Title:  its only tenants.
