Title:  Chapter 24
Title:  
Title:       Thus spoke the sage: the kings without delay
Title:       Dissolve the council, and their chief obey.
Title:  
Title:                                                            POPE'S Iliad
Title:  
Title:  A single moment served to convince the youth that he was mistaken. A hand
Title:  was laid, with a powerful pressure, on his arm, and the low voice of Uncas
Title:  muttered in his ear:
Title:  
Title:  The Hurons are dogs. The sight of a coward's blood can never make a warrior
Title:  tremble. The Gray Head and the Sagamore are safe, and the rifle of Hawkeye
Title:  is not asleep. Go - Uncas and the Open Hand are now strangers. It is enough.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward would gladly have heard more, but a gentle push from his friend
Title:  urged him toward the door, and admonished him of the danger that might
Title:  attend the discovery of their intercourse. Slowly and reluctantly yielding
Title:  to the necessity, he quitted the place, and mingled with the throng that
Title:  hovered nigh. The dying fires in the clearing cast a dim and uncertain light
Title:  on the dusky figures that were silently stalking to and fro; and
Title:  occasionally a brighter gleam than common glanced into the lodge, and
Title:  exhibited the figure of Uncas still maintaining its upright attitude near
Title:  the dead body of the Huron.
Title:  
Title:  A knot of warriors soon entered the place again, and reissuing, they bore
Title:  the senseless remains into the adjacent woods. After this termination of the
Title:  scene, Duncan wandered among the lodges, unquestioned and unnoticed,
Title:  endeavoring to find some trace of her in whose behalf he incurred the risk
Title:  he ran. In the present temper of the tribe it would have been easy to have
Title:  fled and rejoined his companions, had such a wish crossed his mind. But, in
Title:  addition to the never-ceasing anxiety on account of Alice, a fresher though
Title:  feebler interest in the fate of Uncas assisted to chain him to the spot. He
Title:  continued, therefore, to stray from hut to hut, looking into each only to
Title:  encounter additional disappointment, until he had made the entire circuit of
Title:  the village. Abandoning a species of inquiry that proved so fruitless, he
Title:  retraced his steps to the council-lodge, resolved to seek and question
Title:  David, in order to put an end to his doubts.
Title:  
Title:  On reaching the building, which had proved alike the seat of judgment and
Title:  the place of execution, the young man found that the excitement had already
Title:  subsided. The warriors had reassembled, and were now calmly smoking, while
Title:  they conversed gravely on the chief incidents of their recent expedition to
Title:  the head of the Horican. Though the return of Duncan was likely to remind
Title:  them of his character, and the suspicious circumstances of his visit, it
Title:  produced no visible sensation. So far, the terrible scene that had just
Title:  occurred proved favorable to his views, and he required no other prompter
Title:  than his own feelings to convince him of the expediency of profiting by so
Title:  unexpected an advantage.
Title:  
Title:  Without seeming to hesitate, he walked into the lodge, and took his seat
Title:  with a gravity that accorded admirably with the deportment of his hosts. A
Title:  hasty but searching glance sufficed to tell him that, though Uncas still
Title:  remained where he had left him, David had not reappeared. No other restraint
Title:  was imposed on the former than the watchful looks of a young Huron, who had
Title:  placed himself at hand; though an armed warrior leaned against the post that
Title:  formed one side of the narrow doorway. In every other respect, the captive
Title:  seemed at liberty; still he was excluded from all participation in the
Title:  discourse, and possessed much more of the air of some finely molded statue
Title:  than a man having life and volition.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward had too recently witnessed a frightful instance of the prompt
Title:  punishments of the people into whose hands he had fallen to hazard an
Title:  exposure by any officious boldness. He would greatly have preferred silence
Title:  and meditation to speech, when a discovery of his real condition might prove
Title:  so instantly fatal. Unfortunately for this prudent resolution, his
Title:  entertainers appeared otherwise disposed. He had not long occupied the seat
Title:  wisely taken a little in the shade, when another of the elder warriors, who
Title:  spoke the French language, addressed him:
Title:  
Title:  My Canada father does not forget his children, said the chief; I thank him.
Title:  An evil spirit lives in the wife of one of my young men. Can the cunning
Title:  stranger frighten him away?
Title:  
Title:  Heyward possessed some knowledge of the mummery practised among the Indians,
Title:  in the cases of such supposed visitations. He saw, at a glance, that the
Title:  circumstance might possibly be improved to further his own ends. It would,
Title:  therefore, have been difficult, just then to have uttered a proposal that
Title:  would have given him more satisfaction. Aware of the necessity of preserving
Title:  the dignity of his imaginary character, however, he repressed his feelings,
Title:  and answered with suitable mystery:
Title:  
Title:  Spirits differ; some yield to the power of wisdom, while others are too
Title:  strong.
Title:  
Title:  My brother is a great medicine, said the cunning savage; he will try?
Title:  
Title:  A gesture of assent was the answer. The Huron was content with the
Title:  assurance, and, resuming his pipe, he awaited the proper moment to move. The
Title:  impatient Heyward, inwardly execrating the cold customs of the savages,
Title:  which required such sacrifices to appearance, was fain to assume an air of
Title:  indifference, equal to that maintained by the chief, who was, in truth, a
Title:  near relative of the afflicted woman. The minutes lingered, and the delay
Title:  had seemed an hour to the adventurer in empiricism, when the Huron laid
Title:  aside his pipe and drew his robe across his breast, as if about to lead the
Title:  way to the lodge of the invalid. Just then, a warrior of powerful frame,
Title:  darkened the door, and stalking silently among the attentive group, he
Title:  seated himself on one end of the low pile of brush which sustained Duncan.
Title:  The latter cast an impatient look at his neighbor, and felt his flesh creep
Title:  with uncontrollable horror when he found himself in actual contact with
Title:  Magua.
Title:  
Title:  The sudden return of this artful and dreaded chief caused a delay in the
Title:  departure of the Huron. Several pipes, that had been extinguished, were
Title:  lighted again; while the newcomer, without speaking a word, drew his
Title:  tomahawk from his girdle, and filling the bowl on its head began to inhale
Title:  the vapors of the weed through the hollow handle, with as much indifference
Title:  as if he had not been absent two weary days on a long and toilsome hunt. Ten
Title:  minutes, which appeared so many ages to Duncan, might have passed in this
Title:  manner; and the warriors were fairly enveloped in a cloud of white smoke
Title:  before any of them spoke.
Title:  
Title:  Welcome! one at length uttered; has my friend found the moose?
Title:  
Title:  The young men stagger under their burdens, returned Magua. Let
Title:  Reed-that-bends go on the hunting path; he will meet them.
Title:  
Title:  A deep and awful silence succeeded the utterance of the forbidden name. Each
Title:  pipe dropped from the lips of its owner as though all had inhaled an
Title:  impurity at the same instant. The smoke wreathed above their heads in little
Title:  eddies, and curling in a spiral form it ascended swiftly through the opening
Title:  in the roof of the lodge, leaving the place beneath clear of its fumes, and
Title:  each dark visage distinctly visible. The looks of most of the warriors were
Title:  riveted on the earth; though a few of the younger and less gifted of the
Title:  party suffered their wild and glaring eyeballs to roll in the direction of a
Title:  white-headed savage, who sat between two of the most venerated chiefs of the
Title:  tribe. There was nothing in the air or attire of this Indian that would seem
Title:  to entitle him to such a distinction. The former was rather depressed, than
Title:  remarkable for the bearing of the natives; and the latter was such as was
Title:  commonly worn by the ordinary men of the nation. Like most around him for
Title:  more than a minute his look, too, was on the ground; but, trusting his eyes
Title:  at length to steal a glance aside, he perceived that he was becoming an
Title:  object of general attention. Then he arose and lifted his voice in the
Title:  general silence.
Title:  
Title:  It was a lie, he said; I had no son. He who was called by that name is
Title:  forgotten; his blood was pale, and it came not from the veins of a Huron;
Title:  the wicked Chippewas cheated my squaw. The Great Spirit has said, that the
Title:  family of Wiss-entush should end; he is happy who knows that the evil of his
Title:  race dies with himself. I have done.
Title:  
Title:  The speaker, who was the father of the recreant young Indian, looked round
Title:  and about him, as if seeking commendation of his stoicism in the eyes of the
Title:  auditors. But the stern customs of his people had made too severe an
Title:  exaction of the feeble old man. The expression of his eye contradicted his
Title:  figurative and boastful language, while every muscle in his wrinkled visage
Title:  was working with anguish. Standing a single minute to enjoy his bitter
Title:  triumph, he turned away, as if sickening at the gaze of men, and, veiling
Title:  his face in his blanket, he walked from the lodge with the noiseless step of
Title:  an Indian seeking, in the privacy of his own abode, the sympathy of one like
Title:  himself, aged, forlorn and childless.
Title:  
Title:  The Indians, who believe in the hereditary transmission of virtues and
Title:  defects in character, suffered him to depart in silence. Then, with an
Title:  elevation of breeding that many in a more cultivated state of society might
Title:  profitably emulate, one of the chiefs drew the attention of the young men
Title:  from the weakness they had just witnessed, by saying, in a cheerful voice,
Title:  addressing himself in courtesy to Magua, as the newest comer:
Title:  
Title:  The Delawares have been like bears after the honey pots, prowling around my
Title:  village. But who has ever found a Huron asleep?
Title:  
Title:  The darkness of the impending cloud which precedes a burst of thunder was
Title:  not blacker than the brow of Magua as he exclaimed:
Title:  
Title:  The Delawares of the Lakes!
Title:  
Title:  Not so. They who wear the petticoats of squaws, on their own river. One of
Title:  them has been passing the tribe.
Title:  
Title:  Did my young men take his scalp?
Title:  
Title:  His legs were good, though his arm is better for the hoe than the tomahawk,
Title:  returned the other, pointing to the immovable form of Uncas.
Title:  
Title:  Instead of manifesting any womanish curiosity to feast his eyes with the
Title:  sight of a captive from a people he was known to have so much reason to
Title:  hate, Magua continued to smoke, with the meditative air that he usually
Title:  maintained, when there was no immediate call on his cunning or his
Title:  eloquence. Although secretly amazed at the facts communicated by the speech
Title:  of the aged father, he permitted himself to ask no questions, reserving his
Title:  inquiries for a more suitable moment. It was only after a sufficient
Title:  interval that he shook the ashes from his pipe, replaced the tomahawk,
Title:  tightened his girdle, and arose, casting for the first time a glance in the
Title:  direction of the prisoner, who stood a little behind him. The wary, though
Title:  seemingly abstracted Uncas, caught a glimpse of the movement, and turning
Title:  suddenly to the light, their looks met. Near a minute these two bold and
Title:  untamed spirits stood regarding one another steadily in the eye, neither
Title:  quailing in the least before the fierce gaze he encountered. The form of
Title:  Uncas dilated, and his nostrils opened like those of a tiger at bay; but so
Title:  rigid and unyielding was his posture, that he might easily have been
Title:  converted by the imagination into an exquisite and faultless representation
Title:  of the warlike diety of his tribe. The lineaments of the quivering features
Title:  of Magua proved more ductile; his countenance gradually lost its character
Title:  of defiance in an expression of ferocious joy, and heaving a breath from the
Title:  very bottom of his chest, he pronounced aloud the formidable name of:
Title:  
Title:  Le Cerf Agile!
Title:  
Title:  Each warrior sprang upon his feet at the utterance of the well-known
Title:  appellation, and there was a short period during which the stoical constancy
Title:  of the natives was completely conquered by surprise. The hated and yet
Title:  respected name was repeated as by one voice, carrying the sound even beyond
Title:  the limits of the lodge. The women and children, who lingered around the
Title:  entrance, took up the words in an echo, which was succeeded by another
Title:  shrill and plaintive howl. The latter was not yet ended, when the sensation
Title:  among the men had entirely abated. Each one in presence seated himself, as
Title:  though ashamed of his precipitation; but it was many minutes before their
Title:  meaning eyes ceased to roll toward their captive, in curious examination of
Title:  a warrior who had so often proved his prowess on the best and proudest of
Title:  their nation. Uncas enjoyed his victory, but was content with merely
Title:  exhibiting his triumph by a quiet smile - an emblem of scorn which belongs
Title:  to all time and every nation.
Title:  
Title:  Magua caught the expression, and raising his arm, he shook it at the
Title:  captive, the light silver ornaments attached to his bracelet rattling with
Title:  the trembling agitation of the limb, as, in a tone of vengeance, he
Title:  exclaimed, in English:
Title:  
Title:  Mohican, you die!
Title:  
Title:  The healing waters will never bring the dead Hurons to life, returned Uncas,
Title:  in the music of the Delawares; the tumbling river washes their bones; their
Title:  men are squaws: their women owls. Go! call together the Huron dogs, that
Title:  they may look upon a warrior, My nostrils are offended; they scent the blood
Title:  of a coward.
Title:  
Title:  The latter allusion struck deep, and the injury rankled. Many of the Hurons
Title:  understood the strange tongue in which the captive spoke, among which number
Title:  was Magua. This cunning savage beheld, and instantly profited by his
Title:  advantage. Dropping the light robe of skin from his shoulder, he stretched
Title:  forth his arm, and commenced a burst of his dangerous and artful eloquence.
Title:  However much his influence among his people had been impaired by his
Title:  occasional and besetting weakness, as well as by his desertion of the tribe,
Title:  his courage and his fame as an orator were undeniable. He never spoke
Title:  without auditors, and rarely without making converts to his opinions. On the
Title:  present occasion, his native powers were stimulated by the thirst of
Title:  revenge.
Title:  
Title:  He again recounted the events of the attack on the island at Glenn's, the
Title:  death of his associates and the escape of their most formidable enemies.
Title:  Then he described the nature and position of the mount whither he had led
Title:  such captives as had fallen into their hands. Of his own bloody intentions
Title:  toward the maidens, and of his baffled malice he made no mention, but passed
Title:  rapidly on to the surprise of the party by La Longue Carabine, and its fatal
Title:  termination. Here he paused, and looked about him, in affected veneration
Title:  for the departed, but, in truth, to note the effect of his opening
Title:  narrative. As usual, every eye was riveted on his face. Each dusky figure
Title:  seemed a breathing statue, so motionless was the posture, so intense the
Title:  attention of the individual.
Title:  
Title:  Then Magua dropped his voice which had hitherto been clear, strong and
Title:  elevated, and touched upon the merits of the dead. No quality that was
Title:  likely to command the sympathy of an Indian escaped his notice. One had
Title:  never been known to follow the chase in vain; another had been indefatigable
Title:  on the trail of their enemies. This was brave, that generous. In short, he
Title:  so managed his allusions, that in a nation which was composed of so few
Title:  families, he contrived to strike every chord that might find, in its turn,
Title:  some breast in which to vibrate.
Title:  
Title:  Are the bones of my young men, he concluded, in the burial-place of the
Title:  Hurons? Yu know they are not. Their spirits are gone toward the setting sun,
Title:  and are already crossing the great waters, to the happy hunting-grounds. But
Title:  they departed without food, without guns or knives, without moccasins, naked
Title:  and poor as they were born. Shall this be? Are their souls to enter the land
Title:  of the just like hungry Iroquois or unmanly Delawares, or shall they meet
Title:  their friends with arms in their hands and robes on their backs? What will
Title:  our fathers think the tribes of the Wyandots have become? They will look on
Title:  their children with a dark eye, and say, Go! a Chippewa has come hither with
Title:  the name of a Huron. Brothers, we must not forget the dead; a red-skin never
Title:  ceases to remember. We will load the back of this Mohican until he staggers
Title:  under our bounty, and dispatch him after my young men. They call to us for
Title:  aid, though our ears are not open; they say, Forget us not. When they see
Title:  the spirit of this Mohican toiling after them with his burden, they will
Title:  know we are of that mind.Then will they go on happy; and our children will
Title:  say, So did our fathers to their friends, so must we do to them What is a
Title:  Yengee? we have slain many, but the earth is still pale. A stain on the name
Title:  of Huron can only be hid by blood that comes from the veins of an Indian.
Title:  Let this Delaware die.
Title:  
Title:  The effect of such an harangue, delivered in the nervous language and with
Title:  the emphatic manner of a Huron orator, could scarcely be mistaken. Magua had
Title:  so artfully blended the natural sympathies with the religious superstition
Title:  of his auditors, that their minds, already prepared by custom to sacrifice a
Title:  victim to the manes of their countrymen, lost every vestige of humanity in a
Title:  wish for revenge. One warrior in particular, a man of wild and ferocious
Title:  mien, had been conspicuous for the attention he had given to the words of
Title:  the speaker. His countenance had changed with each passing emotion, until it
Title:  settled into a look of deadly malice. As Magua ended he arose and, uttering
Title:  the yell of a demon, his polished little axe was seen glancing in the
Title:  torchlight as he whirled it above his head. The motion and the cry were too
Title:  sudden for words to interrupt his bloody intention. It appeared as if a
Title:  bright gleam shot from his hand, which was crossed at the same moment by a
Title:  dark and powerful line. The former was the tomahawk in its passage; the
Title:  latter the arm that Magua darted forward to divert its aim. The quick and
Title:  ready motion of the chief was not entirely too late. The keen weapon cut the
Title:  war plume from the scalping tuft of Uncas, and passed through the frail wall
Title:  of the lodge as though it were hurled from some formidable engine.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan had seen the threatening action, and sprang upon his feet, with a
Title:  heart which, while it leaped into his throat, swelled with the most generous
Title:  resolution in behalf of his friend. A glance told him that the blow had
Title:  failed, and terror changed to admiration. Uncas stood still, looking his
Title:  enemy in the eye with features that seemed superior to emotion. Marble could
Title:  not be colder, calmer, or steadier than the countenance he put upon this
Title:  sudden and vindictive attack. Then, as if pitying a want of skill which had
Title:  proved so fortunate to himself, he smiled, and muttered a few words of
Title:  contempt in his own tongue.
Title:  
Title:  No! said Magua, after satisfying himself of the safety of the captive; the
Title:  sun must shine on his shame; the squaws must see his flesh tremble, or our
Title:  revenge will be like the play of boys. Go! take him where there is silence;
Title:  let us see if a Delaware can sleep at night, and in the morning die.
Title:  
Title:  The young men whose duty it was to guard the prisoner instantly passed their
Title:  ligaments of bark across his arms, and led him from the lodge, amid a
Title:  profound and ominous silence. It was only as the figure of Uncas stood in
Title:  the opening of the door that his firm step hesitated. There he turned, and,
Title:  in the sweeping and haughty glance that he threw around the circle of his
Title:  enemies, Duncan caught a look which he was glad to construe into an
Title:  expression that he was not entirely deserted by hope.
Title:  
Title:  Magua was content with his success, or too much occupied with his secret
Title:  purposes to push his inquiries any further. Shaking his mantle, and folding
Title:  it on his bosom, he also quitted the place, without pursuing a subject which
Title:  might have proved so fatal to the individual at his elbow. Nothwithstanding
Title:  his rising resentment, his natural firmness, and his anxiety on behalf of
Title:  Uncas, Heyward felt sensibly relieved by the absence of so dangerous and so
Title:  subtle a foe. The excitement produced by the speech gradually subsided. The
Title:  warriors resumed their seats and clouds of smoke once more filled the lodge.
Title:  For near half an hour, not a syllable was uttered, or scarcely a look cast
Title:  aside; a grave and meditative silence being the ordinary succession to every
Title:  scene of violence and commotion among these beings, who were alike so
Title:  impetuous and yet so self-restrained.
Title:  
Title:  When the chief, who had solicited the aid of Duncan, finished his pipe, he
Title:  made a final and successful movement toward departing. A motion of a finger
Title:  was the intimation he gave the supposed physician to follow; and passing
Title:  through the clouds of smoke, Duncad was glad, on more accounts than one, to
Title:  be able at last to breathe the pure air of a cool and refreshing summer
Title:  evening.
Title:  
Title:  Instead of pursuing his way among those lodges where Heyward had already
Title:  made his unsuccessful search, his companion turned aside, and proceeded
Title:  directly toward the base of an adjacent mountain, which overhung the
Title:  temporary village. A thicket of brush skirted its foot, and it became
Title:  necessary to proceed through a crooked and narrow path. The boys had resumed
Title:  their sports in the clearing, and were enacting a mimic chase to the post
Title:  among themselves. In order to render their games as like the reality as
Title:  possible, one of the boldest of their number had conveyed a few brands into
Title:  some piles of tree-tops that had hitherto escaped the burning. The blaze of
Title:  one of these fires lighted the way of the chief and Duncan, and gave a
Title:  character of additional wildness to the rude scenery. At a little distance
Title:  from a bald rock, and directly in its front, they entered a grassy opening,
Title:  which they prepared to cross. Just then fresh fuel was added to the fire,
Title:  and a powerful light penetrated even to that distant spot. It fell upon the
Title:  white surface of the mountain, and was reflected downward upon a dark and
Title:  mysterious-looking being that arose, unexpectedly, in their path. The Indian
Title:  paused, as if doubtful whether to proceed, and permitted his companion to
Title:  approach his side. A large black ball, which at first seemed stationary, now
Title:  began to move in a manner that to the latter was inexplicable. Again the
Title:  fire brightened and its glare fell more distinctly on the object. Then even
Title:  Duncan knew it, by its restless and sidling attitudes, which kept the upper
Title:  part of its form in constant motion, while the animal itself appeared
Title:  seated, to be a bear. Though it growled loudly and fiercely, and there were
Title:  instants when its glistening eyeballs might be seen, it gave no other
Title:  indications of hostility. The Huron, at least, seemed assured that the
Title:  intentions of this singular intruder were peaceable, for after giving it an
Title:  attentive examination, he quietly pursued his course.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, who knew that the animal was often domesticated among the Indians,
Title:  followed the example of his companion, believing that some favorite of the
Title:  tribe had found its way into the thicket, in search of food. They passed it
Title:  unmolested. Though obliged to come nearly in contact with the monster, the
Title:  Huron, who had at first so warily determined the character of his strange
Title:  visitor, was now content with proceeding without wasting a moment in further
Title:  examination; but Heyward was unable to prevent his eyes from looking
Title:  backward, in salutary watchfulness against attacks in the rear. His
Title:  uneasiness was in no degree diminished when he perceived the beast rolling
Title:  along their path, and following their footsteps. He would have spoken, but
Title:  the Indian at that moment shoved aside a door of bark, and entered a cavern
Title:  in the bosom of the mountain.
Title:  
Title:  Profiting by so easy a method of retreat, Duncan stepped after him, and was
Title:  gladly closing the slight cover to the opening, when he felt it drawn from
Title:  his hand by the beast, whose shaggy form immediately darkened the passage.
Title:  They were now in a straight and long gallery, in a chasm of the rocks, where
Title:  retreat without encountering the animal was impossible. Making the best of
Title:  the circumstances, the young man pressed forward, keeping as close as
Title:  possible to his conductor. The bear growled frequently at his heels, and
Title:  once or twice its enormous paws were laid on his person, as if disposed to
Title:  prevent his further passage into the den.
Title:  
Title:  How long the nerves of Heyward would have sustained him in this
Title:  extraordinary situation, it might be difficult to decide, for, happily, he
Title:  soon found relief. A glimmer of light had constantly been in their front,
Title:  and they now arrived at the place whence it proceeded.
Title:  
Title:  A large cavity in the rock had been rudely fitted to answer the purposes of
Title:  many apartments. The subdivisions were simple but ingenious, being composed
Title:  of stone, sticks, and bark, intermingled. Openings above admitted the light
Title:  by day, and at night fires and torches supplied the place of the sun. Hither
Title:  the Hurons had brought most of their valuables, especially those which more
Title:  particularly pertained to the nation; and hither, as it now appeared, the
Title:  sick woman, who was believed to be the victim of supernatural power, had
Title:  been transported also, under an impression that her tormentor would find
Title:  more difficulty in making his assaults through walls of stone than through
Title:  the leafy coverings of the lodges. The apartment into which Duncan and his
Title:  guide first entered, had been exclusively devoted to her accommodation. The
Title:  latter approached her bedside, which was surrounded by females, in the
Title:  center of whom Heyward was surprised to find his missing friend David.
Title:  
Title:  A single look was sufficient to apprise the pretended leech that the invalid
Title:  was far beyond his powers of healing. She lay in a sort of paralysis,
Title:  indifferent to the objects which crowded before her sight, and happily
Title:  unconscious of suffering. Heyward was far from regretting that his mummeries
Title:  were to be performed on one who was much too ill to take an interest in
Title:  their failure or success. The slight qualm of conscience which had been
Title:  excited by the intended deception was instantly appeased, and he began to
Title:  collect his thoughts, in order to enact his part with suitable spirit, when
Title:  he found he was about to be anticipated in his skill by an attempt to prove
Title:  the power of music.
Title:  
Title:  Gamut, who had stood prepared to pour forth his spirit in song when the
Title:  visitors entered, after delaying a moment, drew a strain from his pipe, and
Title:  commenced a hymn that might have worked a miracle, had faith in is efficacy
Title:  been of much avail. He was allowed to proceed to the close, the Indians
Title:  respecting his imaginary infirmity, and Duncan too glad of the delay to
Title:  hazard the slightest interruption. As the dying cadence of his strains was
Title:  falling on the ears of the latter, he started aside at hearing them repeated
Title:  behind him, in a voice half human and half sepulchral. Looking around, he
Title:  beheld the shaggy monster seated on end in a shadow of the cavern, where,
Title:  while his restless body swung in the uneasy manner of the animal, it
Title:  repeated, in a sort of low growl, sounds, if not words, which bore some
Title:  slight resemblance to the melody of the singer.
Title:  
Title:  The effect of so strange an echo on David may better be imagined than
Title:  described. His eyes opened as if he doubted their truth; and his voice
Title:  became instantly mute in excess of wonder. A deep-laid scheme, of
Title:  communicating some important intelligence to Heyward, was driven from his
Title:  recollection by an emotion which very nearly resembled fear, but which he
Title:  was fain to believe was admiration. Under its influence, he exclaimed aloud:
Title:  She expects you, and is at hand; and precipitately left the cavern.

Title:       Snug: Have you the lion's part written?
Title:       Pray you, if it be, give it to me, for I am slow of study.

Title:       Quince: You may do it extempore, for it is nothing but roaring.

Title:                                                 MIDSUMMER NIGHT'S DREAM
Title:  
Title:  There was a strange blending of the ridiculous with that which was solemn in
Title:  this scene. The beast sill continued its rolling, and apparently untiring
Title:  movements, though its ludicrous attempt to imitate the melody of David
Title:  ceased the instant the latter abandoned the field. The words of Gamut were,
Title:  as has been seen, in his native tongue; and to Duncan they seem pregnant
Title:  with some hidden meaning, though nothing present assisted him in discovering
Title:  the object of their allusion. A speedy end was, however, put to every
Title:  conjecture on the subject, by the manner of the chief, who advanced to the
Title:  bedside of the invalid, and beckoned away the whole group of female
Title:  attendants that had clustered there to witness the skill of the stranger. He
Title:  was implicitly, though reluctantly, obeyed; and when the low echo which rang
Title:  along the hollow, natural gallery, from the distant closing door, had
Title:  ceased, pointing toward his insensible daughter, he said:
Title:  
Title:  Now let my brother show his power.
Title:  
Title:  Thus unequivocally called on to exercise the functions of his assumed
Title:  character, Heyward was apprehensive that the smallest delay might prove
Title:  dangerous. Endeavoring, then, to collect his ideas, he prepared to perform
Title:  that species of incantation, and those uncouth rites, under which the Indian
Title:  conjurers are accustomed to conceal their ingnorance and impotency. It is
Title:  more than probable that, in the disordered state of his thoughts, he would
Title:  soon have fallen into some suspicious, if not fatal, error had not his
Title:  incipient attempts been interrupted by a fierce growl from the quadruped.
Title:  Three several times did he renew his efforts to proceed, and as often was he
Title:  met by the same unaccountable opposition, each interruption seeming more
Title:  savage and threatening than the preceding.
Title:  
Title:  The cunning ones are jealous, said the Huron; I go Brother, the woman is the
Title:  wife of one of my bravest young men; deal justly by her. Peace! he added,
Title:  beckoning to the discontented beast to be quiet; I go.
Title:  
Title:  The chief was as good as his word, and Duncan now found himself alone in
Title:  that wild and desolate abode with the helpless invalid and the fierce and
Title:  dangerous brute. The latter listened to the movements of the Indian with
Title:  that air of sagacity that a bear is known to possess, until another echo
Title:  announced that he had also left the cavern, when it turned and came waddling
Title:  up to Duncan before whom it seated itself in its natural attitude, erect
Title:  like a man. The youth looked anxiously about him for some weapon, with which
Title:  he might make a resistance against the attack he now seriously expected.
Title:  
Title:  It seemed, however, as if the humor of the animal had suddenly changed.
Title:  Instead of continuing its discontented growls, or manifesting any further
Title:  signs of anger, the whole of its shaggy body shook violently, as if agitated
Title:  by some strange internal convulsion. The huge and unwieldy talons pawed
Title:  stupidly about the grinning muzzle, and while Heyward kept his eyes riveted
Title:  on its movements with jealous watchfulness, the grim head fell on one side
Title:  and in its place appeared the honest sturdy countenance of the scout, who
Title:  was indulging from the bottom of his soul in his own peculiar expression of
Title:  merriment.
Title:  
Title:  Hist! said the wary woodsman, interrupting Heyward's exclamation of
Title:  surprise; the varlets are about the place, and any sounds that are not
Title:  natural to witchcraft would bring them back upon us in a body.
Title:  
Title:  Tell me the meaning of this masquerade; and why you have attempted so
Title:  desperate an adventure?
Title:  
Title:  Ah, reason and calculation are often outdone by accident, returned the
Title:  scout. But, as a story should always commence at the beginning, I will tell
Title:  you the whole in order. After we parted I placed the commandant and the
Title:  Sagamore in an old beaver lodge, where they are safer from the Hurons than
Title:  they would be in the garrison of Edward for your high north-west Indians,
Title:  not having as yet got the traders among them, continued to venerate the
Title:  beaver. After which Uncas and I pushed for the other encampment as was
Title:  agreed. Have you seen the lad?
Title:  
Title:  To my great grief! He is captive, and condemned to die at the rising of the
Title:  sun.
Title:  
Title:  I had misgivings that such would be his fate, resumed the scout, in a less
Title:  confident and joyous tone. But soon regaining his naturally firm voice, he
Title:  continued: His bad fortune is the true reason of my being here, for it would
Title:  never do to abandon such a boy to the Hurons. A rare time the knaves would
Title:  have of it, could they tie The Bounding Elk and The Long Carabine, as they
Title:  call me, to the same stake! Though why they have given me such a name I
Title:  never knew, there being as little likeness between the gifts of killdeer and
Title:  the performance of one of your real Canada carabynes, as there is between
Title:  the natur' of a pipe-stone and a flint.
Title:  
Title:  Keep to your tale, said the impatient Heyward; we know not at what moment
Title:  the Hurons may return.
Title:  
Title:  No fear of them. A conjurer must have his time, like a straggling priest in
Title:  the settlements. We are as safe from interruption as a missionary would be
Title:  at the beginining of a two hours' discourse. Well, Uncas and I fell in with
Title:  a return party of the varlets; the lad was much too forward for a scout;
Title:  nay, for that matter, being of hot blood, he was not so much to blame; and,
Title:  after all, one of the Hurons proved a coward, and in fleeing led him into an
Title:  ambushment.
Title:  
Title:  And dearly has he paid for the weakness.
Title:  
Title:  The scout significantly passed his hand across his own throat, and nodded,
Title:  as if he said, I comprehend your meaning. After which he continued, in a
Title:  more audible though scarcely more intelligible language:
Title:  
Title:  After the loss of the boy I turned upon the Hurons, as you may judge. There
Title:  have been scrimmages atween one or two of their outlyers and myself; but
Title:  that is neither here nor there. So, after I had shot the imps, I got in
Title:  pretty nigh to the lodges without further commotion. Then what should luck
Title:  do in my favor but lead me to the very spot where one of the most famous
Title:  conjurers of the tribe was dressing himself, as I well knew, for some great
Title:  battle with Satan - though why should I call that luck, which it now seems
Title:  was an especial ordering of Providence. So a judgmatical rap over the head
Title:  stiffened the lying imposter for a time, and leaving him a bit of walnut for
Title:  his supper, to prevent an uproar, and stringing him up atween two saplings,
Title:  I made free with his finery, and took the part of the bear on myself, in
Title:  order that the operations might proceed.
Title:  
Title:  And admirably did you enact the character; the animal itself might have been
Title:  shamed by the representation.
Title:  
Title:  Lord, major, returned the flattered woodsman, I should be but a poor scholar
Title:  for one who has studied so long in the wilderness, did I not know how to set
Title:  forth the movements of natur' of such a beast. Had it been now a catamount,
Title:  or even a full-size panther, I would have embellished a performance for you
Title:  worth regarding. But it is no such marvelous feat to exhibit the feats of so
Title:  dull a beast; though, for that matter, too, a bear may be overacted. Yes,
Title:  yes; it is not every imitator that knows natur' may be outdone easier than
Title:  she is equalled. But all our work is yet before us. Where is the gentle one?
Title:  
Title:  Heaven knows. I have examined every lodge in the village, without
Title:  discovering the slightest trace of her presence in the tribe.
Title:  
Title:  You heard what the singer said, as he left us: She is at hand, and expects
Title:  you?
Title:  
Title:  I have been compelled to believe he alluded to this unhappy woman.
Title:  
Title:  The simpleton was frightened, and blundered through his message; but he had
Title:  a deeper meaning. Here are walls enough to separate the hole settlement. A
Title:  bear ought to climb; therefore will I take a look above them. There may be
Title:  honey-pots hid in these rocks, and I am a beast, you know, that has a
Title:  hankering for the sweets.
Title:  
Title:  The scout looked behind him, laughing at his own conceit, while he clambered
Title:  up the partition, imitating, as he went, the clumsy motions of the beast he
Title:  represented; but the instant the summit was gained he made a gesture for
Title:  silence, and slid down with the utmost precipitation.
Title:  
Title:  She is here, he whispered, and by that door you will find her. I would have
Title:  spoken a word of comfort to the afflicted soul; but the sight of such a
Title:  monster might upset her reason. Though for that matter, major, you are none
Title:  of the most inviting yourself in your paint.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, who had already swung eagerly forward, drew instantly back on
Title:  hearing these discouraging words.
Title:  
Title:  Am I, then, so very revolting? he demanded, with an air of chagrin.
Title:  
Title:  You might not startle a wolf, or turn the Royal Americans from a discharge;
Title:  but I have seen the time when you had a better favored look; your streaked
Title:  countenances are not ill-judged of by the squaws, but young women of white
Title:  blood give the preference to their own color. See, he added, pointing to a
Title:  place where the water trickled from a rock, forming a little crystal spring,
Title:  before it found an issue through the adjacent crevices; you may easily get
Title:  rid of the Sagamore's daub, and when you come back I will try my hand at a
Title:  new embellishment. It's as common for a conjurer to alter his paint as for a
Title:  buck in the settlements to change his finery.
Title:  
Title:  The deliberate woodsman had little occasion to hunt for arguments to enforce
Title:  his advice. He was yet speaking when Duncan availed himself of the water. In
Title:  a moment every frightful or offensive mark was obliterated, and the youth
Title:  appeared again in the lineaments with which he had been gifted by nature.
Title:  Thus prepared for an interview with his mistress, he took a hasty leave of
Title:  his companion, and disappeared through the indicated passage. The scout
Title:  witnessed his departure with complacency, nodding his head after him, and
Title:  muttering his good wishes; after which he very coolly set about an
Title:  examination of the state of the larder, among the Hurons, the cavern, among
Title:  other purposes, being used as a receptacle for the fruits of their hunts.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan had no other guide than a distant glimmering light, which served,
Title:  however, the office of a polar star to the lover. By its aid he was enabled
Title:  to enter the haven of his hopes, which was merely another apartment of the
Title:  cavern, that had been solely appropriated to the safekeeping of so important
Title:  a prisoner as a daughter of the commandant of William Henry. It was
Title:  profusely strewed with the plunder of that unlucky fortress. In the midst of
Title:  this confusion he found her he sought, pale, anxious and terrified, but
Title:  lovely. David had prepared her for such a visit.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan! she exclaimed, in a voice that seemed to tremble at the sounds
Title:  created by itself.
Title:  
Title:  Alice! he answered, leaping carelessly among trunks, boxes, arms, and
Title:  furniture, until he stood at her side.
Title:  
Title:  I knew that you would never desert me, she said, looking up with a momentary
Title:  glow on her otherwise dejected countenance. But you are alone! Grateful as
Title:  it is to be thus remembered, I could wish to think you are not entirely
Title:  alone.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, observing that she trembled in a manner which betrayed her inability
Title:  to stand, gently induced her to be seated, while he recounted those leading
Title:  incidents which it has been our task to accord. Alice listened with
Title:  breathless interest; and though the young man touched lightly on the sorrows
Title:  of the stricken father; taking care, however, not to wound the self-love of
Title:  his auditor, the tears ran as freely down the cheeks of the daughter as

Title:  
Title:  And now, Alice, he added, you will see how much is still expected of you. By
Title:  the assistance of our experienced and invaluable friend, the scout, we may
Title:  find our way from this savage people, but you will have to exert your utmost
Title:  fortitude. Remember that you fly to the arms of your venerable parent, and
Title:  how much his happiness, as well as your own, depends on those exertions.
Title:  
Title:  Can I do otherwise for a father who has done so much for me?
Title:  
Title:  And for me, too, continued the youth, gently pressing the hand he held in
Title:  both his own.
Title:  
Title:  The look of innocence and surprise which he received in return convinced
Title:  Duncan of the necessity of being more explicit.
Title:  
Title:  This is neither the place nor the occasion to detain you with selfish
Title:  wishes, he added; but what heart loaded like mine would not wish to cast its
Title:  burden? They say misery is the closest of all ties; our common suffering in
Title:  your behalf left but little to be explained between your father and myself.
Title:  
Title:  And, dearest Cora, Duncan; surely Cora was not forgotten?
Title:  
Title:  Not forgotten! no; regretted, as woman was seldom mourned before. Your
Title:  venerable father knew no difference between his children; but I - Alice, you
Title:  will not be offended when I say, that to me her worth was in a degree
Title:  obscured - -
Title:
