Title:  of you she ever speaks as of one who is her dearest friend.
Title:  
Title:  I would gladly believe her such, returned Duncan, hastily; I could wish her
Title:  to be even more; but with you, Alice, I have the permission of your father
Title:  to aspire to a still nearer and dearer tie.
Title:  
Title:  Alice trembled violently, and there was an instant during which she bent her
Title:  face aside, yielding to the emotions common to her sex; but they quickly
Title:  passed away, leaving her mistress of her deportment, if not of her
Title:  affections.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward, she said, looking him full in the face with a touching expression
Title:  of innocence and dependency, give me the sacred presence and the holy
Title:  sanction of that parent before you urge me further.
Title:  
Title:  Though more I should not, less I could not say, the youth was about to
Title:  answer, when he was interrupted by a light tap on his shoulder. Starting to
Title:  his feet, he turned, and, confronting the intruder, his looks fell on the
Title:  dark form and malignant visage of Magua. The deep guttural laugh of the
Title:  savage sounded, at such a moment, to Duncan, like the hellish taunt of a
Title:  demon. Had he pursued the sudden and fierce impulse of the instant, he would
Title:  have cast himself on the Huron, and committed their fortunes to the issue of
Title:  a deadly struggle. But, without arms of any description, ignorant of what
Title:  succor his subtle enemy could command, and charged with the safety of one
Title:  who was just then dearer than ever to his heart, he no sooner entertained
Title:  than he abandoned the desperate intention.
Title:  
Title:  What is your purpose? said Alice, meekly folding her arms on her bosom, and
Title:  struggling to conceal an agony of apprehension in behalf of Heyward, in the
Title:  usual cold and distant manner with which she received the visits of her
Title:  captor.
Title:  
Title:  The exulting Indian had resumed his austere countenance, though he drew
Title:  warily back before the menancing glance of the young man's fiery eye. He
Title:  regarded both his captives for a moment with a steady look, and then,
Title:  stepping aside, he dropped a log of wood across a door different from that
Title:  by which Duncan had entered. The latter now comprehended the manner of his
Title:  surprise, and, believing himself irretrievably lost, he drew Alice to his
Title:  bosom, and stood prepared to meet a fate which he hardly regretted, since it
Title:  was to be suffered in such company. But Magua meditated no immediate
Title:  violence. His first measures were very evidently taken to secure his new
Title:  captive; nor did he even bestow a second glance at the motionless forms in
Title:  the center of the cavern, until he had completely cut off every hope of
Title:  retreat through the private outlet he had himself used. He was watched in
Title:  all his movements by Heyward, who, however, remained firm, still folding the
Title:  fragile form of Alice to his heart, at once too proud and too hopeless to
Title:  ask favor of an enemy so often foiled. When Magua had effected his object he
Title:  approached his prisoners, and said in English:
Title:  
Title:  The pale faces trap the cunning beavers; but the red-skins know how to take
Title:  the Yengeese.
Title:  
Title:  Huron, do your worst! exclaimed the excited Heyward, forgetful that a double
Title:  stake was involved in his life; you and your vengeance are alike despised.
Title:  
Title:  Will the white man speak these words at the stake? asked Magua; manifesting,
Title:  at the same time, how little faith he had in the other's resolution by the
Title:  sneer that accompanied his words.
Title:  
Title:  Here; singly to your face, or in the presence of your nation.
Title:  
Title:  Le Renard Subtil is a great chief! returned the Indian; he will go and bring
Title:  his young men, to see how bravely a pale face can laugh at tortures.
Title:  
Title:  He turned away while speaking, and was about to leave the place through the
Title:  avenue by which Duncan had approached, when a growl caught his ear, and
Title:  caused him to hesitate. The figure of the bear appeared in the door, where
Title:  it sat, rolling from side to side in its customary restlessness. Magua, like
Title:  the father of the sick woman, eyed it keenly for a moment, as if to
Title:  ascertain its character. He was far above the more vulgar superstitions of
Title:  his tribe, and so soon as he recognized the well-known attire of the
Title:  conjurer, he prepared to pass it in cool contempt. But a louder and more
Title:  threatening growl caused him again to pause. Then he seemed as if suddenly
Title:  resolved to trifle no longer, and moved resolutely forward.
Title:  
Title:  The mimic animal, which had advanced a little, retired slowly in his front,
Title:  until it arrived again at the pass, when, rearing on his hinder legs, it
Title:  beat the air with its paws, in the manner practised by its brutal prototype.
Title:  
Title:  Fool! exclaimed the chief, in Huron, go play with the children and squaws;
Title:  leave men to their wisdom.
Title:  
Title:  He once more endeavored to pass the supposed empiric, scorning even the
Title:  parade of threatening to use the knife, or tomahawk, that was pendent from
Title:  his belt. Suddenly the beast extended its arms, or rather legs, and inclosed
Title:  him in a grasp that might have vied with the far-famed power of the bear's
Title:  hug itself. Heyward had watched the whole procedure, on the part of Hawkeye,
Title:  with breathless interest. At first he relinquished his hold of Alice; then
Title:  he caught up a thong of buckskin, which had been used around some bundle,
Title:  and when he beheld his enemy with his two arms pinned to his side by the
Title:  iron muscles of the scout, he rushed upon him, and effectually secured them
Title:  there. Arms, legs, and feet were encircled in twenty folds of the thong, in
Title:  less time than we have taken to record the circumstance. When the formidable
Title:  Huron was completely pinioned, the scout released his hold, and Duncan laid
Title:  his enemy on his back, utterly helpless.
Title:  
Title:  Throughout the whole of this sudden and extraordinary operation, Magua,
Title:  though he had struggled violently, until assured he was in the hands of one
Title:  whose nerves were far better strung than his own, had not uttered the
Title:  slightest exclamation. But when Hawkeye, by way of making a summary
Title:  explanation of his conduct, removed the shaggy jaws of the beast, and
Title:  exposed his own rugged and earnest countenance to the gaze of the Huron, the
Title:  philosophy of the latter was so far mastered as to permit him to utter the
Title:  never failing:
Title:  
Title:  Hugh!
Title:  
Title:  Ay, you've found your tongue, said his undisturbed conqueror; now, in order
Title:  that you shall not use it to our ruin, I must make free to stop your mouth.
Title:  
Title:  As there was no time to be lost, the scout immediately set about effecting
Title:  so necessary a precaution; and when he had gagged the Indian, his enemy
Title:  might safely have been considered as hors de combat.
Title:  
Title:  By what place did the imp enter? asked the industrious scout, when his work
Title:  was ended. Not a soul has passed my way since you left me.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan pointed out the door by which Magua had come, and which now presented
Title:  too many obstacles to a quick retreat.
Title:  
Title:  Bring on the gentle one, then, continued his friend; we must make a push for
Title:  the woods by the other outlet.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis impossible! said Duncan; fear has overcome her, and she is helpless.
Title:  Alice! my sweet, my own Alice, arouse yourself; now is the moment to fly.
Title:  'Tis in vain! she hears, but is unable to follow. Go, noble and worthy
Title:  friend; save yourself, and leave me to my fate.
Title:  
Title:  Every trail has its end, and every calamity brings its lesson! returned the
Title:  scout. There, wrap her in them Indian cloths. Conceal all of her little
Title:  form. Nay, that foot has no fellow in the wilderness; it will betray her.
Title:  All, every part. Now take her in your arms, and follow. Leave the rest to
Title:  me.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, as may be gathered from the words of his companion, was eagerly
Title:  obeying; and, as the other finished speaking, he took the light person of
Title:  Alice in his arms, and followed in the footsteps of the scout. They found
Title:  the sick woman as they had left her, still alone, and passed swiftly on, by
Title:  the natural gallery, to the place of entrance. As they approached the little
Title:  door of bark, a murmur of voices without announced that the friends and
Title:  relatives of the invalid were gathered about the place, patiently awaiting a
Title:  summons to re-enter.
Title:  
Title:  If I open my lips to speak, Hawkeye whispered, my English, which is the
Title:  genuine tongue of a white-skin, will tell the varlets that an enemy is among
Title:  them. You must give 'em your jargon, major; and say that we have shut the
Title:  evil spirit in the cave, and are taking the woman to the woods in order to
Title:  find strengthening roots. Practise all your cunning, for it is a lawful
Title:  undertaking.
Title:  
Title:  The door opened a little, as if one without was listening to the proceedings
Title:  within, and compelled the scout to cease his directions. A fierce growl
Title:  repelled the eavesdropper, and then the scout boldly threw open the covering
Title:  of bark, and left the place, enacting the character of a bear as he
Title:  proceeded. Duncan kept close at his heels, and soon found himself in the
Title:  center of a cluster of twenty anxious relatives and friends.
Title:  
Title:  The crowd fell back a little, and permitted the father, and one who appeared
Title:  to be the husband of the woman, to approach.
Title:  
Title:  Has my brother driven away the evil spirit? demanded the former. What has he
Title:  in his arms?
Title:  
Title:  Thy child, returned Duncan, gravely; the disease has gone out of her; it is
Title:  shut up in the rocks. I take the woman to a distance, where I will
Title:  strengthen her against any further attacks. She will be in the wigwam of the
Title:  young man when the sun comes again.
Title:  
Title:  When the father had translated the meaning of the stranger's words into the
Title:  Huron language, a suppressed murmur announced the satisfaction with which
Title:  this intelligence was received. The chief himself waved his hand for Duncan
Title:  to proceed, saying aloud, in a firm voice, and with a lofty manner:
Title:  
Title:  Go; I am a man, and I will enter the rock and fight the wicked one.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward had gladly obeyed, and was already past the little group, when these
Title:  startling words arrested him.
Title:  
Title:  Is my brother mad? he exclaimed; is he cruel? He wil meet the disease, and
Title:  it will enter him; or he will drive out the disease, and it will chase his
Title:  daughter into the woods. No; let my children wait without, and if the spirit
Title:  appears beat him down with clubs. He is cunning, and will bury himself in
Title:  the mountain, when he sees how many are ready to fight him.
Title:  
Title:  This singular warning had the desired effect. Instead of entering the
Title:  cavern, the father and husband drew their tomahawks, and posted themselves
Title:  in readiness to deal their vengeance on the imaginary tormentor of their
Title:  sick relative, while the women and children broke branches from the bushes,
Title:  or seized fragments of the rock, with a similar intention. At this favorable
Title:  moment the counterfeit conjurers disappeared.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye, at the same time that he had presumed so far on the nature of the
Title:  Indian superstitions, was not ignorant that they were rather tolerated than
Title:  relied on by the wisest of the chiefs. He well knew the value of time in the
Title:  present emergency. Whatever might be the extent of the self-delusion of his
Title:  enemies, and however it had tended to assist his schemes, the slightest
Title:  cause of suspicion, acting on the subtle nature of an Indian, would be
Title:  likely to prove fatal. Taking the path, therefore, that was most likely to
Title:  avoid observation, he rather skirted than entered the village. The warriors
Title:  were still to be seen in the distance, by the fading light of the fires,
Title:  stalking from lodge to lodge. But the children had abandoned their sports
Title:  for their beds of skins, and the quiet of night was already beginning to
Title:  prevail over the turbulence and excitement of so busy and important an
Title:  evening.
Title:  
Title:  Alice revived under the renovating influence of the open air, and, as her
Title:  physical rather than her mental powers had been the subject of weakness, she
Title:  stood in no need of any explanation of that which had occurred.
Title:  
Title:  Now let me make an effort to walk, she said, when they had entered the
Title:  forest, blushing, though unseen, that she had not been sooner able to quit
Title:  the arms of Duncan; I am indeed restored.
Title:  
Title:  Nay, Alice, you are yet too weak.
Title:  
Title:  The maiden struggled gently to release herself, and Heyward was compelled to
Title:  part with his precious burden. The representative of the bear had certainly
Title:  been an entire stranger to the delicious emotions of the lover while his
Title:  arms encircled his mistress; and he was, perhaps, a stranger also to the
Title:  nature of that feeling of ingenuous shame that oppressed the trembling
Title:  Alice. But when he found himself at a suitable distance from the lodges he
Title:  made a halt, and spoke on a subject of which he was thoroughly the master.
Title:  
Title:  This path will lead you to the brook, he said; follow its northern bank
Title:  until you come to a fall; mount the hill on your right, and you will see the
Title:  fires of the other people. There you must go and demand protection; if they
Title:  are true Delawares you will be safe. A distant flight with that gentle one,
Title:  just now, is impossible. The Hurons would follow up our trail, and master
Title:  our scalps before we had got a dozen miles. Go, and Providence be with you.
Title:  
Title:  And you! demanded Heyward, in surprise; surely we part not here?
Title:  
Title:  The Hurons hold the pride of the Delawares; the last of the high blood of
Title:  the Mohicans is in their power, returned the scout; I go to see what can be
Title:  done in his favor. Had they mastered your scalp, major, a knave should have
Title:  fallen for every hair it held, as I promised; but if the young Sagamore is
Title:  to be led to the stake, the Indians shall see also how a man without a cross
Title:  can die.
Title:  
Title:  Not in the least offended with the decided preference that the sturdy
Title:  woodsman gave to one who might, in some degree, be called the child of his
Title:  adoption, Duncan still continued to urge such reasons against so desperate
Title:  an effort as presented themselves. He was aided by Alice, who mingled her
Title:  entreaties with those of Heyward that he would abandon a resolution that
Title:  promised so much danger, with so little hope of success. Their eloquence and
Title:  ingenuity were expended in vain. The scout heard them attentively, but
Title:  impatiently, and finally closed the discussion, by answering, in a tone that
Title:  instantly silenced Alice, while it told Heyward how fruitless any further
Title:  remonstrances would be.
Title:  
Title:  I have heard, he said, that there is a feeling in youth which binds man to
Title:  woman closer than the father is tied to the son. It may be so. I have seldom
Title:  been where women of my color dwell; but such may be the gifts of nature in
Title:  the settlements. You have risked life, and all that is dear to you, to bring
Title:  off this gentle one, and I suppose that some such disposition is at the
Title:  bottom of it all. As for me, I taught the lad the real character of a rifle;
Title:  and well has he paid me for it. I have fou't at his side in many a bloody
Title:  scrimmage; and so long as I could hear the crack of his piece in one ear,
Title:  and that of the Sagamore in the other, I knew no enemy was on my back.
Title:  Winters and summer, nights and days, have we roved the wilderness in
Title:  company, eating of the same dish, one sleeping while the other watched; and
Title:  afore it shall be said that Uncas was taken to the torment, and I at hand -
Title:  There is but a single Ruler of us all, whatever may the color of the skin;
Title:  and Him I call to witness, that before the Mohican boy shall perish for the
Title:  want of a friend, good faith shall depart the 'arth, and killdeer become as
Title:  harmless as the tooting we'pon of the singer!
Title:  
Title:  Duncan released his hold on the arm of the scout, who turned, and steadily
Title:  retraced his steps toward the lodges. After pausing a moment to gaze at his
Title:  retiring form, the successful and yet sorrowful Heyward and Alice took their
Title:  way together toward the distant village of the Delawares.
Title:  
Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 26
Title:  
Title:       Bottom: Let me play the lion too.
Title:  
Title:                                                 MIDSUMMER NIGHT'S DREAM
Title:  
Title:  Notwithstanding the high resolution of Hawkeye he fully comprehended all the
Title:  difficulties and danger he was about to incur. In his return to the camp,
Title:  his acute and practised intellects were intently engaged in devising means
Title:  to counteract a watchfulness and suspicion on the part of his enemies, that
Title:  he knew were, in no degree, inferior to his own. Nothing but the color of
Title:  his skin had saved the lives of Magua and the conjurer, who would have been
Title:  the first victims sacrificed to his own security, had not the scout believed
Title:  such an act, however congenial it might be to the nature of an Indian,
Title:  utterly unworthy of one who boasted a descent from men that knew no cross of
Title:  blood. Accordingly, he trusted to the withes and ligaments with which he had
Title:  bound his captives, and pursued his way directly toward the center of the
Title:  lodges. As he approached the buildings, his steps become more deliberate,
Title:  and his vigilant eye suffered no sign, whether friendly or hostile, to
Title:  escape him. A neglected hut was a little in advance of the others, and
Title:  appeared as if it had been deserted when half completed - most probably on
Title:  account of failing in some of the more important requisites; such as wood or
Title:  water. A faint light glimmered through its cracks, however, and announced
Title:  that, notwithstanding its imperfect structure, it was not without a tenant.
Title:  Thither, then, the scout proceeded, like a prudent general, who was about to
Title:  feel the advanced positions of his enemy, before he hazarded the main
Title:  attack.
Title:  
Title:  Throwing himself into a suitable posture for the beast he represented,
Title:  Hawkeye crawled to a little opening, where he might command a view of the
Title:  interior. It proved to be the abiding place of David Gamut. Hither the
Title:  faithful singing-master had now brought himself, together with all his
Title:  sorrows, his apprehensions, and his meek dependence on the protection of
Title:  Providence. At the precise moment when his ungainly person came under the
Title:  observation of the scout, in the manner just mentioned, the woodsman
Title:  himself, though in his assumed character, was the subject of the solitary
Title:  being's profounded reflections.
Title:  
Title:  However implicit the faith of David was in the performance of ancient
Title:  miracles, he eschewed the belief of any direct supernatural agency in the
Title:  management of modern morality. In other words, while he had implicit faith
Title:  in the ability of Balaam's ass to speak, he was somewhat skeptical on the
Title:  subject of a bear's singing; and yet he had been assured of the latter, on
Title:  the testimony of his own exquisite organs. There was something in his air
Title:  and manner that betrayed to the scout the utter confusion of the state of
Title:  his mind. He was seated on a pile of brush, a few twigs from which
Title:  occasionally fed his low fire, with his head leaning on his arm, in a
Title:  posture of melancholy musing. The costume of the votary of music had
Title:  undergone no other alteration from that so lately described, except that he
Title:  had covered his bald head with the triangular beaver, which had not proved
Title:  sufficiently alluring to excite the cupidity of any of his captors.
Title:  
Title:  The ingeniousHawkeye, who recalled the hasty manner in which the other had
Title:  abandoned his post at the bedside of the sick woman, was not without his
Title:  suspicions concerning the subject of so much solemn deliberation. First
Title:  making the circuit of the hut, and ascertaining that it stood quite alone,
Title:  and that the character of its inmate was likely to protect it from visitors,
Title:  he ventured through its low door, into the very presence of Gamut. The
Title:  position of the latter brought the fire between them; and when Hawkeye had
Title:  seated himself on end, near a minute elapsed, during which the two remained
Title:  regarding each other without speaking. The suddenness and the nature of the
Title:  surprise had nearly proved too much for - we will not say the philosophy -
Title:  but for the pitch and resolution of David. He fumbled for his pitch-pipe,
Title:  and arose with a confused intention of attempting a musical exorcism.
Title:  
Title:  Dark and mysterious monster! he exclaimed, while with trembling hands he
Title:  disposed of his auxiliary eyes, and sought his never-failing resource in
Title:  trouble, the gifted version of the psalms; I know not your nature nor
Title:  intents; but if aught you meditate against the person and rights of one of
Title:  the humblest servants of the temple, listen to the inspired language of the
Title:  youth of Israel, and repent.
Title:  
Title:  The bear shook his shaggy sides, and then a well-known voice replied:
Title:  
Title:  Put up the tooting we'pon, and teach your throat modesty. Five words of
Title:  plain and comprehendible English are worth just now an hour of squalling.
Title:  
Title:  What art thou? demanded David, utterly disqualified to pursue his original
Title:  intention, and nearly gasping for breath.
Title:  
Title:  A man like yourself; and one whose blood is as little tainted by the cross
Title:  of a bear, or an Indian, as your own. Have you so soon forgotten from whom
Title:  you received the foolish instrument you hold in your hand?
Title:  
Title:  Can these things be? returned David, breathing more freely, as the truth
Title:  began to dawn upon him. I have found many marvels during my sojourn with the
Title:  heathen, but surely nothing to excel this.
Title:  
Title:  Come, come, returned Hawkeye, uncasing his honest countenance, the better to
Title:  assure the wavering confidence of his companion; you may see a skin, which,
Title:  if it be not as white as one of the gentle ones, has no tinge of red to it
Title:  that the winds of the heaven and the sun have not bestowed. Now let us to
Title:  business.
Title:  
Title:  First tell me of the maiden, and of the youth who so bravely sought her,
Title:  interrupted David.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, they are happily freed from the tomahawks of these varlets. But can you
Title:  put me on the scent of Uncas?
Title:  
Title:  The young man is in bondage, and much I fear his death is decreed. I greatly
Title:  mourn that one so well disposed should die in his ignorance, and I have
Title:  sought a goodly hymn - -
Title:  
Title:  Can you lead me to him?
Title:  
Title:  The task will not be difficult, returned David, hesitating; though I greatly
Title:  fear your presence would rather increase than mitigate his unhappy fortunes.
Title:  
Title:  No more words, but lead on, returned Hawkeye, concealing his face again, and
Title:  setting the example in his own person, by instantly quitting the lodge.
Title:  
Title:  As they proceeded, the scout ascertained that his companion found access to
Title:  Uncas, under privilege of his imaginary infirmity, aided by the favor he had
Title:  acquired with one of the guards, who, in consequence of speaking a little
Title:  English, had been selected by David as the subject of a religious
Title:  conversion. How far the Huron comprehended the intentions of his new friend
Title:  may well be doubted; but as exclusive attention is as flattering to a savage
Title:  as to a more civilized individual, it had produced the effect we have
Title:  mentioned. It is unnecessary to repeat the shrewd manner with which the
Title:  scout extracted these particulars from the simple David; neither shall we
Title:  dwell in this place on the nature of the instruction he delivered, when
Title:  completely master of all the necessary facts; as the whole will be
Title:  sufficiently explained to the reader in the course of the narrative.
Title:  
Title:  The lodge in which Uncas was confined was in the very center of the village,
Title:  and in a situation, perhaps, more difficult than any other to approach, or
Title:  leave, without observation. But it was not the policy of Hawkeye to affect
Title:  the least concealment. Presuming on his disguise, and his ability to sustain
Title:  the character he had assumed, he took the most plain and direct route to the
Title:  place. The hour, however, afforded him some little of that protection which
Title:  he appeared so much to despise. The boys were already buried in sleep, and
Title:  all the women, and most of the warriors, had retired to their lodges for the
Title:  night. Four or five of the latter only lingered about the door of the prison
Title:  of Uncas, wary by close observers of the manner of their captive.
Title:  
Title:  At the sight of Gamut, accompanied by one in the well-known masquerade of
Title:  their most distinguished conjurer, they readily made way for them both.
Title:  Still they betrayed no intention to depart. On the other hand, they were
Title:  evidently disposed to remain bound to the place by an additional interest in
Title:  the mysterious mummeries that they of course expected from such a visit.
Title:  
Title:  From the total inability of the scout to address the Hurons in their own
Title:  language, he was compelled to trust the conversation entirely to David.
Title:  Notwithstanding the simplicity of the latter, he did ample justice to the
Title:  instructions he had received, more than fulfilling the strongest hopes of
Title:  his teacher.
Title:  
Title:  The Delawares are women! he exclaimed, addressing himself to the savage who
Title:  had a slight understanding of the language in which he spoke; the Yengeese,
Title:  my foolish countrymen, have told them to take up the tomahawk, and strike
Title:  their fathers in the Canadas, and they have forgotten their sex. Does my
Title:  brother wish to hear Le Cerf Agile ask for his petticoats, and see him weep
Title:  before the Hurons, at the stake?
Title:  
Title:  The exclamation Hugh! delivered in a strong tone of assent, announced the
Title:  gratification the savage would receive in witnessing such an exhibition of
Title:  weakness in an enemy so long hated and so much feared.
Title:  
Title:  Then let him step aside, and the cunning man will blow upon the dog. Tell it
Title:  to my brothers.
Title:  
Title:  The Huron explained the meaning of David to his fellows, who, in their turn,
Title:  listened to the project with that sort of satisfaction that their untamed
Title:  spirits might be expected to find in such a refinement in cruelty. They drew
Title:  back a little from the entrance and motioned to the supposed conjurer to
Title:  enter. But the bear, instead of obeying, maintained the seat it had taken,
Title:  and growled:
Title:  
Title:  The cunning man is afraid that his breath will blow upon his brothers, and
Title:  take away their courage too, continued David, improving the hint he
Title:  received; they must stand further off.
Title:  
Title:  The Hurons, who would have deemed such a misfortune the heaviest calamity
Title:  that could befall them, fell back in a body, taking a position where they
Title:  were out of earshot, though at the same time they could command a view of
Title:  the entrance to the lodge. Then, as if satisfied of their safety, the scout
Title:  left his position, and slowly entered the place. It was silent and gloomy,
Title:  being tenanted solely by the captive, and lighted by the dying embers of a
Title:  fire, which had been used for the purposed of cookery.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas occupied a distant corner, in a reclining attitude, being rigidly
Title:  bound, both hands and feet, by strong and painful withes. When the frightful
Title:  object first presented itself to the young Mohican, he did not deign to
Title:  bestow a single glance on the animal. The scout, who had left David at the
Title:  door, to ascertain they were not observed, thought it prudent to preserve
Title:  his disguise until assured of their privacy. Instead of speaking, therefore,
Title:  he exerted himself to enact one of the antics of the animal he represented.
Title:  The young Mohican, who at first believed his enemies had sent in a real
Title:  beast to torment him, and try his nerves, detected in those performances
Title:  that to Heyward had appeared so accurate, certain blemishes, that at once
Title:  betrayed the counterfeit. Had Hawkeye been aware of the low estimation in
Title:  which the skilful Uncas held his representations, he would probably have
Title:  prolonged the entertainment a little in pique. But the scornful expression
Title:  of the young man's eye admitted of so many constructions, that the worthy
Title:  scout was spared the mortification of such a discovery. As soon, therefore,
Title:  as David gave the preconcerted signal, a low hissing sound was heard in the
Title:  lodge in place of the fierce growlings of the bear.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas had cast his body back against the wall of the hut and closed his
Title:  eyes, as if willing to exclude so contemptible and disagreeable an object
Title:  from his sight. But the moment the noise of the serpent was heard, he arose,
Title:  and cast his looks on each side of him, bending his head low, and turning it
Title:  inquiringly in every direction, until his keen eye rested on the shaggy
Title:  monster, where it remained riveted, as though fixed by the power of a charm.
Title:  Again the same sounds were repeated, evidently proceeding from the mouth of
Title:  the beast. Once more the eyes of the youth roamed over the interior of the
Title:  lodge, and returning to the former resting place, he uttered, in a deep,
Title:  suppressed voice:
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye!
Title:  
Title:  Cut his bands, said Hawkeye to David, who just then approached them.
Title:  
Title:  The singer did as he was ordered, and Uncas found his limbs released. At the
Title:  same moment the dried skin of the animal rattled, and presently the scout
Title:  arose to his feet, in proper person. The Mohican appeared to comprehend the
Title:  nature of the attempt his friend had made, intuitively, neither tongue nor
Title:  feature betraying another symptom of surprise. When Hawkeye had cast his
Title:  shaggy vestment, which was done by simply loosing certain thongs of skin, he
Title:  drew a long, glittering knife, and put it in the hands of Uncas.
Title:  
Title:  The red Hurons are without, he said; let us be ready. At the same time he
Title:  laid hisfinger significantly on another similar weapon, both being the
Title:  fruits of his prowess among their enemies during the evening.
Title:  
Title:  We will go, said Uncas.
Title:  
Title:  Whither?
Title:  
Title:  To the Tortoises; they are the children of my grandfathers.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, lad, said the scout in English - a language he was apt to use when a
Title:  little abstracted in mind; the same blood runs in your veins, I believe; but
Title:  time and distance has a little changed its color. What shall we do with the
Title:  Mingoes at the door? They count six, and this singer is as good as nothing.
Title:  
Title:  The Hurons are boasters, said Uncas, scornfully; their totem is a moose, and
Title:  they run like snails. The Delawares are children of the tortoise, and they
Title:  outstrip the deer.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, lad, there is truth in what you say; and I doubt not, on a rush, you
Title:  would pass the whole nation; and, in a straight race of two miles, would be
Title:  in, and get your breath again, afore a knave of them all was within hearing
Title:  of the other village. But the gift of a white man lies more in his arms than
Title:  in his legs. As for myself, I can brain a Huron as well as a better man; but
Title:  when it comes to a race the knaves would prove too much for me.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas, who had already approached the door, in readiness to lead the way,
Title:  now recoiled, and placed himself, once more, in the bottom of the lodge. But
Title:  Hawkeye, who was too much occupied with his own thoughts to note the
Title:  movement, continued speaking more to himself than to his companion.
Title:  
Title:  After all, he said, it is unreasonable to keep one man in bondage to the
Title:  gifts of another. So, Uncas, you had better take the lead, while I will put
Title:  on the skin again, and trust to cunning for want of speed.
Title:  
Title:  The young Mohican made no reply, but quietly folded his arms, and leaned his
Title:  body against one of the upright posts that supported the wall of the hut.
Title:  
Title:  Well, said the scout looking up at him, why do you tarry? There will be time
Title:  enough for me, as the knaves will give chase to you at first.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas will stay, was the calm reply.
Title:  
Title:  For what?
Title:  
Title:  To fight with his father's brother, and die with the friend of the
Title:  Delawares.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, lad, returned Hawkeye, squeezing the hand of Uncas between his own iron
Title:  fingers; 'twould have been more like a Mingo than a Mohican had you left me.
Title:  But I thought I would make the offer, seeing that youth commonly loves life.
Title:  Well, what can't be done by main courage, in war, must be done by
Title:  circumvention. Put on the skin; I doubt not you can play the bear nearly as
Title:  well as myself.
Title:  
Title:  Whatever might have been the private opinion of Uncas of their respective
Title:  abilities in this particular, his grave countenance manifested no opinion of
Title:  his superiority. He silently and expeditiously encased himself in the
Title:  covering of the beast, and then awaited such other movements as his more
Title:  aged companion saw fit to dictate.
Title:  
Title:  Now, friend, said Hawkeye, addressing David, an exchange of garments will be
Title:  a great convenience to you, inasmuch as you are but little accustomed to the
Title:  make-shifts of the wilderness. Here, take my hunting shirt and cap, and give
Title:  me your blanket and hat. You must trust me with the book and spectacles, as
Title:  well as the tooter, too; if we ever meet again, in better times, you shall
Title:  have all back again, with many thanks into the bargain.
Title:  
Title:  David parted with the several articles named with a readiness that would
Title:  have done great credit to his liberality, had he not certainly profited, in
Title:  many particulars, by the exchange. Hawkeye was not long in assuming his
Title:  borrowed garments; and when his restless eyes were hid behind the glasses,
Title:  and his head was surmounted by the triangular beaver, as their statures were
Title:  not dissimilar, he might readily have passed for the singer, by starlight.
Title:  As soon as these dispositions were made, the scout turned to David, and gave
Title:  him his parting instructions.
Title:  
Title:  Are you much given to cowardice? he bluntly asked, by way of obtaining a
Title:  suitable understanding of the whole case before he ventured a prescription.
Title:  
Title:  My pursuits are peaceful, and my temper, I humbly trust, is greatly given to
Title:  mercy and love, returned David, a little nettled at so direct an attack on
Title:  his manhood; but there are none who can say that I have ever forgotten my
Title:  faith in the Lord, even in the greatest straits.
Title:  
Title:  Your chiefest danger will be at the moment when the savages find out that
Title:  they have been deceived. If you are not then knocked on the head, your being
Title:  a non-composser will protect you; and you'll then have a good reason to
Title:  expect to die in your bed. If you stay, it must be to sit down here in the
Title:  shadow, and take the part of Uncas, until such times as the cunning of the
Title:  Indians discover the cheat, when, as I have already said, your times of
Title:  trial will come. So choose for yourself - to make a rush or tarry here.
Title:  
Title:  Even so, said David, firmly; I will abide in the place of the Delaware.
Title:  Bravely and generously has he battled in my behalf, and this, and more, will
Title:  I dare in his service.
Title:  
Title:  You have spoken as a man, and like one who, under wiser schooling, would
Title:  have been brought to better things. Hold your head down, and draw in your
Title:  legs; their formation might tell the truth too early. Keep silent as long as
Title:  may be; and it would be wise, when you do speak, to break out suddenly in
Title:  one of your shoutings, which will serve to remind the Indians that you are
Title:  not altogether as responsible as men should be. If however, they take your
Title:  scalp, as I trust and believe they will not, depend on it, Uncas and I will
Title:  not forget the deed, but revenge it as becomes true warriors and trusty
Title:  friends.
Title:  
Title:  Hold! said David, perceiving that with this assurance they were about to
Title:  leave him; I am an unworthy and humble follower of one who taught not the
Title:  damnable principle of revenge. Should I fall, therefore, seek no victims to
Title:  my manes, but rather forgive my destroyers; and if you remember them at all,
Title:  let it be in prayers for the enlightening of their minds, and for their
Title:  eternal welfare.
Title:  
Title:  The scout hesitated, and appeared to muse.
Title:  
Title:  There is a principle in that, he said, different from the law of the woods;
Title:  and yet it is fair and noble to reflect upon. Then heaving a heavy sigh,
Title:  probably among the last he ever drew in pining for a condition he had so
Title:  long abandoned, he added: it is what I would wish to practise myself, as one
Title:  without a cross of blood, though it is not always easy to deal with an
Title:  Indian as you would with a fellow Christian. God bless you, friend; I do
Title:  believe your scent is not greatly wrong, when the matter is duly considered,
Title:  and keeping eternity before the eyes, though much depends on the natural
Title:  gifts, and the force of temptation.
Title:  
Title:  So saying, the scout returned and shook David cordially by the hand; after
Title:  which act of friendship he immediately left the lodge, attended by the new
Title:  representative of the beast.
Title:  
Title:  The instant Hawkeye found himself under the observation of the Hurons, he
Title:  drew up his tall form in the rigid manner of David, threw out his arm in the
Title:  act of keeping time, and commenced what he intended for an imitation of his
Title:  psalmody. Happily for the success of this delicate adventure, he had to deal
Title:  with ears but little practised in the concord of sweet sounds, or the
Title:  miserable effort would infallibly have been detected. It was necessary to
Title:  pass within a dangerous proximity of the dark group of the savages, and the
Title:  voice of the scout grew louder as they drew nigher. When at the nearest
Title:  point the Huron who spoke the English thrust out an arm, and stopped the
Title:  supposed singing-master.
Title:  
Title:  The Delaware dog! he said, leaning forward, and peering through the dim
Title:  light to catch the expression of the other's features; is he afraid? Will
Title:  the Hurons hear his groans?
Title:  
Title:  A growl, so exceedingly fierce and natural, proceeded from the beast, that
Title:  the young Indian released his hold and started aside, as if to assure
Title:  himself that it was not a veritable bear, and no counterfeit, that was
Title:  rolling before him. Hawkeye, who feared his voice would betray him to his
Title:  subtle enemies, gladly profited by the interruption, to break out anew in
Title:  such a burst of muscial expression as would, probably, in a more refined
Title:  state of society have been termed a grand crash. Among his actual auditors,
Title:  however, it merely gave him an additional claim to that respect which they
Title:  never withhold from such as are believed to be the subjects of mental
Title:  alienation. The little knot on Indians drew back in a body, and suffered, as
Title:  they thought, the conjurer and his inspired assistant to proceed.
Title:  
Title:  It required no common exercise of fortitude in Uncas and the scout to
Title:  continue the dignified and deliberate pace they had assumed in passing the
Title:  lodge; especially as they immediately perceived that curiosity had so far
Title:  mastered fear, as to induce the watchers to approach the hut, in order to
Title:  witness the effect of the incantations. The least injudicious or impatient
Title:  movement on the part of David might betray them, and time was absolutely
Title:  necessary to insure the safety of the scout. The loud noise the latter
Title:  conceived it politic to continue, drew many curious gazers to the doors of
Title:  the different huts as thy passed; and once or twice a dark-looking warrior
Title:  stepped across their path, led to the act by superstition and watchfulness.
Title:  They were not, however, interrupted, the darkness of the hour, and the
Title:  boldness of the attempt, proving their principal friends.
Title:  
Title:  The adventurers had got clear of the village, and were now swiftly
Title:  approaching the shelter of the woods, when a loud and long cry arose from
Title:  the lodge where Uncas had been confined. The Mohican started on his feet,
Title:  and shook his shaggy covering, as though the animal he counterfeited was
Title:  about to make some desperate effort.
Title:  
Title:  Hold! said the scout, grasping his friend by the shoulder, let them yell
Title:  again! 'Twas nothing but wonderment.
Title:  
Title:  He had no occasion to delay, for at the next instant a burst of cries filled
Title:  the outer air, and ran along the whole extent of the village. Uncas cast his
Title:  skin, and stepped forth in his own beautiful proportions. Hawkeye tapped him
Title:  lightly on the shoulder, and glided ahead.
Title:  
Title:  Now let the devils strike our scent! said the scout, tearing two rifles,
Title:  with all their attendant accouterments, from beneath a bush, and flourishing
Title:  killdeer as he handed Uncas his weapon; two, at least, will find it to their
Title:  deaths.
Title:  
Title:  Then, throwing their pieces to a low trail, like sportsmen in readiness for
Title:  their game, they dashed forward, and were soon buried in the somber darkness
Title:  of the forest.

Title:  
Title:  Chapter 27
Title:  
Title:       Antony: I shall remember:
Title:       When Caesar says Do this, it is performed
Title:  
Title:                                                      JULIUS C&AELIG;SAR
Title:  
Title:  The impatience of the savages who lingered about the prison of Uncas, as has
Title:  been seen, had overcome their dread of the conjurer's breath. They stole
Title:  cautiously, and with beating hearts, to a crevice, through which the faint
Title:  light of the fire was glimmering. For several minutes they mistook the form
Title:  of David for that of the prisoner; but the very accident which Hawkeye had
Title:  foreseen occurred. Tired of keeping the extremities of his long person so
Title:  near together, the singer gradually suffered the lower limbs to extend
Title:  themselves, until one of his misshapen feet actually came in contact with
Title:  and shoved aside the embers of the fire. At first the Hurons believed the
Title:  Delaware had been thus deformed by witchcraft. But when David, unconscious
Title:  of being observed, turned his head, and exposed his simple, mild
Title:  countenance, in place of the haughty lineaments of their prisoner, it would
Title:  have exceeded the credulity of even a native to have doubted any longer.
Title:  They rushed together into the lodge, and, laying their hands, with but
Title:  little ceremony, on their captive, immediately detected the imposition. They
Title:  arose the cry first heard by the fugitives. It was succeeded by the most
Title:  frantic and angry demonstrations of vengeance. David, however, firm in his
Title:  determination to cover the retreat of his friends, was compelled to believe
Title:  that his own final hour had come. Deprived of his book and his pipe, he was
Title:  fain to trust to a memory that rarely failed him on such subjects; and
Title:  breaking forth in a loud and impassioned strain, he endeavored to smooth his
Title:  passage into the other world by singing the opening verse of a funeral
Title:  anthem. The Indians were seasonably reminded of his infirmity, and, rushing
Title:  into the open air, they aroused the village in the manner described.
Title:  
Title:  A native warrior fights as he sleeps, without the protection of anything
Title:  defensive. The sounds of the alarm were, therefore, hardly uttered before
Title:  two hundred men were afoot, and ready for the battle or the chase, as either
Title:  might be required. The escape was soon known; and the whole tribe crowded,
Title:  in a body, around the council-lodge, impatiently awaiting the instruction of
Title:  their chiefs. In such a sudden demand on their wisdom, the presence of the
Title:  cunning Magua could scarcely fail of being needed. His name was mentioned,
Title:  and all looked round in wonder that he did not appear. Messengers were then
Title:  despatched to his lodge requiring his presence.
Title:  
Title:  In the meantime, some of the swiftest and most discreet of the young men
Title:  were ordered to make the circuit of the clearing, under cover of the woods,
Title:  in order to ascertain that their suspected neighbors, the Delawares,
Title:  designed no mischief. Women and children ran to and fro; and, in short, the
Title:  whole encampment exhibited another scene of wild and savage confusion.
Title:  Gradually, however, these symptoms of disorder diminished; and in a few
Title:  minutes the oldest and most distinguished chiefs were assembled in the
Title:  lodge, in grave consultation.
Title:  
Title:  The clamor of many voices soon announced that a party approached, who might
Title:  be expected to communicate some intelligence that would explain the mystery
Title:  of the novel surprise. The crowd without gave way, and several warriors
Title:  entered the place, bringing with them the hapless conjurer, who had been
Title:  left so long by the scout in duress.
Title:  
Title:  Notwithstanding this man was held in very unequal estimation among the
Title:  Hurons, some believing implicitly in his power, and others deeming him an
Title:  imposter, he was now listened to by all with the deepest attention. When his
Title:  brief story was ended, the father of the sick woman stepped forth, and, in a
Title:  few pithy expression, related, in his turn, what he knew. These two
Title:  narratives gave a proper direction to the subsequent inquiries, which were
Title:  now made with the characteristic cunning of savages.
Title:  
Title:  Instead of rushing in a confused and disorderly throng to the cavern, ten of
Title:  the wisest and firmest among the chiefs were selected to prosecute the
Title:  investigation. As no time was to be lost, the instant the choice was made
Title:  the individuals appointed rose in a body and left the place without
Title:  speaking. On reaching the entrance, the younger men in advance made way for
Title:  their seniors; and the whole proceeded along the low, dark gallery, with the
Title:  firmness of warriors ready to devote themselves to the public good, though,
Title:  at the same time, secretly doubting the nature of the power with which they
Title:  were about to contend.
Title:  
Title:  The outer apartment of the cavern was silent and gloomy. The woman lay in
Title:  her usual place and posture, though there were those present who affirmed
Title:  they had seen her borne to the woods by the supposed medicine of the white
Title:  men. Such a direct and palpable contradiction of the tale related by the
Title:  father caused all eyes to be turned on him. Chafed by the silent imputation,
Title:  and inwardly troubled by so unaccountable a circumstance, the chief advanced
Title:  to the side of the bed, and, stooping, cast an incredulous look at the
Title:  features, as if distrusting their reality. His daughter was dead.
Title:  
Title:  The unerring feeling of nature for a moment prevailed and the old warrior
Title:  hid his eyes in sorrow. Then, recovering his self-possession, he faced his
Title:  companions, and, pointing toward the corpse, he said, in the language of his
Title:  people:
Title:  
Title:  The wife of my young man has left us! The Great Spirit is angry with his
Title:  children.
Title:  
Title:  The mournful intelligence was received in solemn silence. After a short
Title:  pause, one of the elder Indians was about to speak, when a dark-looking
Title:  object was seen rolling out of an adjoining apartment, into the very center
Title:  of the room where they stood. Ignorant of the nature of the beings they had
Title:  to deal with, the whole party drew back a little, and, rising on end,
Title:  exhibited the distorted but still fierce and sullen features of Magua. The
Title:  discovery was succeeded by a general exclamation of amazement.
Title:  
Title:  As soon, however, as the true situation of the chief was understood, several
Title:  knives appeared, and his limbs and tongue were quickly released. The Huron
Title:  arose, and shook himself like a lion quitting his lair. Not a word escaped
Title:  him, though his hand played convulsively with the handle of his knife, while
Title:  his lowering eyes scanned the whole party, as if they sought an object
Title:  suited to the first burst of his vengeance.
Title:  
Title:  It was happy for Uncas and the scout, and even David, that they were all
Title:  beyond the reach of his arm at such a moment; for, assuredly, no refinement
Title:  in cruelty would then have deferred their deaths, in opposition to the
Title:  promptings of the fierce temper that nearly choked him. Meeting everywhere
Title:  faces that he knew as friends, the savage grated his teeth together like
Title:  rasps of iron, and swallowed his passion for want of a victim on whom to
Title:  vent it. This exhibition of anger was noted by all present; and from an
Title:  apprehension of exasperating a temper that was already chafed nearly to
Title:  madness, several minutes were suffered to pass before another word was
Title:  uttered. When, however, suitable time had elapsed, the oldest of the party
Title:  spoke.
Title:  
Title:  My friend has found an enemy, he said. Is he nigh that the Hurons might take
Title:  revenge?
Title:  
Title:  Let the Delaware die! exclaimed Magua, in a voice of thunder.
Title:  
Title:  Another longer and expressive silence was observed, and was broken, as
Title:  before, with due precaution, by the same individual.
Title:  
Title:  The Mohican is swift of foot, and leaps far, he said; but my young men are
Title:  on his trail.
Title:  
Title:  Is he gone? demanded Magua, in tones so deep and gutteral, that they seemed
Title:  to proceed from his inmost chest.
Title:  
Title:  An evil spirit has been among us, and the Delaware has blinded our eyes.
Title:  
Title:  An evil spirit! repeated the other, mockingly; 'tis the spirit that has
Title:  taken the lives of so many Hurons; the spirit that slew my young men at the
Title:  tumbling river'; that took their scalps at the healing spring'; and who has,
Title:  now, bound the arms of Le Renard Subtil!
Title:  
Title:  Of whom does my friend speak?
Title:  
Title:  Of the dog who carries the heart and cunning of a Huron under a pale skin -
Title:  La Longue Carabine.
Title:  
Title:  The pronunciation of so terrible a name produced the usual effect among his
Title:  auditors. But when time was given for reflection, and the warriors
Title:  remembered that their formidable and daring enemy had even been in the bosom
Title:  of their encampment, working injury, fearful rage took the place of wonder,
Title:  and all those fierce passions with which the bosom of Magua had just been
Title:  struggling were suddenly transferred to his companions. Some among them
Title:  gnashed their teeth in anger, others vented their feelings in yells, and
Title:  some, again, beat the air as frantically as if the object of their
Title:  resentment were suffering under their blows. But this sudden outbreaking of
Title:  temper as quickly subsided in the still and sullen restraint they most
Title:  affected in their moments of inaction.
Title:  
Title:  Magua, who had in his turn found leisure for reflection, now changed his
Title:  manner, and assumed the air of one who knew how to think and act with a
Title:  dignity worthy of so grave a subject.
Title:  
Title:  Let us go to my people, he said; they wait for us.
Title:  
Title:  His companions consented in silence, and the whole of the savage party left
Title:  the cavern and returned to the council-lodge. When they were seated, all
Title:  eyes turned on Magua, who understood, from such an indication, that, by
Title:  common consent, they had devolved the duty of relating what had passed on
Title:  him. He arose, and told his tale without duplicity or reservation. The whole
Title:  deception practised by both Duncan and Hawkeye was, of course, laid naked,
Title:  and no room was found, even for the most superstitious of the tribe, any
Title:  longer to affix a doubt on the character of the occurrences. It was but too
Title:  apparent that they had been insultingly, shamefully, disgracefully deceived.
Title:  When he had ended, and resumed his seat, the collected tribe - for his
Title:  auditors, in substance, included all the fighting men of the party - sat
Title:  regarding each other like men astonished equally at the audacity and the
Title:  success of their enemies. The next consideration, however, was the means and
Title:  opportunities for revenge.
Title:  
Title:  Additional pursuers were sent on the trail of the fugitives; and then the
Title:  chiefs applied themselves, in earnest, to the business of consultation. Many
Title:  different expedients were proposed by the elder warriors, in succession, to
Title:  all of which Magua was a silent and respectful listener. That subtle savage
Title:  had recovered his artifice and self-command, and now proceeded toward his
Title:  object with his customary caution and skill. It was only when each one
Title:  disposed to speak had uttered his sentiments, that he prepared to advance
Title:  his own opinions. They were given with additional weight from the
Title:  circumstance that some of the runners had already returned, and reported
Title:  that their enemies had been traced so far as to leave no doubt of their
Title:  having sought safety in the neighboring camp of their suspected allies, the
Title:  Delawares. With the advantage of possessing this important intelligence, the
Title:  chief warily laid his plans before his fellows, and, as might have been
Title:  anticipated from his eloquence and cunning, they were adopted without a
Title:  dissenting voice. They were, briefly, as follows, both in opinions and in
Title:  motives.
Title:  
Title:  It has been already stated that, in obedience to a policy rarely departed
Title:  from, the sisters were separated so soon as they reached the Huron village.
Title:  Magua had early discovered that in retaining the person of Alice, he
Title:  possessed the most effectual check on Cora. When they parted, therefore, he
Title:  kept the former within reach of his hand, consigning the one he most valued
Title:  to the keeping of their allies. The arrangement was understood to be merely
Title:  temporary, and was made as much with a view to flatter his neighbors as in
Title:  obedience to the invariable rule of Indian policy.
Title:  
Title:  While goaded incessantly by these revengeful impulses that in a savage
Title:  seldom slumber, the chief was still attentive to his more permanent personal
Title:  interests. The follies and disloyalty committed in his youth were to be
Title:  expiated by a long and painful penance, ere he could be restored to the full
Title:  enjoyment of the confidence of his ancient people; and without confidence
Title:  there could be no authority in an Indian tribe. In this delicate and arduous
Title:  situation, the crafty native had neglected no means of increasing his
Title:  influence; and one of the happiest of his expedients had been the success
Title:  with which he had cultivated the favor of their powerful and dangerous
Title:  neighbors. The result of his experiment had answered all the expectations of
Title:  his policy; for the Hurons were in no degree exempt from that governing
Title:  principle of nature, which induces man to value his gifts precisely in the
Title:  degree that they are appreciated by others.
Title:  
Title:  But, while he was making this ostensible sacrifice to general
Title:  considerations, Magua never lost sight of his individual motives. The latter
Title:  had been frustrated by the unlooked-for events which had placed all his
Title:  prisoners beyond his control; and he now found himself reduced to the
Title:  necessity of suing for favors to those whom it had so lately been his policy
Title:  to oblige.
Title:  
Title:  Several of the chiefs had proposed deep and treacherous schemes to surprise
Title:  the Delawares and, by gaining possession of their camp, to recover their
Title:  prisoners by the same blow; for all agreed that their honor, their
Title:  interests, and the peace and happiness of their dead countrymen, imperiously
Title:  required them speedily to immolate some victims to their revenge. But plans
Title:  so dangerous to attempt, and of such doubtful issue, Magua found little
Title:  difficulty in defeating. He exposed their risk and fallacy with his usual
Title:  skill; and it was only after he had removed every impediment, in the shape
Title:  of opposing advice, that he ventured to propose his own projects.
Title:  
Title:  He commenced by flattering the self-love of his auditors; a never-failing
Title:  method of commanding attention. When he had enumerated the many different
Title:  occasions on which the Hurons had exhibited their courage and prowess, in
Title:  the punishment of insults, he digressed in a high encomium on the virtue of
Title:  wisdom. He painted the quality as forming the great point of difference
Title:  between the beaver and other brutes; between the brutes and men; and,
Title:  finally, between the Hurons, in particular, and the rest of the human race.
Title:  After he had sufficiently extolled the property of discretion, he undertook
Title:  to exhibit in what manner its use was applicable to the present situation of
Title:  their tribe. On the one hand, he said, was their great pale father, the
Title:  governor of the Canadas, who had looked upon his children with a hard eye
Title:  since their tomahawks had been so red; on the other, a people as numerous as
Title:  themselves, who spoke a different language, possessed different interests,
Title:  and loved them not, and who would be glad of any pretense to bring them in
Title:  disgrace with the great white chief. Then he spoke of their necessities; of
Title:  the gifts they had a right to expect for their past services; of their
Title:  distance from their proper hunting-grounds and native villages; and of the
Title:  necessity of consulting prudence more, and inclination less, in so critical
Title:  circumstances. When he perceived that, while the old men applauded his
Title:  moderation, many of the fiercest and most distinguished of the warriors
Title:  listened to these politic plans with lowering looks, he cunningly led them
Title:  back to the subject which they most loved. He spoke openly of the fruits of
Title:  their wisdom, which he boldly pronounced would be a complete and final
Title:  triumph over their enemies. He even darkly hinted that their success might
Title:  be extended, with proper caution, in such a manner as to include the
Title:  destruction of all whom they had reason to hate. In short, he so blended the
Title:  warlike with the artful, the obvious with the obscure, as to flatter the
Title:  propensities of both parties, and to leave to each subject of hope, while
Title:  neither could say it clearly comprehended his intentions.
Title:  
Title:  The orator, or the politician, who can produce such a state of things, is
Title:  commonly popular with his contemporaries, however he may be treated by
Title:  posterity. All perceived that more was meant than was uttered, and each one
Title:  believed that the hidden meaning was precisely such as his own faculties
Title:  enabled him to understand, or his own wishes led him to anticipate.
Title:  
Title:  In this happy state of things, it is not surprising that the management of
Title:  Magua prevailed. The tribe consented to act with deliberation, and with one
Title:  voice they committed the direction of the whole affair to the government of
Title:  the chief who had suggested such wise and intelligible expedients.
Title:  
Title:  Magua had now attained one great object of all his cunning and enterprise.
Title:  The ground he had lost in the favor of his people was completely regained,
Title:  and he found himself even placed at the head of affairs. He was, in truth,
Title:  their ruler; and, so long as he could maintain his popularity, no monarch
Title:  could be more despotic, especially while the tribe continued in a hostile
Title:  country. Throwing off, therefore, the appearance of consultation, he assumed
Title:  the grave air of authority necessary to support the dignity of his office.
Title:  
Title:  Runners were despatched for intelligence in different directions; spies were
Title:  ordered to approach and feel the encampment of the Delawares; the warriors
Title:  were dismissed to their lodges, with an intimation that their services would
Title:  soon be needed; and the women and children were ordered to retire, with a
Title:  warning that it was their province to be silent. When these several
Title:  arrangements were made, Magua passed through the village, stopping here and
Title:  there to pay a visit where he thought his presence might be flattering to
Title:  the individual. He confirmed his friends in their confidence, fixed the
Title:  wavering, and gratified all. Then he sought his own lodge. The wife the
Title:  Huron chief had abandoned, when he was chased from among his people, was
Title:  dead. Children he had none; and he now occupied a hut, without companion of
Title:  any sort. It was, in fact, the dilapidated and solitary structure in which
Title:  David had been discovered, and whom he had tolerated in his presence, on
Title:  those few occasions when they met, with the contemptuous indifference of a
Title:  haughty superiority.
Title:  
Title:  Hither, then, Magua retired, when his labors of policy were ended. While
Title:  others slept, however, he neither knew or sought repose. Had there been one
Title:  sufficiently curious to have watched the movements of the newly elected
Title:  chief, he would have seen him seated in a corner of his lodge, musing on the
Title:  subject of his future plans, from the hour of his retirement to the time he
Title:  had appointed for the warriors to assemble again. Occasionally the air
Title:  breathed through the crevices of the hut, and the low flame that fluttered
Title:  about the embers of the fire threw their wavering light on the person of the
Title:  sullen recluse. At such moments it would not have been difficult to have
Title:  fancied the dusky savage the Prince of Darkness brooding on his own fancied
Title:  wrongs, and plotting evil.
Title:  
Title:  Long before the day dawned, however, warrior after warrior entered the
Title:  solitary hut of Magua, until they had collected to the number of twenty.
Title:  Each bore his rifle, and all the other accouterments of war, though the
Title:  paint was uniformly peaceful. The entrance of these fierce-looking beings
Title:  was unnoticed: some seating themselves in the shadows of the place, and
Title:  others standing like motionless statues, until the whole of the designated
Title:  band was collected.
Title:  
Title:  Then Magua arose and gave the signal to proceed, marching himself in
Title:  advance. They followed their leader singly, and in that well-known order
Title:  which has obtained the distinguishing appellation of Indian file. Unlike
Title:  other men engaged in the spirit-stirring business of war, they stole from
Title:  their camp unostentatiously and unobserved resembling a band of gliding
Title:  specters, more than warriors seeking the bubble reputation by deeds of
Title:  desperate daring.
Title:  
Title:  Instead of taking the path which led directly toward the camp of the
Title:  Delawares, Magua led his party for some distance down the windings of the
Title:  stream, and along the little artificial lake of the beavers. The day began
Title:  to dawn as they entered the clearing which had been formed by those
Title:  sagacious and industrious animals. Though Magua, who had resumed his ancient
Title:  garb, bore the outline of a fox on the dressed skin which formed his robe,
Title:  there was one chief of his party who carried the beaver as his peculiar
Title:  symbol, or totem. There would have been a species of profanity in the
Title:  omission, had this man passed so powerful a community of his fancied
Title:  kindred, without bestowing some evidence of his regard. Accordingly, he
Title:  paused, and spoke in words as kind and friendly as if he were addressing
Title:  more intelligent beings. He called the animals his cousins, and reminded
Title:  them that his protecting influence was the reason they remained unharmed,
Title:  while many avaricious traders were prompting the Indians to take their
Title:  lives. He promised a continuance of his favors, and admonished them to be
Title:  grateful. After which, he spoke of the expedition in which he was himself
Title:  engaged, and intimated, though with sufficient delicacy and circumlocution,
Title:  the expediency of bestowing on their relative a portion of that wisdom for
Title:  which they were so renowned.1
Title:  
Title:  During the utterance of this extraordinary address, the companions of the
Title:  speaker were as grave and as attentive to his language as though they were
Title:  all equally impressed with its propriety. Once or twice black objects were
Title:  seen rising to the surface of the water, and the Huron expressed pleasure,
Title:  conceiving that his words were not bestowed in vain. Just as he ended his
Title:  address, the head of a large beaver was thrust from the door of a lodge,
Title:  whose earthen walls had been much injured, and which the party had believed,
Title:  from its situation, to be uninhabited. Such an extraordinary sign of
Title:  confidence was received by the orator as a highly favorable omen; and though
Title:  the animal retreated a little precipitately, he was lavish of his thanks and
Title:  commendations.
Title:  
Title:  When Magua thought sufficient time had been lost in gratifying the family
Title:  affection of the warrior, he again made the signal to proceed. As the
Title:  Indians moved away in a body, and with a step that would have been inaudible
Title:  to the ears of any common man, the same venerable-looking beaver once more
Title:  ventured his head from its cover. Had any of the Hurons turned to look
Title:  behind them, they would have seen the animal watching their movements with
Title:  an interest and sagacity that might easily have been mistaken for reason.
Title:  Indeed, so very distinct and intelligible were the devices of the quadruped,
Title:  that even the most experienced observer would have been at a loss to account
Title:  for its actions, until the moment when the party entered the forest, when
Title:  the whole would have been explained, by seeing the entire animal issue from
Title:  the lodge, uncasing, by the act, the grave features of Chingachgook from his
Title:  mask of fur.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 These harangues of the beasts were frequent among the Indians. They often
Title:  address their victims in this way, reproaching them for cowardice or
Title:  commending their resolution, as they may happen to exhibit fortitude or the
Title:  reverse, in suffering.
