Title:  
Title:  Chapter 28
Title:  
Title:       Brief, I pray for you; for you see, 'tis a busy time with me.
Title:  
Title:                                                  Much Ado About Nothing
Title:  
Title:  The tribe, or rather half tribe, of Delawares, which has been so often
Title:  mentioned, and whose present place of encampment was so nigh the temporary
Title:  village of the Hurons, could assemble about an equal number of warriors with
Title:  the latter people. Like their neighbors, they had followed Montcalm into the
Title:  territories of the English crown, and were making heavy and serious inroads
Title:  on the hunting-grounds of the Mohawks; though they had seen fit, with the
Title:  mysterious reserve so common among the natives, to withhold their assistance
Title:  at the moment when it was most required. The French had accounted for this
Title:  unexpected defection on the part of their ally in various ways. It was the
Title:  prevalent opinion, however, that they had been influenced by veneration for
Title:  the ancient treaty, that had once made them dependent on the Six Nations for
Title:  military protection, and now rendered them reluctant to encounter their
Title:  former masters. As for the tribe itself, it had been content to announce to
Title:  Montcalm, through his emissaries, with Indian brevity, that their hatchets
Title:  were dull, and time was necessary to sharpen them. The politic captain of
Title:  the Canadas had deemed it wiser to submit to entertain a passive friend,
Title:  than by any acts of ill-judged severity to convert him into an open enemy.
Title:  
Title:  On that morning when Magua led his silent party from the settlement of the
Title:  beavers into the forests, in the manner described, the sun rose upon the
Title:  Delaware encampment as if it had suddenly burst upon a busy people, actively
Title:  employed in all the customary avocations of high noon. The women ran from
Title:  lodge to lodge, some engaged in preparing their morning's meal, a few
Title:  earnestly bent on seeking the comforts necessary to their habits, but more
Title:  pausing to exchange hasty and whispered sentences with their friends. The
Title:  warriors were lounging in groups, musing more than they conversed and when a
Title:  few words were uttered, speaking like men who deeply weighed their opinions.
Title:  The instruments of the chase were to be seen in abundance among the lodges;
Title:  but none departed. Here and there a warrior was examining his arms, with an
Title:  attention that is rarely bestowed on the implements, when no other enemy
Title:  than the beasts of the forest is expected to be encountered. And
Title:  occasionally, the eyes of a whole group were turned simultaneously toward a
Title:  large and silent lodge in the center of the village, as if it contained the
Title:  subject of their common thoughts.
Title:  
Title:  During the existence of this scene, a man suddenly appeared at the furthest
Title:  extremity of a platform of rock which formed the level of the village. He
Title:  was without arms, and his paint tended rather to soften than increase the
Title:  natural sternness of his austere countenance. When in full view of the
Title:  Delawares he stopped, and made a gesture of amity, by throwing his arm
Title:  upward toward heaven, and then letting it fall impressively on his breast.
Title:  The inhabitants of the village answered his salute by a low murmur of
Title:  welcome, and encouraged him to advance by similar indications of friendship.
Title:  Fortified by these assurances, the dark figure left the brow of the natural
Title:  rocky terrace, where it had stood a moment, drawn in a strong outline
Title:  against the blushing morning sky, and moved with dignity into the very
Title:  center of the huts. As he approached, nothing was audible but the rattling
Title:  of the light silver ornaments that loaded his arms and neck, and the
Title:  tinkling of the little bells that fringed his deerskin moccasins. He made,
Title:  as he advanced, many courteous signs of greeting to the men he passed,
Title:  neglecting to notice the women, however, like one who deemed their favor, in
Title:  the present enterprise, of no importance. When he had reached the group in
Title:  which it was evident, by the haughtiness of their common mien, that the
Title:  principal chiefs were collected, the stranger paused, and then the Delawares
Title:  saw that the active and erect form that stood before them was that of the
Title:  well-known Huron chief, Le Renard Subtil.
Title:  
Title:  His reception was grave, silent, and wary. The warriors in front stepped
Title:  aside, opening the way to their most approved orator by the action; one who
Title:  spoke all those languages that were cultivated among the northern
Title:  aborigines.
Title:  
Title:  The wise Huron is welcome, said the Delaware, in the language of the Maquas;
Title:  he is come to eat his succatash,1 with his brothers of the lakes.
Title:  
Title:  He is come, repeated Magua, bending his head with the dignity of an eastern
Title:  prince.
Title:  
Title:  The chief extended his arm and taking the other by the wrist, they once more
Title:  exchanged friendly salutations. Then the Delaware invited his guest to enter
Title:  his own lodge, and share his morning meal. The invitation was accepted; and
Title:  the two warriors, attended by three or four of the old men, walked calmly
Title:  away, leaving the rest of the tribe devoured by a desire to understand the
Title:  reasons of so unusual a visit, and yet not betraying the least impatience by
Title:  sign or word.
Title:  
Title:  During the short and frugal repast that followed, the conversation was
Title:  extremely circumspect, and related entirely to the events of the hunt, in
Title:  which Magua had so lately been engaged. It would have been impossible for
Title:  the most finished breeding to wear more of the appearance of considering the
Title:  visit as a thing of course, than did his hosts, notwithstanding every
Title:  individual present was perfectly aware that it must be connected with some
Title:  secret object and that probably of importance to themselves. When the
Title:  appetites of the whole were appeased, the squaws removed the trenchers and
Title:  gourds, and the two parties began to prepare themselves for a subtle trial
Title:  of their wits.
Title:  
Title:  Is the face of my great Canada father turned again toward his Huron
Title:  children? demanded the orator of the Delawares.
Title:  
Title:  When was it ever otherwise? returned Magua. He calls my people most beloved.
Title:  
Title:  The Delaware gravely bowed his acquiescence to what he knew to be false, and
Title:  continued:
Title:  
Title:  The tomahawks of your young men have been very red.
Title:  
Title:  It is so; but they are now bright and dull; for the Yengeese are dead, and
Title:  the Delawares are our neighbors.
Title:  
Title:  The other acknowledged the pacific compliment by a gesture of the hand, and
Title:  remained silent. Then Magua, as if recalled to such a recollection, by the
Title:  allusion to the massacre, demanded:
Title:  
Title:  Does my prisoner give trouble to my brothers?
Title:  
Title:  She is welcome.
Title:  
Title:  The path between the Hurons and the Delawares is short and it is open; let
Title:  her be sent to my squaws, if she gives trouble to my brother.
Title:  
Title:  She is welcome, returned the chief of the latter nation, still more
Title:  emphatically.
Title:  
Title:  The baffled Magua continued silent several minutes, apparently indifferent,
Title:  however, to the repulse he had received in this his opening effort to regain
Title:  possession of Cora.
Title:  
Title:  Do my young men leave the Delawares room on the mountains for their hunts?
Title:  he at length continued.
Title:  
Title:  The Lenape are rulers of their own hills, returned the other a little
Title:  haughtily.
Title:  
Title:  It is well. Justice is the master of a red-skin. Why should they brighten
Title:  their tomahawks and sharpen their knives against each other? Are not the
Title:  pale faces thicker than the swallows in the season of flowers?
Title:  
Title:  Good! exclaimed two or three of his auditors at the same time.
Title:  
Title:  Magua waited a little, to permit his words to soften the feelings of the
Title:  Delawares, before he added:
Title:  
Title:  Have there not been strange moccasins in the woods? Have not my brothers
Title:  scented the feet of white men?
Title:  
Title:  Let my Canada father come, returned the other, evasively; his children are
Title:  ready to see him.
Title:  
Title:  When the great chief comes, it is to smoke with the Indians in their
Title:  wigwams. The Hurons say, too, he is welcome. But the Yengeese have long
Title:  arms, and legs that never tire! My young men dreamed they had seen the trail
Title:  of the Yengeese nigh the village of the Delawares!
Title:  
Title:  They will not find the Lenape asleep.
Title:  
Title:  It is well. The warrior whose eye is open can see his enemy, said Magua,
Title:  once more shifting his ground, when he found himself unable to penetrate the
Title:  caution of his companion. I have brought gifts to my brother. His nation
Title:  would not go on the warpath, because they did not think it well, but their
Title:  friends have remembered where they lived.
Title:  
Title:  When he had thus announced his liberal intention, the crafty chief arose,
Title:  and gravely spread his presents before the dazzled eyes of his hosts. They
Title:  consisted principally of trinkets of little value, plundered from the
Title:  slaughtered females of William Henry. In the division of the baubles the
Title:  cunning Huron discovered no less art than in their selection. While he
Title:  bestowed those of greater value on the two most distinguished warriors, one
Title:  of whom was his host, he seasoned his offerings to their inferiors with such
Title:  well-timed and apposite compliments, as left them no ground of complaint. In
Title:  short, the whole ceremony contained such a happy blending of the profitable
Title:  with the flattering, that it was not difficult for the donor immediately to
Title:  read the effect of a generosity so aptly mingled with praise, in the eyes of
Title:  those he addressed.
Title:  
Title:  This well-judged and politic stroke on the part of Magua was not without
Title:  instantaneous results. The Delawares lost their gravity in a much more
Title:  cordial expression; and the host, in particular, after contemplating his own
Title:  liberal share of the spoil for some moments with peculiar gratification,
Title:  repeated with strong emphasis, the words:
Title:  
Title:  My brother is a wise chief. He is welcome.
Title:  
Title:  The Hurons love their friends the Delawares, returned Magua. Why should they
Title:  not? they are colored by the same sun, and their just men will hunt in the
Title:  same grounds after death. The red-skins should be friends, and look with
Title:  open eyes on the white men. Has not my brother scented spies in the woods?
Title:  
Title:  The Delaware, whose name in English signified Hard Heart, an appellation
Title:  that the French had translated into le Coeur-dur, forgot that obduracy of
Title:  purpose, which had probably obtained him so significant a title. His
Title:  countenance grew very sensibly less stern and he now deigned to answer more
Title:  directly.
Title:  
Title:  There have been strange moccasins about my camp. They have been tracked into
Title:  my lodges.
Title:  
Title:  Did my brother beat out the dogs? asked Magua, without adverting in any
Title:  manner to the former equivocation of the chief.
Title:  
Title:  It would not do. The stranger is always welcome to the children of the
Title:  Lenape.
Title:  
Title:  The stranger, but not the spy.
Title:  
Title:  Would the Yengeese send their women as spies? Did not the Huron chief say he
Title:  took women in the battle?
Title:  
Title:  He told no lie. The Yengeese have sent out their scouts. They have been in
Title:  my wigwams, but they found there no one to say welcome. Then they fled to
Title:  the Delawares - for, say they, the Delawares are our friends; their minds
Title:  are turned from their Canada father!
Title:  
Title:  This insinuation was a home thrust, and one that in a more advanced state of
Title:  society would have entitled Magua to the reputation of a skillful
Title:  diplomatist. The recent defection of the tribe had, as they well knew
Title:  themselves, subjected the Delawares to much reproach among their French
Title:  allies; and they were now made to feel that their future actions were to be
Title:  regarded with jealousy and distrust. There was no deep insight into causes
Title:  and effects necessary to foresee that such a situation of things was likely
Title:  to prove highly prejudicial to their future movements. Their distant
Title:  villages, their hunting-grounds and hundreds of their women and children,
Title:  together with a material part of their physical force, were actually within
Title:  the limits of the French territory. Accordingly, this alarming annunciation
Title:  was received, as Magua intended, with manifest disapprobation, if not with
Title:  alarm.
Title:  
Title:  Let my father look in my face, said Le Coeur-dur; he will see no change. It
Title:  is true, my young men did not go out on the war-path; they had dreams for
Title:  not doing so. But they love and venerate the great white chief.
Title:  
Title:  Will he think so when he hears that his greatest enemy is fed in the camp of
Title:  his children? When he is told a bloody Yengee smokes at your fire? That the
Title:  pale face who has slain so many of his friends goes in and out among the
Title:  Delawares? Go! my great Canada father is not a fool!
Title:  
Title:  Where is the Yengee that the Delawares fear? returned the other; who has
Title:  slain my young men? who is the mortal enemy of my Great Father?
Title:  
Title:  La Longue Carabine!
Title:  
Title:  The Delaware warriors started at the well-known name, betraying by their
Title:  amazement, that they now learned, for the first time, one so famous among
Title:  the Indian allies of France was within their power.
Title:  
Title:  What does my brother mean? demanded Le Coeur-dur, in a tone that, by its
Title:  wonder, far exceeded the usual apathy of his race.
Title:  
Title:  A Huron never lies! returned Magua, coldly, leaning his head against the
Title:  side of the lodge, and drawing his slight robe across his tawny breast. Let
Title:  the Delawares count their prisoners; they will find one whose skin is
Title:  neither red nor pale.
Title:  
Title:  A long and musing pause succeeded. The chief consulted apart with his
Title:  companions, and messengers despatched to collect certain others of the most
Title:  distinguished men of the tribe.
Title:  
Title:  As warrior after warrior dropped in, they were each made acquainted, in
Title:  turn, with the important intelligence that Magua had just communicated. The
Title:  air of surprise, and the usual low, deep, guttural exclamation, were common
Title:  to them all. The news spread from mouth to mouth, until the whole encampment
Title:  became powerfully agitated. The women suspended their labors, to catch such
Title:  syllables as unguardedly fell from the lips of the consulting warriors. The
Title:  boys deserted their sports, and walking fearlessly among their fathers,
Title:  looked up in curious admiration, as they heard the brief exclamations of
Title:  wonder they so freely expressed the temerity of their hated foe. In short,
Title:  every occupation was abandoned for the time, and all other pursuits seemed
Title:  discarded in order that the tribe might freely indulge, after their own
Title:  peculiar manner, in an open expression of feeling.
Title:  
Title:  When the excitement had a little abated, the old men disposed themselves
Title:  seriously to consider that which it became the honor and safety of their
Title:  tribe to perform, under circumstances of so much delicacy and embarrassment.
Title:  During all these movements, and in the midst of the general commotion, Magua
Title:  had not only maintained his seat, but the very attitude he had originally
Title:  taken, against the side of the lodge, where he continued as immovable, and,
Title:  apparently, as unconcerned, as if he had no interest in the result. Not a
Title:  single indication of the future intentions of his hosts, however, escaped
Title:  his vigilant eyes. With his consummate knowledge of the nature of the people
Title:  with whom he had to deal, he anticipated every measure on which they
Title:  decided; and it might almost be said, that, in many instances, he knew their
Title:  intentions, even before they became known to themselves.
Title:  
Title:  The council of the Delawares was short. When it was ended, a general bustle
Title:  announced that it was to be immediately succeeded by a solemn and formal
Title:  assemblage of the nation. As such meetings were rare, and only called on
Title:  occasions of the last importance, the subtle Huron, who still sat apart, a
Title:  wily and dark observer of the proceedings, now knew that all his projects
Title:  must be brought to their final issue. He, therefore, left the lodge and
Title:  walked silently forth to the place, in front of the encampment, whither the
Title:  warriors were already beginning to collect.
Title:  
Title:  It might have been half an hour before each individual, including even the
Title:  women and children, was in his place. The delay had been created by the
Title:  grave preparations that were deemed necessary to so solemn and unusual a
Title:  conference. But when the sun was seen climbing above the tops of that
Title:  mountain, against whose bosom the Delawares had constructed their
Title:  encampment, most were seated; and as his bright rays darted from behind the
Title:  outline of trees that fringed the eminence, they fell upon as grave, as
Title:  attentive, and as deeply interested a multitude, as was probably ever before
Title:  lighted by his morning beams. Its number somewhat exceeded a thousand souls.
Title:  
Title:  In a collection of so serious savages, there is never to be found any
Title:  impatient aspirant after premature distinction, standing ready to move his
Title:  auditors to some hasty, and, perhaps, injudicious discussion, in order that
Title:  his own reputation may be the gainer. An act of so much precipitancy and
Title:  presumption would seal the downfall of precocious intellect forever. It
Title:  rested solely with the oldest and most experienced of the men to lay the
Title:  subject of the conference before the people. Until such a one chose to make
Title:  some movement, no deeds in arms, no natural gifts, nor any renown as an
Title:  orator, would have justified the slightest interruption. On the present
Title:  occasion, the aged warrior whose privilege it was to speak, was silent,
Title:  seemingly oppressed with the magnitude of his subject. The delay had already
Title:  continued long beyond the usual deliberative pause that always preceded a
Title:  conference; but no sign of impatience or surprise escaped even the youngest
Title:  boy. Occasionally an eye was raised from the earth, where the looks of most
Title:  were riveted, and strayed toward a particular lodge, that was, however, in
Title:  no manner distinguished from those around it, except in the peculiar care
Title:  that had been taken to protect it against the assaults of the weather.
Title:  
Title:  At length one of those low murmurs, that are so apt to disturb a multitude,
Title:  was heard, and the whole nation arose to their feet by a common impulse. At
Title:  that instant the door of the lodge in question opened, and three men,
Title:  issuing from it, slowly approached the place of consultation. They were all
Title:  aged, even beyond that period to which the oldest present had reached; but
Title:  one in the center, who leaned on his companions for support, had numbered an
Title:  amount of years to which the human race is seldom permitted to attain. His
Title:  frame, which had once been tall and erect, like the cedar, was now bending
Title:  under the pressure of more than a century. The elastic, light step of an
Title:  Indian was gone, and in its place he was compelled to toil his tardy way
Title:  over the ground, inch by inch. His dark, wrinkled countenance was in
Title:  singular and wild contrast with the long white locks which floated on his
Title:  shoulders, in such thickness, as to announce that generations had probably
Title:  passed away since they had last been shorn.
Title:  
Title:  The dress of this patriarch - for such, considering his vast age, in
Title:  conjunction with his affinity and influence with his people, he might very
Title:  properly be termed - was rich and imposing, though strictly after the simple
Title:  fashions of the tribe. His robe was of the finest skins, which had been
Title:  deprived of their fur, in order to admit of a hieroglyphical representation
Title:  of various deeds in arms, done in former ages. His bosom was loaded with
Title:  medals, some in massive silver, and one or two even in gold, the gifts of
Title:  various Christian potentates during the long period of his life. He also
Title:  wore armlets, and cinctures above the ankles, of the latter precious metal.
Title:  His head, on the whole of which the hair had been permitted to grow, the
Title:  pursuits of war having so long been abandoned, was encircled by a sort of
Title:  plated diadem, which, in its turn, bore lesser and more glittering
Title:  ornaments, that sparkled amid the glossy hues of three drooping ostrich
Title:  feathers, dyed a deep black, in touching contrast to the color of his
Title:  snow-white locks. His tomahawk was nearly hid in silver, and the handle of
Title:  his knife shone like a horn of solid gold.
Title:  
Title:  So soon as the first hum of emotion and pleasure, which the sudden
Title:  appearance of this venerated individual created, had a little subsided, the
Title:  name of Tamenund was whispered from mouth to mouth. Magua had often heard
Title:  the fame of this wise and just Delaware; a reputation that even proceeded so
Title:  far as to bestow on him the rare gift of holding secret communion with the
Title:  Great Spirit, and which has since transmitted his name, with some slight
Title:  alteration, to the white usurpers of his ancient territory, as the imaginary
Title:  tutelar saint2 of a vast empire. The Huron chief, therefore, stepped eagerly
Title:  out a little from the throng, to a spot whence he might catch a nearer
Title:  glimpse of the features of the man, whose decision was likely to produce so
Title:  deep an influence on his own fortunes.
Title:  
Title:  The eyes of the old man were closed, as though the organs were wearied with
Title:  having so long witnessed the selfish workings of the human passions. The
Title:  color of his skin differed from that of most around him, being richer and
Title:  darker, the latter having been produced by certain delicate and mazy lines
Title:  of complicated and yet beautiful figures, which had been traced over most of
Title:  his person by the operation of tattooing. Notwithstanding the position of
Title:  the Huron, he passed the observant and silent Magua without notice, and
Title:  leaning on his two venerable supporters proceeded to the high place of the
Title:  multitude, where he seated himself in the center of his nation, with the
Title:  dignity of a monarch and the air of a father.
Title:  
Title:  Nothing could surpass the reverence and affection with which this unexpected
Title:  visit from one who belongs rather to another world than to this, was
Title:  received by his people. After a suitable and decent pause, the principal
Title:  chiefs arose, and, approaching the patriarch, they placed his hands
Title:  reverently on their heads, seeming to entreat a blessing. The younger men
Title:  were content with touching his robe, or even drawing nigh his person, in
Title:  order to breathe in the atmosphere of one so aged, so just, and so valiant.
Title:  None but the most distinguished among the youthful warriors even presumed to
Title:  far as to perform the latter ceremony, the great mass of the multitude
Title:  deeming it a sufficient happiness to look upon a form so deeply venerated,
Title:  and so well beloved. When these acts of affection and respect were
Title:  performed, the chiefs drew back again to their several places, and silence
Title:  reigned in the whole encampment.
Title:  
Title:  After a short delay, a few of the young men, to whom instructions had been
Title:  whispered by one of the aged attendants of Tamenund, arose, left the crowd,
Title:  and entered the lodge which has already been noted as the object of so much
Title:  attention throughout that morning. In a few minutes they reappeared,
Title:  escorting the individuals who had caused all these solemn preparations
Title:  toward the seat of judgment. The crowd opened in a lane; and when the party
Title:  had re-entered, it closed in again, forming a large and dense belt of human
Title:  bodies, arranged in an open circle.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 A dish composed of cracked corn and beans. It is much used also by the
Title:  whites. By corn is meant maize.
Title:  
Title:  2 The Americans sometimes called their tutelar saint Tamenay, a corruption
Title:  of the name of the renowned chief here introduced. There are many traditions
Title:  which speak of the character and power of Tamenund.

Title:                 ----------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:  Chapter 29
Title:  
Title:       The assembly seated, rising o'er the rest,
Title:       Achilles thus the king of men addressed.
Title:  
Title:                                                            POPE'S Homer
Title:  
Title:  Cora stood foremost among the prisoners, entwining her arms in those of
Title:  Alice, in the tenderness of sisterly love. Notwithstanding the fearful and
Title:  menacing array of savages on every side of her, no apprehension on her own
Title:  account could prevent the nobler-minded maiden from keeping her eyes
Title:  fastened on the pale and anxious features of the trembling Alice. Close at
Title:  their side stood Heyward, with an interest in both, that, at such a moment
Title:  of intense uncertainty, scarcely knew a preponderance in favor of her whom
Title:  he most loved. Hawkeye had placed himself a little in the rear, with a
Title:  deference to the superior rank of his companions, that no similarity in the
Title:  state of their present fortunes could induce him to forget. Uncas was not
Title:  there.
Title:  
Title:  When perfect silence was again restored, and after the usual long,
Title:  impressive pause, one of the two aged chiefs who sat at the side of the
Title:  patriarch arose, and demanded aloud, in very intelligible English:
Title:  
Title:  Which of my prisoners is La Longue Carabine?
Title:  
Title:  Neither Duncan nor the scout answered. The former, however, glanced his eyes
Title:  around the dark and silent assembly, and recoiled a pace, when they fell on
Title:  the malignant visage of Magua. He saw, at once, that this wily savage had
Title:  some secret agency in their present arraignment before the nation, and
Title:  determined to throw every possible impediment in the way of the execution of
Title:  his sinister plans. He had witnessed one instance of the summary punishments
Title:  of the Indians, and now dreaded that his companion was to be selected for a
Title:  second. In this dilemma, with little or no time for reflection, he suddenly
Title:  determined to cloak his invaluable friend, at any or every hazard to
Title:  himself. Before he had time, however, to speak, the question was repeated in
Title:  a louder voice, and with a clearer utterance.
Title:  
Title:  Give us arms, the young man haughtily replied, and place us in yonder woods.
Title:  Our deeds shall speak for us!
Title:  
Title:  This is the warrior whose name has filled our ears! returned the chief,
Title:  regarding Heyward with that sort of curious interest which seems inseparable
Title:  from man, when first beholding one of his fellows to whom merit or accident,
Title:  virtue or crime, has given notoriety. What has brought the white man into
Title:  the camp of the Delawares?
Title:  
Title:  My necessities. I come for food, shelter, and friends.
Title:  
Title:  It cannot be. The woods are full of game. The head of a warrior needs no
Title:  other shelter than a sky without clouds; and the Delawares are the enemies,
Title:  and not the friends of the Yengeese. Go, the mouth has spoken, while the
Title:  heart said nothing.
Title:  
Title:  Duncan, a little at a loss in what manner to proceed, remained silent; but
Title:  the scout, who had listened attentively to all that passed, now advanced
Title:  steadily to the front.
Title:  
Title:  That I did not answer to the call for La Longue Carabine, was not owing
Title:  either to shame or fear, he said, for neither one nor the other is the gift
Title:  of an honest man. But I do not admit the right of the Mingoes to bestow a
Title:  name on one whose friends have been mindful of his gifts, in this
Title:  particular; especially as their title is a lie, killdeer being a grooved
Title:  barrel and no carabyne. I am the man, however, that got the name of
Title:  Nathaniel from my kin; the compliment of Hawkeye from the Delawares, who
Title:  live on their own river; and whom the Iroquois have presumed to style the
Title:  Long Rifle, without any warranty from him who is most concerned in the
Title:  matter.
Title:  
Title:  The eyes of all present, which had hitherto been gravely scanning the person
Title:  of Duncan, were now turned, on the instant, toward the upright iron frame of
Title:  this new pretender to the distinguished appellation. It was in no degree
Title:  remarkable that there should be found two who were willing to claim so great
Title:  an honor, for imposters, though rare, were not unknown among the natives;
Title:  but it was altogether material to the just and severe intentions of the
Title:  Delawares, that there should be no mistake in the matter. Some of their old
Title:  men consulted together in private, and then, as it would seem, they
Title:  determined to interrogate their visitor on the subject.
Title:  
Title:  My brother has said that a snake crept into my camp, said the chief to
Title:  Magua; which is he?
Title:  
Title:  The Huron pointed to the scout.
Title:  
Title:  Will a wise Delaware believe the barking of a wolf? exclaimed Duncan, still
Title:  more confirmed in the evil intentions of his ancient enemy: a dog never
Title:  lies, but when was a wolf known to speak the truth?
Title:  
Title:  The eyes of Magua flashed fire; but suddenly recollecting the necessity of
Title:  maintaining his presence of mind, he turned away in silent disdain, well
Title:  assured that the sagacity of the Indians would not fail to extract the real
Title:  merits of the point in controversy. He was not deceived; for, after another
Title:  short consultation, the wary Delaware turned to him again, and expressed the
Title:  determination of the chiefs, though in the most considerate language.
Title:  
Title:  My brother has been called a liar, he said, and his friends are angry. They
Title:  will show that he has spoken the truth. Give my prisoners guns, and let them
Title:  prove which is the man.
Title:  
Title:  Magua affected to consider the expedient, which he well knew proceeded from
Title:  distrust of himself, as a compliment, and made a gesture of acquiescence,
Title:  well content that his veracity should be supported by so skillful a marksman
Title:  as the scout. The weapons were instantly placed in the hands of the friendly
Title:  opponents, and they were bid to fire, over the heads of the seated
Title:  multitude, at an earthen vessel, which lay, by accident, on a stump, some
Title:  fifty yards from the place where they stood.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward smiled to himself at the idea of a competition with the scout,
Title:  though he determined to persevere in the deception, until apprised of the
Title:  real designs of Magua.
Title:  
Title:  Raising his rifle with the utmost care, and renewing his aim three several
Title:  times, he fired. The bullet cut the wood within a few inches of the vessel;
Title:  and a general exclamation of satisfaction announced that the shot was
Title:  considered a proof of great skill in the use of a weapon. Even Hawkeye
Title:  nodded his head, as if he would say, it was better than he expected. But,
Title:  instead of manifesting an intention to contend with the successful marksman,
Title:  he stood leaning on his rifle for more than a minute, like a man who was
Title:  completely buried in thought. From this reverie, he was, however, awakened
Title:  by one of the young Indians who had furnished the arms, and who now touched
Title:  his shoulder, saying in exceedingly broken English:
Title:  
Title:  Can the pale face beat it?
Title:  
Title:  Yes, Huron! exclaimed the scout, raising the short rifle in his right hand,
Title:  and shaking it at Magua, with as much apparent ease as if it were a reed;
Title:  yes, Huron, I could strike you now, and no power on earth could prevent the
Title:  deed! The soaring hawk is not more certain of the dove than I am this moment
Title:  of you, did I choose to send a bullet to your heart! Why should I not? Why!
Title:  - because the gifts of my color forbid it, and I might draw down evil on
Title:  tender and innocent heads. If you know such a being as God, thank Him,
Title:  therefore, in your inward soul; for you have reason!
Title:  
Title:  The flushed countenance, angry eye and swelling figure of the scout,
Title:  produced a sensation of secret awe in all that heard him. The Delawares held
Title:  their breath in expectation; but Magua himself, even while he distrusted the
Title:  forbearance of his enemy, remained immovable and calm, where he stood wedged
Title:  in by the crowd, as one who grew to the spot.
Title:  
Title:  Beat it, repeated the young Delaware at the elbow of the scout.
Title:  
Title:  Beat what, fool! - what? exclaimed Hawkeye, still flourishing the weapon
Title:  angrily above his head, though his eye no longer sought the person of Magua.
Title:  
Title:  If the white man is the warrior he pretends, said the aged chief, let him
Title:  strike nigher to the mark.
Title:  
Title:  The scout laughed aloud - a noise that produced the startling effect of an
Title:  unnatural sound on Heyward; then dropping the piece, heavily, into his
Title:  extended left hand, it was discharged, apparently by the shock, driving the
Title:  fragments of the vessel into the air, and scattering them on every side.
Title:  Almost at the same instant, the rattling sound of the rifle was heard, as he
Title:  suffered it to fall, contemptuously, to the earth.
Title:  
Title:  The first impression of so strange a scene was engrossing admiration. Then a
Title:  low, but increasing murmur, ran through the multitude, and finally swelled
Title:  into sounds that denoted a lively opposition in the sentiments of the
Title:  spectators. While some openly testified their satisfaction at so unexampled
Title:  dexterity, by far the larger portion of the tribe were inclined to believe
Title:  the success of the shot was the result of accident. Heyward was not slow to
Title:  confirm an opinion that was so favorable to his own pretensions.
Title:  
Title:  It was chance! he exclaimed; none can shoot without an aim!
Title:  
Title:  Chance! echoed the excited woodsman, who was now stubbornly bent on
Title:  maintaining his identity at every hazard, and on whom the secret hints of
Title:  Heyward to acquiesce in the deception were entirely lost. Does yonder lying
Title:  Huron, too, think it chance? Give him another gun, and place us face to
Title:  face, without cover or dodge, and let Providence, and our own eyes, decide
Title:  the matter atween us! I do not make the offer, to you, major; for our blood
Title:  is of a color, and we serve the same master.
Title:  
Title:  That the Huron is a liar, is very evident, returned Heyward, coolly; you
Title:  have yourself heard him asset you to be La Longue Carabine.
Title:  
Title:  It were impossible to say what violent assertion the stubborn Hawkeye would
Title:  have next made, in his headlong wish to vindicate his identity, had not the
Title:  aged Delaware once more interposed.
Title:  
Title:  The hawk which comes from the clouds can return when he will, he said; give
Title:  them the guns.
Title:  
Title:  This time the scout seized the rifle with avidity; nor had Magua, though he
Title:  watched the movements of the marksman with jealous eyes, any further cause
Title:  for apprehension.
Title:  
Title:  Now let it be proved, in the face of this tribe of Delawares, which is the
Title:  better man, cried the scout, tapping the butt of his piece with that finger
Title:  which had pulled so many fatal triggers.
Title:  
Title:  You see that gourd hanging against yonder tree, major; if you are a marksman
Title:  fit for the borders, let me see you break its shell!
Title:  
Title:  Duncan noted the object, and prepared himself to renew the trial. The gourd
Title:  was one of the usual little vessels used by the Indians, and it was
Title:  suspended from a dead branch of a small pine, by a thong of deerskin, at the
Title:  full distance of a hundred yards. So strangely compounded is the feeling of
Title:  self-love, that the young soldier, while he knew the utter worthlessness of
Title:  the suffrages of his savage umpires, forgot the sudden motives of the
Title:  contest in a wish to excel. It had been seen, already, that his skill was
Title:  far from being contemptible, and he now resolved to put forth its nicest
Title:  qualities. Had his life depended on the issue, the aim of Duncan could not
Title:  have been more deliberate or guarded. He fired; and three or four young
Title:  Indians, who sprang forward at the report, announced with a shout, that the
Title:  ball was in the tree, a very little on one side of the proper object. The
Title:  warriors uttered a common ejaculation of pleasure, and then turned their
Title:  eyes, inquiringly, on the movements of his rival.
Title:  
Title:  It may do for the Royal Americans! said Hawkeye, laughing once more in his
Title:  own silent, heartfelt manner; but had my gun often turned so much from the
Title:  true line, many a marten, whose skin is now in a lady's muff, would still be
Title:  in the woods; ay, and many a bloody Mingo, who has departed to his final
Title:  account, would be acting his deviltries at this very day, atween the
Title:  provinces. I hope the squaw who owns the gourd has more of them in her
Title:  wigwam, for this will never hold water again!
Title:  
Title:  The scout had shook his priming, and cocked his piece, while speaking; and,
Title:  as he ended, he threw back a foot, and slowly raised the muzzle from the
Title:  earth: the motion was steady, uniform, and in one direction. When on a
Title:  perfect level, it remained for a single moment, without tremor or variation,
Title:  as though both man and rifle were carved in stone. During that stationary
Title:  instant, it poured forth its contents, in a bright, glancing sheet of flame.
Title:  Again the young Indians bounded forward; but their hurried search and
Title:  disappointed looks announced that no traces of the bullet were to be seen.
Title:  
Title:  Go! said the old chief to the scout, in a tone of strong disgust; thou art a
Title:  wolf in the skin of a dog. I will talk to the Long Rifle of the Yengeese.
Title:  
Title:  Ah! had I that piece which furnished the name you use, I would obligate
Title:  myself to cut the thong, and drop the gourd without breaking it! returned
Title:  Hawkeye, perfectly undisturbed by the other's manner. Fools, if you would
Title:  find the bullet of a sharpshooter in these woods, you must look in the
Title:  object, and not around it!
Title:  
Title:  The Indian youths instantly comprehended his meaning - for this time he
Title:  spoke in the Delaware tongue - and tearing the gourd from the tree, they
Title:  held it on high with an exulting shout, displaying a hole in its bottom,
Title:  which had been but by the bullet, after passing through the usual orifice in
Title:  the center of its upper side. At this unexpected exhibition, a loud and
Title:  vehement expression of pleasure burst from the mouth of every warrior
Title:  present. It decided the question, and effectually established Hawkeye in the
Title:  possession of his dangerous reputation. Those curious and admiring eyes
Title:  which had been turned again on Heyward, were finally directed to the
Title:  weather-beaten form of the scout, who immediately became the principal
Title:  object of attention to the simple and unsophisticated beings by whom he was
Title:  surrounded. When the sudden and noisy commotion had a little subsided, the
Title:  aged chief resumed his examination.
Title:  
Title:  Why did you wish to stop my ears? he said, addressing Duncan; are the
Title:  Delawares fools that they could not know the young panther from the cat?
Title:  
Title:  They will yet find the Huron a singing-bird, said Duncan, endeavoring to
Title:  adopt the figurative language of the natives.
Title:  
Title:  It is good. We will know who can shut the ears of men. Brother, added the
Title:  chief turning his eyes on Magua, the Delawares listen.
Title:  
Title:  Thus singled, and directly called on to declare his object, the Huron arose;
Title:  and advancing with great deliberation and dignity into the very center of
Title:  the circle, where he stood confronted by the prisoners, he placed himself in
Title:  an attitude to speak. Before opening his mouth, however, he bent his eyes
Title:  slowly along the whole living boundary of earnest faces, as if to temper his
Title:  expressions to the capacities of his audience. On Hawkeye he cast a glance
Title:  of respectful enmity; on Duncan, a look of inextinguishable hatred; the
Title:  shrinking figure of Alice he scarcely deigned to notice; but when his glance
Title:  met the firm, commanding, and yet lovely form of Cora, his eye lingered a
Title:  moment, with an expression that it might have been difficult to define.
Title:  Then, filled with his own dark intentions, he spoke in the language of the
Title:  Canadas, a tongue that he well knew was comprehended by most of his
Title:  auditors.
Title:  
Title:  The Spirit that made men colored them differently, commenced the subtle
Title:  Huron. Some are blacker than the sluggish bear. These He said should be
Title:  slaves; and He ordered them to work forever, like the beaver. You may hear
Title:  them groan, when the south wind blows, louder than the lowing buffaloes,
Title:  along the shores of the great salt lake, where the big canoes come and go
Title:  with them in droves. Some He made with faces paler than the ermine of the
Title:  forests; and these He ordered to be traders; dogs to their women, and wolves
Title:  to their slaves. He gave this people the nature of the pigeon; wings that
Title:  never tire; young, more plentiful than the leaves on the trees, and
Title:  appetites to devour the earth. He gave them tongues like the false call of
Title:  the wildcat; hearts like rabbits; the cunning of the hog (but none of the
Title:  fox), and arms longer than the legs of the moose. With his tongue he stops
Title:  the ears of the Indians; his heart teaches him to pay warriors to fight his
Title:  battles; his cunning tells him how to get together the goods of the earth;
Title:  and his arms inclose the land from the shores of the salt-water to the
Title:  islands of the great lake. His gluttony makes him sick. God gave him enough,
Title:  and yet he wants all. Such are the pale faces.
Title:  
Title:  Some the Great Spirit made with skins brighter and redder than yonder sun,
Title:  continued Magua, pointing impressively upward to the lurid luminary, which
Title:  was struggling through the misty atmosphere of the horizon; and these did He
Title:  fashion to His own mind. He gave them this island as He had made it, covered
Title:  with trees, and filled with game. The wind made their clearings; the sun and
Title:  rain ripened their fruits; and the snows came to tell them to be thankful.
Title:  What need had they of roads to journey by! They saw through the hills! When
Title:  the beavers worked, they lay in the shade, and looked on. The winds cooled
Title:  them in summer; in winter, skins kept them warm. If they fought among
Title:  themselves, it was to prove that they were men. They were brave; they were
Title:  just; they were happy.
Title:  
Title:  Here the speaker paused, and again looked around him to discover if his
Title:  legend had touched the sympathies of his listeners. He met everywhere, with
Title:  eyes riveted on his own, heads erect and nostrils expanded, as if each
Title:  individual present felt himself able and willing, singly, to redress the
Title:  wrongs of his race.
Title:  
Title:  If the Great Spirit gave different tongues to his red children, he
Title:  continued, in a low, still melancholy voice, it was that all animals might
Title:  understand them. Some He placed among the snows, with their cousin, the
Title:  bear. Some he placed near the setting sun, on the road to the happy hunting
Title:  grounds. Some on the lands around the great fresh waters; but to His
Title:  greatest, and most beloved, He gave the sands of the salt lake. Do my
Title:  brothers know the name of this favored people?
Title:  
Title:  It was the Lenape! exclaimed twenty eager voices in a breath.
Title:  
Title:  It was the Lenni Lenape, returned Magua, affecting to bend his head in
Title:  reverence to their former greatness. It was the tribes of the Lenape! The
Title:  sun rose from water that was salt, and set in water that was sweet, and
Title:  never hid himself from their eyes. But why should I, a Huron of the woods,
Title:  tell a wise people their own traditions? Why remind them of their injuries;
Title:  their ancient greatness; their deeds; their glory; their happiness; their
Title:  losses; their defeats; their misery? Is there not one among them who has
Title:  seen it all, and who knows it to be true? I have done. My tongue is still
Title:  for my heart is of lead. I listen.
Title:  
Title:  As the voice of the speaker suddenly ceased, every face and all eyes turned,
Title:  by a common movement, toward the venerable Tamenund. From the moment that he
Title:  took his seat, until the present instant, the lips of the patriarch had not
Title:  severed, and scarcely a sign of life had escaped him. He sat bent in
Title:  feebleness, and apparently unconscious of the presence he was in, during the
Title:  whole of that opening scene, in which the skill of the scout had been so
Title:  clearly established. At the nicely graduated sound of Magua's voice,
Title:  however, he betrayed some evidence of consciousness, and once or twice he
Title:  even raised his head, as if to listen. But when the crafty Huron spoke of
Title:  his nation by name, the eyelids of the old man raised themselves, and he
Title:  looked out upon the multitude with that sort of dull, unmeaning expression
Title:  which might be supposed to belong to the countenance of a specter. Then he
Title:  made an effort to rise, and being upheld by his supporters, he gained his
Title:  feet, in a posture commanding by its dignity, while he tottered with
Title:  weakness.
Title:  
Title:  Who calls upon the children of the Lenape? he said, in a deep, guttural
Title:  voice, that was rendered awfully audible by the breathless silence of the
Title:  multitude; who speaks of things gone? Does not the egg become a worm - the
Title:  worm a fly, and perish? Why tell the Delawares of good that is past? Better
Title:  thank the Manitou for that which remains.
Title:  
Title:  It is a Wyandot, said Magua, stepping nigher to the rude platform on which
Title:  the other stood; a friend of Tamenund.
Title:  
Title:  A friend! repeated the sage, on whose brow a dark frown settled, imparting a
Title:  portion of that severity which had rendered his eye so terrible in middle
Title:  age. Are the Mingoes rulers of the earth? What brings a Huron in here?
Title:  
Title:  Justice. His prisoners are with his brothers, and he comes for his own.
Title:  
Title:  Tamenund turned his head toward one of his supporters, and listened to the
Title:  short explanation the man gave.
Title:  
Title:  Then, facing the applicant, he regarded him a moment with deep attention;
Title:  after which he said, in a low and reluctant voice:
Title:  
Title:  Justice is the law of the great Manitou. My children, give the stranger
Title:  food. Then, Huron, take thine own and depart.
Title:  
Title:  On the delivery of this solemn judgment, the patriarch seated himself, and
Title:  closed his eyes again, as if better pleased with the images of his own
Title:  ripened experience than with the visible objects of the world. Against such
Title:  a decree there was no Delaware sufficiently hardy to murmur, much less
Title:  oppose himself. The words were barely uttered when four or five of the
Title:  younger warriors, stepping behind Heyward and the scout, passed thongs so
Title:  dexterously and rapidly around their arms, as to hold them both in instant
Title:  bondage. The former was too much engrossed with his precious and nearly
Title:  insensible burden, to be aware of their intentions before they were
Title:  executed; and the latter, who considered even the hostile tribes of the
Title:  Delawares a superior race of beings, submitted without resistance. Perhaps,
Title:  however, the manner of the scout would not have been so passive, had he
Title:  fully comprehended the language in which the preceding dialogue had been
Title:  conducted.
Title:  
Title:  Magua cast a look of triumph around the whole assembly before he proceeded
Title:  to the execution of his purpose. Perceiving that the men were unable to
Title:  offer any resistance, he turned his looks on her he valued most. Cora met
Title:  his gaze with an eye so calm and firm, that his resolution wavered. Then,
Title:  recollecting his former artifice, he raised Alice from the arms of the
Title:  warrior against whom she leaned, and beckoning Heyward to follow, he
Title:  motioned for the encircling crowd to open. But Cora, instead of obeying the
Title:  impulse he had expected, rushed to the feet of the patriarch, and, raising
Title:  her voice, exclaimed aloud:
Title:  
Title:  Just and venerable Delaware, on thy wisdom and power we lean for mercy! Be
Title:  deaf to yonder artful and remorseless monster, who poisons thy ears with
Title:  falsehoods to feed his thirst for blood. Thou that hast lived long, and that
Title:  hast seen the evil of the world, should know how to temper its calamities to
Title:  the miserable.
Title:  
Title:  The eyes of the old man opened heavily, and he once more looked upward at
Title:  the multitude. As the piercing tones of the suppliant swelled on his ears,
Title:  they moved slowly in the direction of her person, and finally settled there
Title:  in a steady gaze. Cora had cast herself to her knees; and, with hands
Title:  clenched in each other and pressed upon her bosom, she remained like a
Title:  beauteous and breathing model of her sex, looking up in his faded but
Title:  majestic countenance, with a species of holy reverence. Gradually the
Title:  expression of Tamenund's features changed, and losing their vacancy in
Title:  admiration, they lighted with a portion of that intelligence which a century
Title:  before had been wont to communicate his youthful fire to the extensive bands
Title:  of the Delawares. Rising without assistance, and seemingly without an
Title:  effort, he demanded, in a voice that startled its auditors by its firmness:
Title:  
Title:  What art thou?
Title:  
Title:  A woman. One of a hated race, it thou wilt - a Yengee. But one who has never
Title:  harmed thee, and who cannot harm thy people, if she would; who asks for
Title:  succor.
Title:  
Title:  Tell me, my children, continued the patriarch, hoarsely, motioning to those
Title:  around him, though his eyes still dwelt upon the kneeling form of Cora,
Title:  where have the Delawares camped?
Title:  
Title:  In the mountains of the Iroquois, beyond the clear springs of the Horican.
Title:  
Title:  Many parching summers are come and gone, continued the sage, since I drank
Title:  of the water of my own rivers. The children of Minquon1 are the justest
Title:  white men, but they were thirsty and they took it to themselves. Do they
Title:  follow us so far?
Title:  
Title:  We follow none, we covet nothing, answered Cora. Captives against our wills,
Title:  have we been brought amongst you; and we ask but permission to depart to our
Title:  own in peace. Art thou not Tamenund - the father, the judge, I had almost
Title:  said, the prophet - of this people?
Title:  
Title:  I am Tamenund of many days.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis now some seven years that one of thy people was at the mercy of a white
Title:  chief on the borders of this province. He claimed to be of the blood of the
Title:  good and just Tamenund. Go, said the white man, for thy parent's sake thou
Title:  art free. Dost thou remember the name of that English warrior?
Title:  
Title:  I remember, that when a laughing boy, returned the patriarch, with the
Title:  peculiar recollection of vast age, I stood upon the sands of the sea shore,
Title:  and saw a big canoe, with wings whiter than the swan's, and wider than many
Title:  eagles, come from the rising sun.
Title:  
Title:  Nay, nay; I speak not of a time so very distant, but of favor shown to thy
Title:  kindred by one of mine, within the memory of thy youngest warrior.
Title:  
Title:  Was it when the Yengeese and the Dutchmanne fought for the hunting-grounds
Title:  of the Delawares? Then Tamenund was a chief, and first laid aside the bow
Title:  for the lightning of the pale faces - -
Title:  
Title:  Not yet then, interrupted Cora, by many ages; I speak of a thing of
Title:  yesterday. Surely, surely, you forget it not.
Title:  
Title:  It was but yesterday, rejoined the aged man, with touching pathos, that the
Title:  children of the Lenape were masters of the world. The fishes of the salt
Title:  lake, the birds, the beasts, and the Mengee of the woods, owned them for
Title:  Sagamores.
Title:  
Title:  Cora bowed her head in disappointment, and, for a bitter moment struggled
Title:  with her chagrin. Then, elevating her rich features and beaming eyes, she
Title:  continued, in tones scarcely less penetrating than the unearthly voice of
Title:  the patriarch himself:
Title:  
Title:  Tell me, is Tamenund a father?
Title:  
Title:  The old man looked down upon her from his elevated stand, with a benignant
Title:  smile on his wasted countenance, and then casting his eyes slowly over the
Title:  whole assemblage, he answered:
Title:  
Title:  Of a nation.
Title:  
Title:  For myself I ask nothing. Like thee and thine, venerable chief, she
Title:  continued, pressing her hands convulsively on her heart, and suffering her
Title:  head to droop until her burning cheeks were nearly concealed in the maze of
Title:  dark, glossy tresses that fell in disorder upon her shoulders, the curse of
Title:  my ancestors has fallen heavily on their child. But yonder is one who has
Title:  never known the weight of Heaven's displeasure until now. She is the
Title:  daughter of an old and failing man, whose days are near their close. She has
Title:  many, very many, to love her, and delight in her; and she is too good, much
Title:  too precious, to become the victim of that villain.
Title:  
Title:  I know that the pale faces are a proud and hungry race. I know that they
Title:  claim not only to have the earth, but that the meanest of their color is
Title:  better than the Sachems of the red man. The dogs and crows of their tribes,
Title:  continued the earnest old chieftain, without heeding the wounded spirit of
Title:  his listener, whose head was nearly crushed to the earth in shame, as he
Title:  proceeded, would bark and caw before they would take a woman to their
Title:  wigwams whose blood was not of the color of snow. But let them not boast
Title:  before the face of the Manitou too loud. They entered the land at the
Title:  rising, and may yet go off at the setting sun. I have often seen the locusts
Title:  strip the leaves from the trees, but the season of blossoms has always come
Title:  again.
Title:  
Title:  It is so, said Cora, drawing a long breath, as if reviving from a trance,
Title:  raising her face, and shaking back her shining veil, with a kindling eye,
Title:  that contradicted the death-like paleness of her countenance; but why - it
Title:  is not permitted us to inquire. There is yet one of thine own people who has
Title:  not been brought before thee; before thou lettest the Huron depart in
Title:  triumph, hear him speak.
Title:  
Title:  Observing Tamenund to look about him doubtingly, one of his companions said:
Title:  
Title:  It is a snake - a red-skin in the pay of the Yengeese. We keep him for the
Title:  torture.
Title:  
Title:  Let him come, returned the sage.
Title:  
Title:  Then Tamenund once more sank into his seat, and a silence so deep prevailed
Title:  while the young man prepared to obey his simple mandate, that the leaves,
Title:  which fluttered in the draught of the light morning air, were distinctly
Title:  heard rustling in the surrounding forest.
Title:  
Title:  -----------------------
Title:  
Title:  1 William Penn was termed Minquon by the Delawares, and, as he never used
Title:  violence or injustice in his dealings with them, his reputation for probity
Title:  passed into a proverb. The American is justly proud of the origin of his
Title:  nation, which is perhaps unequaled in the history of the world; but the
Title:  Pennsylvanian and Jerseyman have more reason to value themselves in their
Title:  ancestors than the natives of any other state, since no wrong was done the
Title:  original owners of the soil.
