Title:  
Title:  Chapter 30
Title:  
Title:       Shylock: If you deny me, fie upon your law!
Title:       There is no force in the decrees of Venice:
Title:       I stand for judgment: answer, shall I have it?
Title:  
Title:                                                      MERCHANT OF VENICE
Title:  
Title:  The silence continued unbroken by human sounds for many anxious minutes.
Title:  Then the waving multitude opened and shut again, and Uncas stood in the
Title:  living circle. All those eyes, which had been curiously studying the
Title:  lineaments of the sage, as the source of their own intelligence, turned on
Title:  the instant, and were now bent in secret admiration on the erect, agile, and
Title:  faultless person of the captive. But neither the presence in which he found
Title:  himself, nor the exclusive attention that he attracted, in any manner
Title:  disturbed the self-possession of the young Mohican. He cast a deliberate and
Title:  observing look on every side of him, meeting the settled expression of
Title:  hostility that lowered in the visages of the chiefs with the same calmness
Title:  as the curious gaze of the attentive children. But when, last in this
Title:  haughty scrutiny, the person of Tamenund came under his glance, his eye
Title:  became fixed, as though all other objects were already forgotten. Then,
Title:  advancing with a slow and noiseless step up the area, he placed himself
Title:  immediately before the footstool of the sage. Here he stood unnoted, though
Title:  keenly observant himself, until one of the chiefs apprised the latter of his
Title:  presence.
Title:  
Title:  With what tongue does the prisoner speak to the Manitou? demanded the
Title:  patriarch, without unclosing his eyes.
Title:  
Title:  Like his fathers, Uncas replied; with the tongue of a Delaware.
Title:  
Title:  At this sudden and unexpected annunciation, a low, fierce yell ran through
Title:  the multitude, that might not inaptly be compared to the growl of the lion,
Title:  as his choler is first awakened - a fearful omen of the weight of his future
Title:  anger. The effect was equally strong on the sage, though differently
Title:  exhibited. He passed a hand before his eyes, as if to exclude the least
Title:  evidence of so shameful a spectacle, while he repeated, in his low, guttural
Title:  tones, the words he had just heard.
Title:  
Title:  A Delaware! I have lived to see the tribes of the Lenape driven from their
Title:  council-fires, and scattered, like broken herds of deer, among the hills of
Title:  the Iroquois! I have seen the hatchets of a strong people sweep woods from
Title:  the valleys, that the winds of heaven have spared! The beasts that run on
Title:  the mountains, and the birds that fly above the trees, have I seen living in
Title:  the wigwams of men; but never before have I found a Delaware so base as to
Title:  creep, like a poisonous serpent, into the camps of his nation.
Title:  
Title:  The singing-birds have opened their bills, returned Uncas, in the softest
Title:  notes of his own musical voice; and Tamenund has heard their song.
Title:  
Title:  The sage started, and bent his head aside, as if to catch the fleeting
Title:  sounds of some passing melody.
Title:  
Title:  Does Tamenund dream! he exclaimed. What voice is at his ear! Have the
Title:  winters gone backward! Will summer come again to the children of the Lenape!
Title:  
Title:  A solemn and respectful silence succeeded this incoherent burst from the
Title:  lips of the Delaware prophet. His people readily constructed his
Title:  unintelligible language into one of those mysterious conferences he was
Title:  believed to hold so frequently with a superior intelligence and they awaited
Title:  the issue of the revelation in awe. After a patient pause, however, one of
Title:  the aged men, perceiving that the sage had lost the recollection of the
Title:  subject before them, ventured to remind him again of the presence of the
Title:  prisoner.
Title:  
Title:  The false Delaware trembles lest he should hear the words of Tamenund, he
Title:  said. 'Tis a hound that howls, when the Yengeese show him a trail.
Title:  
Title:  And ye, returned Uncas, looking sternly around him, are dogs that whine,
Title:  when the Frenchman casts ye the offals of his deer!
Title:  
Title:  Twenty knives gleamed in the air, and as many warriors sprang to their feet,
Title:  at this biting, and perhaps merited retort; but a motion from one of the
Title:  chiefs suppressed the outbreaking of their tempers, and restored the
Title:  appearance of quiet. The task might probably have been more difficult, had
Title:  not a movement made by Tamenund indicated that he was again about to speak.
Title:  
Title:  Delaware! resumed the sage, little art thou worthy of thy name. My people
Title:  have not seen a bright sun in many winters; and the warrior who deserts his
Title:  tribe when hid in clouds is doubly a traitor. The law of the Manitou is
Title:  just. It is so; while the rivers run and the mountains stand, while the
Title:  blossoms come and go on the trees, it must be so. He is thine, my children;
Title:  deal justly by him.
Title:  
Title:  Not a limb was moved, nor was a breath drawn louder and longer than common,
Title:  until the closing syllable of this final decree had passed the lips of
Title:  Tamenund. Then a cry of vengeance burst at once, as it might be, from the
Title:  united lips of the nation; a frightful augury of their ruthless intentions.
Title:  In the midst of these prolonged and savage yells, a chief proclaimed, in a
Title:  high voice, that the captive was condemned to endure the dreadful trial of
Title:  torture by fire. The circle broke its order, and screams of delight mingled
Title:  with the bustle and tumult of preparation. Heyward struggled madly with his
Title:  captors; the anxious eye of Hawkeye began to look around him, with an
Title:  expression of peculiar earnestness; and Cora again threw herself at the feet
Title:  of the patriarch, once more a suppliant for mercy.
Title:  
Title:  Throughout the whole of these trying moments, Uncas had alone preserved his
Title:  serenity. He looked on the preparations with a steady eye, and when the
Title:  tormentors came to seize him, he met them with a firm and upright attitude.
Title:  One among them, if possible more fierce and savage than his fellows, seized
Title:  the hunting-shirt of the young warrior, and at a single effort tore it from
Title:  his body. Then, with a yell of frantic pleasure, he leaped toward his
Title:  unresisting victim and prepared to lead him to the stake. But, at that
Title:  moment, when he appeared most a stranger to the feelings of humanity, the
Title:  purpose of the savage was arrested as suddenly as if a supernatural agency
Title:  had interposed in the behalf of Uncas. The eyeballs of the Delaware seemed
Title:  to start from their sockets; his mouth opened and his whole form became
Title:  frozen in an attitude of amazement. Raising his hand with a slow and
Title:  regulated motion, he pointed with a finger to the bosom of the captive. His
Title:  companions crowded about him in wonder and every eye was like his own,
Title:  fastened intently on the figure of a small tortoise, beautifully tattooed on
Title:  the breast of the prisoner, in a bright blue tint.
Title:  
Title:  For a single instant Uncas enjoyed his triumph, smiling calmly on the scene.
Title:  Then motioning the crowd away with a high and haughty sweep of his arm, he
Title:  advanced in front of the nation with the air of a king, and spoke in a voice
Title:  louder than the murmur of admiration that ran through the multitude.
Title:  
Title:  Men of the Lenni Lenape! he said, my race upholds the earth! Your feeble
Title:  tribe stands on my shell! What fire that a Delaware can light would burn the
Title:  child of my fathers, he added, pointing proudly to the simple blazonry on
Title:  his skin; the blood that came from such a stock would smother your flames!
Title:  My race is the grandfather of nations!
Title:  
Title:  Who art thou? demanded Tamenund, rising at the startling tones he heard,
Title:  more than at any meaning conveyed by the language of the prisoner.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas, the son of Chingachgook, answered the captive modestly, turning from
Title:  the nation, and bending his head in reverence to the other's character and
Title:  years; a son of the great Unamis.1 The hour of Tamenund is nigh! exclaimed
Title:  the sage; the day is come, at last, to the night! I thank the Manitou, that
Title:  one is here to fill my place at the council-fire. Uncas, the child of Uncas,
Title:  is found! Let the eyes of a dying eagle gaze on the rising sun.
Title:  
Title:  The youth stepped lightly, but proudly on the platform, where he became
Title:  visible to the whole agitated and wondering multitude. Tamenund held him
Title:  long at the length of his arm and read every turn in the fine lineaments of
Title:  his countenance, with the untiring gaze of one who recalled days of
Title:  happiness.
Title:  
Title:  Is Tamenund a boy? at length the bewildered prophet exclaimed. Have I
Title:  dreamed of so many snows - that my people were scattered like floating sands
Title:  - of Yengeese, more plenty than the leaves on the trees! The arrow of
Title:  Tamenund would not frighten the fawn; his arm if withered like the branch of
Title:  a dead oak; the snail would be swifter in the race; yet is Uncas before him
Title:  as they went to battle against the pale faces! Uncas, the panther of his
Title:  tribe, the eldest son of the Lenape, the wisest Sagamore of the Mohicans!
Title:  Tell me, ye Delawares has Tamenund been a sleeper for a hundred winters?
Title:  
Title:  The calm and deep silence which succeeded these words sufficiently anounced
Title:  the awful reverence with which his people received the communication of the
Title:  patriarch. None dared to answer, though all listened in breathless
Title:  expectation of what might follow. Uncas, however, looking in his face with
Title:  the fondness and veneration of a favored child, presumed on his own high and
Title:  acknowledged rank, to reply.
Title:  
Title:  Four warriors of his race have lived and died, he said, since the friend of
Title:  Tamenund led his people in battle. The blood of the turtle has been in many
Title:  chiefs, but all have gone back into the earth from whence they came, except
Title:  Chingachgook and his son.
Title:  
Title:  It is true - it is true, returned the sage, a flash of recollection
Title:  destroying all his pleasing fancies, and restoring him at once to a
Title:  consciousness of the true history of his nation. Our wise men have often
Title:  said that two warriors of the unchanged race were in the hills of the
Title:  Yengeese; why have their seats at the council-fires of the Delawares been so
Title:  long empty?
Title:  
Title:  At these words the young man raised his head, which he had still kept bowed
Title:  a little, in reverence; and lifting his voice so as to be heard by the
Title:  multitude, as if to explain at once and forever the policy of his family, he
Title:  said aloud:
Title:  
Title:  Once we slept where we could hear the salt lake speak in its anger. Then we
Title:  were rulers and Sagamores over the land. But when a pale face was seen on
Title:  every brook, we followed the deer back to the river of our nation. The
Title:  Delawares were gone. Few warriors of them all stayed to drink of the stream
Title:  they loved. Then said my fathers, Here will we hunt. The waters of the river
Title:  go into the salt lake. If we go toward the setting sun, we shall find
Title:  streams that run into the great lakes of sweet water; there would a Mohican
Title:  die, like fishes of the sea, in the clear springs. When the Manitou is ready
Title:  and shall say Come, we will follow the river to the sea, and take our own
Title:  again. Such, Delawares, is the belief of the children of the Turtle. Our
Title:  eyes are on the rising and not toward the setting sun. We know whence he
Title:  comes, but we know not whither he goes. It is enough.
Title:  
Title:  The men of the Lenape listened to his words with all the respect that
Title:  superstition could lend, finding a secret charm even in the figurative
Title:  language with which the young Sagamore imparted his ideas. Uncas himself
Title:  watched the effect of his brief explanation with intelligent eyes, and
Title:  gradually dropped the air of authority he had assumed, as he perceived that
Title:  his auditors were content. Then, permitting his looks to wander over the
Title:  silent throng that crowded around the elevated seat of Tamenund, he first
Title:  perceived Hawkeye in his bonds. Stepping eagerly from his stand, he made way
Title:  for himself to the side of his friend; and cutting his thongs with a quick
Title:  and angry stroke of his own knife, he motioned to the crowd to divide. The
Title:  Indians silently obeyed, and once more they stood ranged in their circle, as
Title:  before his appearance among them. Uncas took the scout by the hand, and led
Title:  him to the feet of the patriarch.
Title:  
Title:  Father, he said, look at this pale face; a just man, and the friend of the
Title:  Delawares.
Title:  
Title:  Is he a son of Minquon?
Title:  
Title:  Not so; a warrior known to the Yengeese, and feared by the Maquas.
Title:  
Title:  What name has he gained by his deeds?
Title:  
Title:  We call him Hawkeye, Uncas replied, using the Delaware phrase; for his sight
Title:  never fails. The Mingoes know him better by the death he gives their
Title:  warriors; with them he is The Long Rifle.
Title:  
Title:  La Longue Carabine! exclaimed Tamenund, opening his eyes, and regarding the
Title:  scout sternly. My son has not done well to call him friend.
Title:  
Title:  I call him so who proves himself such, returned the young chief, with great
Title:  calmness, but with a steady mien. If Uncas is welcome among the Delawares,
Title:  then is Hawkeye with his friends.
Title:  
Title:  The pale face has slain my young men; his name is great for the blows he has
Title:  struck the Lenape.
Title:  
Title:  If a Mingo has whispered that much in the ear of the Delaware, he has only
Title:  shown that he is a singing-bird, said the scout, who now believed that it
Title:  was time to vindicate himself from such offensive charges, and who spoke as
Title:  the man he addressed, modifying his Indian figures, however, with his own
Title:  peculiar notions. That I have slain the Maquas I am not the man to deny,
Title:  even at their own council-fires; but that, knowingly, my hand has never
Title:  harmed a Delaware, is opposed to the reason of my gifts, which is friendly
Title:  to them, and all that belongs to their nation.
Title:  
Title:  A low exclamation of applause passed among the warriors who exchanged looks
Title:  with each other like men that first began to perceive their error.
Title:  
Title:  Where is the Huron? demanded Tamenund. Has he stopped my ears?
Title:  
Title:  Magua, whose feelings during that scene in which Uncas had triumphed may be
Title:  much better imagined than described, answered to the call by stepping boldly
Title:  in front of the patriarch.
Title:  
Title:  The just Tamenund, he said, will not keep what a Huron has lent.
Title:  
Title:  Tell me, son of my brother, returned the sage, avoiding the dark countenance
Title:  of Le Subtil, and turning gladly to the more ingenuous features of Uncas,
Title:  has the stranger a conqueror's right over you?
Title:  
Title:  He has none. The panther may get into snares set by the women; but he is
Title:  strong, and knows how to leap through them.
Title:  
Title:  La Longue Carabine?
Title:  
Title:  Laughs at the Mingoes. Go, Huron, ask your squaws the color of a bear.
Title:  
Title:  The stranger and white maiden that come into my camp together?
Title:  
Title:  Should journey on an open path.
Title:  
Title:  And the woman that Huron left with my warriors?
Title:  
Title:  Uncas made no reply.
Title:  
Title:  And the woman that the Mingo has brought into my camp? repeated Tamenund,
Title:  gravely.
Title:  
Title:  She is mine, cried Magua, shaking his hand in triumph at Uncas. Mohican, you
Title:  know that she is mine.
Title:  
Title:  My son is silent, said Tamenund, endeavoring to read the expression of the
Title:  face that the youth turned from him in sorrow.
Title:  
Title:  It is so, was the low answer.
Title:  
Title:  A short and impressive pause succeeded, during which it was very apparent
Title:  with what reluctance the multitude admitted the justice of the Mingo's
Title:  claim. At length the sage, on whom alone the decision depended, said, in a
Title:  firm voice:
Title:  
Title:  Huron, depart.
Title:  
Title:  As he came, just Tamenund, demanded the wily Magua, or with hands filled
Title:  with the faith of the Delawares? The wigwam of Le Renard Subtil is empty.
Title:  Make him strong with his own.
Title:  
Title:  The aged man mused with himself for a time; and then, bending his head
Title:  toward one of his venerable companions, he asked:
Title:  
Title:  Are my ears open?
Title:  
Title:  It is true.
Title:  
Title:  Is this Mingo a chief?
Title:  
Title:  The first in his nation.
Title:  
Title:  Girl, what wouldst thou? A great warrior takes thee to wife. Go! thy race
Title:  will not end.
Title:  
Title:  Better, a thousand times, it should, exclaimed the horror-struck Cora, than
Title:  meet with such a degradation!
Title:  
Title:  Huron, her mind is in the tents of her fathers. An unwilling maiden makes an
Title:  unhappy wigwam.
Title:  
Title:  She speaks with the tongue of her people, returned Magua, regarding his
Title:  victim with a look of bitter irony.
Title:  
Title:  She is of a race of traders, and will bargain for a bright look. Let
Title:  Tamenund speak the words.
Title:  
Title:  Take you the wampum, and our love.
Title:  
Title:  Nothing hence but what Magua brought hither.
Title:  
Title:  Then depart with thine own. The Great Manitou forbids that a Delaware should
Title:  be unjust.
Title:  
Title:  Magua advanced, and seized his captive strongly by the arm; the Delawares
Title:  fell back, in silence; and Cora, as if conscious that remonstrance would be
Title:  useless, prepared to submit to her fate without resistance.
Title:  
Title:  Hold, hold! cried Duncan, springing forward; Huron, have mercy! her ransom
Title:  shall make thee richer than any of thy people were ever yet known to be.
Title:  
Title:  Magua is a red-skin; he wants not the beads of the pale faces.
Title:  
Title:  Gold, silver, powder, lead - all that a warrior needs shall be in thy
Title:  wigwam; all that becomes the greatest chief.
Title:  
Title:  Le Subtil is very strong, cried Magua, violently shaking the hand which
Title:  grasped the unresisting arm of Cora; he has his revenge!
Title:  
Title:  Mighty ruler of Providence! exclaimed Heyward, clasping his hands together
Title:  in agony, can this be suffered! To you, just Tamenund, I appeal for mercy.
Title:  
Title:  The words of the Delaware are said, returned the sage, closing his eyes, and
Title:  dropping back into his seat, alike wearied with his mental and his bodily
Title:  exertion. Men speak not twice.
Title:  
Title:  That a chief should not misspend his time in unsaying what has once been
Title:  spoken is wise and reasonable, said Hawkeye, motioning to Duncan to be
Title:  silent; but it is also prudent in every warrior to consider well before he
Title:  strikes his tomahawk into the head of his prisoner. Huron, I love you not;
Title:  nor can I say that any Mingo has ever received much favor at my hands. It is
Title:  fair to conclude that, if this war does not soon end, many more of your
Title:  warriors will meet me in the woods. Put it to your judgment, then, whether
Title:  you would prefer taking such a prisoner as that into your encampment, or one
Title:  like myself, who am a man that it would greatly rejoice your nation to see
Title:  with naked hands.
Title:  
Title:  Will The Long Rifle give his life for the woman? demanded Magua,
Title:  hesitatingly; for he had already made a motion toward quitting the place
Title:  with his victim.
Title:  
Title:  No, no; I have not said so much as that, returned Hawkeye, drawing back with
Title:  suitable discretion, when he noted the eagerness with which Magua listened
Title:  to his proposal. It would be an unequal exchange, to give a warrior, in the
Title:  prime of his age and usefulness, for the best woman on the frontiers. I
Title:  might consent to go into winter quarters, now - at least six weeks afore the
Title:  leaves will turn - on condition you will release the maiden.
Title:  
Title:  Magua shook his head, and made an impatient sign for the crowd to open.
Title:  
Title:  Well, then, added the scout, with the musing air of a man who had not half
Title:  made up his mind; I will throw killdeer into the bargain. Take the word of
Title:  an experienced hunter, the piece has not its equal atween the provinces.
Title:  
Title:  Magua still disdained to reply, continuing his efforts to disperse the
Title:  crowd.
Title:  
Title:  Perhaps, added the scout, losing his dissembled coolness exactly in
Title:  proportion as the other manifested an indifference to the exchange, if I
Title:  should condition to teach your young men the real virtue of the we'pon, it
Title:  would smoothe the little differences in our judgments.
Title:  
Title:  Le Renard fiercely ordered the Delawares, who still lingered in an
Title:  impenetrable belt around him, in hopes he would listen to the amicable
Title:  proposal, to open his path, threatening, by the glance of his eye, another
Title:  appeal to the infallible justice of their prophet.
Title:  
Title:  What is ordered must sooner or later arrive, continued Hawkeye, turning with
Title:  a sad and humbled look to Uncas. The varlet knows his advantage and will
Title:  keep it! God bless you, boy; you have found friends among your natural kin,
Title:  and I hope they will prove as true as some you have met who had no Indian
Title:  cross. As for me, sooner or later, I must die; it is, therefore, fortunate
Title:  there are but few to make my death-howl. After all, it is likely the imps
Title:  would have managed to master my scalp, so a day or two will make no great
Title:  difference in the everlasting reckoning of time. God bless you, added the
Title:  rugged woodsman, bending his head aside, and then instantly changing its
Title:  direction again, with a wistful look toward the youth; I loved both you and
Title:  your father, Uncas, though our skins are not altogether of a color, and our
Title:  gifts are somewhat difficult. Tell the Sagamore I never lost sight of him in
Title:  my greatest trouble; and, as for you, think of me sometimes when on a lucky
Title:  trail, and depend on it, boy, whether there be one heaven or two, there is a
Title:  path in the other world by which honest men may come together again. You'll
Title:  find the rifle in the place we hid it; take it, and keep it for my sake;
Title:  and, harkee, lad, as your natural gifts don't deny you the use of vengeance,
Title:  use it a little freely on the Mingoes; it may unburden griefs at my loss,
Title:  and ease your mind. Huron, I accept your offer; release the woman. I am your
Title:  prisoner!
Title:  
Title:  A suppressed, but still distinct murmur of approbation ran through the crowd
Title:  at this generous proposition; even the fiercest among the Delaware warriors
Title:  manifesting pleasure at the manliness of the intended sacrifice. Magua
Title:  paused, and for an anxious moment, it might be said, he doubted; then,
Title:  casting his eyes on Cora, with an expression in which ferocity and
Title:  admiration were strangely mingled, his purpose became fixed forever.
Title:  
Title:  He intimated his contempt of the offer with a backward motion of his head,
Title:  and said, in a steady and settled voice:
Title:  
Title:  Le Renard Subtil is a great chief; he has but one mind. Come, he added,
Title:  laying his hand too familiarly on the shoulder of his captive to urge her
Title:  onward; a Huron is no tattler; we will go.
Title:  
Title:  The maiden drew back in lofty womanly reserve, and her dark eye kindled,
Title:  while the rich blood shot, like the passing brightness of the sun, into her
Title:  very temples, at the indignity.
Title:  
Title:  I am your prisoner, and, at a fitting time shall be ready to follow, even to
Title:  my death. But violence is unnecessary, she coldly said; and immediately
Title:  turning to Hawkeye, added: Generous hunter! from my soul I thank you. Your
Title:  offer is vain, neither could it be accepted; but still you may serve me,
Title:  even more than in your own noble intention. Look at that drooping humbled
Title:  child! Abandon her not until you leave her in the habitations of civilized
Title:  men. I will not say, wringing the hard hand of the scout, that her father
Title:  will reward you - for such as you are above the rewards of men - but he will
Title:  thank you and bless you. And, believe me, the blessing of a just and aged
Title:  man has virtue in the sight of Heaven. Would to God I could hear one word
Title:  from his lips at this awful moment! Her voice became choked, and, for an
Title:  instant, she was silent; then, advancing a step nigher to Duncan, who was
Title:  supporting her unconscious sister, she continued, in more subdued tones, but
Title:  in which feeling and the habits of her sex maintained a fearful struggle: I
Title:  need not tell you to cherish the treasure you will possess. You love her,
Title:  Heyward; that would conceal a thousand faults, though she had them. She is
Title:  kind, gentle, sweet, good, as mortal may be. There is not a blemish in mind
Title:  or person at which the proudest of you all would sicken. She is fair - oh!
Title:  how surpassingly fair! laying her own beautiful, but less brilliant, hand in
Title:  melancholy affection on the alabaster forehead of Alice, and parting the
Title:  golden hair which clustered about her brows; and yet her soul is pure and
Title:  spotless as her skin! I could say much - more, perhaps, than cooler reason
Title:  would approve; but I will spare you and myself - Her voice became inaudible,
Title:  and her face was bent over the form of her sister. After a long and burning
Title:  kiss, she arose, and with features of the hue of death, but without even a
Title:  tear in her feverish eye, she turned away, and added, to the savage, with
Title:  all her former elevation of manner: Now, sir, if it be your pleasure, I will
Title:  follow.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, go, cried Duncan, placing Alice in the arms of an Indian girl; go,
Title:  Magua, go. these Delawares have their laws, which forbid them to detain you;
Title:  but I - I have no such obligation. Go, malignant monster - why do you delay?
Title:  
Title:  It would be difficult to describe the expression with which Magua listened
Title:  to this threat to follow. There was at first a fierce and manifest display
Title:  of joy, and then it was instantly subdued in a look of cunning coldness.
Title:  
Title:  The words are open, he was content with answering, The Open Hand can come.
Title:  
Title:  Hold, cried Hawkeye, seizing Duncan by the arm, and detaining him by
Title:  violence; you know not the craft of the imp. He would lead you to an
Title:  ambushment, and your death -
Title:  
Title:  Huron, interrupted Uncas, who submissive to the stern customs of his people,
Title:  had been an attentive and grave listener to all that passed; Huron, the
Title:  justice of the Delawares comes from the Manitou. Look at the sun. He is now
Title:  in the upper branches of the hemlock. Your path is short and open. When he
Title:  is seen above the trees, there will be men on your trail.
Title:  
Title:  I hear a crow! exclaimed Magua, with a taunting laugh. Go! he added, shaking
Title:  his hand at the crowd, which had slowly opened to admit his passage. Where
Title:  are the petticoats of the Delawares! Let them send their arrows and their
Title:  guns to the Wyandots; they shall have venison to eat, and corn to hoe. Dogs,
Title:  rabbits, thieves - I spit on you!
Title:  
Title:  His parting gibes were listened to in a dead, boding silence, and, with
Title:  these biting words in his mouth, the triumphant Magua passed unmolested into
Title:  the forest, followed by his passive captive, and protected by the inviolable
Title:  laws of Indian hospitality.

Title:  
Title:  Chapter 31
Title:  
Title:       Fluellen: Kill the poys and the luggage! 'Tis expressly against
Title:       the law of arms; 'tis as arrant a piece of knavery, mark you now,
Title:       as can be offered in the 'orld
Title:  
Title:                                                            KING HENRY V
Title:  
Title:  So long as their enemy and his victim continued in sight, the multitude
Title:  remained motionless as beings charmed to the place by some power that was
Title:  friendly to the Huron; but, the instant he disappeared, it became tossed and
Title:  agitated by fierce and powerful passion. Uncas maintained his elevated
Title:  stand, keeping his eyes on the form of Cora, until the colors of her dress
Title:  were blended with the foliage of the forest; when he descended, and, moving
Title:  silently through the throng, he disappeared in that lodge from which he had
Title:  so recently issued. A few of the graver and more attentive warriors, who
Title:  caught the gleams of anger that shot from the eyes of the young chief in
Title:  passing, followed him to the place he had selected for his meditations.
Title:  After which, Tamenund and Alice were removed, and the women and children
Title:  were ordered to disperse. During the momentous hour that succeeded, the
Title:  encampment resembled a hive of troubled bees, who only awaited the
Title:  appearance and example of their leader to take some distant and momentous
Title:  flight.
Title:  
Title:  A young warrior at length issued from the lodge of Uncas; and, moving
Title:  deliberately, with a sort of grave march, toward a dwarf pine that grew in
Title:  the crevices of the rocky terrace, he tore the bark from its body, and then
Title:  turned whence he came without speaking. He was soon followed by another, who
Title:  stripped the sapling of its branches, leaving it a naked and blazed1 trunk.
Title:  A third colored the post with stripes of a dark red paint; all which
Title:  indications of a hostile design in the leaders of the nation were received
Title:  by the men without in a gloomy and ominous silence. Finally, the Mohican
Title:  himself reappeared, divested of all his attire, except his girdle and
Title:  leggings, and with one-half of his fine features hid under a cloud of
Title:  threatening black.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas moved with a slow and dignified tread toward the post, which he
Title:  immediately commenced encircling with a measured step, not unlike an ancient
Title:  dance, raising his voice, at the same time, in the wild and irregular chant
Title:  of his war song. The notes were in the extremes of human sounds; being
Title:  sometimes melancholy and exquisitely plaintive, even rivaling the melody of
Title:  birds - and then, by sudden and startling transitions, causing the auditors
Title:  to tremble by their depth and energy. The words were few and often repeated,
Title:  proceeding gradually from a sort of invocation, or hymn, to the Deity, to an
Title:  intimation of the warrior's object, and terminating as they commenced with
Title:  an acknowledgment of his own dependence on the Great Spirit. If it were
Title:  possible to translate the comprehensive and melodious language in which he
Title:  spoke, the ode might read something like the following:
Title:  
Title:       Manitou! Manitou! Manitou!
Title:       Thou art great, thou art good, thou art wise:
Title:       Manitou! Manitou!
Title:       Thou art just.
Title:  
Title:       In the heavens, in the clouds, oh, I see
Title:       Many spots - many dark, many red:
Title:       In the heavens, oh, I see
Title:       Many clouds.
Title:  
Title:       In the woods, in the air, oh, I hear
Title:       The whoop, the long yell, and the cry:
Title:       In the woods, oh, I hear
Title:       The loud whoop!
Title:  
Title:       Manitou! Manitou! Manitou!
Title:       I am weak - thou art strong; I am slow -
Title:       Manitou! Manitou!
Title:       Give me aid.
Title:  
Title:  At the end of what might be called each verse he made a pause, by raising a
Title:  note louder and longer than common, that was peculiarly suited to the
Title:  sentiment just expressed. The first close was solemn, and intended to convey
Title:  the idea of veneration; the second descriptive, bordering on the alarming;
Title:  and the third was the well-known and terrific war-whoop, which burst from
Title:  the lips of the young warrior, like a combination of all the frightful
Title:  sounds of battle. The last was like the first, humble and imploring. Three
Title:  times did he repeat this song, and as often did he encircle the post in his
Title:  dance.
Title:  
Title:  At the close of the first turn, a grave and highly esteemed chief of the
Title:  Lenape followed his example, singing words of his own, however, to music of
Title:  a similar character. Warrior after warrior enlisted in the dance, until all
Title:  of any renown and authority were numbered in its mazes. The spectacle now
Title:  became wildly terrific; the fierce-looking and menacing visages of the
Title:  chiefs receiving additional power from the appalling strains in which they
Title:  mingled their guttural tones. Just then Uncas struck his tomahawk deep into
Title:  the post, and raised his voice in a shout, which might be termed his own
Title:  battle cry. The act anounced that he had assumed the chief authority in the
Title:  intended expedition.
Title:  
Title:  It was a signal that awakened all the slumbering passions of the nation. A
Title:  hundred youths, who had hitherto been restrained by the diffidence of their
Title:  years, rushed in a frantic body on the fancied emblem of their enemy, and
Title:  severed it asunder, splinter by splinter, until nothing remained of the
Title:  trunk but its roots in the earth. During this moment of tumult, the most
Title:  ruthless deeds of war were performed on the fragments of the tree, with as
Title:  much apparent ferocity as if they were the living victims of their cruelty.
Title:  Some were scalped; some received the keen and trembling axe; and others
Title:  suffered by thrusts from the fatal knife. In short, the manifestations of
Title:  zeal and fierce delight were so great and unequivocal, that the expedition
Title:  was declared to be a war of the nation.
Title:  
Title:  The instant Uncas had struck the blow, he moved out of the circle, and cast
Title:  his eyes up to the sun, which was just gaining the point, when the truce
Title:  with Magua was to end. The fact was soon announced by a significant gesture,
Title:  accompanied by a corresponding cry; and the whole of the excited multitude
Title:  abandoned their mimic warfare, with shrill yells of pleasure, to prepare for
Title:  the more hazardous experiment of the reality.
Title:  
Title:  The whole face of the encampment was instantly changed. The warriors, who
Title:  were already armed and painted, became as still as if they were incapable of
Title:  any uncommon burst of emotion. On the other hand, the women broke out of the
Title:  lodges, with the songs of joy and those of lamentation so strangely mixed
Title:  that it might have been difficult to have said which passion preponderated.
Title:  None, however, was idle. Some bore their choicest articles, others their
Title:  young, and some their aged and infirm, into the forest, which spread itself
Title:  like a verdant carpet of bright green against the side of the mountain.
Title:  Thither Tamenund also retired, with calm composure, after a short and
Title:  touching interview with Uncas; from whom the sage separated with the
Title:  reluctance that a parent would quit a long lost and just recovered child. In
Title:  the meantime, Duncan saw Alice to a place of safety, and then sought the
Title:  scout, with a countenance that denoted how eagerly he also panted for the
Title:  approaching contest.
Title:  
Title:  But Hawkeye was too much accustomed to the war song and the enlistments of
Title:  the natives, to betray any interest in the passing scene. He merely cast an
Title:  occasional look at the number and quality of the warriors, who, from time to
Title:  time, signified their readiness to accompany Uncas to the field. In this
Title:  particular he was soon satisfied; for, as has been already seen, the power
Title:  of the young chief quickly embraced every fighting man in the nation. After
Title:  this material point was so satisfactorily decided, he despatched an Indian
Title:  boy in quest of killdeer and the rifle of Uncas, to the place where they had
Title:  deposited their weapons on approaching the camp of the Delawares; a measure
Title:  of double policy, inasmuch as it protected the arms from their own fate, if
Title:  detained as prisoners, and gave them the advantage of appearing among the
Title:  strangers rather as sufferers than as men provided with means of defense and
Title:  subsistence. In selecting another to perform the office of reclaiming his
Title:  highly prized rifle, the scout had lost sight of none of his habitual
Title:  caution. He knew that Magua had not come unattended, and he also knew that
Title:  Huron spies watched the movements of their new enemies, along the whole
Title:  boundary of the woods. It would, therefore, have been fatal to himself to
Title:  have attempted the experiment; a warrior would have fared no better; but the
Title:  danger of a boy would not be likely to commence until after his object was
Title:  discovered. When Heyward joined him, the scout was coolly awaiting the
Title:  result of this experiment.
Title:  
Title:  The boy , who had been well instructed, and was sufficiently crafty,
Title:  proceeded, with a bosom that was swelling with the pride of such a
Title:  confidence, and all the hopes of young ambition, carelessly across the
Title:  clearing to the wood, which he entered at a point at some little distance
Title:  from the place where the guns were secreted. The instant, however, he was
Title:  concealed by the foliage of the bushes, his dusky form was to be seen
Title:  gliding, like that of a serpent, toward the desired treasure. He was
Title:  successful; and in another moment he appeared flying across the narrow
Title:  opening that skirted the base of the terrace on which the village stood,
Title:  with the velocity of an arrow, and bearing a prize in each hand. He had
Title:  actually gained the crags, and was leaping up their sides with incredible
Title:  activity, when a shot from the woods showed how accurate had been the
Title:  judgment of the scout. The boy answered it with a feeble but contemptuous
Title:  shout; and immediately a second bullet was sent after him from another part
Title:  of the cover. At the next instant he appeared on the level above, elevating
Title:  his guns in triumph, while he moved with the air of a conqueror toward the
Title:  renowned hunter who had honored him by so glorious a commission.
Title:  
Title:  Notwithstanding the lively interest Hawkeye had taken in the fate of his
Title:  messenger, he received killdeer with a satisfaction that, momentarily, drove
Title:  all other recollections from his mind. After examining the piece with an
Title:  intelligent eye, and opening and shutting the pan some ten or fifteen times,
Title:  and trying sundry other equally important experiments on the lock, he turned
Title:  to the boy and demanded with great manifestations of kindness, if he was
Title:  hurt. The urchin looked proudly up in his face, but made no reply.
Title:  
Title:  Ah! I see, lad, the knaves have barked your arm! added the scout, taking up
Title:  the limb of the patient sufferer, across which a deep flesh wound had been
Title:  made by one of the bullets; but a little bruised alder will act like a
Title:  charm. In the meantime I will wrap it in a badge of wampum! You have
Title:  commenced the business of a warrior early, my brave boy, and are likely to
Title:  bear a plenty of honorable scars to your grave. I know many young men that
Title:  have taken scalps who cannot show such a mark as this. Go! having bound up
Title:  the arm; you will be a chief!
Title:  
Title:  The lad departed, prouder of his flowing blood than the vainest courtier
Title:  could be of his blushing ribbon; and stalked among the fellows of his age,
Title:  an object of general admiration and envy.
Title:  
Title:  But, in a moment of so many serious and important duties, this single act of
Title:  juvenile fortitude did not attract the general notice and commendation it
Title:  would have received under milder auspices. It had, however, served to
Title:  apprise the Delawares of the position and the intentions of their enemies.
Title:  Accordingly a party of adventurers, better suited to the task than the weak
Title:  though spirited boy, was ordered to dislodge the skulkers. The duty was soon
Title:  performed; for most of the Hurons retired of themselves when they found they
Title:  had been discovered. The Delawares followed to a sufficient distance from
Title:  their own encampment, and then halted for orders, apprehensive of being led
Title:  into an ambush. As both parties secreted themselves, the woods were again as
Title:  still and quiet as a mild summer morning and deep solitude could render
Title:  them.
Title:  
Title:  The calm but still impatient Uncas now collected his chiefs, and divided his
Title:  power. He presented Hawkeye as a warrior, often tried, and always found
Title:  deserving of confidence. When he found his friend met with a favorable
Title:  reception, he bestowed on him the command of twenty men, like himself,
Title:  active, skilful and resolute. He gave the Delawares to understand the rank
Title:  of Heyward among the troops of the Yengeese, and then tendered to him a
Title:  trust of equal authority. But Duncan declined the charge, professing his
Title:  readiness to serve as a volunteer by the side of the scout. After this
Title:  disposition, the young Mohican appointed various native chiefs to fill the
Title:  different situations of responsibility, and, the time pressing, he gave
Title:  forth the word to march. He was cheerfully, but silently obeyed by more than
Title:  two hundred men.
Title:  
Title:  Their entrance into the forest was perfectly unmolested; nor did they
Title:  encounter any living objects that could either give the alarm, or furnish
Title:  the intelligence they needed, until they came upon the lairs of their own
Title:  scouts. Here a halt was ordered, and the chiefs were assembled to hold a
Title:  whispering council.
Title:  
Title:  At this meeting divers plans of operation were suggested, though none of a
Title:  character to meet the wishes of their ardent leader. Had Uncas followed the
Title:  promptings of his own inclinations, he would have led his followers to the
Title:  charge without a moment's delay, and put the conflict to the hazard of an
Title:  instant issue; but such a course would have been in opposition to all the
Title:  received practises and opinions of his countrymen. He was, therefore, fain
Title:  to adopt a caution that in the present temper of his mind he execrated, and
Title:  to listen to advice at which his fiery spirit chafed, under the vivid
Title:  recollection of Cora's danger and Magua's insolence.
Title:  
Title:  After an unsatisfactory conference of many minutes, a solitary individual
Title:  was seen advancing from the side of the enemy, with such apparent haste, as
Title:  to induce the belief he might be a messenger charged with pacific overtures.
Title:  When within a hundred yards, however, of the cover behind which the Delaware
Title:  council had assembled, the stranger hesitated, appeared uncertain what
Title:  course to take, and finally halted. All eyes were turned now on Uncas, as if
Title:  seeking directions how to proceed.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye, said the young chief, in a low voice, he must never speak to the
Title:  Hurons again.
Title:  
Title:  His time has come, said the laconic scout, thrusting the long barrel of his
Title:  rifle through the leaves, and taking his deliberate and fatal aim. But,
Title:  instead of pulling the trigger, he lowered the muzzle again, and indulged
Title:  himself in a fit of his peculiar mirth. I took the imp for a Mingo, as I'm a
Title:  miserable sinner! he said; but when my eye ranged along his ribs for a place
Title:  to get the bullet in - would you think it, Uncas - I saw the musicianer's
Title:  blower; and so, after all, it is the man they call Gamut, whose death can
Title:  profit no one, and whose life, if this tongue can do anything but sing, may
Title:  be made serviceable to our own ends. If sounds have not lost their virtue,
Title:  I'll soon have a discourse with the honest fellow, and that in a voice he'll
Title:  find more agreeable than the speech of killdeer.
Title:  
Title:  So saying, Hawkeye laid aside his rifle; and, crawling through the bushes
Title:  until within hearing of David, he attempted to repeat the musical effort,
Title:  which had conducted himself, with so much safety and eclat, through the
Title:  Huron encampment. The exquisite organs of Gamut could not readily be
Title:  deceived (and, to say the truth, it would have been difficult for any other
Title:  than Hawkeye to produce a similar noise), and, consequently, having once
Title:  before heard the sounds, he now knew whence they proceeded. The poor fellow
Title:  appeared relieved from a state of great embarrassment; for, pursuing the
Title:  direction of the voice - a task that to him was not much less arduous that
Title:  it would have been to have gone up in the face of a battery - he soon
Title:  discovered the hidden songster.
Title:  
Title:  I wonder what the Hurons will think of that! said the scout, laughing, as he
Title:  took his companion by the arm, and urged him toward the rear. If the knaves
Title:  lie within earshot, they will say there are two non-compossers instead of
Title:  one! But here we are safe, he added, pointing to Uncas and his associates.
Title:  Now give us the history of the Mingo inventions in natural English, and
Title:  without any ups and downs of voice.
Title:  
Title:  David gazed about him, at the fierce and wild-looking chiefs, in mute
Title:  wonder; but assured by the presence of faces that he knew, he soon rallied
Title:  his faculties so far as to make an intelligent reply.
Title:  
Title:  The heathen are abroad in goodly numbers, said David; and, I fear, with evil
Title:  intent. There has been much howling and ungodly revelry, together with such
Title:  sounds as it is profanity to utter, in their habitations within the past
Title:  hour, so much so, in truth, that I have fled to the Delawares in search of
Title:  peace.
Title:  
Title:  Your ears might not have profited much by the exchange, had you been quicker
Title:  of foot, returned the scout a little dryly. But let that be as it may; where
Title:  are the Hurons?
Title:  
Title:  They lie hid in the forest, between this spot and their village in such
Title:  force, that prudence would teach you instantly to return.
Title:  
Title:  Uncas cast a glance along the range of trees which concealed his own band
Title:  and mentioned the name of:
Title:  
Title:  Magua?
Title:  
Title:  Is among them. He brought in the maiden that had sojourned with the
Title:  Delawares; and, leaving her in the cave, has put himself, like a raging
Title:  wolf, at the head of his savages. I know not what has troubled his spirit so
Title:  greatly!
Title:  
Title:  He has left her, you say, in the cave! interrupted Heyward; 'tis well that
Title:  we know its situation! May not something be done for her instant relief?
Title:  
Title:  Uncas looked earnestly at the scout, before he asked:
Title:  
Title:  What says Hawkeye?
Title:  
Title:  Give me twenty rifles, and I will turn to the right, along the stream; and,
Title:  passing by the huts of the beaver, will join the Sagamore and the colonel.
Title:  You shall then hear the whoop from that quarter; with this wind one may
Title:  easily send it a mile. Then, Uncas, do you drive in the front; when they
Title:  come within range of our pieces, we will give them a blow that, I pledge the
Title:  good name of an old frontiersman, shall make their line bend like an ashen
Title:  bow. After which, we will carry the village, and take the woman from the
Title:  cave; when the affair may be finished with the tribe, according to a white
Title:  man's battle, by a blow and a victory; or, in the Indian fashion, with dodge
Title:  and cover. There may be no great learning, major, in this plan, but with
Title:  courage and patience it can all be done.
Title:  
Title:  I like it very much, cried Duncan, who saw that the release of Cora was the
Title:  primary object in the mind of the scout; I like it much. Let it be instantly
Title:  attempted.
Title:  
Title:  After a short conference, the plan was matured, and rendered more
Title:  intelligible to the several parties; the different signals were appointed,
Title:  and the chiefs separated, each to his allotted station.
Title:

Title:  1 A tree which has been partially or entirely stripped of its bark is said,
Title:  in the language of the country, to be blazed. The term is strictly English,
Title:  for a horse is said to be blazed when it has a white mark.

Title:  Chapter 32
Title:  
Title:       But plagues shall spread, and funeral fires increase,
Title:       Till the great king, without a ransom paid,
Title:       To her own Chrysa send the black-eyed maid.
