Title:                                                                    POPE
Title:  
Title:  During the time Uncas was making this disposition of his forces, the woods
Title:  were as still, and, with the exception of those who had met in council,
Title:  apparently as much untenanted as when they came fresh from the hands of
Title:  their Almighty Creator. The eye could range, in every direction, through the
Title:  long and shadowed vistas of the trees; but nowhere was any object to be seen
Title:  that did not properly belong to the peaceful and slumbering scenery.
Title:  
Title:  Here and there a bird was heard fluttering among the branches of the
Title:  beeches, and occasionally a squirrel dropped a nut, drawing the startled
Title:  looks of the party for a moment to the place; but the instant the casual
Title:  interruption ceased, the passing air was heard murmuring above their heads,
Title:  along that verdant and undulating surface of forest, which spread itself
Title:  unbroken, unless by stream or lake, over such a vast region of country.
Title:  Across the tract of wilderness which lay between the Delawares and the
Title:  village of their enemies, it seemed as if the foot of man had never trodden,
Title:  so breathing and deep was the silence in which it lay. But Hawkeye, whose
Title:  duty led him foremost in the adventure, knew the character of those with
Title:  whom he was about to contend too well to trust the treacherous quiet.
Title:  
Title:  When he saw his little band collected, the scout threw killdeer into the
Title:  hollow of his arm, and making a silent signal that he would be followed, he
Title:  led them many rods toward the rear, into the bed of a little brook which
Title:  they had crossed in advancing. Here he halted, and after waiting for the
Title:  whole of his grave and attentive warriors to close about him, he spoke in
Title:  Delaware, demanding:
Title:  
Title:  Do any of my young men know whither this run will lead us?
Title:  
Title:  A Delaware stretched forth a hand, with the two fingers separated, and
Title:  indicating the manner in which they were joined at the root, he answered:
Title:  
Title:  Before the sun could go his own length, the little water will be in the big.
Title:  Then he added, pointing in the direction of the place he mentioned, the two
Title:  make enough for the beavers.
Title:  
Title:  I thought as much, returned the scout, glancing his eye upward at the
Title:  opening in the tree-tops, from the course it takes, and the bearings of the
Title:  mountains. Men, we will keep within the cover of its banks till we scent the
Title:  Hurons.
Title:  
Title:  His companions gave the usual brief exclamation of assent, but, perceiving
Title:  that their leader was about to lead the way in person, one or two made signs
Title:  that all was not as it should be. Hawkeye, who comprehended their meaning
Title:  glances, turned and perceived that his party had been followed thus far by
Title:  the singing-master.
Title:  
Title:  Do you know, friend, asked the scout, gravely, and perhaps with a little of
Title:  the pride of conscious deserving in his manner, that this is a band of
Title:  rangers chosen for the most desperate service, and put under the command of
Title:  one who, though another might say it with a better face, will not be apt to
Title:  leave them idle. It may not be five, it cannot be thirty minutes, before we
Title:  tread on the body of a Huron, living or dead.
Title:  
Title:  Though not admonished of your intentions in words, returned David, whose
Title:  face was a little flushed, and whose ordinarily quiet and unmeaning eyes
Title:  glimmered with an expression of unusual fire, your men have reminded me of
Title:  the children of Jacob going out to battle against the Shechemites, for
Title:  wickedly aspiring to wedlock with a woman of a race that was favored of the
Title:  Lord. Now, I have journeyed far, and sojourned much in good and evil with
Title:  the maiden ye seek; and, though not a man of war, with my loins girded and
Title:  my sword sharpened, yet would I gladly strike a blow in her behalf.
Title:  
Title:  The scout hesitated, as if weighing the chances of such a strange enlistment
Title:  in his mind before he answered:
Title:  
Title:  You know not the use of any we'pon. You carry no rifle; and believe me, what
Title:  the Mingoes take they will freely give again.
Title:  
Title:  Though not a vaunting and bloodily disposed Goliath, returned David, drawing
Title:  a sling from beneath his parti-colored and uncouth attire, I have not
Title:  forgotten the example of the Jewish boy. With this ancient instrument of war
Title:  have I practised much in my youth, and peradventure the skill has not
Title:  entirely departed from me.
Title:  
Title:  Ay! said Hawkeye, considering the deer-skin thong and apron, with a cold and
Title:  discouraging eye; the thing might do its work among arrows, or even knives;
Title:  but these Mengwe have been furnished by the Frenchers with a good grooved
Title:  barrel a man. However, it seems to be your gift to go unharmed amid fire;
Title:  and as you have hitherto been favored - major, you have left your rifle at a
Title:  cock; a single shot before the time would be just twenty scalps lost to no
Title:  purpose - singer, you can follow; we may find use for you in the shoutings.
Title:  
Title:  I thank you, friend, returned David, supplying himself, like his royal
Title:  namesake, from among the pebbles of the brook; though not given to the
Title:  desire to kill, had you sent me away my spirit would have been troubled.
Title:  
Title:  Remember, added the scout, tapping his own head significantly on that spot
Title:  where Gamut was yet sore, we come to fight, and not to musickate. Until the
Title:  general whoop is given, nothing speaks but the rifle.
Title:  
Title:  David nodded, as much to signify his acquiescence with the terms; and then
Title:  Hawkeye, casting another observant glance over this followers made the
Title:  signal to proceed.
Title:  
Title:  Their route lay, for the distance of a mile, along the bed of the
Title:  water-course. Though protected from any great danger of observation by the
Title:  precipitous banks, and the thick shrubbery which skirted the stream, no
Title:  precaution known to an Indian attack was neglected. A warrior rather crawled
Title:  than walked on each flank so as to catch occasional glimpses into the
Title:  forest; and every few minutes the band came to a halt, and listened for
Title:  hostile sounds, with an acuteness of organs that would be scarcely
Title:  conceivable to a man in a less natural state. Their march was, however,
Title:  unmolested, and they reached the point where the lesser stream was lost in
Title:  the greater, without the smallest evidence that their progress had been
Title:  noted. Here the scout again halted, to consult the signs of the forest.
Title:  
Title:  We are likely to have a good day for a fight, he said, in English,
Title:  addressing Heyward, and glancing his eyes upward at the clouds, which began
Title:  to move in broad sheets across the firmament; a bright sun and a glittering
Title:  barrel are no friends to true sight. Everything is favorable; they have the
Title:  wind, which will bring down their noises and their smoke, too, no little
Title:  matter in itself; whereas, with us it will be first a shot, and then a clear
Title:  view. But here is an end to our cover; the beavers have had the range of
Title:  this stream for hundreds of years, and what atween their food and their
Title:  dams, there is, as you see, many a girdled stub, but few living trees.
Title:  
Title:  Hawkeye had, in truth, in these few words, given no bad description of the
Title:  prospect that now lay in their front. The brook was irregular in its width,
Title:  sometimes shooting through narrow fissures in the rocks, and at others
Title:  spreading over acres of bottom land, forming little areas that might be
Title:  termed ponds. Everywhere along its bands were the moldering relics of dead
Title:  trees, in all the stages of decay, from those that groaned on their
Title:  tottering trunks to such as had recently been robbed of those rugged coats
Title:  that so mysteriously contain their principle of life. A few long, low, and
Title:  moss-covered piles were scattered among them, like the memorials of a former
Title:  and long-departed generation.
Title:  
Title:  All these minute particulars were noted by the scout, with a gravity and
Title:  interest that they probably had never before attracted. He knew that the
Title:  Huron encampment lay a short half mile up the brook; and, with the
Title:  characteristic anxiety of one who dreaded a hidden danger, he was greatly
Title:  troubled at not finding the smallest trace of the presence of his enemy.
Title:  Once or twice he felt induced to give the order for a rush, and to attempt
Title:  the village by surprise; but his experience quickly admonished him of the
Title:  danger of so useless an experiment. Then he listened intently, and with
Title:  painful uncertainty, for the sounds of hostility in the quarter where Uncas
Title:  was left; but nothing was audible except the sighing of the wind, that began
Title:  to sweep over the bosom of the forest in gusts which threatened a tempest.
Title:  At length, yielding rather to his unusual impatience than taking counsel
Title:  from his knowledge, he determined to bring matters to an issue, by unmasking
Title:  his force, and proceeding cautiously, but steadily, up the stream.
Title:  
Title:  The scout had stood, while making his observations, sheltered by a brake,
Title:  and his companions still lay in the bed of the ravine, through which the
Title:  smaller stream debouched; but on hearing his low, though intelligible,
Title:  signal the whole party stole up the bank, like so many dark specters, and
Title:  silently arranged themselves around him. Pointing in the direction he wished
Title:  to proceed, Hawkeye advanced, the band breaking off in single files, and
Title:  following so accurately in his footsteps, as to leave it, if we except
Title:  Heyward and David, the trail of but a single man.
Title:  
Title:  The party was, however, scarcely uncovered before a volley from a dozen
Title:  rifles was heard in their rear; and a Delaware leaping high in to the air,
Title:  like a wounded deer, fell at his whole length, dead.
Title:  
Title:  Ah, I feared some deviltry like this! exclaimed the scout, in English,
Title:  adding, with the quickness of thought, in his adopted tongue: To cover, men,
Title:  and charge!
Title:  
Title:  The band dispersed at the word, and before Heyward had well recovered from
Title:  his surprise, he found himself standing alone with David. Luckily the Hurons
Title:  had already fallen back, and he was safe from their fire. But this state of
Title:  things was evidently to be of short continuance; for the scout set the
Title:  example of pressing on their retreat, by discharging his rifle, and darting
Title:  from tree to tree as his enemy slowly yielded ground.
Title:  
Title:  It would seem that the assault had been made by a very small party of the
Title:  Hurons, which, however, continued to increase in numbers, as it retired on
Title:  its friends, until the return fire was very nearly, if not quite, equal to
Title:  that maintained by the advancing Delawares. Heyward threw himself among the
Title:  combatants, and imitating the necessary caution of his companions, he made
Title:  quick discharges with his own rifle. The contest now grew warm and
Title:  stationary. Few were injured, as both parties kept their bodies as much
Title:  protected as possible by the trees; never, indeed, exposing any part of
Title:  their persons except in the act of taking aim. But the chances were
Title:  gradually growing unfavorable to Hawkeye and his band. The quick-sighted
Title:  scout perceived his danger without knowing how to remedy it. He saw it was
Title:  more dangerous to retreat than to maintain his ground: while he found his
Title:  enemy throwing out men on his flank; which rendered the task of keeping
Title:  themselves covered so very difficult to the Delawares, as nearly to silence
Title:  their fire. At this embarrassing moment, when they began to think the whole
Title:  of the hostile tribe was gradually encircling them, they heard the yell of
Title:  combatants and the rattling of arms echoing under the arches of the wood at
Title:  the place where Uncas was posted, a bottom which, in a manner, lay beneath
Title:  the ground on which Hawkeye and his party were contending.
Title:  
Title:  The effects of this attack were instantaneous, and to the scout and his
Title:  friends greatly relieving. It would seem that, while his own surprise had
Title:  been anticipated, and had consequently failed, the enemy, in their turn,
Title:  having been deceived in its object and in his numbers, had left too small a
Title:  force to resist the impetuous onset of the young Mohican. This fact was
Title:  doubly apparent, by the rapid manner in which the battle in the forest
Title:  rolled upward toward the village, and by an instant falling off in the
Title:  number of their assailants, who rushed to assist in maintaining the front,
Title:  and, as it now proved to be, the principal point of defense.
Title:  
Title:  Animating his followers by his voice, and his own example, Hawkeye then gave
Title:  the word to bear down upon their foes. The charge, in that rude species of
Title:  warfare, consisted merely in pushing from cover to cover, nigher to the
Title:  enemy; and in this maneuver he was instantly and successfully obeyed. The
Title:  Hurons were compelled to withdraw, and the scene of the contest rapidly
Title:  changed from the more open ground, on which it had commenced, to a spot
Title:  where the assailed found a thicket to rest upon. Here the struggle was
Title:  protracted, arduous and seemingly of doubtful issue; the Delawares, though
Title:  none of them fell, beginning to bleed freely, in consequence of the
Title:  disadvantage at which they were held.
Title:  
Title:  In this crisis, Hawkeye found means to get behind the same tree as that
Title:  which served for a cover to Heyward; most of his own combatants being within
Title:  call, a little on his right, where they maintained rapid, though fruitless,
Title:  discharges on their sheltered enemies.
Title:  
Title:  You are a young man, major, said the scout, dropping the butt of killdeer to
Title:  the earth, and leaning on the barrel, a little fatigued with his previous
Title:  industry; and it may be your gift to lead armies, at some future day, ag'in
Title:  these imps, the Mingoes. You may here see the philosophy of an Indian fight.
Title:  It consists mainly in ready hand, a quick eye and a good cover. Now, if you
Title:  had a company of the Royal Americans here, in what manner would you set them
Title:  to work in this business?
Title:  
Title:  The bayonet would make a road.
Title:  
Title:  Ay, there is white reason in what you say; but a man must ask himself, in
Title:  this wilderness, how many lives he can spare. No - horse1, continued the
Title:  scout, shaking his head, like one who mused; horse, I am ashamed to say must
Title:  sooner or later decide these scrimmages. The brutes are better than men, and
Title:  to horse must we come at last. Put a shodden hoof on the moccasin of a
Title:  red-skin, and, if his rifle be once emptied, he will never stop to load it
Title:  again.
Title:  
Title:  This is a subject that might better be discussed at another time, returned
Title:  Heyward; shall we charge?
Title:  
Title:  I see no contradiction to the gifts of any man in passing his breathing
Title:  spells in useful reflections, the scout replied. As to rush, I little relish
Title:  such a measure; for a scalp or two must be thrown away in the attempt. And
Title:  yet, he added, bending his head aside, to catch the sounds of the distant
Title:  combat, if we are to be of use to Uncas, these knaves in our front must be
Title:  got rid of.
Title:  
Title:  Then, turning with a prompt and decided air, he called aloud to his Indians,
Title:  in their own language. His words were answered by a shout; and, at a given
Title:  signal, each warrior made a swift movement around his particular tree. The
Title:  sight of so many dark bodies, glancing before their eyes at the same
Title:  instant, drew a hasty and consequently an ineffectual fire from the Hurons.
Title:  Without stopping to breathe, the Delawares leaped in long bounds toward the
Title:  wood, like so many panthers springing upon their prey. Hawkeye was in front,
Title:  brandishing his terrible rifle and animating his followers by his example. A
Title:  few of the older and more cunning Hurons, who had not been deceived by the
Title:  artifice which had been practiced to draw their fire, now made a close and
Title:  deadly discharge of their pieces and justified the apprehensions of the
Title:  scout by felling three of his foremost warriors. But the shock was
Title:  insufficient to repel the impetus of the charge. The Delawares broke into
Title:  the cover with the ferocity of their natures and swept away every trace of
Title:  resistance by the fury of the onset.
Title:  
Title:  The combat endured only for an instant, hand to hand, and then the assailed
Title:  yielded ground rapidly, until they reached the opposite margin of the
Title:  thicket, where they clung to the cover, with the sort of obstinacy that is
Title:  so often witnessed in hunted brutes. At this critical moment, when the
Title:  success of the struggle was again becoming doubtful, the crack of a rifle
Title:  was heard behind the Hurons, and a bullet came whizzing from among some
Title:  beaver lodges, which were situated in the clearing, in their rear, and was
Title:  followed by the fierce and appalling yell of the war-whoop.
Title:  
Title:  There speaks the Sagamore! shouted Hawkeye, answering the cry with his own
Title:  stentorian voice; we have them now in face and back!
Title:  
Title:  The effect on the Hurons was instantaneous. Discouraged by an assault from a
Title:  quarter that left them no opportunity for cover, the warriors uttered a
Title:  common yell of disappointment, and breaking off in a body, they spread
Title:  themselves across the opening, heedless of every consideration but flight.
Title:  Many fell, in making the experiment, under the bullets and the blows of the
Title:  pursuing Delawares.
Title:  
Title:  We shall not pause to detail the meeting between the scout and Chingachgook,
Title:  or the more touching interview that Duncan held with Munro. A few brief and
Title:  hurried words served to explain the state of things to both parties; and
Title:  then Hawkeye, pointing out the Sagamore to his band, resigned the chief
Title:  authority into the hands of the Mohican chief. Chingachgook assumed the
Title:  station to which his birth and experience gave him so distinguished a claim,
Title:  with the grave dignity that always gives force to the mandates of a native
Title:  warrior. Following the footsteps of the scout, he led the party back through
Title:  the thicket, his men scalping the fallen Hurons and secreting the bodies of
Title:  their own dead as they proceeded, until they gained a point where the former
Title:  was content to make a halt.
Title:  
Title:  The warriors, who had breathed themselves freely in the preceding struggle,
Title:  were now posted on a bit of level ground, sprinkled with trees in sufficient
Title:  numbers to conceal them. The land fell away rather precipitately in front,
Title:  and beneath their eyes stretched, for several miles, a narrow, dark, and
Title:  wooded vale. It was through this dense and dark forest that Uncas was still
Title:  contending with the main body of the Hurons.
Title:  
Title:  The Mohican and his friends advanced to the brow of the hill, and listened,
Title:  with practised ears, to the sounds of the combat. A few birds hovered over
Title:  the leafy bosom of the valley, frightened from their secluded nests; and
Title:  here and there a light vapory cloud, which seemed already blending with the
Title:  atmosphere, arose above the trees, and indicated some spot where the
Title:  struggle had been fierce and stationary.
Title:  
Title:  The fight is coming up the ascent, said Duncan, pointing in the direction of
Title:  a new explosion of firearms; we are too much in the center of their line to
Title:  be effective.
Title:  
Title:  They will incline into the hollow, where the cover is thicker, said the
Title:  scout, and that will leave us well on their flank. Go, Sagamore; you will
Title:  hardly be in time to give the whoop, and lead on the young men. I will fight
Title:  this scrimmage with warriors of my own color. You know me, Mohican; not a
Title:  Huron of them all shall cross the swell, into your rear, without the notice
Title:  of killdeer.
Title:  
Title:  The Indian chief paused another moment to consider the signs of the contest,
Title:  which was now rolling rapidly up the ascent, a certain evidence that the
Title:  Delawares triumphed; nor did he actually quit the place until admonished of
Title:  the proximity of his friends, as well as enemies, by the bullets of the
Title:  former, which began to patter among the dried leaves on the ground, like the
Title:  bits of falling hail which precede the bursting of the tempest. Hawkeye and
Title:  his three companions withdrew a few paces to a shelter, and awaited the
Title:  issue with calmness that nothing but great practise could impart in such a
Title:  scene.
Title:  
Title:  It was not long before the reports of the rifles began to lose the echoes of
Title:  the woods, and to sound like weapons discharged in the open air. Then a
Title:  warrior appeared, here and there, driven to the skirts of the forest, and
Title:  rallying as he entered the clearing, as at the place where the final stand
Title:  was to be made. These were soon joined by others, until a long line of
Title:  swarthy figures was to be seen clinging to the cover with the obstinacy of
Title:  desperation. Heyward began to grow impatient, and turned his eyes anxiously
Title:  in the direction of Chingachgook. The chief was seated on a rock, with
Title:  nothing visible but his calm visage, considering the spectacle with an eye
Title:  as deliberate as if he were posted there merely to view the struggle.
Title:  
Title:  The time has come for the Delaware to strike'! said Duncan.
Title:  
Title:  Not so, not so, returned the scout; when he scents his friends, he will let
Title:  them know that he is here. See, see; the knaves are getting in that clump of
Title:  pines, like bees settling after their flight. By the Lord, a squaw might put
Title:  a bullet into the center of such a knot of dark skins!
Title:  
Title:  At that instant the whoop was given, and a dozen Hurons fell by a discharge
Title:  from Chingachgook and his band. The shout that followed was answered by a
Title:  single war-cry from the forest, and a yell passed through the air that
Title:  sounded as if a thousand throats were united in a common effort. The Hurons
Title:  staggered, deserting the center of their line, and Uncas issued from the
Title:  forest through the opening they left, at the head of a hundred warriors.
Title:  
Title:  Waving his hands right and left, the young chief pointed out the enemy to
Title:  his followers, who separated in pursuit. The war now divided, both wings of
Title:  the broken Hurons seeking protection in the woods again, hotly pressed by
Title:  the victorious warriors of the Lenape. A minute might have passed, but the
Title:  sounds were already receding in different directions, and gradually losing
Title:  their distinctness beneath the echoing arches of the woods. One little knot
Title:  of Hurons, however, had disdained to seek a cover, and were retiring, like
Title:  lions at bay, slowly and sullenly up the acclivity which Chingachgook and
Title:  his band had just deserted, to mingle more closely in the fray. Magua was
Title:  conspicuous in this party, both by his fierce and savage mien, and by the
Title:  air of haughty authority he yet maintained.
Title:  
Title:  In his eagerness to expedite the pursuit, Uncas had left himself nearly
Title:  alone; but the moment his eye caught the figure of Le Subtil, every other
Title:  consideration was forgotten. Raising his cry of battle, which recalled some
Title:  six or seven warriors, and reckless of the disparity of their numbers, he
Title:  rushed upon his enemy. Le Renard, who watched the movement, paused to
Title:  receive him with secret joy. But at the moment when he thought the rashness
Title:  of his impetuous young assailant had left him at his mercy, another shout
Title:  was given, and La Longue Carabine was seen rushing to the rescue, attended
Title:  by all his white associates. The Huron instantly turned, and commenced a
Title:  rapid retreat up the ascent.
Title:  
Title:  There was no time for greetings or congratulations; for Uncas, though
Title:  unconscious of the presence of his friends, continued the pursuit with the
Title:  velocity of the wind. In vain Hawkeye called to him to respect the covers;
Title:  the young Mohican braved the dangerous fire of his enemies, and soon
Title:  compelled them to a flight as swift as his own headlong speed. It was
Title:  fortunate that the race was of short continuance, and that the white men
Title:  were much favored by their position, or the Delaware would soon have
Title:  outstripped all his companions, and fallen a victim to his own temerity.
Title:  But, ere such a calamity could happen, the pursuers and pursued entered the
Title:  Wyandot village, within striking distance of each other.
Title:  
Title:  Excited by the presence of their dwellings, and tired of the chase, the
Title:  Hurons now made a stand, and fought around their council-lodge with the fury
Title:  of despair. The onset and the issue were like the passage and destruction of
Title:  a whirlwind. The tomahawk of Uncas, the blows of Hawkeye, and even the still
Title:  nervous arm of Munro were all busy for that passing moment, and the ground
Title:  was quickly strewed with their enemies. Still Magua, though daring and much
Title:  exposed, escaped from every effort against his life, with that sort of
Title:  fabled protection that was made to overlook the fortunes of favored heroes
Title:  in the legends of ancient poetry. Raising a yell that spoke volumes of anger
Title:  and disappointment, the subtle chief, when he saw his comrades fallen,
Title:  darted away from the place, attended by his two only surviving friends,
Title:  leaving the Delawares engaged in stripping the dead of the bloody trophies
Title:  of their victory.
Title:  
Title:  But Uncas, who had vainly sought him in the melee, bounded forward in
Title:  pursuit; Hawkeye, Heyward and David still pressing on his footsteps. The
Title:  utmost that the scout could effect, was to keep the muzzle of his rifle a
Title:  little in advance of his friend, to whom, however, it answered every purpose
Title:  of a charmed shield. Once Magua appeared disposed to make another and a
Title:  final effort to revenge his losses; but, abandoning his intention as soon as
Title:  demonstrated, he leaped into a thicket of bushes, through which he was
Title:  followed by his enemies, and suddenly entered the mouth of the cave already
Title:  known to the reader. Hawkeye, who had only forborne to fire in tenderness to
Title:  Uncas, raised a shout of success, and proclaimed aloud that now they were
Title:  certain of their game. The pursuers dashed into the long and narrow
Title:  entrance, in time to catch a glimpse of the retreating forms of the Hurons.
Title:  Their passage through the natural galleries and subterraneous apartments of
Title:  the cavern was preceded by the shrieks and cries of hundreds of women and
Title:  children. The place, seen by its dim and uncertain light, appeared like the
Title:  shades of the infernal regions, across which unhappy ghosts and savage
Title:  demons were flitting in multitudes.
Title:  
Title:  Still Uncas kept his eye on Magua, as if life to him possessed but a single
Title:  object. Heyward and the scout still pressed on his rear, actuated, though
Title:  possibly in a less degree, by a common feeling. But their way was becoming
Title:  intricate, in those dark and gloomy passages, and the glimpses of the
Title:  retiring warriors less distinct and frequent; and for a moment the trace was
Title:  believed to be lost, when a white robe was seen fluttering in the further
Title:  extremity of a passage that seemed to lead up the mountain.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis Cora! exclaimed Heyward, in a voice in which horror and delight were
Title:  wildly mingled.
Title:  
Title:  Cora! Cora! echoed Uncas, bounding forward like a deer.
Title:  
Title:  'Tis the maiden! shouted the scout. Courage, lady; we come! we come!
Title:  
Title:  The chase was renewed with a diligence rendered tenfold encouraging by this
Title:  glimpse of the captive. But the way was rugged, broken, and in spots nearly
Title:  impassable. Uncas abandoned his rifle, and leaped forward with headlong
Title:  precipitation. Heyward rashly imitated his example, though both were, a
Title:  moment afterward, admonished of his madness by hearing the bellowing of a
Title:  piece, that the Hurons found time to discharge down the passage in the
Title:  rocks, the bullet from which even gave the young Mohican a slight wound.
Title:  
Title:  We must close! said the scout, passing his friends by a desperate leap; the
Title:  knaves will pick us all off at this distance; and see, they hold the maiden
Title:  so as the shield themselves!
Title:  
Title:  Though his words were unheeded, or rather unheard, his example was followed
Title:  by his companions, who, by incredible exertions, got near enough to the
Title:  fugitives to perceive that Cora was borne along between the two warriors
Title:  while Magua prescribed the direction and manner of their flight. At this
Title:  moment the forms of all four were strongly drawn against an opening in the
Title:  sky, and they disappeared. Nearly frantic with disappointment, Uncas and
Title:  Heyward increased efforts that already seemed superhuman, and they issued
Title:  from the cavern on the side of the mountain, in time to note the route of
Title:  the pursued. The course lay up the ascent, and still continued hazardous and
Title:  laborious.
Title:  
Title:  Encumbered by his rifle, and, perhaps, not sustained by so deep an interest
Title:  in the captive as his companions, the scout suffered the latter to precede
Title:  him a little, Uncas, in his turn, taking the lead of Heyward. In this
Title:  manner, rocks, precipices and difficulties were surmounted in an incredibly
Title:  short space, that at another time, and under other circumstances, would have
Title:  been deemed almost insuperable. But the impetuous young man were rewarded by
Title:  finding that, encumbered with Cora, the Hurons were losing ground in the
Title:  race.
Title:  
Title:  Stay, dog of the Wyandots! exclaimed Uncas, shaking his bright tomahawk at
Title:  Magua; a Delaware girl calls stay!
Title:  
Title:  I will go no further! cried Cora, stopping unexpectedly on a ledge of rock,
Title:  that overhung a deep precipice, at no great distance from the summit of the
Title:  mountain. Kill me if thou wilt, detestable Huron; I will go no further.
Title:  
Title:  The supporters of the maiden raised their ready tomahawks with the impious
Title:  joy that fiends are thought to take in mischief, but Magua stayed the
Title:  uplifted arms. The Huron chief, after casting the weapons he had wrested
Title:  from his companions over the rock, drew his knife, and turned to his
Title:  captive, with a look in which conflicting passions fiercely contended.
Title:  
Title:  Woman, he said, chose; the wigwam or the knife of Le Subtil!
Title:  
Title:  Cora regarded him not, but dropping on her knees, she raised her eyes and
Title:  stretched her arms toward heaven, saying in a meek and yet confiding voice:
Title:  
Title:  I am thine; do with me as thou seest best!
Title:  
Title:  Woman, repeated Magua, hoarsely, and endeavoring in vain to catch a glance
Title:  from her serene and beaming eye, choose!
Title:  
Title:  But Cora neither heard nor heeded his demand. The form of the Huron trembled
Title:  in every fibre, and he raised his arm on high, but dropped it again with a
Title:  bewildered air, like one who doubted. Once more he struggled with himself
Title:  and lifted the keen weapon again; but just then a piercing cry was heard
Title:  above them, and Uncas appeared, leaping frantically, from a fearful height,
Title:  upon the ledge. Magua recoiled a step; and one of his assistants, profiting
Title:  by the chance, sheathed his own knife in the bosom of Cora.
Title:  
Title:  The Huron sprang like a tiger on his offending and already retreating
Title:  country man, but the falling form of Uncas separated the unnatural
Title:  combatants. Diverted from his object by this interruption, and maddened by
Title:  the murder he had just witnessed, Magua buried his weapon in the back of the
Title:  prostrate Delaware, uttering an unearthly shout as he committed the
Title:  dastardly deed. But Uncas arose from the blow, as the wounded panther turns
Title:  upon his foe, and struck the murderer of Cora to his feet, by an effort in
Title:  which the last of his failing strength was expended. Then, with a stern and
Title:  steady look, he turned to Le Subtil, and indicated by the expression of his
Title:  eye all that he would do had not the power deserted him. The latter seized
Title:  the nerveless arm of the unresisting Delaware, and passed his knife into his
Title:  bosom three several times, before his victim, still keeping his gaze riveted
Title:  on his enemy, with a look of inextinguishable scorn, feel dead at his feet.
Title:  
Title:  Mercy! mercy! Huron, cried Heyward, from above, in tones nearly choked by
Title:  horror; give mercy, and thou shalt receive from it!
Title:  
Title:  Whirling the bloody knife up at the imploring youth, the victorious Magua
Title:  uttered a cry so fierce, so wild, and yet so joyous, that it conveyed the
Title:  sounds of savage triumph to the ears of those who fought in the valley, a
Title:  thousand feet below. He was answered by a burst from the lips of the scout,
Title:  whose tall person was just then seen moving swiftly toward him, along those
Title:  dangerous crags, with steps as bold and reckless as if he possessed the
Title:  power to move in air. But when the hunter reached the scene of the ruthless
Title:  massacre, the ledge was tenanted only by the dead.
Title:  
Title:  His keen eye took a single look at the victims, and then shot its glances
Title:  over the difficulties of the ascent in his front. A form stood at the brow
Title:  of the mountain, on the very edge of the giddy height, with uplifted arms,
Title:  in an awful attitude of menace. Without stopping to consider his person, the
Title:  rifle of Hawkeye was raised; but a rock, which fell on the head of one of
Title:  the fugitives below, exposed the indignant and glowing countenance of the
Title:  honest Gamut. Then Magua issued from a crevice, and, stepping with calm
Title:  indifference over the body of the last of his associates, he leaped a wide
Title:  fissure, and ascended the rocks at a point where the arm of David could not
Title:  reach him. A single bound would carry him to the brow of the precipice, and
Title:  assure his safety. Before taking the leap, however, the Huron paused, and
Title:  shaking his hand at the scout, he shouted:
Title:  
Title:  The pale faces are dogs! the Delawares women! Magua leaves them on the
Title:  rocks, for the crows!
Title:  
Title:  Laughing hoarsely, he made a desperate leap, and fell short of his mark,
Title:  though his hands grasped a shrub on the verge of the height. The form of
Title:  Hawkeye had crouched like a beast about to take its spring, and his frame
Title:  trembled so violently with eagerness that the muzzle of the half-raised
Title:  rifle played like a leaf fluttering in the wind. Without exhausting himself
Title:  with fruitless efforts, the cunning Magua suffered his body to drop to the
Title:  length of his arms, and found a fragment for his feet to rest on. Then,
Title:  summoning all his powers, he renewed the attempt, and so far succeeded as to
Title:  draw his knees on the edge of the mountain. It was now, when the body of his
Title:  enemy was most collected together, that the agitated weapon of the scout was
Title:  drawn to his shoulder. The surrounding rocks themselves were not steadier
Title:  than the piece became, for the single instant that it poured out its
Title:  contents. The arms of the Huron relaxed, and his body fell back a little,
Title:  while his knees still kept their position. Turning a relentless look on his
Title:  enemy, he shook a hand in grim defiance. But his hold loosened, and his dark
Title:  person was seen cutting the air with its head downward, for a fleeting
Title:  instant, until it glided past the fringe of shrubbery which clung to the
Title:  mountain, in its rapid flight to destruction.
Title:

Title:  
Title:  1 The American forest admits of the passage of horses, there being little
Title:  underbrush, and few tangled brakes. The plan of Hawkeye is the one which has
Title:  always proved the most successful in the battles between the whites and the
Title:  Indians. Wayne, in his celebrated campaign on the Miami, received the fire
Title:  of his enemies in line; and then causing his dragoons to wheel round his
Title:  flanks, the Indians were driven from their covers before they had time to
Title:  load. One of the most conspicuous of the chiefs who fought in the battle of
Title:  Miami assured the writer, that the red men could not fight the warriors with
Title:  long knives and leather stockings; meaning the dragoons with their sabers
Title:  and boots.

Title:  Chapter 33
Title:  
Title:       They fought - like brave men, long and well,
Title:       They piled that ground with Moslem slain,
Title:       They conquered - but Bozzaris fell,
Title:       Bleeding at every vein.
Title:       His few surviving comrades saw
Title:       His smile when rang their loud hurrah,
Title:       And the red field was won;
Title:       Then saw in death his eyelids close
Title:       Calmly, as to a night's repose,
Title:       Like flowers at set of sun
Title:  
Title:                                                                 HALLECK
Title:  
Title:  The sun found the Lenape, on the succeeding day, a nation of mourners. The
Title:  sounds of the battle were over, and they had fed fat their ancient grudge,
Title:  and had avenged their recent quarrel with the Mengwe, by the destruction of
Title:  a whole community. The black and murky atmosphere that floated around the
Title:  spot where the Hurons had encamped, sufficiently announced of itself, the
Title:  fate of that wandering tribe; while hundreds of ravens, that struggled above
Title:  the summits of the mountains, or swept, in noisy flocks, across the wide
Title:  ranges of the woods, furnished a frightful direction to the scene of the
Title:  combat. In short, any eye at all practised in the signs of a frontier
Title:  warfare might easily have traced all those unerring evidences of the
Title:  ruthless results which attend an Indian vengeance.
Title:  
Title:  Still, the sun rose on the Lenape a nation of mourners. No shouts of
Title:  success, no songs of triumph, were heard, in rejoicings for their victory.
Title:  The latest straggler had returned from his fell employment, only to strip
Title:  himself of the terrific emblems of his bloody calling, and to join in the
Title:  lamentations of his countrymen, as a stricken people. Pride and exultation
Title:  were supplanted by humility, and the fiercest of human passions was already
Title:  succeeded by the most profound and unequivocal demonstrations of grief.
Title:  
Title:  The lodges were deserted; but a broad belt of earnest faces encircled a spot
Title:  in their vicinity, whither everything possessing life had repaired, and
Title:  where all were now collected, in deep and awful silence. Though beings of
Title:  every rank and age, of both sexes, and of all pursuits, had united to form
Title:  this breathing wall of bodies, they were influenced by a single emotion.
Title:  Each eye was riveted on the center of that ring, which contained the objects
Title:  of so much and of so common an interest.
Title:  
Title:  Six Delaware girls, with their long, dark, flowing tresses falling loosely
Title:  across their bosoms, stood apart, and only gave proof of their existence as
Title:  they occasionally strewed sweet-scented herbs and forest flowers on a litter
Title:  of fragrant plants that, under a pall of Indian robes, supported all that
Title:  now remained of the ardent, high-souled, and generous Cora. Her form was
Title:  concealed in many wrappers of the same simple manufacture, and her face was
Title:  shut forever from the gaze of men. At her feet was seated the desolate
Title:  Munro. His aged head was bowed nearly to the earth, in compelled submission
Title:  to the stroke of Providence; but a hidden anguish struggled about his
Title:  furrowed brow, that was only partially concealed by the careless locks of
Title:  gray that had fallen, neglected, on his temples. Gamut stood at his side,
Title:  his meek head bared to the rays of the sun, while his eyes, wandering and
Title:  concerned, seemed to be equally divided between that little volume, which
Title:  contained so many quaint but holy maxims, and the being in whose behalf his
Title:  soul yearned to administer consolation. Heyward was also nigh, supporting
Title:  himself against a tree, and endeavoring to keep down those sudden risings of
Title:  sorrow that it required his utmost manhood to subdue.
Title:  
Title:  But sad and melancholy as this group may easily be imagined, it was far less
Title:  touching than another, that occupied the opposite space of the same area.
Title:  Seated, as in life, with his form and limbs arranged in grave and decent
Title:  composure, Uncas appeared, arrayed in the most gorgeous ornaments that the
Title:  wealth of the tribe could furnish. Rich plumes nodded above his head;
Title:  wampum, gorgets, bracelets, and medals, adorned his person in profusion;
Title:  though his dull eye and vacant lineaments too strongly contradicted the idle
Title:  tale of pride they would convey.
Title:  
Title:  Directly in front of the corpse Chingachgook was placed, without arms, paint
Title:  or adornment of any sort, except the bright blue blazonry of his race, that
Title:  was indelibly impressed on his naked bosom. During the long period that the
Title:  tribe had thus been collected, the Mohican warrior had kept a steady,
Title:  anxious look on the cold and senseless countenance of his son. So riveted
Title:  and intense had been that gaze, and so changeless his attitude, that a
Title:  stranger might not have told the living from the dead, but for the
Title:  occasional gleamings of a troubled spirit, that shot athwart the dark visage
Title:  of one, and the deathlike calm that had forever settled on the lineaments of
Title:  the other. The scout was hard by, leaning in a pensive posture on his own
Title:  fatal and avenging weapon; while Tamenund, supported by the elders of his
Title:  nation, occupied a high place at hand, whence he might look down on the mute
Title:  and sorrowful assemblage of his people.
Title:  
Title:  Just within the inner edge of the circle stood a soldier, in the military
Title:  attire of a strange nation; and without it was his warhorse, in the center
Title:  of a collection of mounted domestics, seemingly in readiness to undertake
Title:  some distant journey. The vestments of the stranger announced him to be one
Title:  who held a responsible situation near the person of the captain of the
Title:  Canadas; and who, as it would now seem, finding his errand of peace
Title:  frustrated by the fierce impetuosity of his allies, was content to become a
Title:  silent and sad spectator of the fruits of a contest that he had arrived too
Title:  late to anticipate.
Title:  
Title:  The day was drawing to the close of its first quarter, and yet had the
Title:  multitude maintained its breathing stillness since its dawn.
Title:  
Title:  No sound louder than a stifled sob had been heard among them, nor had even a
Title:  limb been moved throughout that long and painful period, except to perform
Title:  the simple and touching offerings that were made, from time to time, in
Title:  commemoration of the dead. The patience and forbearance of Indian fortitude
Title:  could alone support such an appearance of abstraction, as seemed now to have
Title:  turned each dark and motionless figure into stone.
Title:  
Title:  At length, the sage of the Delawares stretched forth an arm, and leaning on
Title:  the shoulders of his attendants, he arose with an air as feeble as if
Title:  another age had already intervened between the man who had met his nation
Title:  the preceding day, and him who now tottered on his elevated stand.
Title:  
Title:  Men of the Lenape! he said, in low, hollow tones, that sounded like a voice
Title:  charged with some prophetic mission: the face of the Manitou is behind a
Title:  cloud! His eye is turned from you; His ears are shut; His tongue gives no
Title:  answer. You see him not; yet His judgments are before you. Let your hearts
Title:  be open and your spirits tell no lie. Men of the Lenape! the face of the
Title:  Manitou is behind a cloud.
Title:  
Title:  As this simple and yet terrible annunciation stole on the ears of the
Title:  multitude, a stillness as deep and awful succeeded as if the venerated
Title:  spirit they worshiped had uttered the words without the aid of human organs;
Title:  and even the inanimate Uncas appeared a being of life, compared with the
Title:  humbled and submissive throng by whom he was surrounded. As the immediate
Title:  effect, however, gradually passed away, a low murmur of voices commenced a
Title:  sort of chant in honor of the dead. The sounds were those of females, and
Title:  were thrillingly soft and wailing. The words were connected by no regular
Title:  continuation, but as one ceased another took up the eulogy, or lamentation,
Title:  whichever it might be called, and gave vent to her emotions in such language
Title:  as was suggested by her feelings and the occasion. At intervals the speaker
Title:  was interrupted by general and loud bursts of sorrow, during which the girls
Title:  around the bier of Cora plucked the plants and flowers blindly from her
Title:  body, as if bewildered with grief. But, in the milder moments of their
Title:  plaint, these emblems of purity and sweetness were cast back to their
Title:  places, with every sign of tenderness and regret. Though rendered less
Title:  connected by many and general interruptions and outbreakings, a translation
Title:  of their language would have contained a regular descant, which, in
Title:  substance, might have proved to possess a train of consecutive ideas.
Title:  
Title:  A girl, selected for the task by her rank and qualifications, commenced by
Title:  modest allusions to the qualities of the deceased warrior, embellishing her
Title:  expressions with those oriental images that the Indians have probably
Title:  brought with them from the extremes of the other continent, and which form
Title:  of themselves a link to connect the ancient histories of the two worlds. She
Title:  called him the panther of his tribe; and described him as one whose moccasin
Title:  left no trail on the dews; whose bound was like the leap of a young fawn;
Title:  whose eye was brighter than a star in the dark night; and whose voice, in
Title:  battle, was loud as the thunder of the Manitou. She reminded him of the
Title:  mother who bore him, and dwelt forcibly on the happiness she must feel in
Title:  possessing such a son. She bade him tell her, when they met in the world of
Title:  spirits, that the Delaware girls had shed tears above the grave of her
Title:  child, and had called her blessed.
Title:  
Title:  Then, they who succeeded, changing their tones to a milder and still more
Title:  tender strain, alluded, with the delicacy and sensitiveness of women, to the
Title:  stranger maiden, who had left the upper earth at a time so near his own
Title:  departure, as to render the will of the Great Spirit too manifest to be
Title:  disregarded. They admonished him to be kind to her, and to have
Title:  consideration for her ignorance of those arts which were so necessary to the
Title:  comfort of a warrior like himself. They dwelled upon her matchless beauty,
Title:  and on her noble resolution, without the taint of envy, and as angels may be
Title:  thought to delight in a superior excellence; adding, that these endowments
Title:  should prove more than equivalent for any little imperfection in her
Title:  education.
Title:  
Title:  After which, others again, in due succession, spoke to the maiden herself,
Title:  in the low, soft language of tenderness and love. They exhorted her to be of
Title:  cheerful mind, and to fear nothing for her future welfare. A hunter would be
Title:  her companion, who knew how to provide for her smallest wants; and a warrior
Title:  was at her side who was able to protect he against every danger. They
Title:  promised that her path should be pleasant, and her burden light. They
Title:  cautioned her against unavailing regrets for the friends of her youth, and
Title:  the scenes where her father had dwelt; assuring her that the blessed hunting
Title:  grounds of the Lenape, contained vales as pleasant, streams as pure; and
Title:  flowers as sweet, as the heaven of the pale faces. They advised her to be
Title:  attentive to the wants of her companion, and never to forget the distinction
Title:  which the Manitou had so wisely established between them. Then, in a wild
Title:  burst of their chant they sang with united voices the temper of the
Title:  Mohican's mind. They pronounced him noble, manly and generous; all that
Title:  became a warrior, and all that a maid might love. Clothing their ideas in
Title:  the most remote and subtle images, they betrayed, that, in the short period
Title:  of their intercourse, they had discovered, with the intuitive perception of
Title:  their sex, the truant disposition of his inclinations. The Delaware girls
Title:  had found no favor in his eyes! He was of a race that had once been lords on
Title:  the shores of the salt lake, and his wishes had led him back to a people who
Title:  dwelt about the graves of his fathers. Why should not such a predilection be
Title:  encouraged! That she was of a blood purer and richer than the rest of her
Title:  nation, any eye might have seen; that she was equal to the dangers and
Title:  daring of a life in the woods, her conduct had proved; and now, they added,
Title:  the wise one of the earth had transplanted her to a place where she would
Title:  find congenial spirits, and might be forever happy.
Title:  
Title:  Then, with another transition in voice and subject, allusions were made to
Title:  the virgin who wept in the adjacent lodge. They compared her to flakes of
Title:  snow; as pure, as white, as brilliant, and as liable to melt in the fierce
Title:  heats of summer, or congeal in the frosts of winter. They doubted not that
Title:  she was lovely in the eyes of the young chief, whose skin and whose sorrow
Title:  seemed so like her own; but though far from expressing such a preference, it
Title:  was evident they deemed her less excellent than the maid they mourned. Still
Title:  they denied her no need her rare charms might properly claim. Her ringlets
Title:  were compared to the exuberant tendrils of the vine, her eye to the blue
Title:  vault of heavens, and the most spotless cloud, with its glowing flush of the
Title:  sun, was admitted to be less attractive than her bloom.
Title:  
Title:  During these and similar songs nothing was audible but the murmurs of the
Title:  music; relieved, as it was, or rather rendered terrible, by those occasional
Title:  bursts of grief which might be called its choruses. The Delawares themselves
Title:  listened like charmed men; and it was very apparent, by the variations of
Title:  their speaking countenances, how deep and true was their sympathy. Even
Title:  David was not reluctant to lend his ears to the tones of voices so sweet;
Title:  and long ere the chant was ended, his gaze announced that his soul was
Title:  enthralled.
Title:  
Title:  The scout, to whom alone, of all the white men, the words were intelligible,
Title:  suffered himself to be a little aroused from his meditative posture, and
Title:  bent his face aside, to catch their meaning, as the girls proceeded. But
Title:  when they spoke of the future prospects of Cora and Uncas, he shook his
Title:  head, like one who knew the error of their simple creed, and resuming his
Title:  reclining attitude, he maintained it until the ceremony, if that might be
Title:  called a ceremony, in which feeling was so deeply imbued, was finished.
Title:  Happily for the self-command of both Heyward and Munro, they knew not the
Title:  meaning of the wild sounds they heard.
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook was a solitary exception to the interest manifested by the
Title:  native part of the audience. His look never changed throughout the whole of
Title:  the scene, nor did a muscle move in his rigid countenance, even at the
Title:  wildest or the most pathetic parts of the lamentation. The cold and
Title:  senseless remains of his son was all to him, and every other sense but that
Title:  of sight seemed frozen, in order that his eyes might take their final gaze
Title:  at those lineaments he had so long loved, and which were now about to be
Title:  closed forever from his view.
Title:  
Title:  In this stage of the obsequies, a warrior much renowned for deed in arms,
Title:  and more especially for services in the recent combat, a man of stern and
Title:  grave demeanor, advanced slowly from the crowd, and placed himself nigh the
Title:  person of the dead.
Title:  
Title:  Why hast thou left us, pride of the Wapanachki? he said, addressing himself
Title:  to the dull ears of Uncas, as if the empty clay retained the faculties of
Title:  the animated man; thy time has been like that of the sun when in the trees;
Title:  they glory brighter than his light at noonday. Thou art gone, youthful
Title:  warrior, but a hundred Wyandots are clearing the briers from thy path to the
Title:  world of the spirits. Who that saw thee in battle would believe that thou
Title:  couldst die? Who before thee has ever shown Uttawa the way into the fight?
Title:  Thy feet were like the wings of eagles; thine arm heavier than falling
Title:  branches from the pine; and thy voice like the Manitou when He speaks in the
Title:  clouds. The tongue of Uttawa is weak, he added, looking about him with a
Title:  melancholy gaze, and his heart exceeding heavy. Pride of the Wapanachki, why
Title:  hast thou left us?
Title:  
Title:  He was succeeded by others, in due order, until most of the high and gifted
Title:  men of the nation had sung or spoken their tribute of praise over the manes
Title:  of the deceased chief. When each had ended, another deep and breathing
Title:  silence reigned in all the place.
Title:  
Title:  Then a low, deep sound was heard, like the suppressed accompaniment of
Title:  distant music, rising just high enough on the air to be audible, and yet so
Title:  indistinctly, as to leave its character, and the place whence it proceeded,
Title:  alike matters of conjecture. It was, however, succeeded by another and
Title:  another strain, each in a higher key, until they grew on the ear, first in
Title:  long drawn and often repeated interjections, and finally in words. The lips
Title:  of Chingachgook had so far parted, as to announce that it was the monody of
Title:  the father. Though not an eye was turned toward him nor the smallest sign of
Title:  impatience exhibited, it was apparent, by the manner in which the multitude
Title:  elevated their heads to listen, that they drank in the sounds with an
Title:  intenseness of attention, that none but Tamenund himself had ever before
Title:  commanded. But they listened in vain. The strains rose just so loud as to
Title:  become intelligible, and then grew fainter and more trembling, until they
Title:  finally sank on the ear, as if borne away by a passing breath of wind. The
Title:  lips of the Sagamore closed, and he remained silent in his seat, looking
Title:  with his riveted eye and motionless form, like some creature that had been
Title:  turned from the Almighty hand with the form but without the spirit of a man.
Title:  The Delawares who knew by these symptoms that the mind of their friend was
Title:  not prepared for so mighty an effort of fortitude, relaxed in their
Title:  attention; and, with an innate delicacy, seemed to bestow all their thoughts
Title:  on the obsequies of the stranger maiden.
Title:  
Title:  A signal was given, by one of the elder chiefs, to the women who crowded
Title:  that part of the circle near which the body of Cora lay. Obedient to the
Title:  sign, the girls raised the bier to the elevation of their heads, and
Title:  advanced with slow and regulated steps, chanting, as they proceeded, another
Title:  wailing song in praise of the deceased. Gamut, who had been a close observer
Title:  of rites he deemed so heathenish, now bent his head over the shoulder of the
Title:  unconscious father, whispering:
Title:  
Title:  They move with the remains of thy child; shall we not follow, and see them
Title:  interred with Christian burial?
Title:  
Title:  Munro started, as if the last trumpet had sounded in his ear, and bestowing
Title:  one anxious and hurried glance around him, he arose and followed in the
Title:  simple train, with the mien of a soldier, but bearing the full burden of a
Title:  parent's suffering. His friends pressed around him with a sorrow that was
Title:  too strong to be termed sympathy - even the young Frenchman joining in the
Title:  procession, with the air of a man who was sensibly touched at the early and
Title:  melancholy fate of one so lovely. But when the last and humblest female of
Title:  the tribe had joined in the wild and yet ordered array, the men of the
Title:  Lenape contracted their circle, and formed again around the person of Uncas,
Title:  as silent, as grave, and as motionless as before.
Title:  
Title:  The place which had been chosen for the grave of Cora was a little knoll,
Title:  where a cluster of young and healthful pines had taken root, forming of
Title:  themselves a melancholy and appropriate shade over the spot. On reaching it
Title:  the girls deposited their burden, and continued for many minutes waiting,
Title:  with characteristic patience, and native timidity, for some evidence that
Title:  they whose feelings were most concerned were content with the arrangement.
Title:  At length the scout, who alone understood their habits, said, in their own
Title:  language:
Title:  
Title:  My daughters have done well; the white men thank them.
Title:  
Title:  Satisfied with this testimony in their favor, the girls proceeded to deposit
Title:  the body in a shell, ingeniously, and not inelegantly, fabricated of the
Title:  bark of the birch; after which they lowered it into its dark and final
Title:  abode. The ceremony of covering the remains, and concealing the marks of the
Title:  fresh earth, by leaves and other natural and customary objects, was
Title:  conducted with the same simple and silent forms. But when the labors of the
Title:  kind beings who had performed these sad and friendly offices were so far
Title:  completed, they hesitated, in a way to show that they knew not how much
Title:  further they might proceed. It was in this stage of the rites that the scout
Title:  again addressed them:
Title:  
Title:  My young women have done enough, he said: the spirit of the pale face has no
Title:  need of food or raiment, their gifts being according to the heaven of their
Title:  color. I see, he added, glancing an eye at David, who was preparing his book
Title:  in a manner that indicated an intention to lead the way in sacred song, that
Title:  one who better knows the Christian fashions is about to speak.
Title:  
Title:  The females stood modestly aside, and, from having been the principal actors
Title:  in the scene, they now became the meek and attentive observers of that which
Title:  followed. During the time David occupied in pouring out the pious feelings
Title:  of his spirit in this manner, not a sign of surprise, nor a look of
Title:  impatience, escaped them. They listened like those who knew the meaning of
Title:  the strange words, and appeared as if they felt the mingled emotions of
Title:  sorrow, hope, and resignation, they were intended to convey.
Title:  
Title:  Excited by the scene he had just witnessed, and perhaps influenced by his
Title:  own secret emotions, the master of song exceeded his usual efforts. His full
Title:  rich voice was not found to suffer by a comparison with the soft tones of
Title:  the girls; and his more modulated strains possessed, at least for the ears
Title:  of those to whom they were peculiarly addressed, the additional power of
Title:  intelligence. He ended the anthem, as he had commenced it, in the midst of a
Title:  grave and solemn stillness.
Title:  
Title:  When, however, the closing cadence had fallen on the ears of his auditors,
Title:  the secret, timorous glances of the eyes, and the general and yet subdued
Title:  movement of the assemblage, betrayed that something was expected from the
Title:  father of the deceased. Munro seemed sensible that the time was come for him
Title:  to exert what is, perhaps, the greatest effort of which human nature is
Title:  capable. He bared his gray locks, and looked around the timid and quiet
Title:  throng by which he was encircled, with a firm and collected countenance.
Title:  Then, motioning with his hand for the scout to listen, he said:
Title:  
Title:  Say to these kind and gentle females, that a heart-broken and failing man
Title:  returns them his thanks. Tell them, that the Being we all worship, under
Title:  different names, will be mindful of their charity; and that the time shall
Title:  not be distant when we may assemble around His throne without distinction of
Title:  sex, or rank, or color.
Title:  
Title:  The scout listened to the tremulous voice in which the veteran delivered
Title:  these words, and shook his head slowly when they were ended, as one who
Title:  doubted their efficacy.
Title:  
Title:  To tell them this, he said, would be to tell them that the snows come not in
Title:  the winter, or that the sun shines fiercest when the trees are stripped of
Title:  their leaves.
Title:  
Title:  Then turning to the women, he made such a communication of the other's
Title:  gratitude as he deemed most suited to the capacities of his listeners. The
Title:  head of Munro had already sunk upon his chest, and he was again fast
Title:  relapsing into melancholy, when the young Frenchman before named ventured to
Title:  touch him lightly on the elbow. As soon as he had gained the attention of
Title:  the mourning old man, he pointed toward a group of young Indians, who
Title:  approached with a light but closely covered litter, and then pointed upward
Title:  toward the sun.
Title:  
Title:  I understand you, sir, returned Munro, with a voice of forced firmness; I
Title:  understand you. It is the will of Heaven, and I submit. Cora, my child! if
Title:  the prayers of a heart-broken father could avail thee now, how blessed
Title:  shouldst thou be! Come, gentlemen, he added, looking about him with an air
Title:  of lofty composure, though the anguish that quivered in his faded
Title:  countenance was far too powerful to be concealed, our duty here is ended;
Title:  let us depart.
Title:  
Title:  Heyward gladly obeyed a summons that took them from a spot where, each
Title:  instant, he felt his self-control was about to desert him. While his
Title:  companions were mounting, however, he found time to press the hand of the
Title:  scout, and to repeat the terms of an engagement they had made to meet again
Title:  within the posts of the British army. Then, gladly throwing himself into the
Title:  saddle, he spurred his charger to the side of the litter, whence law and
Title:  stifled sobs alone announced the presence of Alice. In this manner, the head
Title:  of Munro again drooping on his bosom, with Heyward and David following in
Title:  sorrowing silence, and attended by the aid of Montcalm with his guard, all
Title:  the white men, with the exception of Hawkeye, passed from before the eyes of
Title:  the Delawares, and were buried in the vast forests of that region.
Title:  
Title:  But the tie which, through their common calamity, had united the feelings of
Title:  these simple dwellers in the woods with the strangers who had thus
Title:  transiently visited them, was not so easily broken. Years passed away before
Title:  the traditionary tale of the white maiden, and of the young warrior of the
Title:  Mohicans ceased to beguile the long nights and tedious marches, or to
Title:  animate their youthful and brave with a desire for vengeance. Neither were
Title:  the secondary actors in these momentous incidents forgotten. Through the
Title:  medium of the scout, who served for years afterward as a link between them
Title:  and civilized life, they learned, in answer to their inquiries, that the
Title:  Gray Head was speedily gathered to his fathers - borne down, as was
Title:  erroneously believed, by his military misfortunes; and that the Open Hand
Title:  had conveyed his surviving daughter far into the settlements of the pale
Title:  faces, where her tears had at last ceased to flow, and had been succeeded by
Title:  the bright smiles which were better suited to her joyous nature.
Title:  
Title:  But these were events of a time later than that which concerns our tale.
Title:  Deserted by all of his color, Hawkeye returned to the spot where his
Title:  sympathies led him, with a force that no ideal bond of union could destroy.
Title:  He was just in time to catch a parting look of the features of Uncas, whom
Title:  the Delawares were already inclosing in his last vestment of skins. They
Title:  paused to permit the longing and lingering gaze of the sturdy woodsman, and
Title:  when it was ended, the body was enveloped, never to be unclosed again. Then
Title:  came a procession like the other, and the whole nation was collected about
Title:  the temporary grave of the chief - temporary, because it was proper that, at
Title:  some future day, his bones should rest among those of this own people.
Title:  
Title:  The movement, like the feeling, had been simultaneous and general. The same
Title:  grave expression of grief, the same rigid silence, and the same deference to
Title:  the principal mourner, were observed around the place of interment as have
Title:  been already described. The body was deposited in an attitude of repose,
Title:  facing the rising sun, with the implements of war and of the chase at hand,
Title:  in readiness for the final journey. An opening was left in the shell, by
Title:  which it was protected from the soil, for the spirit to communicate with its
Title:  earthly tenement, when necessary; and the whole was concealed from the
Title:  instinct, and protected from the ravages of the beasts of prey, with an
Title:  ingenuity peculiar to the natives. The manual rites then ceased and all
Title:  present reverted to the more spiritual part of the ceremonies.
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook became once more the object of the common attention. He had not
Title:  yet spoken, and something consolatory and instructive was expected from so
Title:  renowned a chief on an occasion of such interest. Conscious of the wishes of
Title:  the people, the stern and self-restrained warrior raised his face, which had
Title:  latterly been buried in his robe, and looked about him with a steady eye.
Title:  His firmly compressed and expressive lips then severed, and for the first
Title:  time during the long ceremonies his voice was distinctly audible. Why do my
Title:  brothers mourn? he said, regarding the dark race of dejected warriors by
Title:  whom he was environed; why do my daughters weep? that a young man has gone
Title:  to the happy hunting-grounds; that a chief has filled his time with honor?
Title:  He was good; he was dutiful; he was brave. Who can deny it? The Manitou had
Title:  need of such a warrior, and He has called him away. As for me, the son and
Title:  the father of Uncas, I am a blazed pine, in a clearing of the pale faces. My
Title:  race has gone from the shores of the salt lake and the hills of the
Title:  Delawares. But who can say that the serpent of his tribe has forgotten his
Title:  wisdom? I am alone - -
Title:  
Title:  No, no, cried Hawkeye, who had been gazing with a yearning look at the rigid
Title:  features of his friend, with something like his own self-command, but whose
Title:  philosophy could endure no longer; no, Sagamore, not alone. The gifts of our
Title:  colors may be different, but God has so placed us as to journey in the same
Title:  path. I have no kin, and I may also say, like you, no people. He was your
Title:  son, and a red-skin by nature; and it may be that your blood was nearer -
Title:  but, if ever I forget the lad who has so often fou't at my side in war, and
Title:  slept at my side in peace, may He who made us all, whatever may be our color
Title:  or our gifts, forget me! The boy has left us for a time; but, Sagamore, you
Title:  are not alone.
Title:  
Title:  Chingachgook grasped the hand that, in the warmth of feeling, the scout had
Title:  stretched across the fresh earth, and in an attitude of friendship these two
Title:  sturdy and intrepid woodsmen bowed their heads together, while scalding
Title:  tears fell to their feet, watering the grave of Uncas like drops of falling
Title:  rain.
Title:  
Title:  In the midst of the awful stillness with which such a burst of feeling,
Title:  coming as it did, from the two most renowned warriors of that region, was
Title:  received, Tamenund lifted his voice to disperse the multitude.
Title:  
Title:  It is enough, he said. Go, children of the Lenape, the anger of the Manitou
Title:  is not done. Why should Tamenund stay? The pale faces are masters of the
Title:  earth, and the time of the red men has not yet come again. My day has been
Title:  too long. In the morning I saw the sons of Unamis happy and strong; and yet,
Title:  before the night has come, have I lived to see the last warrior of the wise
Title:  race of the Mohicans.
Title:  
Title:                                     FINIS
